
# Ryndor, the Weirded Lands

## Hail, and Well Met

Welcome to Ryndor
The winds shift, the rift calls, and the stars stir in their slumber. To walk Ryndor
is to walk between worlds—tread lightly, or be swept into the current of forces older
than time."
— Ophelia, Praetor Oracle and Leader of the Sev’rinn Rebellion
Welcome, Traveler, to the Weird Lands of Ryndor
Across Ryndor’s realms, the scars of old wars linger in stone, steel, and memory,
but now, The Weirding spreads through the land, bending reality itself. Nobles and
warlords hide ambitions behind silk curtains, while ancient cults stir beneath city
foundations, drawn to the shifting astral tides. The land responds to the ambitions of
its people—**floods, magical storms, and temporal anomalies** emerge when the
delicate balance is disturbed. Merchants whisper of roads that loop back upon
themselves, and scholars dream of cosmic awakenings that are impossible to explain.
In Ryndor, magic, technology, and faith weave together, their fragile interplay
destabilized by the flow of Primordial Resonance. This volatile magic, drawn from the
tension between the material and astral planes, is now affected by the Weirding,
making every spell both a resource and a risk. Sev’rinn practitioners carefully harness
this magic, knowing that each use risks fracturing reality further, inviting strange,
unintended effects. Entire villages have become trapped in time fractures, while
animals and plants mutate unpredictably under the influence of the astral surge.
Technology, once the Ullac Regime’s tool to suppress magic, has also been
warped by the Weirding. Automaton sentinels malfunction, and old artifacts taken
from Nebernoria behave unpredictably. The Rift, initially opened by the reckless
ambition of the Regime, is now a gaping wound leaking unstable magic that neither
science nor faith can fully control. Praetor Ophelia and Riven Trug, leaders of the
Sev’rinn rebellion, rallied against these forces to protect what remains of Ryndor’s
magic, but the Weirding’s spread has complicated their hard-won victory.
Faith, too, is altered by the Weirding. Gods still lend power, but their blessings
twist in strange ways, shaped not only by the hearts of their worshippers but by the
strange energies that surround them. Magic, science, and faith reflect the intent of
those who wield them, but under the influence of the Weirding, even the best
intentions can ripple outward unpredictably, bringing unexpected consequences.
Ryndor teeters on the edge of uncontrolled transformation. The Sev’rinn’s
mastery of elemental essences, the twisted remnants of Ullac technology, and the
entities stirring within Nebernoria—all struggle for dominance. Yet, fate in Ryndor is
not written in stone; it is woven from the choices of those brave enough to act. In a
world where possibility reigns, every step forward shifts the balance—toward
salvation or ruin—as The Weirding reshapes the path ahead.
Primordial Resonance
Primordial Resonance is born from the friction between realms, where the fabric

of Ryndor brushes against the chaotic expanse of the astral plane. This metaphysical
tension creates pockets of raw, unformed energy—an echo of creation itself. At these
seams where reality bends, Resonance leaks into the mortal world in unpredictable
bursts, as if the two planes cannot help but collide. It is neither stable nor infinite,
emerging only where existence trembles—whether from great conflict, moments of
heightened emotion, or disruptions in natural law.
The interaction between these planes generates a delicate balance: too much
resonance in one place destabilizes the environment, spawning astral storms or
temporal anomalies, while too little leaves regions drained of magic entirely.
Practitioners who draw on this energy, like the Sev’rinn, tap into the resonance at their
own risk, knowing that with every spell they cast, they not only shape reality but also
erode the boundary between worlds. As this energy ebbs and flows, so too does the
power of those connected to it—leaving Ryndor forever caught between order and
chaos, creation and collapse.
Rift to Nebernoria
The rift to Nebernoria is a mystical and mysterious gateway that connects Ryndor
to a small part of the astral plane called Nebernoria. The rift is located in the center of
Eveltoft, yet it remains a source of wonder and fear for many. The rift is guarded by
powerful enchantments and mystical creatures, ensuring that only the most skilled and
experienced travelers can pass through it safely. The rift itself is a shimmering,
pulsating portal that seems to vibrate with otherworldly energy.
The Rift to Nebernoria was born from the violent friction between the planes,
where the boundaries of Ryndor and the astral realm ground against each other until
they ripped open a hole in reality itself. This breach occurred in the heart of Eveltoft,
unleashing torrents of Primordial Resonance and astral anomalies into the world. The
Rift is not just a gateway—it is a wound, ever-expanding and unpredictable, spilling
forth both untapped power and unimaginable horrors. Those who venture too close are
changed, drawn into its currents or consumed by its chaos.
The Rift's formation altered the balance of magic in Ryndor, creating surges of
energy that empowered some while draining others. Attempts by the Ullac Regime to
control the Rift through technology and nullification fields failed, for the energy it
releases lies beyond mortal comprehension. Now, the Rift looms as both a promise and
a threat—offering ancient knowledge and boundless power to those bold enough to
claim it, but at the cost of inviting the astral’s relentless chaos into the fabric of the
mortal world.
Despite the risks, the rift is a source of great significance for the people of Ryndor.
It is a gateway to a world of incredible wonder and magic, where the laws of physics and
reality as we know them do not apply. It is a place where dreams and nightmares come
to life, and where the impossible becomes possible.
The interaction between these planes generates a delicate balance: too much
resonance in one place destabilizes the environment, spawning astral storms or
temporal anomalies, while too little leaves regions drained of magic entirely.
Practitioners who draw on this energy, like the Sev’rinn, tap into the resonance at their

own risk, knowing that with every spell they cast, they not only shape reality but also
erode the boundary between worlds. As this energy ebbs and flows, so too does the
power of those connected to it—leaving Ryndor forever caught between order and
chaos, creation and collapse.
The Weirding
The Weirding is a chaotic force born from the friction between the material and
astral planes, first unleashed with the appearance of the Rift to Nebernoria. It
permeates all aspects of Ryndor, warping reality in both subtle and catastrophic ways.
The familiar is transformed into the strange—**environments shift**, objects behave
unpredictably, and creatures mutate into unnatural forms. Time becomes unstable,
sometimes freezing or looping inexplicably, and spells can malfunction with dangerous
consequences.
No part of society is spared from the Weirding’s influence. Magic, technology,
and even faith are destabilized, forcing factions to adapt or fall victim to its strange
effects. Weird Zones, pockets of extreme distortion, appear unpredictably, altering the
landscape and posing new dangers to adventurers and citizens alike. Some see
opportunity in the chaos, delving into these anomalies for arcane power or forbidden
knowledge, while others work to contain or control it.
As the Weirding spreads, it reshapes Ryndor from a once familiar world into
something alien, uncanny, and unstable, forcing those within to rethink survival,
progress, and power.
How to Use this Book
The World of Ryndor offers a rich set of tools to enhance any game, whether
you’re running a homebrew campaign or supplementing an existing setting. Inside,
you’ll find:
- Characters, NPCs, and Settings: Easily integrate or adapt unique personalities
and locations into your world.
- Factions, Powers, and Governments: Introduce shifting alliances and political
intrigue.
- Reliquary of Items and Artifacts: Add magical artifacts, advanced technology,
and enchanted gear to invigorate gameplay.
- Bestiary of Magical Creatures: Populate your world with drakes, astral entities,
and more.
- Encounters, Adventures, and Campaign Arcs: Ready-to-use quests and events
to fit seamlessly into any campaign.
- New Player Options: Includes an entirely new class—the Sev’rinn—with
elemental customization, new features for existing classes, five new races, and one
racial variant.
- Random Tables: A collection of tables for inspiration and quick session
planning.
Whether you use the material wholesale or pick and choose what fits your needs,
this book serves as a flexible toolkit to bring the complex, magical world of Ryndor to

life.

# The All-Ryndor Catalogue

Welcome to the comprehensive guide to Ryndor, a land steeped in history, shaped
by its geography, and defined by its unique calendar system. From the bustling port city
of Surreymouth to the floating island of Holmea, Ryndor is a place of adventure and
wonder. But to truly appreciate the land and its people, one must understand its rich
history and geography. The land of Ryndor was shaped by powerful magical forces,
which created vast forests, towering mountains, and sprawling plains. Its many cities
and townships are as diverse as the land itself, with their own unique cultures,
histories, and traditions.

# History

The Sev'rinns of Ryndor are powerful magic wielders. Some Sev'rinns exhibit
strengths in certain Earth elements like water or wind, and some Sev'rinns seem to be
able to commune with the dead, or see the future. Sev'rinns usually begin to exhibit
their powers at a very young age. Their hair is usually the first indicator of which kind of
power runs through their veins, as it will begin to grow in vibrant colors when they are
about three or four years old. A young Sev'rinn will usually show an affinity for items or
places that match their powers, like Ziran Sev'rinns will become overjoyed when
surrounded by nature or animals, Sorash Sev'rinns will enjoy flying and being at great
heights.
A young Sev'rinn will usually show an affinity for items or places that match their
powers, like nature Sev'rinns will become overjoyed when surrounded by nature or
animals, air Sev'rinns will enjoy flying and being at great heights.
The Royal Sev'rinn Bloodline
The Sev'rinns were the rulers of Ryndor for three centuries, since Aldrin Shun
became the first Sev'rinn after the Battle of Ardentor.
After years of torment and torture at the claws of the giant Fire Wyrm Ardentor,
the armies of Ryndor marched upon his mountain lair and called him out to face them in
battle. Thousands of men and women were lost in the Battle of Ardentor, and so it
seemed that the nations of Ryndor would also be lost to Ardentor's fires.
Standing alone in an ashen field among the thousands of dead, Aldrin Shun stood
and raised his arms aloft as the fearsome Ardentor released a final, massive fireball
from his jaws. Instead of being consumed by the flames, Aldrin's skin glowed fiercely,
and his hair stood upon its end, as the flames were absorbed into his body.
He swirled the flames around himself, and outstretched an arm to command
Ardentor to submit to his will. Ardentor writhed and recoiled from Aldrin's command,
and was engulfed in white fire. Ardentor screamed and swiped his massive claws at
Aldrin. They fought this way for days, until the dawn of the tenth day when Ardentor

finally bowed his head before Aldrin. And Aldrin collapsed in exhaustion upon the giant
Fire Wyrm's snout. Ardentor carried him back to his dwelling in the city of Eveltoft,
where Aldrin would be declared the Emberclad Sev'rinn.
He became a beloved ruler of Ryndor, and birthed a bloodline of magical progeny
that would unite and rule over Ryndor for a prosperous and peaceful age. Aldrin took a
wife named Kaida, who was a gifted healer. Some believe her to have possessed some
magic of her own, although the truth of her gifts has been lost to time. Kaida and Aldrin
had three children: the youngest were twin girls Miyu and Eira, and the eldest a boy
named Destin. Miyu and Eira were both gentle and kind, but possessed no magical gift
in their blood.
Destin, however, proved to be a powerful wielder of nature magics. He became
the first Greenheart Sev'rinn, and contributed much to the taming of wild beasts to use
in Eveltoft as work beasts and magical familiars. Destin had two children with his wife
Kari: Gyda the elder, and Einar the younger. Kari sadly passed during the birth of their
third child, named Sylvi, who did not survive much longer than an hour. So saddened
was he by the death of his wife and third child, Destin retreated to the woods with his
closest companion, a giant male albino elk called Inge. Ten days passed before he
returned, and he was never the same, but far more powerful than before. He started the
Hilderturgy, a tradition by which the Elder Sev'rinn would teach and pass down their
magical knowledge to their progeny. He taught Gyda and Einar rigorously, and both
exhibited magically touched blood. Gyda would soon become the stronger. She
possessed power over both water and wind, and became the Tideborn Skycaller Sev'rinn
when she was no more than 18.
The following decades were fruitful for the descendants of Aldrin Shun, and many
beloved Sev'rinn would bring prosperity and knowledge to all of Ryndor:
Gyda's daughter Celestia, the Lithomage Sev'rinn, who built most of the sanctuary
city of Eveltoft.
Celestia's son Aethelric, the Eidolon Sev'rinn, who ruled for only five years before
his untimely death.
Aethelric's son Kenjiro, the Voidstrider Sev'rinn, who ruled for more than 80 years.
Kenjiro 's daughter Runa, the Emberclad Eidolon Sev'rinn, said to be the most
powerful since Aldrin himself.
Descent into Darkness
Runa, powerful as she was, birthed no magical children of her own. None of her
seven progeny could pass the Hilderturgy, and she became desperate to pass her magic
on to the next heir of Ryndor. She used her ability to commune with the dead to create
the dark magic of necromancy, sacrificing the soul of her newest born child in an
attempt to create the magical soul of a Sev'rinn. It was thought that this child died in
the womb, and none but her eldest Knute knew the truth.
Runa birthed a grey skinned child that she named Torgar. He passed the
Hilderturgy before the age of ten, and was a full blooded Sev'rinn by the time he was 15.
Torgar was vicious, cruel, and greedy. He lacked the gentleness that was the hallmark of
the previous Sev'rinns. He reveled in war and violence, and bred the strongest military

Eveltoft had ever seen. He introduced crippling taxes on the surrounding cities in
Ryndor, and marched his armies upon them when they couldn't pay.
The Torgarian War
A civil war was brewing against Torgar, led by his own brother Knute. Runa
attempted to quell the rage in her son Torgar to save Ryndor and Knute. She told him he
was birthed from the spirit of her own sacrificed child. Torgar was enraged and
heartbroken, and took the life of his mother Runa, while Knute was watching, unknown
to both of them. In that moment, Knute called the guerilla army to march against the
army of Torgar, and their war tore the city of Eveltoft to shreds. It is said that the war
raged for ten years, as the Atmani Sev'rinn Torgar resurrected his armies over and over.
Knute won only by brute force and determination. He marched nearly the entire
population of Ryndor to their death to defeat Torgar, and the entire island was
devastated for decades following the war. Eveltoft had been razed to the ground, and
much of the history of the Sev'rinns was lost. Little is known about what became of the
other six children of Runa. It is generally assumed that they were killed by Torgar before
the Torgarian war.
The Ullac Regime
After the victory of Knute, he called his regime Ullac, named for law and order.
The bylaws of Ryndors were drawn, and the oppressive nature of Knute’s regime began
to reveal itself
The ruling class became more interested in accumulating wealth and power than
in serving the people of Ryndors. Taxes were raised to exorbitant levels, and minor
offenses were punished harshly, with many innocent people being imprisoned or even
executed.
In addition, magical creatures and people were hunted down and killed
ruthlessly, leading to a rebellion known as the Sev'rinn Rebellion. The Sev'rinns, who
were descendants of the first Sev'rinn, Aldrin Shun, began to revive the old ways, and
many people began to turn to them for guidance and protection.
The Sev'rinn Rebellion
Led by the powerful magical Sev'rinn, Praetor Oracle Ophelia, the Sev'rinn
Rebellion fought against the Ullac Regime for years. The Sev'rinns, were on the brink of
defeat when the rift to Nebernoria suddenly appeared in the heart of Ryndor.
At first, no one knew what to make of the strange portal, but it quickly became
apparent that it was the key to the Sev'rinns' salvation. The rift opened up a pathway to
Nebernoria, where the Sev'rinns discovered powerful magical artifacts and advanced
technology that they used to turn the tide of the war.
The Sev'rinns' forces became augmented with new weapons and armor made
from the strange materials found in Nebernoria, and their fighters were trained in
powerful spells and magical abilities that gave them a decisive edge in combat. The
Ullac Regime was caught off guard by the Sev'rinns' sudden shift in power, and they
were unable to withstand the rebels' new arsenal.

In the end, the rift to Nebernoria was a key factor in the Sev'rinns' ultimate
victory over the Ullac Regime. The rebels were able to use the resources they found in
Nebernoria to improve their lives and the lives of their people, and the rift itself became
a symbol of hope and freedom in Ryndor.
The Ullac Regime became increasingly desperate as the rebellion continued to
gain momentum. They began to rely more heavily on brutality, which only served to
further alienate them from the people of Ryndor. Eventually, their forces were
weakened to the point where they could no longer resist the rebels.
In the end, the Sev'rinn Rebellion was victorious, and the Ullac Regime was
overthrown. Praetor Oracle Ophelia emerged as a beloved leader and a symbol of hope
for the people of Ryndors. She helped to establish a new system of governance that was
fair and just for all, and she worked to rebuild the damaged relationships between the
various nations that had been torn apart by the conflict.
The Nebernorian Accord
The Rift to Nebernoria brought more than knowledge and danger—it ushered in
the beginnings of The Weirding, fundamentally altering the terms of the Nebernorian
Accord. As reality itself frayed under the influence of the Rift, the Sev’rinn Council and
scholars struggled to maintain control. Strange mutations and anomalies began to
emerge among artifacts and explorers alike, complicating efforts to catalog and
regulate items retrieved from Nebernoria.
The Keepers of the Rift, once focused solely on controlling passage between
realms, were forced to confront escalating Weird Zones forming near the portal. These
areas twisted space and time unpredictably, creating challenges for the Keepers and
opportunities for rogue factions. The airships of Skyhaven—once reliable vessels for
trade and exploration—reported that routes through Weird Zones had begun to change
mid-flight, leaving expeditions stranded or lost.
Attempts to negotiate with Nebernorian entities became more erratic as the
Weirding intensified, warping communications and intentions. Benevolent spirits
became cryptic or volatile, and previously cooperative beings now offered deals laced
with strange conditions and lingering curses. The Crystal Scholars scrambled to
contain the growing instability, realizing that the very fabric of the Accord could not
withstand the shifting nature of the Rift’s influence.
Over time, rumors of corruption within the Keepers of the Rift gained traction, as
some members grew obsessed with the strange power of the Weirding. Factions seeking
to exploit the Rift took advantage of these distractions, smuggling cursed artifacts
across Ryndor, spreading further instability. Tensions between the major cities—
especially Ban Mynydd and Eveltoft—intensified, with each vying to secure the
resources and knowledge the Rift offered, no matter the cost.
Today, the future of the Accord is precarious. With the Weirding now a
permanent part of Ryndor, the Rift stands as both a gateway to limitless possibility
and a harbinger of chaos. Every expedition, every artifact, and every deal carries risks
that can no longer be fully understood. Adventurers must ask themselves not only if the
rewards of Nebernoria are worth the danger, but also if the world can survive the

consequences of what they bring back.
A Weird Utopia
The Crystal Scholars emerged from the devastation of the War of the Sev’rinns,
determined to rebuild society with fairness, justice, and opportunity for all. Under the
leadership of the visionary Ophelia, they established a government centered on
knowledge, inclusivity, and exploration. Yet their dream of utopia faces an unforeseen
challenge—the growing influence of The Weirding.
The Weirding has transformed the Scholars' ambitions, particularly their work
around the Rift to Nebernoria. While the rift offers access to unparalleled magical
insights and powerful resources, it also leaks chaotic astral energies that twist reality.
Artifacts brought back from Nebernoria sometimes carry hidden dangers, causing
unexpected mutations or time distortions, forcing the Scholars to adopt stricter
protocols. Despite their best efforts, the Weirding has made every expedition a gamble,
with potential rewards as great as the risks.
The presence of the Weird Zones complicates everyday life. Agriculture and trade
have been disrupted by spatial anomalies, forcing society to adapt quickly. Education
and healthcare—pillars of Ryndor’s new order—must now contend with astral plagues
and weird afflictions, yet the Scholars remain dedicated to ensuring access to these
resources for all. Magical misfires and technological glitches occur more frequently,
but the Sev’rinns work tirelessly to maintain the delicate balance between elements.
Though diversity and equality remain core ideals of the Scholars, the Weirding
strains even the most robust structures of this utopia. Factions and rogue groups take
advantage of the chaos, smuggling dangerous artifacts or exploiting the instability for
personal gain. Despite these growing tensions, the people of Ryndor remain committed
to their shared vision of progress and unity.
This new era demands adaptability. The Crystal Scholars’ pursuit of knowledge
and the Sev’rinns’ mastery of magic have never been more important. The citizens of
Ryndor know that while The Weirding may change the rules, the dream of a better
future still endures—if they are willing to pay the price.

# Factions & Powers

Factions and Powers
Ryndor is shaped by shifting alliances and powerful factions, each vying for
control over magic, technology, and political influence. This section explores the major
players—governments, rogue groups, and ideological movements—that shape the
world’s fate. From the Crystal Scholars and their pursuit of knowledge, to the Keepers of
the Rift, dedicated to safeguarding astral breaches, and the remnants of the Ullac
Regime, factions offer both opportunities and challenges. Each faction presents
narrative depth and moral ambiguity, allowing players to ally, infiltrate, or oppose
forces throughout their adventures.
The Ullac Regime
The Ullac Regime was built on centralized authoritarian control, with Knute

Shun-Rote at its apex as the first Supreme Chancellor. Power was consolidated in a rigid
hierarchy, where each region of Ryndor was governed by appointed bureaucrats and
military commanders, all directly accountable to the central government in Eveltoft.
The regime maintained its dominance through a council of technocrats who oversaw
the development of powerful technologies, and an internal security force tasked with
rooting out magical practitioners and dissenters. This tightly controlled structure
ensured compliance through surveillance, taxation, and the suppression of magic.
Though the Ullac Regime has fallen, its influence lingers in the form of black
market trade. The most sought-after commodities are nullification engines and antimagic technology, highly coveted by factions that wish to suppress magic or control its
use. Former regime operatives, mercenaries, and rogue inventors smuggle these
artifacts into cities like Eveltoft and Wyrmbost, where they fetch exorbitant prices. The
underground trade of these devices threatens the delicate balance of Ryndor, offering
dangerous power to those bold enough to claim it.
The Crystal Scholars
The Crystal Scholars, the modern technocratic government of Ryndor, emerged
from the ashes of the War of the Sev’rinns, determined to create a society rooted in
justice, equality, and knowledge. Led by the visionary Ophelia, they have since become
a beacon of hope. However, their mission has grown more complex with the emergence
of The Weirding, a force that warps magic, time, and space. This phenomenon has
challenged their ideals, forcing them to adapt their methods in unprecedented ways.
The Rift to Nebernoria serves as both an opportunity and a threat, channeling the
strange energies of The Weirding into Ryndor. Scholars stationed around the Rift
navigate these chaotic forces, balancing exploration with containment. Despite strict
safeguards, anomalies have crept into Eveltoft, threatening the city’s stability. The
Weirding has impacted council decisions, as new dangers force the Scholars to confront
uncertainty in ways that test their resolve and leadership.
The 12 Seats of the Crystal Scholars
The twelve members of the council play pivotal roles in guiding Ryndor through
both progress and unpredictability. Each seat represents a value essential to society, but
The Weirding has added new complexities to their work. Elections to the council remain
rigorous, requiring unanimous agreement among the remaining members, but now
evaluations also account for candidates’ resilience against Weirding influence.
Seat of Justice – Celia Gray: The unpredictable effects of The Weirding
complicate law enforcement, and Celia now navigates strange cases where time and
intent blur, forcing her to redefine justice in uncertain circumstances
Seat of Wisdom – Agatha Raine: Agatha oversees magical education but now
must restructure the curriculum to address anomalies and magical surges. Her role
includes guiding scholars to safely research both magic and Weirding phenomena.
Seat of Compassion – Amara Moonflower: The Weirding introduces new
afflictions and magical illnesses, requiring Amara to devise unique treatments while
maintaining equal healthcare access. Some ailments are so strange they alter not just

the body but the soul.
Seat of Innovation – Zephyr Ironsmith: Zephyr harnesses Weirding energy for
new technologies but must tread carefully, as experiments frequently result in
unpredictable consequences. His inventions help contain anomalies, but each
breakthrough comes with unknown risks.
Seat of Faith – Sister Althea: With The Weirding distorting even divine magic,
Sister Althea guides the faithful through crises of belief. She works tirelessly to ensure
that spirituality remains a grounding force in an increasingly surreal world.
Seat of Harmony – Lysandra Dawnstar: Diplomacy becomes more difficult as
cities demand control of Weird Zones for their resources. Lysandra works to broker
peace between factions while maintaining the unity of the council amidst rising
tensions.
Seat of Nature – Jasper Windwhisper: The Weirding has caused mutations in
flora and fauna, threatening ecosystems. Jasper leads efforts to stabilize these changes
while learning to coexist with the new, strange lifeforms emerging from the anomalies.
Seat of Industry – Bartholomew Solis: Bartholomew must balance economic
growth with the dangers of Weirding artifacts that disrupt trade. He brokers deals to
ensure trade routes remain open, even as airships and caravans are lost to spatial shifts.
Seat of Courage – Galen Stormbreaker: Galen’s warriors now face astral
creatures and temporal threats, training for conflicts far beyond conventional warfare.
His leadership inspires others to confront the unknown with bravery and
determination.
The Crystal Scholars strive to maintain stability as The Weirding redefines the
fabric of their society. Each of the twelve seats plays a vital role in adapting to these
new realities, blending tradition with flexibility to guide Ryndor through a strange and
volatile era. Their commitment to knowledge, progress, and unity remains
unwavering, even as they stand on the precipice of the unknown.
Keepers of the Rift
The Keepers of the Rift remain a secretive, elite order of scholars, mages, and
warriors, charged with safeguarding the Rift to Nebernoria. However, the emergence of
The Weirding has altered both their mission and methods. As reality itself frays, the
Keepers now face threats not only from Nebernoria’s astral entities but from the
strange anomalies spreading across Ryndor. Weird Zones near the Rift distort time and
space, complicating the tasks of maintaining wards and documenting findings.
The scholars struggle to keep pace with the unstable nature of the Rift, as
discoveries become erratic and sometimes dangerous. Artifacts retrieved from the Rift
are now laced with unpredictable Weirding energy, leading to unexpected phenomena
and mutations. The mages bolster the magical wards not only to block malevolent
entities but to contain the surges of reality-warping energy that threaten to spread into
the city of Eveltoft. Some among them have begun to experiment with new forms of
astral magic, though these efforts carry risks of corruption.
The warriors face new challenges as astral creatures grow stronger and more
unpredictable, mutated by The Weirding’s influence. They train tirelessly, preparing for

encounters that defy logic, where space shifts beneath their feet and time loops create
strange echoes of battles.
The Keepers now operate with increased secrecy from their hidden fortress, as
both the public and rogue factions grow suspicious of their activities. Tensions rise
between the Keepers and the Crystal Scholars, with some whispering that exposure to
the Rift has begun to corrupt the Keepers themselves. Yet, the Keepers remain loyal to
their charge, willing to do whatever it takes to safeguard the Rift, knowing that if the
balance tips too far, Ryndor itself could unravel.
The Holmean Magical Creature Society
The Holmean Magical Creature Society is dedicated to the study, preservation,
and ethical management of Ryndor’s magical creatures, headquartered on the island of
Holmea. They collaborate with scholars, Sev’rinns, and drake trainers from
Wyrmbost, focusing on endangered species and monitoring the effects of Primordial
Resonance. However, The Weirding has introduced unforeseen challenges, further
complicating their mission.
Many creatures have begun to display bizarre mutations—some become more
aggressive, others develop strange abilities, and certain fauna now resonate with astral
energies, warping ecosystems. The Society works tirelessly to contain and study these
mutations, but the unpredictable nature of the Weirding forces constant adaptation.
They have expanded their focus to include astral incursions, as creatures born from the
Rift wander into Ryndor, disrupting local ecosystems and threatening native species.
The Society also combats the illicit trade of Weird-touched creatures. These
mutated beings are highly sought after on the black market, prized for their
unpredictable properties and dangerous allure. Their efforts are critical to preventing
the spread of unstable creatures throughout Ryndor. Teams of researchers and
conservationists now venture into Weird Zones, recording changes and retrieving
creatures before they are exploited.
Through it all, the Society remains committed to balancing exploration with
preservation. They work alongside the Crystal Scholars to predict and mitigate
Weirding effects on fauna, ensuring that Ryndor’s magical ecosystems can survive this
strange new era. Yet, the Society knows that every encounter with the Weirding carries
risks, as even the creatures they protect may become something unrecognizable.

# Geography & Resources

Geography
Ryndor’s volcanic origins shape its dynamic landscape, from lava fields and
natural hot springs to black sand beaches and snow-capped mountains. The arrival of
The Weirding has further altered the land—**entire villages now lie trapped in slow
time zones**, caught in endless twilight, while Holmea’s islands float mysteriously
above the sea, suspended in the thick mists of a powerful Weird Zone.
Ryndor’s waterfalls and rivers, harnessed for energy, now run unpredictably.
Wind-tunnel channels through Eveltoft bring erratic storms, yet the city thrives on its
wind and water power. Ban Mynydd’s mining industry still flourishes, with aluminum

and iron veins, though miners report strange seismic anomalies deep in the earth—
shifting tunnels and creatures emerging from forgotten layers.
While Surreymouth’s fishing grounds remain fertile, peculiar fish exhibiting
mutations and astral properties have begun to appear, complicating trade. In
Wyrmbost, where beasts are bred to work alongside the people, hybrid Fire Wyrms
show signs of new behavior patterns influenced by astral energies. The city’s few crops
struggle, as time fractures create erratic growing seasons, making food management
more challenging than ever.
Holmea, once thought uninhabitable, now floats ominously above the ocean,
surrounded by mist and twisting gravity anomalies. While the smaller islands remain
barren, they serve as launching points for expeditions into the strange heights of
Holmea’s floating isle—a place that defies conventional laws of time and space.
The people of Ryndor adapt, but The Weirding has embedded uncertainty into
every aspect of life. Progress and survival demand resilience, as the forces of magic,
nature, and technology increasingly warp under this strange new reality.
Natural Resources
Ryndor’s natural wealth lies in its rivers, waterfalls, and powerful winds, but
even these familiar resources have not escaped the influence of The Weirding. Eveltoft,
the windiest city in the region, sits within a volatile wind tunnel between two
mountains. While the city's wind and water power once brought reliable prosperity,
unstable currents and storms caused by Weird Zones have made energy harvesting
unpredictable. Sudden wind shifts can overload turbines, and rivers occasionally flow
backward or run dry overnight, forcing engineers to constantly adapt to the shifting
elements.
In addition to wind, water, and geothermal energy, Ryndor’s mineral veins
provide crucial resources. Ban Mynydd thrives on its aluminum and iron mines, but
miners have begun reporting strange anomalies deep underground—entire shafts
vanish, and veins shift positions seemingly overnight. Some believe astral energies are
slowly permeating the earth, turning once-stable resources unstable. Miners rely on
the assistance of miniature hybrid Fire Wyrms, bred in Wyrmbost, to navigate these
treacherous conditions. However, these beasts have begun showing signs of mutation,
sometimes growing extra limbs or exhibiting unexpected magical abilities—an
unsettling byproduct of prolonged exposure to Primordial Resonance.
While the southern fishing grounds off Surreymouth remain a vital source of
food, the ocean has been affected by the unpredictable influence of the Weirding.
Strange mutated sea creatures have been caught, some glowing with astral energy,
others poisonous or capable of slipping between dimensions. This makes fishing a more
dangerous task, though nearly inexhaustible food resources continue to flow from the
sea to feed Ryndor’s population.
Beyond Ryndor, Nebernoria’s rare resources are in high demand but have
become more perilous to extract. Nebernite, a prized mineral used to create potent
magical artifacts and potions, has grown even harder to locate. Astral storms and time
fractures in Nebernoria make mining operations unpredictable, with some expeditions

never returning. Those who do return often find their nebernite deposits altered or
corrupted, giving the material strange and often volatile new properties.
Neberbloom, a rare and sought-after plant, is also affected by The Weirding.
Known for its ability to absorb and store magical energy, the plant has mutated
alongside its environment. Some blooms exhibit strange behavior— releasing waves of
raw magic when disturbed or shifting to different planes without warning. Extracting
neberbloom requires not just expertise but significant caution, as improperly harvested
specimens can warp the surrounding landscape or trigger dangerous magical surges.
The Weirding’s pervasive influence has made Ryndor’s natural wealth both a
blessing and a curse. While the land still provides, its gifts are increasingly
unpredictable, volatile, and dangerous. Every harvest, whether from the sea, the
mines, or the Rift, is a gamble, and only those bold enough to adapt can hope to thrive
in this new, strange world.

# Society & Culture

Society and Culture
The Society and Culture of Ryndor is as diverse and multifaceted as the land itself,
shaped by the interplay of traditions, economy, and competition. Cities like Eveltoft and
Wyrmbost boast vibrant festivals and public competitions, with sports being both
entertainment and symbolic of regional pride. Currency flows through the hands of
merchants and nobles alike, with coins such as the Fimbulmynt and Hrafnmynt
forming the lifeblood of trade. Holidays tied to celestial events punctuate the year, while
cultural practices reflect regional identities and ancient customs, grounding the people
in both heritage and ambition.
Seasons and Celebrations
Winter's Requiem marks the beginning of the year in Ryndor. The first month of
the calendar marks the arrival of winter, with the three moons visible in the night sky,
each with its unique shape and color. The people of this place have learned to brace
themselves for the harsh weather that accompanies the arrival of this month. The
nights are long, and the temperatures drop dramatically, covering the land in a blanket
of snow and ice. Most of the animals retreat to their burrows or hibernate during this
time, making food scarce. The people light fires in their hearths, gather around to share
stories and huddle together to keep warm. It is a month of survival, of conserving
energy, and of preparing for the long winter ahead.
Frost's Grip The second month of winter is marked by the coldest and harshest
weather of the year, with the sun barely visible on the horizon during the day. As the icy
winds howl across the land, the people of Ryndor huddle close to their hearths and wrap
themselves in thick furs. The harsh weather makes travel difficult and dangerous, and
many choose to stay close to home during this month.
The mountains and forests are blanketed in snow and ice, creating a stunningly
beautiful but treacherous landscape. Despite the hardships of this month, the people of
Ryndor are a hardy and resilient people, and they take pride in their ability to weather
even the harshest of winters.

Thaw's Promise As winter begins to lose its grip, the people of Ryndor look
forward to the promise of spring, with the sun rising higher in the sky and the moons
becoming more prominent. Thaw's Promise is the third month of the Ryndorian
calendar, and it marks the time when winter begins to lose its grip on the land. The days
start to grow longer, and the temperature slowly begins to rise. Although the snow and
ice still cover the ground, signs of new life start to appear. The first buds on trees and
bushes begin to appear, and the frozen streams and rivers start to thaw. The people of
Ryndor feel a sense of hope and renewal as they anticipate the coming of spring. They
start to prepare for the planting season, knowing that the promise of new growth and
abundance is just around the corner.
Spring's Awakening The fourth month of the Ryndorian calendar is Spring's
Awakening, which marks the arrival of spring in the land of Ryndor. As the snow melts
away, the trees begin to bud, and the flowers start to bloom, filling the air with their
sweet fragrances. Birds return to the forests and fields, and the animals that have been
hibernating throughout the winter start to emerge from their burrows. The people of
Ryndor celebrate the return of the sun and the promise of new life, eagerly preparing for
the warmer months to come.
As for holidays, the most significant event in Ryndor is the Frostmoon Festival,
which takes place in mid-winter, around the time of the winter solstice. It is a
celebration of the changing of the seasons and the rebirth of the sun. People light
bonfires and lanterns to symbolize the returning light, and they exchange gifts and
feasts. Other holidays include the Harvest Festival in autumn and the Spring Equinox
Festival in spring.
Ryndorian Calendar
Winter's Requiem.
The first month of the calendar marks the arrival of winter.
Frost's Grip.
The second month of winter is marked by the coldest and harshest weather of the
year.
Thaw's Promise.
As winter begins to lose its grip, the people of Ryndor look forward to the promise of
spring.
Spring's Awakening.
The arrival of spring is marked by the blooming of flowers and the return of birds to
the forests and fields.
Rain's Blessing.
The fifth month of the calendar is marked by the arrival of heavy rains, which bring
new life and vitality to the land.
Harvest's Bounty.
As the summer wears on, the people of Ryndor begin to harvest the fruits of their
labor.
Autumn's Ember .
The arrival of autumn is marked by the changing of the leaves and the cooler

temperatures that herald the approach of winter.
Hunter's Moon.
The eighth month of the calendar is marked by the arrival of the Hunter's Moon,
which signals the beginning of the hunting season.
The Long Night.
The final month of the year marks the arrival of winter and the longest nights of the
year.
Holidays
In Ryndor, there are several major holidays throughout the year that are
celebrated by its people. These holidays are an important part of the cultural fabric of
Ryndor, and they are celebrated by people of all backgrounds and faiths.
New Year's Day. This is the first day of the year, and it is celebrated with feasting
and fireworks. Many people also make New Year's resolutions to improve their lives in
the coming year.
Spring Equinox. This marks the first day of spring, and it is celebrated with the
planting of seeds and the beginning of new projects. Many people also hold bonfires and
feasts to welcome the return of the warmer weather.
Summer Solstice. This is the longest day of the year, and it is celebrated with
outdoor festivities and games. Many people also hold large feasts to celebrate the
abundance of crops and fruits that come with the summer months.
Autumn Equinox. This marks the first day of fall, and it is celebrated with the
harvesting of crops and the preparation for the long winter ahead. Many people also
hold feasts and bonfires to celebrate the changing of the seasons.
Frostmoon Festival. This is a three-day festival that celebrates the first snowfall
of the year. Many people hold feasts and bonfires, and there are often competitions and
games held to mark the occasion. It is also a time when people honor their ancestors
and loved ones who have passed away, and many visit graveyards to leave offerings of
food and drink.
Winter Solstice. This is the shortest day of the year, and it is celebrated with the
lighting of candles and fires to symbolize the return of the light. Many people also
exchange gifts and hold feasts to celebrate the end of the old year and the beginning of
the new.
Culture
Ryndorian culture is diverse and varied, with different regions having their own
unique traditions and customs. However, there are some common threads that tie all
Ryndorians together.
Family is highly valued in Ryndorian culture, with close-knit extended families
often living together in multi-generational households. Marriage is also an important
institution, with arranged marriages being common in some regions. Respect for elders
and ancestors is another key aspect of Ryndorian culture, with many rituals and
festivals dedicated to honoring those who have come before.
Art and music are highly valued in Ryndorian culture, with many communities

having their own distinct styles of music and dance. Storytelling is also a revered
tradition, with many myths and legends passed down through generations.
Hard work and perseverance are highly valued in Ryndorian culture, with many
communities being self-sufficient and relying on agriculture or artisanal crafts for their
livelihoods. Craftspeople and artisans are highly respected for their skills and creativity.
Magic
Magic in Ryndor is a deeply ingrained part of the culture, with many individuals
having the ability to perform magical feats to varying degrees. Magic is respected and
revered, but also feared, as it is known to have the potential to cause great harm if not
wielded responsibly.
Many people in Ryndor view magic as a gift, with those who are born with
magical abilities often seen as chosen by the gods. As a result, those with magical
abilities are often held in high regard, with some even being seen as spiritual leaders or
advisers to rulers. However, there is also a great deal of superstition surrounding magic,
with some people believing that those who possess magical abilities are cursed or
possessed by demons.
There are also many different types of magic in Ryndor, each with its own set of
practitioners and traditions. Some types of magic, such as healing magic, are widely
accepted and even encouraged, while others, such as dark magic, are feared and often
outlawed. Despite this, many practitioners of dark magic still exist, often operating in
secret or under the guise of other professions.
Sev'rinns
In Ryndor, Sev'rinns hold great cultural significance as powerful magic wielders
and spiritual leaders. Sev'rinns are those who experienced The Spark, and chose to
pursue training in their natural gifts. They are respected members of society, often
sought out for their advice and guidance on matters both mundane and mystical.
Sev'rinns are known for their ability to communicate with the spirits of the natural
world and the ancestors, and are often called upon to perform rituals and ceremonies to
honor these spirits.
The training of a Sev'rinn is a long and arduous process, requiring both natural
talent and extensive study of magical theory and practice. Sev'rinns are expected to
adhere to a strict code of ethics, which emphasizes the responsible use of their powers
and a deep respect for the spirits and the natural world. As such, Sev'rinns are often
seen as stewards of the land and the keepers of ancient wisdom, and play a vital role in
maintaining the balance between the physical and spiritual realms in Ryndor.
Religion
Religion in Ryndor plays a vital role in the cultural identity and spiritual lives of
its people. Much like magic, faith is deeply respected—seen as a source of both hope
and guidance. The gods of Ryndor, though distant and mysterious, are believed to
influence the world in subtle ways, lending their power to those whose convictions
burn brightest. Yet, as with magic, religion is also viewed with a mix of reverence and

fear, for divine blessings can be fickle, and some believe the gods’ attention comes at a
price.
The people of Ryndor view faith not as a passive belief but as an active
relationship with the divine, requiring devotion, rituals, and offerings. Priests and
spiritual leaders are highly respected, often serving as advisers to rulers and
counselors to the community. Religious festivals and ceremonies are woven into the
rhythms of life, marking the changing seasons, the rise and fall of kingdoms, and the
phases of celestial bodies. In some cities, shrines are built atop ancient ley lines or near
astral anomalies, believed to channel divine energy more effectively.
However, as with magic, the influence of faith varies. Different gods and
traditions hold sway in different regions, and worship practices reflect the unique local
cultures and needs. In the coastal city of Surreymouth, sailors offer prayers to gods of
the sea, while the druids of Wyrmbost revere nature spirits and conduct rites to honor
the balance between the elements. Some gods are gentle and benevolent, while others
are demanding or wrathful, rewarding loyalty and punishing betrayal with equal
measure.
The Weirding has further complicated the nature of faith. Miracles are no longer
always distinguishable from magical anomalies, and divine visions have grown
increasingly strange—cryptic dreams, disjointed prophecies, and fragmented symbols.
Some believe that the gods are responding to the disruption of the astral plane, while
others fear that even the divine is no longer beyond the Weirding’s reach. Clergy and
prophets struggle to interpret these signs, leading to rifts between religious sects as
they debate the meaning behind these new occurrences.
Despite this uncertainty, religion remains a powerful force, shaping the political
landscape and cultural practices of Ryndor. Faith is not simply a way to understand the
unknown—it is a tool for survival, a source of strength, and for many, a beacon of
hope amid the growing chaos of the Weirding. Those who walk the path of faith do so
knowing that the gods’ favor is as unpredictable as the world they inhabit, but they
continue their devotions, believing that even in times of strangeness and upheaval, the
divine will guide them toward a greater purpose.
Social Customs
The people of Ryndor take great pride in their traditions and social customs,
viewing them as essential threads in the intricate tapestry of their society. These
practices foster trust, community, and connection, grounding individuals in their
shared history and cultural identity, even as the world shifts around them. In a land
where magic, technology, and faith collide—and where The Weirding constantly
disrupts reality—customs serve as anchors of stability, offering comfort and continuity
amidst the chaos.
Ryndorian customs reflect both the diversity of its people and the influences of
the land itself, which is shaped by ancient forces and turbulent histories. From the Rite
of the Open Hand—a gesture of trust rooted in a tradition of diplomacy—to the
Whispered Promise, which binds strangers with sacred commitments, Ryndor’s
customs help foster bonds of friendship and peace. In times of instability, these shared

rituals become even more important, offering a way to navigate uncertainty together.
Communal practices, such as the Giving Grove, highlight the value Ryndor
places on collective well-being and generosity. The tradition of planting, tending, and
sharing the bounty of these sacred gardens symbolizes a commitment to sustaining
both the land and the community. Likewise, rites of farewell and birth ceremonies
underscore the importance of life cycles in Ryndor's culture—marking transitions,
honoring ancestors, and embracing new beginnings. Each custom, whether it involves
fire, flight, or rooting in the earth, reflects the unique values and identities of
Ryndor’s many races and regions.
As The Weirding continues to spread across the land, distorting the familiar,
some customs are beginning to evolve, while others hold firm against the shifting tides.
Communities find new ways to preserve their traditions, even when strange
phenomena disrupt rituals or alter outcomes. These customs remain essential in
anchoring Ryndorians to what matters most: their connections to one another, their
reverence for life, and their ability to adapt in a world where change is the only
certainty.
The Rite of the Open Hand
In some regions, it is customary for individuals to greet each other by extending
their right hand palm-upward. This is seen as a sign of trust and respect, indicating that
they are not holding any weapons or harmful intentions. Refusing to offer an open hand
is considered a grave insult and could lead to mistrust or even violence. After the Rite is
completed, it is customary for the participants to engage in the Whispered Promise.
The Rite of the Open Hand also serves as a way to foster peaceful relations
between neighboring communities. It is common for representatives from different
towns or villages to participate in the Rite together as a means of strengthening ties and
establishing trade agreements. It is said that in the past, wars and conflicts between
Ryndorian communities were often resolved through the completion of a Rite of the
Open Hand followed by the Whispered Promise, as the act of coming together and
making the sacred pledge of nonviolence was seen as a powerful way to end hostilities
and forge a lasting peace.
The Whispered Promise
In many regions of Ryndor, it is customary to make a whispered promise when
greeting someone for the first time. This promise is usually a commitment to aid the
other person in some way if they ever need help. The act of making the promise is seen
as a way to establish trust and build a bond of friendship between strangers.
Another aspect of the Whispered Promise is that it is meant to be kept secret
between the two individuals who made it. It is not to be shared with anyone else, not
even close friends or family members. Breaking this trust is considered a grave offense
and could result in social ostracism.
In some communities, the Whispered Promise is seen as a spiritual practice, a
way of connecting with the divine through the act of making a commitment to another
person. It is believed that the sincerity and purity of the promise will be rewarded by the

gods, and that those who keep their promises will receive blessings and good fortune in
their lives. As such, the Whispered Promise is not taken lightly, and is considered a
sacred bond between two people.
Giving Grove
Many villages and towns in Ryndor have communal gardens known as Giving
Groves. Members of the community are encouraged to plant and tend to these gardens,
with the understanding that the bounty will be shared with anyone in need. This
practice promotes a sense of community and generosity, and helps to ensure that
everyone has access to fresh produce.
The Giving Grove is a sacred site that is usually protected by the druids of the
area. They believe that the trees in the grove have a spiritual connection to the land and
all living beings. As such, the druids consider it their duty to care for the trees and
ensure their continued health and vitality. They also believe that the grove has healing
properties, and many sick or injured individuals have been brought to the grove to be
healed.
The druids of Ryndor have a tradition of holding ceremonies in their Giving
Groves during the changing of the seasons. These ceremonies involve offerings of food,
flowers, and other gifts to the trees. The druids believe that by making these offerings,
they are strengthening their bond with the trees and showing their gratitude for the
gifts the trees provide. The ceremonies are also seen as a way to renew the energy of the
grove and ensure its continued health and fertility for future generations.
Farewell Vigil
In many regions of Ryndor, it is customary to perform a ritual after the death of a
loved one. This ritual involves creating a small effigy of the deceased out of straw,
wood, or other natural materials. The effigy is then placed on a small raft or boat, and
set adrift in a nearby body of water.
The act of releasing the effigy into the water is seen as a way of symbolically
releasing the spirit of the deceased, allowing them to move on to the afterlife. The
family and friends of the deceased will often gather together to watch the effigy float
away, offering prayers and words of farewell to the departed.
Another common practice after a loved one's death is to create a memorial shrine
in their honor. The shrine may be placed in the family home or in a public space, and
often includes items that were important to the deceased.
New Life
In many regions of Ryndor, the birth of a new child is celebrated with a special
ceremony. This ceremony typically takes place several days after the birth and involves
close family and friends of the new parents. The practices are often different based on
the race of the child and their family.
Hatching
Drakarim When a new Drakarim child is born, the clan elder breathes a fiery
breath onto the child's forehead, marking them with the clan's symbol. The child is

then given a name that represents a virtue that the clan values.
Nesting
Leoporin Upon the birth of a new Leoporin child, the family gathers together and
creates a special piece of clothing for the baby. This garment is embroidered with
symbols that represent the child's ancestry and future potential.
Fledging
Aviari Aviari parents typically perform a ceremonial flight around their nesting
area with their newborn child, introducing them to the spirits of the air and asking for
their protection and guidance.
Rooting
Cervar When a Cervar child is born, the family carves a wooden figurine that
represents the child's spirit animal. This figurine is then placed above the child's crib
and is believed to provide protection and guidance throughout their life.

## Religion

The world of Ryndor is rich in culture and religion. The people of Ryndor have
developed a variety of faiths and traditions, each with their own set of beliefs and
practices. Religion plays a significant role in the daily lives of many individuals,
providing comfort, guidance, and a sense of purpose. In this section, we will explore
some of the primary religions of Ryndor, including their beliefs, practices, and
associated cleric domains.
While there is great diversity in the religions of Ryndor, there is also a strong
sense of tolerance and respect among the people. Religious differences are rarely a
source of conflict, and many festivals and traditions are celebrated across different
faiths. However, there are occasional tensions between different religious groups,
particularly in areas where different faiths compete for influence or resources.
In Ryndor, there are a variety of people and creatures who do not have a formal
religion or belief system. Some of these individuals may be atheists or agnostics who
simply do not believe in the existence of gods or higher powers. Others may have been
raised in a culture or community that does not place a strong emphasis on religion, and
as such they may not have a personal belief system.
There are several organized major religions throughout Ryndor. It is common for
Clerics of these religions to proselytize and evangelize their churches by going on faith
missions or serving in communities in the name of their faith.
The Cult of the New Moon
The Cult of the New Moon venerates the goddess of the night and the moon. They
believe that darkness is a source of power and that the moon's phases represent the
ever-changing nature of existence.
Common prayer: "Embrace the darkness within to unlock the power of the
moon."
Domains: Trickery and Death
The Order of the Iron Sun
The Order of the Iron Sun worships the god of strength, battle, and

craftsmanship. They believe in the power of the forge and the transformative nature of
fire.
Common prayer: "Through the forge of battle, we are tempered and made
strong."
Domains: War and Forge
The Church of the Golden Harvest
The Church of the Golden Harvest venerates the goddess of agriculture, fertility,
and the harvest. They believe in the importance of living in harmony with the natural
world and respecting the cycles of growth and decay.
Common prayer: "Bless the soil and the seeds, may the harvest be bountiful."
Domains: Life and Nature
The Brotherhood of the Shattered Mind
The Brotherhood of the Shattered Mind follows the teachings of a deity of secrets,
knowledge, and madness. They believe in the pursuit of hidden knowledge and
unlocking the mysteries of the universe.
Common prayer: "Unravel the mysteries of the universe and let madness guide
our way."
Domains: Knowledge and Madness
The Order of the Everburning Flame
The Order of the Everburning Flame worships a deity of light, truth, and
protection. They believe that their deity's light illuminates the darkness and that their
protective power shields the innocent from harm.
Common prayer: "May the light guide us through darkness and the flame shield
us from harm."
Domains: Light and Protection
Disciples of the Nether
The Disciples of the Nether believe that the rift to Nebernoria is a gift from the
deity of the underworld, a powerful being who oversees the flow of souls from the
material world to the afterlife.
Common prayer: "Through the Rift we are blessed, in the Nether we find truth."
Domains: Death

## Sports & Games

Sports and Games
Ryndor’s love of competition runs deep, with sports and games serving as
vibrant expressions of the region’s culture, tradition, and unity. From displays of
physical prowess to feats of arcane skill and clever strategy, the people of Ryndor
embrace sport as a way to push their limits, foster camaraderie, and honor their
history. Whether through ancient contests passed down for generations or newer
events shaped by the challenges of the modern era, sporting events bring communities
together, offering both entertainment and meaning in an ever-changing world.
While The Weirding has reshaped many aspects of Ryndor, its influence on the
realm’s official sports remains contested. Weirded objects, creatures, and phenomena

are currently banned from formal competitions, such as the Kigan Uldar and
Utfordring tournaments, as officials debate how to safely incorporate these
unpredictable elements into the rules. Conversations about their inclusion have become
a hot topic among athletes and spectators alike. Some argue that embracing the
Weirding reflects the evolving reality of life in Ryndor, while others warn that its
unpredictable nature could compromise fairness and safety.
For now, competitions remain traditional—focused on skill, strength, and
precision, untainted by the volatile influence of the Weirding. Athletes train hard to
master their craft, whether riding the winds of Eveltoft, taming Wyrmbost’s beasts, or
navigating the hazards of Utfordring’s obstacle courses. These events celebrate not
just the athletes, but the resilience of the communities that gather to cheer them on
and participate in the lively spectacle of sport.
This chapter explores the diverse world of Ryndor’s sports, from ancient
traditions to emerging conversations about change. Whether you're a competitor
preparing to prove your worth, a strategist seeking to master the finer points of the
game, or a fan drawn to the thrill of the contest, Ryndor’s sports offer a testament to
community, dedication, and the joy of friendly rivalry—even as the world shifts under
the influence of The Weirding.
Kigan Uldar
Kigan Uldar is a popular sport in Ryndor that combines elements of magic and
physical prowess. This sport is played on a large open field or arena, where two teams of
four players each compete to score goals by launching a magical orb through a series of
floating rings using only their magical or physical abilities. The orb, which is enchanted
to emit a fiery glow, is fiercely contested by both teams, and players are allowed to use
spells and other magical abilities to try to steal or intercept the orb from their
opponents.
The game is played in a fast-paced, high-energy style, with players constantly on
the move and employing a wide variety of tactics and strategies to gain an advantage
over their opponents. The use of magic adds an exciting and unpredictable element to
the game, as players can create illusions, conjure barriers, and perform other feats of
wizardry to outmaneuver their opponents.
Kigan Uldar is a highly competitive and physically demanding sport, requiring
both speed and agility as well as quick thinking and strategic planning. It is popular
among both wizards and non-magical folk in Ryndor, and has become a staple of many
local festivals and sporting events.
Rules
Kigan Uldar is a team sport played with two teams of four players each. The
objective is to score goals by launching a magical orb through a series of floating rings
using only their magical or physical abilities. The game is played on a large open field or
arena, which is divided into two halves, with each team defending their own half and
attacking the other team's half.
At the start of the game, the orb is placed in the center of the field, and players

from both teams rush forward to try and take possession of it. Players are not allowed to
touch the orb with their hands or any other body part, and must instead use magical or
physical abilities to control it. Non-magic users often use bats, nets, or other tools to
take possession of the orb.
The game is played in two halves, each lasting for 30 minutes, with a 10-minute
break in between. The team with the most goals at the end of the game wins.
Players are allowed to use a wide range of magical and physical abilities to control
the orb and try to score goals. However, there are some rules and limitations to these
abilities. For example, players are not allowed to use any spells or abilities that directly
harm or injure their opponents. Players are also not allowed to fly or levitate more than
three feet off the ground while in possession of the orb.
The game is overseen by a referee, who is responsible for enforcing the rules and
making sure that players are playing safely and fairly.
Skyfire League
The name of the league that plays Kigan Uldar professionally is the Skyfire
League.
Blaze Brigade This team is known for their aggressive playstyle and their ability
to use powerful offensive spells to dominate their opponents.
Frost Giants The Frost Giants are known for their defensive prowess, often using
their magic to create icy barriers to protect their goal.
Thunderbolts This team is known for their lightning-fast speed and quick
reflexes, often scoring goals before their opponents even know what happened.
Shadow Strikers The Shadow Strikers are a mysterious team, often cloaked in
darkness and using illusion spells to confuse their opponents.
Ironclads The Ironclads are a physically imposing team that relies on their brute
strength and toughness to push their way through their opponents' defenses.
Utfordring
Utfordring s a team sport played in the shallow waters near the coast, and is
popular among fishermen and sailors.
In this sport, teams of 6 players compete to collect as many magical pearls as
possible from the bottom of the ocean floor within a set time limit. The pearls are
scattered throughout a designated area and are guarded by a variety of dangerous sea
creatures, both magical and mundane.
Players wear enchanted diving suits that provide them with enhanced mobility
and protection against the dangers of the deep, and they are allowed to use spells and
magical items to fend off any hostile sea creatures they encounter. Each player on the
team has a specific role, such as the diver, the navigator, and the collector, and they
must work together to overcome the obstacles and gather as many pearls as possible.
The team with the most pearls at the end of the game is declared the winner, and
they are awarded a prize that could include anything from magical treasures to a feast
of exotic and fresh seafood. The Reef's Challenge is a thrilling and unpredictable sport
that combines strategy, skill, and bravery, and is a beloved pastime for many coastal

communities in Ryndor.
Rules
Utfordring is a team water sport in which teams of 6 players compete to collect as
many magical pearls as possible from the bottom of the ocean floor within a set time
limit. The game takes place in a designated area of the ocean, which is marked off by
buoys and is typically several acres in size. The pearls are scattered throughout this area
and are guarded by a variety of dangerous sea creatures, both magical and mundane.
Before the game begins, each team selects one player to act as the diver, one
player to act as the navigator, and four players to act as the collectors. The diver is
responsible for swimming to the bottom of the ocean to retrieve the pearls, while the
navigator directs the team from the surface, using a magical compass to locate the
pearls. The collectors work to fend off any hostile sea creatures that may try to attack
the diver and gather any pearls that the diver retrieves.
Each player on the team wears an enchanted diving suit that provides them with
enhanced mobility and protection against the dangers of the deep. They are also allowed
to use spells and magical items to fend off any hostile sea creatures they encounter.
However, players must be careful not to damage the pearls, as any pearls that are
damaged will not count towards the team's final score.
The game typically lasts for one hour, and the team with the most pearls at the
end of the game is declared the winner. In the event of a tie, the team that retrieved the
largest pearl is declared the winner. The winning team is awarded a prize that could
include anything from magical treasures to a feast of fresh seafood.
Utfordring is a thrilling and unpredictable sport that combines strategy, skill, and
bravery. It requires players to work together as a team to overcome the obstacles and
gather as many pearls as possible. It is a beloved pastime for many coastal communities
in Ryndor and is often played as part of local festivals and celebrations.
League of the Deep
The name of the league that plays Utfordring professionally is the League of the
Deep.
Storm Surge Hailing from the northern coast, this team is known for their
fearless approach to the game and their ability to navigate especially treacherous
waters.
Reef Raiders This team is renowned for their exceptional teamwork and
coordination, allowing them to collect pearls quickly and efficiently.
Leviathan's Reach Based in the depths of the ocean, this team is known for their
physical strength and ability to overpower even the toughest of sea creatures.
Ocean's Chosen This team from the western coast of Ryndor is revered for their
magical prowess and their ability to manipulate the tides and sea creatures to their
advantage.
Kraken's Grasp This team from the southern coast is feared for their aggressive
play style and their willingness to take risks to secure the win, often resulting in highscoring games.

Glowstones

Number of Players: 2-6
Game Length: 30-60 minutes
Materials Needed:
1. Glowstones: A set of 36 colored stones in six colors (6 stones per color: red,
blue, green, yellow, white, and black).
2. Glowstone Deck: 54 cards divided into three categories:
- Action Cards: Manipulate stones (e.g., Swap, Steal, Add).
- Event Cards: Introduce random effects (e.g., “Color Surge” or “Reverse Flow”).
- Trap Cards: Played secretly to disrupt opponents’ plans.
3. 6 Dice: One 6-sided die for each color (matching the stones).
4. Player Tokens: One for each player to track individual point totals.
5. Game Board: A grid with six slots for stones (one slot for each color) and a
score tracker.
6. Betting Tokens (Optional): For tavern or gambling variants, where players bet
on outcomes.
--Setup
1. Distribute Glowstones: Place all 36 glowstones in a draw bag or bowl.
2. Deal Starting Hands: Each player draws 5 cards from the Glowstone Deck.
3. Prepare the Board: Lay out the game board with six empty color slots (one for
each color).
4. Turn Order: Players roll their dice. The highest roller goes first, with play
proceeding clockwise.
--How to Play
Each game of Glowstones consists of rounds. During each round, players take
turns performing actions to manipulate the stones on the board. The goal is to match
colors or manipulate the board to achieve specific point thresholds. Points are scored
by completing color sets (three or more matching stones in a row) or achieving a highvalue combination.
--Turn Structure
On a player's turn, they perform the following steps:
1. Draw a Glowstone: Draw a random stone from the bag and place it on the
appropriate slot on the board (e.g., a red stone goes to the red slot). If the slot is already
full (with 3 stones), place it on any other open slot.
2. Play a Card: The player can choose to play one card from their hand.
- Action Cards: Modify the stones on the board (swap, steal, or add stones).
- Trap Cards: Played face-down and triggered later to disrupt another player’s
turn.
- Event Cards: Introduce random effects that affect all players (e.g., shuffle the
stones, reverse turn order).

3. Optional Action - Roll the Glowstone Dice: Players may roll a die matching
the stone color they just placed.
- If they roll a 6, they earn bonus points for that color.
- If they roll a 1, the stone becomes unstable, and they must remove a stone of
the same color from the board.
4. Bluff or Pass: Players may choose to bluff, pretending to have powerful cards
or high-scoring strategies, or pass to avoid suspicion. Bluffing is crucial because some
cards can only be played if another player challenges them.
--Scoring Points
Points are awarded at the end of each round based on the glowstones placed on
the board.
- 3 stones of the same color in a row: 5 points
- 4 stones of the same color in a row: 8 points
- A set of all 6 colors: 12 points
- Bonus points: Earned by rolling a 6 on the Glowstone Dice during a turn (+3
points)
At the end of each round, the stones are reset, and a new round begins.
--Winning the Game
The game continues until one player reaches 25 points or until all the stones have
been used. The player with the most points at the end of the game wins. If there is a tie,
the tied players each draw one glowstone from the bag, and the player with the
highest-value stone (based on color rarity) wins.
--The Weirded Variant (Optional)
In the underground version of Glowstones, Weirded glowstones are used. These
stones shift colors mid-game, making them unpredictable and creating additional
challenges.
Special Rules for Weirded Glowstones:
- At the start of each player's turn, roll a Weird Die (a d6).
- 1-2: A random glowstone on the board changes color.
- 3-4: The current player must discard a card from their hand.
- 5-6: Nothing happens—play continues normally.
While the Weirded version adds chaos and excitement, it also increases the
difficulty—leading to higher stakes and more dramatic comebacks. Official Glowstone
tournaments ban this variant, but it thrives in taverns and underground circles where
unpredictability is part of the fun.
Example Cards
1. Swap Stones – Swap any two stones on the board.
2. Color Surge – Add a second stone of the same color you just placed.
3. Trap: Shattered Bond – The next player loses their turn.
4. Event: Reverse Flow – Reverse the turn order until the end of the round.

5. Sneak Steal – Secretly take one stone from the board and hold it for yourself.
Game Variants
- High Stakes Variant: Players use betting tokens to wager on the outcome of
each round.
- Timed Play: Each player has only 30 seconds per turn to act, increasing
tension.
- Cooperative Variant: Players work together to achieve the highest score against
a shared deck of random events.

## Fashion

High Fashion of Eveltoft
Eveltoft, as the heart of Ryndor's politics, trade, and magic, is a city of opulence
and expression, where fashion is both a statement of status and an art form.
Incorporating pragmatism and layered design, combined with textile elegance and
symbolic ornamentation, the high fashion of Eveltoft is as diverse as its inhabitants,
with each race contributing unique elements to the city's sartorial identity. Nobles,
merchants, and scholars alike use their attire to showcase wealth, lineage, and
personal achievement.
Humans
Elegance through Practicality
Humans in Eveltoft blend utilitarian cuts with ornate embellishments,
showcasing their adaptability and influence across Ryndor.
- Silk-Lined Wool Cloaks: High-status humans wear woolen cloaks lined with
silk, secured with jade or obsidian brooches. Patterns on the cloaks are embroidered to
represent family crests and achievements.
- Layered Robes with Fur Trims: Their formal attire consists of layered robes
over high-collared tunics, with subtle hints of wolf or bear fur at the cuffs and collars.
This combination offers both warmth and sophistication.
- Statement Sashes and Belts: Wide silk sashes are tied over the tunics,
embroidered with personal mottos or ancestral stories. They are often paired with
leather belts adorned with intricate knotwork buckles.
- Jewelry with Function: Humans favor bracelets and rings crafted from bronze
and iron, with embedded runes for protection. Practicality is key—many accessories
have hidden pouches for small items or vials of herbs.
- Structured Caps and Face coverings: In the colder and windier areas of Ryndor,
it is very common to see tall, fur lined caps structured and boxy, with silky face
coverings attached with buttons or straps.
Elves – Ethereal Simplicity with Symbolic Depth
The elves of Eveltoft express their connection to magic and nature through
flowing fabrics and symbolic motifs. Their fashion is graceful and minimalist, but
laden with meaning.

- Flowing Silk Tunics and Sleeveless Robes: Their clothing features layered silk
garments, dyed in soft greens, golds, and blues to mimic natural elements like water,
wind, and sunlight.
- Embroidered Mythological Creatures: Elven garments are embroidered with
delicate, swirling designs of dragons, birds, and flowers that are said to offer
protection and good fortune.
- Feathered and Beaded Hair Adornments: Elves incorporate feathers, beads,
and fine silver chains into their hairstyles, often braiding them into long locks or
wearing them as delicate headpieces.
- Barefoot with Ornamentation: Many elves go barefoot, using anklets and toe
rings adorned with jade or obsidian, signifying their connection to the land and sky.
Dwarves – Precision and Craftsmanship
The dwarves of Eveltoft take great pride in their metalworking and
craftsmanship, and their clothing reflects their mastery over materials.
- Lamellar Vests and Metal-Stitched Cloaks: High-fashion dwarves wear
lamellar vests made of overlapping metal plates, polished to reflect the light. Their
cloaks are often stitched with thin metal threads or adorned with small medallions.
- Earth-Tone Tunics and Trousers: Dwarves prefer practical clothing in muted
earth tones—browns, grays, and deep reds—accented by decorative belts and cuffs.
Their garments are durable but elegant, reflecting their connection to the earth.
- Heavy Jewelry and Beard Beads: Dwarves love heavy jewelry—thick necklaces,
ornate rings, and intricately carved beard beads that show off their lineage. Gold,
silver, and obsidian are favored materials.
- Boots with Runic Soles: Sturdy boots feature runes engraved on the soles for
protection and good fortune. These boots are both practical for underground travel and
stylish for formal events.
