Sev’rinn – Elemental Expression
The Sev’rinn use their fashion to reflect their magical affinities and personal
connection to elemental forces. Their attire shifts based on which element they most
embody—fire, water, air, or earth.
- Color-Shifted Fabrics: Their clothing uses enchanted fabrics that change
colors in response to environmental changes. A water-aligned Sev’rinn’s robes might
shift from deep blue to shimmering silver in the rain.
- Flowing Outerwear: Sev’rinn favor loose, billowing garments, such as robes
and capes, that respond to the wind, mimicking the natural flow of elements around
them.
- Masks and Veils: Many Sev’rinn wear decorative masks or veils, symbolizing
their connection to unseen forces. These are often adorned with crystals or gemstones,
channeling magical energy.
- Bare Feet or Soft-Soled Sandals: Earth-aligned Sev’rinn often go barefoot,
while others wear soft-soled sandals with elemental patterns engraved on the straps.

## Cervar – Nature-Woven Garments

The Cervar, a race connected to nature, weave their clothing directly from plants,
moss, and vines, incorporating living elements into their outfits.
- Living Cloaks and Tunics: Their garments are partially alive, with flowering
plants or glowing fungi woven into their sleeves. These materials symbolize growth and
renewal.
- Vine-Wrapped Jewelry: Cervar wear bracelets, anklets, and chokers made
from vines and roots, decorated with small leaves or blossoms.
- Natural Color Palette: Their clothing reflects seasonal colors—greens and
browns in spring, fiery reds and oranges in autumn.
- Symbolic Antlers and Crowns: High-status Cervar wear wooden antler
crowns, decorated with feathers and stones, marking their connection to nature’s
wisdom.
Aviari – Ornate Layers and Flight-Inspired Designs
The Aviari, with their feathered features and winged heritage, design their
clothing to enhance movement and reflect their connection to the sky.
- Feathered Epaulettes and Capes: Their garments feature epaulettes and capes
lined with feathers, creating an ethereal, flowing effect.
- Lightweight Silk and Leather: Aviari prefer lightweight materials, combining
leather vests with silk undershirts to allow for mobility.
- Gliding Sleeves: Some Aviari garments feature wide, gliding sleeves that catch
the wind as they move, mimicking wings.
- Intricate Wing Designs on Jewelry: Their rings and necklaces often depict
winged motifs, symbolizing freedom and exploration.
Leoporin – Playful Patterns and Practicality
The Leoporin, a rabbit-like race, balance comfort and charm in their fashion,
favoring layered tunics and short capes for agility.
- Bright Colors and Playful Patterns: Leoporin garments feature vibrant
patterns, such as polka dots or geometric designs, reflecting their playful nature.
- Layered Scarves and Sashes: Many Leoporin wear layered scarves wrapped
around their necks, secured with decorative pins.
- Soft Leather Boots: Their boots are designed for quiet movement, made from
soft leather with padded soles.
- Earrings and Charms: Leoporin love small charms and trinkets worn as
earrings or attached to their belts, symbolizing personal milestones or lucky items. It is
common to see Leoporin with cities with heavily adorned ears, encrusted with charms
and jewels.
Fashion and Status in Eveltoft
Fashion in Eveltoft is not merely about aesthetics—it reflects personal
achievement, social status, and magical alignment. The city’s citizens use clothing to
signal alliances, rank, and ambition, with nobles and scholars wearing inscribed

sashes or symbolic accessories that declare their status and affiliations. Special
seasonal festivals require elaborate ceremonial outfits, and citizens are judged by the
richness of the fabrics and the intricacy of the details in their attire.
Through this blend of Norse resilience and Chinese elegance, the people of
Eveltoft express their identity and pride. Every thread, gemstone, and accessory tells a
story—a story woven into the intricate tapestry that is the culture of Eveltoft.

## Balance of Forces

In Ryndor, the forces of magic, religion, and technology are intertwined in a
complex and ever-changing struggle for dominance. Primordial Resonance, the source
of all magic, offers power to those who can wield it—yet it is finite, forcing careful
management. Religion provides divine power through belief, but its influence depends
on the conviction of the faithful. Technology, born from ingenuity, serves as an
equalizer, blending magic and science to empower even the mundane. The balance
between these forces is never static, with shifts in power shaping the fate of nations and
individuals alike.
Magic
Magic in Ryndor is a finite resource, drawn from Primordial Resonance, a
volatile energy that exists in the friction between the material world and the astral
plane. The energy is not endless—each spell or magical act consumes resonance,
creating scarcity over time. Overuse of magic in one area can lead to a resonance
drought, leaving practitioners powerless until the flow naturally returns. Players must
learn to manage resources wisely, as their actions have lasting effects on the magical
ecosystem.
Casting magic influences the environment in subtle and dramatic ways. When
resonance is disturbed, it can result in astral storms, magical anomalies, or dead zones
where magic becomes unreliable or ceases to function entirely. Some areas may
experience wild surges of energy, empowering spells beyond expectation, while others
may drain a mage’s power without warning. Players need to understand that their spells
are not without consequence—reckless casting risks destabilizing the world itself.
| d10 | Effect |
|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1 | Astral Storm. Arcane winds whip through the area, causing unpredictable
spell effects. |
| 2 | Resonance Drought. Magic becomes inert, rendering spells impossible to
cast for hours or days. |
| 3 | Arcane Wildfire. Flames fueled by magic spread uncontrollably, consuming
both magical and mundane materials. |
| 4 | Temporal Slip. Time flows inconsistently—hours pass in moments, or
minutes stretch for days. |
| 5 | Planar Bleed. Creatures or objects from the astral plane temporarily manifest
in the world. |

| 6 | Nullification Pulse. A sudden anti-magic wave depletes spellcasters of all
magical energy. |
| 7 | Magical Mutation. Local flora or fauna transform into strange, enchanted
forms. |
| 8 | Resonance Surge. Spells cast in the area become more powerful but unstable,
with unintended side effects. |
| 9 | Reality Fracture. Small objects float or disassemble, defying physics.|
| 10 | Haunting Echoes. Faint whispers or apparitions appear, remnants of magic
long past.|
The Rift to Nebernoria introduces further complexity, acting as both a boon and a
curse for magic users. In proximity to the Rift, magic becomes stronger but more
volatile—simple spells may yield extraordinary results, or fizzle unexpectedly.
Practitioners venturing too close to the Rift risk exposure to astral influences, which
could alter their abilities or leave them vulnerable to planar corruption. Navigating
these unpredictable energies requires careful planning, especially in areas saturated
with astral resonance.
Finally, magic in Ryndor plays a pivotal role in culture and politics, influencing
alliances, trade, and governance. Factions like the Crystal Scholars seek to control and
understand resonance, while remnants of the Ullac Regime trade in forbidden antimagic technologies to suppress magical power. Some societies treat magic as sacred,
woven into religious practices, while others fear its instability. Players will encounter
both reverence and hostility toward magic, with their characters’ decisions shaping
how the world responds to their power.
Sev'rinns
The Sev’rinns are powerful practitioners who draw their magic from Primordial
Resonance, each bound to a unique Essence ignited during a personal event known as
The Spark. Once rulers of Ryndor, Sev’rinns now play diverse roles—from healers and
scholars to adventurers and revolutionaries. Their presence evokes both reverence and
fear among ordinary citizens, embodying the unpredictable nature of magic. This
section delves into their traditions, history, and evolving place in modern society, as
well as the potential challenges—and opportunities—they bring to those they
encounter.
Traditions
The Sev’rinns are deeply woven into the history and culture of Ryndor, with
traditions that reflect their role as both guardians and practitioners of magic. Central
to their heritage is the Hilderturgy, an ancient rite by which elder Sev’rinns passed their
knowledge and elemental mastery to the next generation. Though the tradition waned
with the rise of the Ullac Regime, it is now being revived on the floating island of
Holmea, where the Skola—a new academy for Sev’rinns—trains initiates in their
elemental Essences.
At the heart of each Sev’rinn’s journey lies The Spark, a pivotal moment in
childhood when exposure to a specific element ignites their magical potential. This

experience determines their primary Essence—whether fire, water, air, or spirit—and
shapes their abilities throughout life. This moment is celebrated as a sacred event
among the Sev’rinns, marking not just the start of their training, but their alignment
with the forces of creation and destruction.
Sev’rinns hold a variety of roles in society, from advisors and healers to
combatants and ritualists. They are both revered and feared for their power, sought
after by noble houses and factions, yet often distrusted for the instability that
accompanies magic. Some Sev’rinns use their abilities for diplomacy and protection,
while others become mercenaries or hermits, following their own path. This duality
reflects the essence of magic itself: neither good nor evil, but shaped by the heart of the
one who wields it.
In Society
For an average citizen of Ryndor, encountering a Sev’rinn can evoke a mix of
awe, reverence, and unease. Sev’rinns carry the weight of ancient magic, and their
presence suggests both potential power and danger. While some Sev’rinns serve as
healers, advisors, or protectors, others walk more mysterious paths, disconnected
from societal norms. Many citizens respect or fear their abilities, knowing the volatility
of Primordial Resonance. Interactions often depend on the Sev’rinn’s personal
demeanor—ranging from inspiring guidance to unsettling reminders of the fragility of
magic.
Sev’rinns in Modern Ryndor
| Name | Essence | Role in Society | Notable Contribution or Influence |
|--------------------|-----------------------|---------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
| Dara Valesh | Muza (Water) | Diplomat and Negotiator | Brokered peace treaties
between coastal factions |
| Kaelen Drust | Huon (Fire) | Renowned Blacksmith | Crafts magical weapons for
noble houses |
| Liora Fen | Sorash (Sky) | Airship Captain and Explorer | Leads expeditions
through Rift anomalies |
| Jasrik Rune | Atmani (Spirit) | Spiritual Leader of the Keepers of the Rift |
Guides rituals to safeguard the Rift |
| Eryn Thalor | Ishin (Stone) | Architect of Ban Mynydd | Designs structures to
contain magical surges |
| Tala Mierin | Ziran (Nature) | Environmental Activist | Protects magical
creatures from exploitation |
| Vesra Kaid | Kala (Time) | Historian and Archivist | Preserves ancient
knowledge from the Sev’rinn archives |
| Oryn Velas | Muza-Sorash (Water/Sky) | Pirate Lord | Controls trade routes
through air and sea |

| Saren Jorath | Keiton (Space) | Astral Researcher | Studies the Rift’s
dimensional effects |
| Rhael Vinn | Atmani (Spirit) | Wandering Healer | Offers aid to outlying
settlements without allegiance |
Religion
The world of Ryndor is rich in culture and religion. The people of Ryndor have
developed a variety of faiths and traditions, each with their own set of beliefs and
practices. Religion plays a significant role in the daily lives of many individuals,
providing comfort, guidance, and a sense of purpose. In this section, we will explore
some of the primary religions of Ryndor, including their beliefs, practices, and
associated cleric domains.
While there is great diversity in the religions of Ryndor, there is also a strong
sense of tolerance and respect among the people. Religious differences are rarely a
source of conflict, and many festivals and traditions are celebrated across different
faiths. However, there are occasional tensions between different religious groups,
particularly in areas where different faiths compete for influence or resources.
In Ryndor, there are a variety of people and creatures who do not have a formal
religion or belief system. Some of these individuals may be atheists or agnostics who
simply do not believe in the existence of gods or higher powers. Others may have been
raised in a culture or community that does not place a strong emphasis on religion, and
as such they may not have a personal belief system.
There are several organized major religions throughout Ryndor. It is common for
Clerics of these religions to proselytize and evangelize their churches by going on faith
missions or serving in communities in the name of their faith.
The Cult of the New Moon
The Cult of the New Moon venerates the goddess of the night and the moon. They
believe that darkness is a source of power and that the moon's phases represent the
ever-changing nature of existence.
"Embrace the darkness within to unlock the power of the moon."
Domains: Trickery and Death
The Order of the Iron Sun
The Order of the Iron Sun worships the god of strength, battle, and
craftsmanship. They believe in the power of the forge and the transformative nature of
fire.
"Through the forge of battle, we are tempered and made strong."
Domains: War and Forge
The Church of the Golden Harvest
The Church of the Golden Harvest venerates the goddess of agriculture, fertility,
and the harvest. They believe in the importance of living in harmony with the natural
world and respecting the cycles of growth and decay.
"Bless the soil and the seeds, may the harvest be bountiful."

## Domains: Life and Nature

The Brotherhood of the Shattered Mind
The Brotherhood of the Shattered Mind follows the teachings of a deity of secrets,
knowledge, and madness. They believe in the pursuit of hidden knowledge and
unlocking the mysteries of the universe.
"Unravel the mysteries of the universe and let madness guide our way."
Domains: Knowledge and Madness
The Order of the Everburning Flame
The Order of the Everburning Flame worships a deity of light, truth, and
protection. They believe that their deity's light illuminates the darkness and that their
protective power shields the innocent from harm.
"May the light guide us through darkness and the flame shield us from harm."
Domains: Light and Protection
Disciples of the Nether
The Disciples of the Nether believe that the rift to Nebernoria is a gift from the
deity of the underworld, a powerful being who oversees the flow of souls from the
material world to the afterlife.
"Through the Rift we are blessed, in the Nether we find truth."
Domains: Death
Astrology
In Ryndor, Nebernorian astrology has resurfaced as a blend of numerology and
celestial magic, drawing from ancient astral practices. Rooted in the alignment of
cosmic forces, this discipline interprets patterns in stars, planets, and numbers as
reflections of fate and potential. Practitioners believe that celestial configurations
influence both personal events and grand societal shifts, providing insight into the ebb
and flow of power. Numbers and constellations are used to divine the future, guide
important decisions, and harness astral resonance for subtle magical influence.
Though traces of Nebernorian astrology have woven their way into Ryndorian
society as numerology and star charts, few outside of Nebernoria fully grasp its true
mechanics—or whether it meaningfully interacts with the other energies of Ryndor,
such as Primordial Resonance. To most Ryndorians, this practice remains a mystery
cloaked in celestial symbolism, believed to influence personal fate or divine cosmic
patterns. Scholars and mystics attempt to interpret these astral arts, but only the
Nebernorians understand their deeper purpose—if there is one at all.
Technology
In Ryndor, technology stands as a powerful equalizer, harnessing magic, science,
and even religious energy to reshape society. Once driven by the Ullac Regime,
technological advancement now operates in a delicate balance with magic, giving rise to
arc-weapons, automaton sentinels, and airships. Despite the regime’s collapse,
nullification engines—devices that suppress magic—continue to circulate through

black markets, allowing non-magical factions to wield power.
The fusion of technology and magic has unlocked vast potential, but not without
consequences. Industrial centers like Ban Mynydd thrive on smelting and production,
while innovations in Holmea blend magic with mechanical precision. However, the rise
of arcane-powered machines has strained both environmental and magical resources,
leading to concerns about sustainability.
In this new age, factions like the Crystal Scholars seek to balance progress with
preservation, while former regime loyalists exploit technology for control. As airships
roam the skies and automata patrol city streets, the people of Ryndor walk a fine line
between prosperity and collapse, knowing that technology, like magic, is only as good
—or dangerous—as those who wield it.
Major Technologies of Ryndor
Modern Ryndor showcases the blending of magic and science, giving rise to
powerful technologies that reshape society:
- Arc-Weapons: Blades and firearms imbued with magic, enhancing both combat
prowess and precision.
- Airships: Massive vessels powered by arcane currents and engines, essential for
trade, exploration, and warfare.
- Automaton Sentinels: Clockwork constructs used to patrol cities and enforce
security.
- Astral Scanners: Devices employed by Crystal Scholars to monitor resonance
surges and astral anomalies.
- Modular Prosthetics: Advanced limbs with magical enhancements, offering
strength and precision to those in need.
These innovations reflect the evolving interplay between magic and technology,
expanding possibilities while demanding careful balance and control. You can find more
specific technologies and devices in the Reliquary appendix.
The Underground Market
Although the Ullac Regime has fallen, its technological legacy lives on in the
shadows. The remnants of military inventions, arc-weapons, automaton blueprints,
and experimental devices are now traded through black markets. These illicit hubs are
particularly active in cities like Eveltoft and Ban Mynydd, where factions and
individuals seek to reclaim or repurpose old technologies for personal gain. The Crystal
Scholars monitor these trades closely, wary of dangerous devices resurfacing. However,
controlling the flow of this technology is nearly impossible, as smugglers and rogue
inventors constantly adapt.

# The Weirded Lands

In this chapter, we journey through Ryndor’s diverse lands, each shaped not only
by its history and culture but also by the unpredictable effects of The Weirding. While
bustling cities and remote villages still thrive, many have been transformed by strange
phenomena—time fractures trap towns in endless days, rivers shift course without
reason, and some communities have become isolated within Weird Zones, lost to the
flow of normal reality.
As you travel through Ryndor, you’ll encounter mutated creatures, warped
landscapes, and altered customs—reminders that the familiar world is slipping into
something far more surreal. Villages adapt to the flow of Primordial Resonance as they
navigate warped seasons and unexpected changes in magic. This guide offers insight
into the customs and survival strategies of each settlement, highlighting how
communities thrive, struggle, or fall apart in this new era. Whether you seek
adventure, trade, or knowledge, these Weird Lands hold both wonders and dangers in
equal measure.

## Abbernusker Lake

Abernnusker Lake
Weird waters below the Dragon Mount
At the base of Mt. Bannockwyrm, where shadow and mist coil around jagged
cliffs, lies the mysterious Abernnusker Lake—a body of water now irrevocably altered
by the Weirding. Meaning "Obsidian Peak" in the ancient tongue, Abernnusker was
once rumored to be the birthplace of the legendary dragon Fafnir, who guards a vast
treasure hoard hidden deep within the mountain. But since the spread of the Weirding,
the lake has taken on a sinister life of its own, warping both reality and legend into
something new and unpredictable.
Waters Twisted by the Weirding
The lake’s frigid, black waters have become a wellspring of strange phenomena,
as though they no longer reflect only the material world but bleed into Nebernoria’s
astral depths. Strange lights drift beneath the surface, flickering like stars submerged
in the abyss. Fishermen swear they see shimmering cities in the water, impossibly
distant landscapes whose structures shift and dissolve when approached. Those who
stare too long into the lake report vivid, dream-like visions—fragments of other lives
or alternate realities that linger long after they leave the shore.
Currents beneath the lake seem to flow out of sync with time, dragging objects
—and even people—into strange eddies where hours or years can pass in an instant.
Some say that fish pulled from the depths are marked with glowing runes or speak in
alien tongues before they expire, further deepening the lake’s mystery. Locals avoid the
waters entirely now, warning that those who swim too close to the lake’s center risk
becoming lost between worlds, vanishing without a trace.
New Monsters in the Deep

The creatures that haunt Abernnusker's depths have also changed since the
Weirding began. Local legends still tell of a giant obsidian-scaled serpent that prowls
the cold waters, but now some claim the beast can split into multiple forms, existing in
several places at once. Malevolent water spirits known as nixes have grown more
aggressive, no longer content to simply drag swimmers to their doom. Witnesses
describe the nixes as distorted figures, with faces that flicker between multiple forms—
often resembling loved ones or long-lost travelers.
Even stranger things have been spotted beneath the lake: enormous, translucent
creatures that seem half-formed, as though caught between two realms. Some believe
these are astral constructs from Nebernoria, pulled through a rift at the bottom of the
lake. Bioluminescent flora, glowing in shifting hues of violet and green, drift across the
surface at night, and strange birdlike creatures circle the water’s edge, croaking
ominous songs in alien tones.

### DM Tools — Abbernusker Lake

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | Strange lights rise and arrange into a constellation map of an unknown sky. DC 13 Arcana: advantage on next Arcana/History roll; failure: disadvantage on Perception for 24 hours. |
| 3–4 | A fish surfaces, speaks one sentence in an unrecognised language, then dies and dissolves. DC 13 Arcana: understood as a warning, a name, or a location — DM's choice. |
| 5–6 | A temporal eddy opens at the water's edge. The party loses 1d4 hours with no memory. Equipment is subtly displaced. One random character has inexplicably wet feet. |
| 7–8 | A shimmering city rises beneath the surface. Touching the water dissolves it instantly. Passive Perception 14+: the figures inside were looking up at the party. |
| 9–10 | A nix surfaces wearing the face of someone one party member has lost. It whispers something only that character could know, then submerges. DC 13 WIS or stunned until end of next turn. |
| 11–12 | The party's reflections move independently, mimicking future actions, then point in the same direction and fade. The direction leads to a landmark, a threat, or a lie — DM's choice. |
| 13–14 | A translucent, half-formed creature surfaces and follows for 2d4 hours. If spoken to, it whispers one word in Common. If attacked, it shatters into mist. |
| 15–16 | The shore water crystallises. DC 10 STR (action) to pull out one Weirded Object before it returns to liquid. |
| 17–18 | One character is suddenly elsewhere on the shore. At their original position: a perfect ice sculpture of themselves, melting. It dissolves in 10 minutes. |
| 19–20 | The obsidian serpent surfaces and studies the party for 1d4 rounds. Holding eye contact for the full duration grants a vision: the lake's past, the character's future, or a glimpse into Nebernoria. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Fisherman's Wife.** A nix has assumed the identity of a fisherman's missing spouse. He hires the party to find his wife's body — but the nix has begun to genuinely believe it is who it pretends to be.
- **The Scholar by the Shore.** A cartographer from Eveltoft has camped here for three weeks mapping the lights. She repeats sentences from hours ago without noticing; her left hand has aged faster than her right. She is very close to finding the pattern.
- **The Voluntary Drowning.** For nine days running, a different person has walked calmly into the lake and not returned. No bodies surface. Whatever is calling them is growing bolder.
- **The Returned Ship.** A vessel that departed three months ago has drifted back. The crew insists they left this morning. Their cargo is addressed to a merchant who died eight weeks ago. One crew member has a journal entry dated in the future.

#### Travel Options

- 🚣 **By Boat (shore only).** Local boatmen charge double and refuse to cross the center. Temporal eddies make open water unpredictable.
- 🥾 **By Foot.** Shore road from Wenport — 2 days. Reliable but exposed to weather off Mt. Bannockwyrm.
- 🏔️ **From Mt. Bannockwyrm.** Steep descent from the southern face — 4 hours. DC 13 Athletics to navigate the scree fields.
- 🦅 **By Air.** Aviari and griffins from Eveltoft — 1 full day. Landing on the shore is safe; on the water is not.
- ⚠️ **Crossing by Water.** No reliable method. Two vessels lost to temporal eddies in the past year.

#### Landmarks

- **Nenusk Water Gardens** — *1 day · 200 XP.* A swampy field of shallow pools, dense with insects that feed on the rare nenusk flower. The blossoms open only at dusk. Located southwest between Abbernusker and the Ardal Plains.
- **The Drowned Dock** — *30 min · 50 XP.* The collapsed remains of the original fishing pier. Planks glow at night. Strange objects surface regularly — personal effects belonging to people no one in the village recognises.
- **The Black Shore** — *2 hours · 100 XP.* A crescent of obsidian sand on the lake's eastern edge, cold regardless of season. The serpent surfaces here most frequently. Compasses behave erratically within 60 feet.
- **Fafnir's Cradle** — *4 hours · 150 XP.* A low cave accessible at low water, where legend holds Fafnir was hatched. The air smells of ozone and old scales. The claw marks on the walls are too large for anything currently living.
- **The Reflection Pool** — *1 hour · 75 XP.* A still inlet separated from the main lake by an obsidian shelf. Reflections show the viewer as they were, or as they might be. Objects retrieved after submersion here are subtly changed.

## Ardal Plains

Ardal Plains
The Sacred Grasslands
The Ardal Plains, stretching between Wyrmbost and Leighmore, are a land
steeped in legend and magic, though its beauty hides the harshness of life beneath the
open skies. According to ancient lore, the Fen elves once called these plains home,
treating them as a sacred sanctuary for the natural world. The Fen were believed to be
guardians of nature, and travelers passing through Ardal would leave offerings in hopes
of receiving their protection and blessings. Even now, some visitors still honor this
tradition, placing tokens beneath ancient standing stones or whispering thanks into the
wind.
Abernnusker Lake, the heart of the Ardal Plains, carries its own mythology.
Legend says it was formed by the tears of a Fen princess, forbidden from marrying her
true love. The lake’s waters are said to possess powerful healing properties, drawing
pilgrims from across Ryndor who seek renewal and blessings. Though no Fen have been
seen for centuries, the mystical reputation of the lake endures. Locals say that during
quiet moments, the surface reflects not the sky, but glimpses of other realms, hinting
that perhaps the Fen's influence lingers.
A Land of Beauty and Tragedy
Despite its tranquil appearance, the Ardal Plains are not untouched by conflict.
During the Torgarian War, the plains witnessed brutal battles between rival clans,
leaving the land scarred with memories of violence. It is said that the ghosts of fallen
warriors still wander the plains, whispering on the wind, watching the living with
unseen eyes. Even today, travelers speak of a chill unease in certain areas, as if the past
clings to the landscape like a shadow. Some who camp on the plains report hearing
voices, faint and distant, carried by the ever-present wind.
Life on the Ardal Plains
The Ardal Plains are sparsely populated, their windswept grasslands and jagged
rocks making life here a challenge. Those who do call the plains home are rugged and

self-reliant, living off the land and weathering the harsh seasons with quiet resilience.
Hunting, herding, and farming sustain most communities, and the rhythms of life are
dictated by the changing seasons. In winter, the land becomes unforgiving—**icy
winds cut across the grasslands**, and families hunker down in their homes, surviving
off stockpiled provisions. Despite these hardships, the people of Ardal are deeply
connected to their land and proud of their heritage, wearing their scars as marks of
honor.
The Annual Kigan Uldar Crown
The Annual Kigan Uldar Crown is one of the most celebrated sporting events in
Ryndor, and the Ardal Plains are the perfect backdrop for this prestigious tournament.
Taking place over three intense days, the championship draws the best teams from
across the land to compete for the coveted title.
Though the Weirding has begun to affect other parts of Ryndor, official Kigan
Uldar competitions on Ardal remain untouched—for now. Discussions about allowing
Weirded artifacts or mutated creatures into future games stir controversy, but the Ardal
Plains offer an unspoiled stage for tradition to thrive. Teams engage in fast-paced
competitions of strength, strategy, and endurance, drawing crowds of fans who set up
makeshift camps across the plains to witness the spectacle. For three days, the plains
come alive with celebration, competition, and camaraderie, making the Kigan Uldar
Crown an event that unites Ryndor in a rare moment of joy.
The Ardal Plains serve as both a reminder of Ryndor’s turbulent past and a
celebration of its resilient spirit. From the mystical waters of Abernnusker Lake to the
fierce competitions of Kigan Uldar, the land weaves together stories of hope, sorrow,
and strength—a place where the echoes of the past shape the possibilities of the future.

### DM Tools — Ardal Plains

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | A standing stone is draped with fresh offerings though no one is visible for miles. DC 13 Perception: footprints lead to the stone, none lead away. |
| 3–4 | A voice on the wind speaks one party member's name clearly and close. It does not repeat. DC 12 WIS save or disadvantage on their next Charisma check. |
| 5–6 | The central lake pulses. DC 12 CON save when drinking from it — success: regain 2d6 HP; failure: lose 1d6 HP as the healing reverses. |
| 7–8 | Spectral warriors rise from the earth and march. Each walks 100 feet before sinking back into the grass. Several more appear in the distance, all moving toward the same point. |
| 9–10 | Pristine Kigan Uldar equipment materialises on the grass. If kept, the carrier gains +1 to Athletics checks but dreams each night of a tournament they never entered. |
| 11–12 | The wind dies for 30 seconds. Every party member hears the same whispered phrase in the silence — each in a different language, each slightly different. It is incomplete. |
| 13–14 | Grass in a 10-foot radius around one character grows to waist height in seconds, then stills. DC 14 Nature: a Fen elf blessing-reflex — the land has recognised something about that character. |
| 15–16 | A Torgarian War relic surfaces from the soil. DC 15 Arcana: the object carries a fragment of its owner's last memory, flooding into the examiner's mind as a brief vision. |
| 17–18 | A fragment of the Torgarian War plays out in translucent overlay around the party for 1 minute. They are invisible to the apparitions. When it ends, one character stands on the exact spot a soldier died. |
| 19–20 | The healing lake pulses hard. Every creature within 30 feet regains HP equal to their proficiency bonus, then immediately loses the same amount as the reversal follows. Net: zero. Wounds look healed for 10 minutes before reopening. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Ghost's Unfinished Business.** A Torgarian War soldier's ghost has been approaching travelers for weeks, repeating the same phrase. The party learns the ghost was a courier whose message was never delivered. The recipient's family lives in Wyrmbost — and the message will reopen wounds the town spent decades sealing.
- **Sabotage at the Crown.** The Annual Kigan Uldar Crown is three days away. A team hires the party to investigate equipment tampering — opponents' mallets produce erratic Weirding effects mid-game. Finding the smuggled artifact before the opening match is preferable. Finding it during play is not.
- **The Volatile Lake.** A shore village has relied on the healing lake for generations. Since the Weirding, results are unpredictable. A healer believes they've found a reliable window and needs the party to hold off desperate travelers who keep arriving at the wrong hours.
- **The Stone Has Moved.** A lone Fen elf has returned to reclaim a sealed offering jar left at a specific standing stone during the early Weirding. The problem: the stone was here. It is not anymore.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **By Foot.** Main road between Wyrmbost and Leighmore — 3 days on open, flat terrain.
- 🐎 **By Horse.** Wyrmbost to Leighmore — 1 day steady, half a day pushed hard.
- 🚣 **By River.** A seasonal river along the western edge. Viable in spring and early summer; dry by late autumn.
- 🦅 **By Air.** Open skies. Eveltoft to the plains — half a day.
- ⚠️ **Lake Crossing.** Crossable by small boat, but two vessels have arrived at the wrong shore.

#### Landmarks

- **The Princess's Tear** — *30 min · 50 XP.* The central lake, formed from the grief of a Fen princess. 1 hour at the water in quiet reflection allows a DC 14 WIS check — success grants proficiency in one DM-chosen skill until the next long rest.
- **The Whispering Stones** — *1 hour · 75 XP.* A circle of standing stones at the plains' northern edge. The stones hum at dawn. DC 15 History at the tallest: a fragment of Fen elf memory — the plains before the Torgarian War.
- **Leighmore** — *1 day · 100 XP.* The market town at the plains' eastern end. Fen elf families who fled during the Torgarian War have begun quietly returning, creating fragile coexistence with human settlers.
- **Ardal Tournament Ground** — *2 hours · 125 XP.* The dedicated Kigan Uldar pitch. Outside tournament season it stands eerily maintained — grass trimmed, lines marked, equipment appearing in the locked shed. No explanation has been found.
- **The Torgarian Hollow** — *3 hours · 150 XP.* A depression where a major battle was fought. Grass will not grow at its center. Spectral warriors converge here at dusk. Relics surface regularly, including once an intact sealed letter in Old Ryndorian.

## Arvanthwaite Woods

Arvanthwaite Woods
The Danger Wood
The Arvanthwaite Woods, nestled along the northwestern coast of Ryndor, have
long been regarded as a gift from the elven gods. The towering trees, some of the oldest
and most powerful in the land, have stood for centuries, their roots entwined with
ancient magic and forgotten secrets. For generations, the elves of Ryndor have lived in
reverence and harmony with the forest, treating it as a sacred sanctuary and defending
it fiercely against those who would cause it harm.
Yet, as The Weirding spreads across Ryndor, even the ancient woods are not
immune to its influence. Strange energies have begun to ripple through the roots and
canopies, reshaping the very essence of the forest. The sentient trees, once wise
guardians, now stir with unpredictable intentions, sometimes attacking intruders with
frenzied force—even those who mean no harm. Twisting paths seem to change
direction with each step, and travelers risk getting lost in temporal loops, emerging
days—or years—after they entered. Some trees hum with low, otherworldly melodies,
as if singing the echoes of distant realms.
The elves, though deeply connected to the woods, find themselves in conflict

with the shifting nature of the forest they have vowed to protect. The magic that once
flowed predictably through Arvanthwaite now pulses with unsettling irregularity.
Spirits that once guided travelers have grown hostile, lashing out at anything they do
not recognize. Druids and fey beings still dwell deep within the woods, but even they
seem changed—**stranger, wilder, and more dangerous**. Some whisper that the
Weirding has awakened ancient beings slumbering beneath the forest floor, beings
that predate the elven gods themselves.
Life in Arvanthwaite Woods
Living within the unpredictable expanse of the Arvanthwaite Woods is more
challenging than ever. The elves who call this forest home have long understood how to
navigate its dangers, but now they must adapt to new anomalies brought on by the
Weirding. Sentient trees, once guardians and allies, occasionally become violent or
uncommunicative, leaving even experienced elves to tread carefully. Paths that were
familiar for generations now shift unpredictably, requiring constant vigilance to avoid
temporal traps or strange rifts.
Despite these challenges, the elves remain resilient and deeply connected to the
forest’s magic. They have developed methods of communicating with the trees,
learning to recognize when a particular grove has been distorted by Weirded energies.
Some trees display new magical properties, offering strange fruits or glowing bark that
can enhance spells—but only at a cost. Elven communities live in hidden sanctuaries,
woven into the trees themselves, blending with the natural world to avoid detection.
These sanctuaries are protected not only by elven magic but also by the forest's own
unpredictable defenses.
Elves of the Arvanthwaite Woods continue their vow to protect the forest, though
they must now defend it against forces beyond mortal control. They walk a fine line
between reverence and wariness, knowing that the forest they love is no longer entirely
what it once was. Some embrace the changes, seeking to understand the new magic
born of the Weirding, while others resist—working tirelessly to return the woods to
their original state, though that may no longer be possible.
A Forest of Wonders and Dangers
The creatures of Arvanthwaite have also been changed by the Weirding. Fey
beings, once playful tricksters, have become unpredictable and dangerous, their
pranks escalating into deadly games. Animals once familiar to the elves now exhibit
strange mutations—**stag-like creatures with glowing antlers**, or wolves that
seem to step between dimensions in pursuit of their prey. Elven rituals, once used to
maintain balance in the forest, now yield unpredictable results, sometimes conjuring
unintended entities from the astral plane.
Abernnusker Lake, the heart of the woods, is said to pulse with new, unstable
magic. While the lake’s waters once offered healing and blessings, they now carry a
risky volatility. Some who drink from the lake experience visions of the past or future,
while others become lost in a waking dream, unable to distinguish reality from illusion.
Yet pilgrims still venture to the lake, drawn by the hope of ancient miracles or the

chance to unlock the secrets of the Weirding.
Travelers are strongly discouraged from venturing into the Arvanthwaite Woods
without a knowledgeable guide, for the forest is no longer a passive place of beauty—it
is alive, aware, and ever-changing. The elves offer their protection to those they trust,
but warn that even they cannot fully control the forest’s whims. Each step through
Arvanthwaite’s depths is a journey through mystery and peril, where ancient magic
and new anomalies blend, creating a landscape as wondrous as it is dangerous.
In the era of the Weirding, Arvanthwaite Woods stand as a testament to both
nature’s resilience and unpredictability—a place where history, magic, and the
unknown intertwine. Those who enter the woods must be prepared for anything, for
what they find within may change them forever.

### DM Tools — Arvanthwaite Woods

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | A path ends at a tree that was not there ten minutes ago — enormous, ancient, too deeply rooted to have grown here. No way around it. It steps aside after 1d4 minutes. Or it doesn't. |
| 3–4 | A guide spirit appears — luminous, roughly humanoid, beckoning. DC 13 Insight: genuinely helpful. On a failure, it leads the party in a wide circle back to their starting point, 1d4 hours later. |
| 5–6 | The forest repeats. The party has passed the same blasted oak three times, from a different direction each time. DC 14 Survival to break the loop; failure means 1d4 hours lost. |
| 7–8 | A wolf steps between dimensions mid-pursuit, vanishing and reappearing 30 feet ahead twice. Then it stops, stares at the party for ten seconds, and walks away. |
| 9–10 | A sentient tree lowers one branch toward one party member. Touching it: a flash of vision — the forest before the Weirding, quiet and whole. The branch withdraws after 1 minute if not touched. |
| 11–12 | A fey creature materialises beside the party — small, iridescent, changed. It speaks nonsense in a beautiful voice. DC 12 Arcana: it is trying to warn them about something ahead. It follows for 1d6 hours. |
| 13–14 | One character steps through a curtain of light no one else can see and emerges from behind a nearby tree. For the rest of the party, 3d10 minutes passed. The character is completely unaware of the gap. |
| 15–16 | A stag with glowing antlers looks directly at one character. DC 13 WIS save or feel a compulsion to follow. DC 15 WIS each turn (or be restrained by the party) to resist. The stag walks for 10 minutes, then vanishes. |
| 17–18 | The root network pulses underfoot. Every party member simultaneously feels something vast and old become aware of them — just aware. Using a spell or magic item within 10 minutes triggers this Weirding again. |
| 19–20 | Total silence. Every natural sound stops. From the roots comes one deep sound, like something enormous shifting position. It lasts 4 seconds. The birds do not return for 1 hour. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Guide They Hired.** The party's elven guide stops at a fork, stares in silence for a full minute, then makes eye contact with each party member and says: "we are not alone" — and walks off the path. Whether this is a Weirding symptom, a threat response, or something else is left to the party.
- **The Children Who Left Yesterday.** Three children wandered into Arvanthwaite "just yesterday." Temporal loops mean "yesterday" for the village may mean years inside. The children may be fine, aged, or dead — or they may walk back through the gate tomorrow, not knowing they were ever gone.
- **The Ancient That Woke.** A logging crew returned from the forest changed — quiet, purposeful, building something in their village without discussion. DC 16 History identifies the shape as a ward designed to put something back to sleep. Whatever they encountered is still working through them.
- **The Druid's Dilemma.** A druid has lived at the forest's heart for decades. She found something awakening beneath the oldest tree and has been holding it in place for eleven days. She won't leave her post. The party must go to her.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **By Foot (interior).** The only option inside — no clear routes, all paths suspect. Plan for twice the expected travel time.
- 🚣 **By Boat (coastal approach).** Several inlets along the northwestern coast allow landing by small boat. Temporal effects are weaker near the shore.
- 🦅 **By Air (above the canopy).** Feasible for scouting. Landing within the forest is extremely difficult.
- 🧭 **Guided Entry.** The only reliable way in. DC 14 Persuasion to find a willing elf guide. Two are currently operating; whereabouts unknown.
- ⚠️ **Unguided Entry.** Possible. Emerging where and when intended is not.

#### Landmarks

- **The Oldest Tree** — *3 hours · 150 XP.* At the heart of Arvanthwaite — trunk wider than three houses, roots extending 200 feet. DC 17 Arcana detects something living beneath it, old enough that its resonance doesn't register as any known creature type.
- **The Shimmer Gate** — *1 hour · 75 XP.* Two ancient trees grown together overhead forming a natural arch. What is visible through it from outside doesn't match what is encountered inside. Elf guides always begin here.
- **The Fey Hollow** — *2 hours · 100 XP.* A clearing with highest fey activity. The fey here are territorial and changed. They still trade — but since the Weirding they no longer accept objects. They ask for memories.
- **The Temporal Clearing** — *4 hours · 200 XP.* A wide break in the canopy with concentrated temporal loops. Investigators have identified three coexisting layers: the present, the forest ~80 years ago, and an unclear future. Items left and retrieved are sometimes found in a different condition.
- **The Elf Watch Post** — *2 hours · 125 XP.* A canopy platform, now abandoned. The tree began to move (~20 feet per hour, no mapped pattern). It still contains journals and a final entry: *"The roots are speaking again. I don't think they're asking anymore."*

## Ban Mynydd

Ban Mynydd
The Forge of Ryndor
A dense aura of mystery clings to Ban Mynydd, a walled city that thrives amidst
darkness and secrecy. Second only to Eveltoft in population, Ban Mynydd’s inhabitants
rarely leave, and those who visit often disappear without a trace. The Weirding has
taken hold deep within the city’s labyrinthine mines, twisting time, space, and reality.
Beneath the surface of Ryndor, the once-ordinary mining tunnels now lead to
unpredictable places—sometimes ending abruptly or looping endlessly, and at other
times emerging into forgotten realms or alternate timelines.
Life in Ban Mynydd revolves around these unstable tunnels, but no one is certain
what lies at their deepest points anymore. The Weirding’s influence has warped both
the creatures dwelling within and the minerals mined from the earth. Shards of reality
fold into the gemstones, creating unpredictable effects—some beneficial, others
disastrous. Time shifts erratically underground, with miners reporting they have
worked for hours only to return to find mere moments have passed on the surface—or,
in some cases, years. Entire mining teams have emerged decades later, unaware that
time outside had moved on without them.
The Weirded Mines of Ban Mynydd
The city's labyrinthine tunnels descend far below Ryndor’s surface, now infused
with fragments of the Weirding. Strange pulses of energy ripple through the rock,
creating shifts in gravity and matter. Miners rely on modified drilling technology and
arcane devices to navigate the treacherous depths, but even these tools are unreliable in
the ever-changing tunnels. Some corridors bend back on themselves, while others open
unexpectedly into pockets of elemental chaos, where fire, water, and strange energies
from Nebernoria collide in unstable bursts.
Miners are trained to avoid the strange anomalies that float through the caverns
—pockets of warped air that displace sound and time. Those caught within these
anomalies return disoriented or changed, with memories of futures that have not yet
come to pass or visions of alternate versions of themselves.
Hybrid beasts—morphed by exposure to the Weirding—now prowl the tunnels,

their forms flickering between physical states. Even the fire wyrms bred to assist miners
have begun to display strange behaviors, developing additional limbs or glowing with
erratic bursts of magical energy.
Life in Ban Mynydd
The enclosed city of Ban Mynydd clings stubbornly to its traditions, though the
Weirding has reshaped much of daily life. Entire districts fluctuate between different
phases of time, creating disjointed routines where markets open and close
unpredictably, and citizens wake to find buildings where none stood before. Visitors
need permits issued by the Custodians of Prosperity to enter the city, but those permits
carry little guarantee of safe passage through the mines or stability within the city itself.
The city’s gates are closed tightly against unannounced travelers, as officials fear the
unpredictable consequences of further exposure to external Weirding influences.
Ban Mynydd has become a haven for artificers and arcane scientists seeking to
understand and harness the effects of the Weirding. Some experiment with the strange
minerals extracted from the tunnels, believing they hold the key to stabilizing reality
or developing powerful new technologies. However, these endeavors carry enormous
risk, as objects infused with the Weirding can behave unpredictably—**tools suddenly
evaporating, or timepieces skipping forward days without warning.**
Despite the risks, the wealth of the city remains unmatched. Merchants and
adventurers alike are drawn by the promise of rare gems, ancient relics, and enchanted
minerals, even though many of those treasures are rumored to carry strange curses or
latent magic that could awaken at any time.
The Custodians of Prosperity: Guardians of Unstable Wealth
The Custodians of Prosperity—formerly the Empyreal Bank—occupy an
imposing fortress within Ban Mynydd, housed behind Ryndor’s thickest walls to
protect both the city's wealth and its secrets. With the rise of the Weirding, the
Custodians have shifted their focus from mere currency management to stabilizing the
financial chaos caused by temporal distortions. The Frostmark, the region's currency,
is vulnerable to fluctuations in value due to the unpredictable effects of the Weirding—
**causing rapid inflation, deflation, and strange phenomena where coins age centuries
in moments.**
The Custodians employ magical wards and nullification fields to safeguard the
central vaults and ensure that transactions occur within stabilized zones, free from the
influence of the Weirding. However, unauthorized experiments within the vaults have
begun to draw scrutiny—rumors abound that the Custodians are hoarding timewarped artifacts, hoping to manipulate the Weirding for financial gain.
The bank is heavily fortified, with its own elite guard force trained to combat
weirded creatures and rogue elements that slip through the mines. No visitors are
allowed near the lower vaults, which are rumored to contain not only immense
treasures but also fractured timelines, where lost miners or forgotten artifacts
occasionally emerge from past epochs.

## The Hidden Depths and Forbidden Knowledge

Ban Mynydd has become a destination for adventurers seeking lost knowledge
or relics of ancient civilizations. Tales circulate of strange discoveries deep within the
mines—**cryptic machines powered by impossible energies** and scrolls inscribed
with languages no scholar can decipher. The city's officials deny these rumors, but
shadowy figures lurk at the city’s edges, offering illicit guides through the Weirded
tunnels in exchange for steep payment—or favors not easily repaid.
Despite the danger, treasure hunters persist in their efforts to uncover the
forgotten riches rumored to lie in the depths, hoping to recover relics untouched by the
Weirding’s influence. Some claim to have glimpsed entire cities frozen in time, or relics
capable of unraveling the mysteries of the Weirding itself. Few who seek these
treasures ever return, but those who do speak of impossible landscapes where gravity
bends and time runs backward, warning that the deeper one ventures, the harder it
becomes to leave.
A City at the Edge of Madness
Ban Mynydd is a paradox—both fortress and prison, a city rich with treasures
but steeped in danger. Its people walk a fine line between innovation and collapse,
navigating a world where time itself betrays them and even the most familiar objects
can transform into threats. The city is both revered and feared throughout Ryndor, a
place where the past, present, and future converge into strange and unpredictable
shapes.
As the Weirding continues to ripple through the tunnels beneath Ban Mynydd,
the city stands on the edge of transformation. Some believe the Weirding offers untold
power, while others fear it could consume the city entirely, leaving nothing behind but
temporal echoes and fractured memories. But one thing remains certain—**those
who step into Ban Mynydd’s shadowed depths are never the same when they emerge—
if they emerge at all.**

### DM Tools — Ban Mynydd

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | A timepiece in a party member's possession skips forward 1d6 days without warning. The date is clearly in the future. The mechanism continues ticking normally. |
| 3–4 | A tunnel entered from one direction exits in a completely different part of the city. The journey felt like 10 minutes. Locals estimate the party was in the tunnel for 3 hours. |
| 5–6 | A pocket of warped air drifts through the tunnel. The party member it passes through makes a DC 13 CON save or takes 1d6 psychic damage and surfaces with a vivid memory of a future event that may or may not come to pass. |
| 7–8 | A hybrid beast blocks the tunnel — its form flickering between two states. Not aggressive; confused. DC 13 Animal Handling to calm it enough to pass. On a failure it lunges — not from malice, but from panic. |
| 9–10 | A cluster of coins in a party member's purse has aged centuries — corroded, bearing dates hundreds of years in the future. The face on the coins belongs to no known ruler. |
| 11–12 | A section of tunnel loops. The party walks 20 minutes and returns to a familiar junction. DC 15 Survival to identify the correct exit; each failed attempt costs 30 minutes. |
| 13–14 | A fire wyrm emerges from a side shaft with a second head, both burning at different temperatures. One head ignores the party; the other watches them. The miner who was leading it has not appeared. |
| 15–16 | A stranger emerges from a collapsed shaft dressed in Ban Mynydd mining gear from 30 years ago. They believe they've been gone for one shift. They carry a sealed letter addressed to someone dead for 25 years. |
| 17–18 | A mineral vein in the tunnel wall pulses with light. DC 13 Arcana on touch: a precise vision of something valuable deeper in the mine — the location is clear. What the thing is, exactly, is not. |
| 19–20 | The entire tunnel shifts. The party's location on any map is now incorrect. The shift takes 2 seconds and produces no sensation. They are not in danger. They have no idea where they are. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Permit Problem.** The party arrives at Ban Mynydd's gates without Custodian permits. The permit office is in the city. The city requires permits to enter. The gate official is not unsympathetic — but the rules are the rules. There is an unofficial entrance on the northeast wall used by off-shift miners.
- **The Missing Team.** A mining team entered the lower tunnels six days ago and has not returned. The Custodians claim they are still working. The foreman knows better — she sent three runners after them; only two returned, both with no memory of what they saw.
- **The Emerged Stranger.** A miner has walked out of a shaft sealed for 40 years. He believes he went down yesterday. He is carrying contracts and correspondence the Custodians urgently want back. The party is hired to escort him to the Custodians — or help him avoid them.
- **The Mineral Buyer.** An artificer hires the party to acquire a specific Weirded mineral vein from a contested tunnel — contested because two mining crews from two different eras are working it simultaneously, each unaware the other exists.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **By Foot.** Main road from Eveltoft — 3 days. The gate requires permits; the road is increasingly watched near the walls.
- ⛏️ **By Mine-Cart.** Underground rail links Ban Mynydd's lower levels to outlying extraction sites. Unreliable since the Weirding.
- 🦅 **By Air.** Legal, but landing outside designated platforms requires a secondary permit.
- 🚢 **No Water Route.** Ban Mynydd is inland.
- ⚠️ **Unofficial Entry.** Northeast wall entrance used by off-shift miners. Requires the current passphrase — DC 14 Persuasion with the right contact.

#### Landmarks

- **The Custodians' Fortress** — *1 hour · 100 XP.* Headquarters of the Custodians of Prosperity, built over Ban Mynydd's central vault. No unauthorized visitor has seen the sub-basement level. Those who claim to know what's down there do not agree on what they saw.
- **The Deep Shaft** — *3 hours · 175 XP.* The deepest accessible point in the mine network, sealed after a temporal event swallowed a crew of twelve. The seal has been broken twice — both times from the inside.
- **The Flickering Market** — *30 min · 50 XP.* A district where time-slippage affects commerce. Stalls open and close on schedules that match no clock. Some vendors sell items from tomorrow's shipment. A few of those claims have proved accurate.
- **The Artificers' Quarter** — *1 hour · 75 XP.* Where Ban Mynydd's arcane researchers work. Two buildings on the eastern edge have been quarantined for six months. No official explanation has been given for what is inside.
- **The Lost Registry** — *2 hours · 125 XP.* A Custodian records office listing every miner who entered the tunnels and didn't return. Currently at 847 entries. Some have been crossed out recently — not because the miners were found dead, but because they walked back out of shafts sealed for decades.

## Bennard Peak

Benard Peak
The Shattered Heights
The towering rock formation known as Benard Peak, or "Firehouse Neck," stands
across from the highest summit of Mt. Bannockwyrm, a monument of stone steeped
in legend and shrouded in strangeness. According to ancient tales, the peak was born
from a battle between giants and gods. In the heat of battle, the giant chief hurled a
colossal boulder at Thor, the thunder god. But with one strike of his mighty hammer,
Thor shattered the stone into a thousand pieces. The fragments scattered across the
landscape, forming the looming cliffs of Benard Peak and the deep canyon below—a
place said to be filled with magic and mischief.
Now, with the spread of the Weirding, Benard Peak has become more than just a
site of legend—it has become a place where reality bends and breaks. Travelers
climbing the jagged paths often report shifting landscapes, as if the peak rearranges
itself when no one is watching. Strange, flickering apparitions—giants, gods, and

warriors frozen in moments from forgotten battles—appear within the mist only to
vanish without a trace. Some pilgrims say that time itself falters near the summit, with
journeys that should take hours stretching into days—or passing by in the blink of an
eye.
The Canyon Below: A Realm of Mischief and Madness
The canyon beneath Benard Peak, once home to mischievous gnomes and
elusive sprites, has become a chaotic labyrinth of magic and mutation. The creatures
that dwell here now bear the marks of the Weirding—**gnomes that flicker like candle
flames**, their forms constantly shifting, and sprites with translucent wings that hum
with otherworldly resonance. Even the flora in the canyon has taken on unsettling
forms—**trees with twisted branches** that seem to reach for travelers, and flowers
that bloom with a sound rather than scent.
Those brave enough to explore the canyon speak of invisible rivers flowing
through the air, carrying not water but whispers of forgotten conversations.
Adventurers have stumbled upon pools of reflective mist, showing memories that do
not belong to them—or sometimes visions of futures they wish not to see. Locals warn
that the deeper one ventures into the canyon, the more the world around them twists,
as though the land is remembering too many versions of itself all at once.
The Sacred Summit and Its Unpredictable Blessings
Benard Peak remains a sacred site for those seeking divine guidance, though now
the blessings of the gods are tinged with uncertainty. Offerings left at the summit—
**stones etched with runes, flowers woven with charms, and carved wooden
figurines**—sometimes shift in form or vanish entirely, only to reappear elsewhere
on the peak. Some pilgrims claim their prayers are answered, though not always in the
ways they expected—**blessings sometimes twist into curses**, and boons often
arrive with hidden costs.
The locals, though wary, continue their pilgrimages, believing that even in its
unpredictability, the Weirding holds a kind of truth. Many say that the gods’ attention
has become fragmented, their influence intertwined with the shifting magic of the
land. Pilgrims are advised to make their offerings carefully—for while the gods may
still grant favor, the price of their blessings has become unknowable.
Navigating the Fractured Pathways
Climbing Benard Peak is not for the faint of heart. The paths leading to the
summit twist and warp, with trails that double back upon themselves or vanish
entirely, leaving travelers lost among the craggy cliffs. Strange weather patterns,
fueled by the Weirding, plague the ascent—**lightning strikes without thunder**, and
snow falls from a clear sky, only to melt into pools of warm mist at the travelers' feet.
Some climbers claim to have met versions of themselves on the trail, offering warnings
—or invitations they dare not accept.
Guides from nearby villages carry charms and talismans, believing these offer
some protection against the Weirding’s influence. They caution climbers to stay close

and move quickly, for the longer one lingers on the trail, the more likely they are to
attract the attention of strange forces. Stories of lost adventurers—wanderers who
stepped off the path only to never be seen again—are told often, serving as grim
reminders of the peak’s shifting nature.
Benard Peak: A Place of Power and Peril
Despite the dangers, Benard Peak continues to draw adventurers and pilgrims,
all seeking something—**answers, blessings, or simply the thrill of discovery**. The
peak remains a place of profound mystery, a point where the mortal world and divine
power collide. Yet now, with the spread of the Weirding, the truths hidden within the
mountain are harder to grasp. What once seemed like fixed legends—the clash of
giants and gods, the creation of stone and canyon—now shift and change, as if the
stories themselves are unraveling.
Benard Peak stands as a testament to both power and uncertainty. Here, among
the shattered cliffs and haunted canyons, the line between reality and myth grows
thin. To climb the peak is to step into the unknown, to face not only the forces of the
past but the strange possibilities of the future. In a world touched by the Weirding,
even the stone remembers things that never happened, and the winds whisper songs
no one ever sang.
For those who dare to ascend the peak, the journey offers no guarantees—only
the promise of transformation, for better or worse. At Benard Peak, where gods, giants,
and strangeness meet, every step forward is both a prayer and a risk, and every
offering a bargain with forces that do not obey mortal rules.

### DM Tools — Bennard Peak

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | Time slips. A climb that should take one hour stretches into a full day — the party arrives exhausted and short one Long Rest's worth of time. |
| 3–4 | The path rearranges. Ledges shift and handholds vanish. Every member must succeed on a DC 12 Athletics check or spend an extra hour navigating. |
| 5–6 | A flickering apparition — titan, god, or warrior — manifests in the mist and appears to look directly at the party. Each character makes a DC 11 Wisdom save or is frightened until end of next turn. |
| 7–8 | Invisible whisper-rivers carry memories that don't belong to anyone present. One random character makes a DC 13 Wisdom save or has disadvantage on their next attack roll or ability check. |
| 9–10 | A mist-pool forms underfoot. The first character to look down sees a feared future (DM's choice); they suffer −1d4 to their next saving throw unless they succeed on DC 14 Wisdom. |
| 11–12 | Canyon gnomes flicker into view beside the party for a few seconds, clearly startled, before vanishing. They leave behind a small carved stone of unknown purpose. |
| 13–14 | An offering changes form. Any item intentionally set down transforms — a coin becomes a wildflower, a weapon becomes a river stone, a scroll becomes ash. The original cannot be found. |
| 15–16 | A twisted blessing. One character who prays gains advantage on their next saving throw but takes 1d6 psychic damage as the boon arrives with an edge. |
| 17–18 | Time compression. A Short Rest passes in moments — the party recovers no Hit Dice and any spell slots spent during it are lost. |
| 19–20 | The peak watches. A vast, stone-still face becomes visible in the cliff for one round. All Weirded creatures on Bennard Peak treat the party as non-hostile for the next hour. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **Shrine Guardians.** Translucent-winged sprites and flickering gnomes defend an ancient offering circle. Not hostile unless an offering is touched; Persuasion DC 13 or a matching offering can stand them down.
- **The Apparition.** A titanic ghostly warrior manifests at dusk and replays ancient combat. It cannot perceive the party, but its strikes deal 2d8 force damage to anyone in its path (DC 14 Dexterity save for half). Ends when the replay concludes.
- **The Time-Locked Traveller.** A pilgrim near the summit repeats the same five steps in an endless loop. Breaking it requires identifying what anchors them — a dropped item, an unspoken name, an unfulfilled vow. Roleplay and Investigation, not combat.
- **The Cursed Seekers.** Four worshippers whose blessings have all inverted are becoming hostile toward newcomers. De-escalation (Insight DC 12, Persuasion DC 14) reveals their predicament; combat is possible but missing the point.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **Mountain Ascent (2 days).** Standard overland route from Mt. Bannockwyrm's base. Each day requires DC 14 Athletics or the character gains one level of exhaustion from shifting terrain.
- 🌊 **Canyon River Approach (1 day).** Follow the river through the canyon below. Faster, but sprites and gnomes make navigation unpredictable — arrival point may vary from intent.
- 🦅 **Aerial Approach (half day).** Aviari, mounts, or *fly* spells bypass the lower distortions. The summit still affects time regardless, but the physical climb is avoided.
- 🪬 **Canyon Gnome Guide (variable).** A flickering gnome who knows safe routes can prevent terrain rearrangements. Convincing one requires Persuasion DC 12 and a personal offering — not coin.
- ✨ **Magical Transit (unreliable).** Teleportation within five miles requires a DC 15 spellcasting check. On a failure the party arrives somewhere on Bennard Peak of the DM's choosing.

#### Landmarks

- **The Shard Circle** — *2 hours · 150 XP.* Seven enormous boulder fragments form a ring at the canyon's edge. Offerings vanish by morning and sometimes reappear altered. Ten minutes of meditation here grants advantage on the next Insight check.
- **The Mist-Pool of Remembrance** — *3 hours · 200 XP.* A still pool of reflective mist showing strangers' memories. DC 13 Wisdom save or gain a short-term dread; on a success, receive a fragment of useful information at the DM's discretion.
- **The Apparition Plateau** — *4 hours · 250 XP.* Flat ledge where ghostly battles replay at dusk. A suit of ancient armour (AC 16, damaged — 200 gp to a collector) is wedged in a crevice at the north edge.
- **The Summit Altar** — *6 hours · 300 XP.* The sacred apex, rearranged since any previous visit. Praying and leaving an offering grants +1d6 to a saving throw of choice within 24 hours. The hidden cost arrives before the bonus is used.
- **The Whisper Canyon** — *1 hour · 100 XP.* Canyon where invisible rivers of memories drift through the air. DC 15 Perception (one minute of stillness) extracts a coherent fragment — clue, warning, or exposition — relevant to the current quest.

## Eveltoft

Eveltoft
The Crystal Capitol
Following the Sev'rinn Rebellion, Eveltoft rose from the ashes of war to become a
beacon of progress and unity, with the Sev’rinn Council guiding the city toward an era
of innovation and magic-fueled rebuilding. But as Eveltoft prospered, the early
tremors of The Weirding began to ripple through its streets. Magic and technology,
once harmoniously intertwined, are now behaving unpredictably—bridges shift, canals
flow in strange directions, and buildings subtly twist over time.
The Weirding effects have transformed the city into a realm both beautiful and
uncanny. Parks bloom with strange flora that glow with astral hues, and the occasional
magical storm sweeps through, disrupting public events and festivals. Citizens now
walk alongside odd manifestations—**astral shadows**, rogue enchantments, or
strange objects that awaken briefly before falling inert again. The city’s vibrant cultural
scene and bustling marketplaces remain at the heart of life, though a lingering unease
settles among the people as the familiar bends toward the unfamiliar.
Despite its achievements, Eveltoft now faces new challenges. Weird Zones—
areas where reality feels frayed—appear without warning, particularly in the poorer
districts, where magical anomalies have intensified existing inequalities. The city's
leadership has launched research initiatives with the Crystal Scholars to contain these

effects, but progress is slow. The Council must balance progress with caution, knowing
that the very magic that brought Eveltoft to greatness now threatens to unravel it from
within.
Yet, Eveltoft's citizens endure. Festivals continue, trade flourishes, and even
amid uncertainty, the people cling to their hope for a better future. As The Weirding
spreads, Eveltoft remains a symbol of the complex dance between magic, technology,
and survival, standing proudly at the edge of a reality transformed.
Life in the City
Eveltoft, the largest metropolis in Ryndor and the economic heart of the isles,
remains a hub of commerce, culture, and innovation—but The Weirding has left its
unsettling mark. Built atop the ruins of an ancient civilization, towering buildings and
busy marketplaces now shift in subtle, eerie ways. Winding streets may bend
differently each day, and the once well-organized districts are sometimes warped by
spatial anomalies. Merchants and craftsmen still fill the bustling streets, but the air
buzzes with rumors of weird occurrences—spontaneous enchantments or goods that
behave strangely after passing through Weird Zones.
The city's diverse population continues to thrive, but life has become
unpredictable. Law enforcement and guilds wrestle not only with crime but with the
dangers of astral disruptions. The Merchants Guild warns of goods spontaneously
decaying or transforming, while the Craftsmen's Guild experiments with strange
materials pulled from warped areas. The city guard patrols Weird Zones, knowing that
even a quiet alley could suddenly shift into an astral rift, dragging those inside into an
unpredictable danger.
Life in Eveltoft is now a thrilling balance between opportunity and peril. Taverns
and theaters brim with stories of strange events—bards sing songs about traders lost in
time loops and objects awakening under Weirding influence. Rival factions use these
anomalies to their advantage, further intensifying political intrigue. Yet, even amid this
chaos, the people of Eveltoft remain resilient and proud, embracing their city’s strange
transformation as a beacon of survival, innovation, and change in a world bent by
magic and uncertainty.
Eveltoft’s districts were not always part of the grand metropolis that now spreads
across the foothills and waterways beneath the shadow of the Bannockwyrm
Mountains. Each district began as an independent settlement—a fishing village here, a
trade outpost there, and an isolated sanctuary hidden in the forests. Over time, as
Eveltoft grew in wealth, power, and influence, it absorbed these outlying communities,
weaving them into the fabric of a unified city. The process was one of both opportunity
and upheaval, creating a city that is as diverse as it is sprawling.
Central District
The Central District
Heart of Power and the Rift
At the core of Eveltoft lies the Central District, where political authority,

commerce, and the strange energies of the Rift to Nebernoria converge. Once home to
bustling government offices, markets, and cultural hubs, the Central District has
become the focal point of Ryndor’s most daring technological experiment—
**containing the Rift's Weirding effects** within powerful nullification fields. These
fields are powered by the hydro engines of the Fenchong Falls, which cascade down the
cliffs beneath the grand Eveltoft City Hall. The City Hall itself is a feat of engineering,
built directly over the roaring waterfall, as if to remind the people of Eveltoft that the
flow of power never ceases.
The Rift Contained—But Not Conquered
The nullification fields surrounding the Rift are state-of-the-art marvels,
capable of suppressing the Rift's unpredictable magic. Large turbines beneath the falls
generate hydroelectric power, driving the machinery that keeps the fields operational
day and night. Without this constant energy, the Weirding would spread unchecked,
warping space and time throughout the district. Even with the containment, the Rift’s
presence hums in the air—a faint, unsettling vibration that leaves citizens feeling
slightly out of sync with reality.
The fields are not perfect, however. Every so often, fluctuations in the
waterfall’s flow cause momentary interruptions, during which strange phenomena
slip through. On such occasions, objects vanish and reappear elsewhere, clocks behave
erratically, and brief portals to unknown locations flicker open, exposing curious
glimpses of Nebernoria’s astral landscapes. Citizens call these incidents “Rift
Reverberations”, and while most are harmless, they serve as a reminder of the
immense power just barely held in check.
Life in the Central District
Living and working near the Rift demands both resilience and caution.
Government officials, merchants, and citizens alike have adapted to the peculiar energy
of the district, though paranoia and strange behaviors are not uncommon. The Rift
creates an atmosphere of constant vigilance, as even those who believe in the safety of
the nullification fields feel the unease of dwelling beside the unknown.
Despite the looming presence of the Rift, the Central District thrives. Trade
agreements and diplomatic pacts are signed within the grand halls of Eveltoft City Hall,
while bustling markets just beyond the Rift's containment sell goods both mundane
and arcane. Merchants from across Ryndor come here not only for commerce but also in
hopes of glimpsing something extraordinary—an object or artifact briefly altered by
the Weirding, or a fleeting view of Nebernoria’s eerie horizon.
Maintaining the Fields: A Race Against Time
The hydro engines that power the nullification fields require constant
maintenance. The waterfalls are unpredictable, with seasonal shifts occasionally
causing disruptions to the flow. Maintenance crews work tirelessly to prevent
breakdowns, knowing that even a momentary lapse could result in catastrophe.
Sev’rinn engineers and scholars often assist, using their magic to stabilize machinery

or predict fluctuations in the Weirding's influence. Still, accidents happen, and every
disruption offers a fleeting glimpse into the chaos the Rift could unleash.
Rumors persist of black market deals involving engineers or officials willing to
disable the nullification fields for a price, hoping to steal something valuable from
Nebernoria’s influence. The Crystal Scholars keep a close watch over the district, but
leaks and failures are inevitable, given the complexity of the system. Few can resist the
allure of secrets from beyond the Rift, even when the risks are immense.
Eveltoft’s Central Nexus: The Meeting of Forces
With the Rift at its heart, the Central District has become a place where all the
great forces of Ryndor collide—**magic, technology, and ambition** interwoven in a
fragile balance. The Council Chambers within City Hall are a battleground for debate,
with factions vying to control the Rift’s resources. Some argue for greater exploration
of Nebernoria, while others fear the consequences of further tampering with forces
beyond comprehension.
This district symbolizes both progress and peril, a reflection of Eveltoft’s
ambition to master the unknowable. The Rift grants the city access to incredible
resources and arcane knowledge, yet every discovery carries a cost. Can Eveltoft
control the Weirding indefinitely, or will the Rift’s influence continue to erode the
boundaries between worlds, making the city’s heart the first to falter?
A City Caught Between Realities
The strange relationship between the Rift and the city grows deeper with each
passing year. The Central District’s residents have grown accustomed to odd temporal
glitches, such as encountering people they’ve already spoken with earlier in the day or
seeing events unfold out of sequence. Occasionally, messages arrive before they are
sent, and some claim to have met their future selves wandering the streets in moments
of Rift instability.
Meanwhile, the Fenchong Falls flow on—a symbol of Eveltoft’s determination to
harness nature’s power and contain the strange forces leaking from Nebernoria. But
how long the city can maintain this delicate equilibrium remains uncertain. As
technology and magic converge, and as the Rift tests the limits of containment, the
people of the Central District walk a fine line between order and oblivion.
Whether the Rift is a boon or a curse is a question yet unanswered, but one thing
is clear: the heart of Eveltoft beats in time with forces not of this world, and every
pulse carries the potential for either revelation or ruin.
Chipping-Gong District
Chipping-Gong District
Woodlands at the edge of the crystal city
Named for the legendary bear that once roamed the forests nearby, ChippingGong has long served as the lumber and woodworking heart of Eveltoft. While the
sounds of axes chopping wood and the whir of saws still fill the air, the Weirding’s
creeping influence has begun to alter both the craft and the forest itself. Now, amidst

timber yards and carpentry shops, visitors may catch glimpses of the strange, as both
tools and timber behave unpredictably, and the forest whispers secrets only the most
attentive can hear.
A Forest Touched by the Strange
Chipping-Gong sits on the outskirts of Eveltoft, where the forests once offered
