abundant resources—but the Weirding has changed the way the land provides. Trees
sometimes grow overnight, forming unnatural patterns in their bark that seem like
arcane glyphs. Lumberjacks report that fallen trees shift location by morning, and
some timber, when cut, releases a brief gust of fragrant mist that leaves hallucinations
in its wake.
Though some fear the forest’s increasing unpredictability, others see the
opportunity within the anomaly. Strange, twisted Weirdwood has become a coveted
material, with patterns shifting beneath the grain like a flowing river. Items crafted
from Weirdwood are believed to contain latent magic, although prolonged exposure is
rumored to alter their owners' thoughts or dreams. Visitors to Chipping-Gong are
encouraged to wander the woods, but never alone, for paths have been known to loop
endlessly, trapping the unwary in strange, time-lost pockets.
Craftsmanship in a Shifting World
The woodworkers and carpenters of Chipping-Gong are among the most skilled
in Eveltoft, but even they must now adapt to the quirks of the Weirding. Tools
sometimes refuse to obey commands, saws cut at angles no one intended, and
completed items occasionally shift shape or function without warning. The district’s
finest craftsmen now incorporate charms and protective wards into their workshops,
ensuring that their creations remain stable—at least for a while.
Some craftsmen have embraced the change, using Weirdwood and other affected
materials to create dynamic, living pieces—**chairs that shift to fit the sitter**,
carvings that grow new details on their own, and furniture that seems to rearrange
itself when no one is watching. These enchanted goods fetch high prices, though buyers
are warned: no one knows how long the magic will hold.
Living Architecture: Buildings with Minds of Their Own
Chipping-Gong has long been known for its innovative wooden architecture, but
in the era of the Weirding, wooden buildings have taken on a life of their own—
sometimes literally. Some of the tallest wooden structures in the city now creak and
shift subtly at night, changing their layout slightly, as if trying to express something
unsaid. Visitors on guided tours may notice new carvings appearing on walls or
stairways shifting position, though the locals insist that these changes are harmless—
so far.
Builders in Chipping-Gong are experimenting with Weirded timber in
architecture, creating structures that react to changes in the environment. Walls
tighten against storms and floors soften underfoot, responding to the presence of
people and weather. However, these experiments are not without risk—several

unfortunate incidents have occurred where houses sealed their occupants inside or
refused entry to strangers, their wooden frames acting on some unknown whim.
Markets and Merchants Amid the Anomaly
Despite its strangeness, the Chipping-Gong marketplace remains a lively center
of commerce. Merchants flock here to purchase lumber and wooden goods, though
now the market also sells Weirded artifacts—objects carved from wood that might shift
in purpose, shape, or sound without warning. Visitors to the market often encounter
vendors selling protective wards against the strange effects, or guides offering maps
that claim to help navigate the shifting streets.
Handmade wooden toys, once the pride of the district, now carry an air of
unpredictability—**puppets that sing forgotten songs**, dolls that whisper riddles
when touched, and wooden animals that sometimes blink when no one is watching.
While these enchanted curiosities attract collectors and tourists, locals remain wary of
such goods—many refuse to keep them in their homes, fearing what they may become.
A Community Embracing Change
Though the Weirding has altered Chipping-Gong in unsettling ways, the
residents remain resilient. The district’s craftsmen and lumberjacks have learned to
work with the strangeness, adapting their skills to an ever-shifting world. For many,
the Weirding is just one more challenge—a new opportunity to innovate and create in
ways that defy the ordinary.
At night, the district comes alive with music and conversation. Locals gather in
taverns built from Weirded timber, where flickering carvings dance on the walls and
songs change mid-verse, as if influenced by some distant, unseen force. It is said that
some residents have begun to understand the strange rhythms of the Weirding, using
them to predict subtle shifts and find fortune where others see only chaos.
A District of Tradition, Innovation, and Anomaly
Chipping-Gong stands as a symbol of both tradition and transformation, a
district where ancient craftsmanship meets the unpredictable magic of the Weirding.
The people of Chipping-Gong do not resist the change—they adapt, innovate, and
thrive, finding ways to balance stability with spontaneity.
In this corner of Eveltoft, axes swing, saws hum, and wood takes on new life.
Whether you're visiting for the furniture, the architecture, or the strangeness,
Chipping-Gong offers an experience that is both rooted in the past and forever shifting
toward the unknown. Here, timber speaks, and craft becomes magic—if only for those
brave enough to listen.
Dogun District
Dogun District
Your one-stop for shopping, food, entertainment—and unpredictable anomalies!
The Dogun District of Eveltoft, long celebrated for its bustling markets and
vibrant cultural scene, has become both a commercial hub and a zone of strange
happenings in the wake of the Weirding. While it remains one of the city’s most

popular destinations, visitors must now navigate not just lively streets but shifting
spaces and fleeting phenomena—oddities that make every trip to Dogun an adventure.
Shops, restaurants, and theaters still thrive, but unpredictable twists of reality ensure
that no two visits are ever the same.
A Market Transformed by the Strange
Dogun’s famous marketplace continues to thrive, but strange sights are
becoming increasingly common. Vendors report merchandise changing color, flavor,
or function unexpectedly—**silk scarves turn to metal in the rain**, spices shift to
different tastes mid-cooking, and customers have occasionally purchased objects that
vanish entirely by nightfall. Some shops embrace the chaos, marketing themselves as
"Weird Shops," offering goods that promise both delight and surprise.
Merchants have also learned to adapt—those with connections to magical
artisans now create items that can shift and adjust to the Weirding’s influence.
Meanwhile, temporary stalls pop up overnight, selling bizarre trinkets and relics that
disappear by morning. Rumor has it these stalls are run by beings touched by the astral
plane, though no one has ever confirmed where the stall-keepers go once their wares
vanish.
A Cultural Scene in Flux
Dogun’s artistic and creative heart beats on, though the Weirding has deeply
influenced the district’s artists, musicians, and performers. Paintings now seem to
move subtly when viewed from certain angles, music resonates with odd harmonies
that echo long after the notes end, and performances change in ways that even the
actors cannot explain—**dialogue rewriting itself mid-play**, or instruments playing
notes from unknown songs.
The annual Festivals of Light and Song, once joyful celebrations, now feature
unexpected and eerie elements. Lanterns drift into the sky, only to multiply into
hundreds and disappear into strange constellations, while songs performed at the
festival seem to summon forgotten memories from the audience. Some visitors leave
enchanted and inspired, while others feel unsettled by the glimpses of otherworldly
forces lingering just beneath the surface of each celebration.
A History Written in Chaos
The Dogun District has always been a place of transformation, having grown
from a small fishing village into a vibrant commercial hub. Immigrants from eastern
lands first settled here, drawn by abundant fish and fertile soil, and built a community
that quickly evolved into a center of trade and culture. However, as the Weirding
spread, the district began to change in ways no one could have anticipated.
Shops that have stood for decades now report phantom customers—strange
figures flickering at the edge of sight who leave coins of unfamiliar origin. Theater
performances spontaneously alter, and restaurants sometimes serve dishes not listed
on the menu, with flavors described as both delightful and impossible. The district’s
long history of resilience serves it well, as residents continue to adapt to the new

normal, finding opportunity even in uncertainty.
Navigating the District’s Anomalies
While the Dogun District remains a thriving part of Eveltoft, venturing through
it now carries new risks and surprises. Streets have been known to shift subtly,
creating new paths and shortcuts—or leading travelers in endless loops. Visitors are
advised to stick to well-marked routes or hire guides familiar with the district's
peculiarities. Those who wander too far may encounter unexpected phenomena, such
as conversations overheard from other times or markets that appear, conduct
business, and disappear within hours.
Despite the oddities, locals maintain a sense of humor and resilience. The phrase
“**Dogun will provide**” has become a common saying, reflecting both the district’s
unpredictability and its potential for surprising good fortune. Many residents even
welcome the Weirding as a creative muse, believing it adds an element of magic to
everyday life. However, the district guard remains vigilant, ensuring that the strange
occurrences remain manageable and public safety is not compromised.
A New Era of Innovation and Wonder
Though the Dogun District has been reshaped by the Weirding, it thrives on
change. The district’s merchants, artists, and performers continue to celebrate the
unexpected, making Dogun a place where commerce and creativity intertwine in ways
no one could have imagined. Visitors come not only to shop and dine but also to
experience the magic of unpredictability, knowing that anything can happen.
Despite the uncertainty, Dogun remains a place where opportunity thrives, and
both locals and travelers find wonder in the chaos. The Weirding may have altered the
district, but it has also enriched its character, transforming Dogun into a dynamic,
ever-evolving experience. Here, on the streets where markets flow like rivers and art
takes on a life of its own, the people of Dogun continue to embrace the strange—
finding beauty, humor, and profit in the unpredictable tides of this new era.
Fishmark District
Fiskmark District
Center for waterfront fun, delicious seafood, and strange maritime encounters.
The Fiskmark District is renowned for its bustling fish markets, seafood
restaurants, and thriving waterfront. Yet, like the rest of Ryndor, Fiskmark has not
escaped the influence of the Weirding, which has subtly—and sometimes overtly—
warped its coastal charms. While seagulls still call and the salty sea breeze fills the air,
visitors to Fiskmark may notice unusual phenomena lurking just beneath the surface of
everyday life.
Fish Markets and Strange Catches
The markets of Fiskmark continue to thrive, with vendors offering the freshest
seafood in Eveltoft—but not without a few strange surprises. The nearby waters, once
predictable and generous, have become less reliable under the influence of the
Weirding. Fishermen occasionally return with odd catches—fish that glow faintly in

the moonlight, crabs with extra limbs, or eels that seem to sing eerie melodies when
submerged in water. Some of these strange creatures fetch high prices from curious
buyers, though most fishermen remain wary of selling them, fearing the curses or
unpredictable effects they may carry.
Many visitors are drawn to the allure of the Weirding, hoping to catch glimpses
of strange aquatic life or try delicacies said to be infused with residual magic from the
astral plane. Some dishes have even become local legends—from soups that give
fleeting visions of the future to oysters that leave a strange hum in the ears of those
who eat them. While these peculiarities attract the curious, local fishermen take
precautions when casting their nets, as too many encounters with Weirded creatures
have left vessels lost to time disturbances or tangled in phantom storms.
Seafood Delights and Bewildering Tastes
Fiskmark's seafood restaurants remain second to none, offering both classic
dishes and new creations influenced by the Weirding. Culinary experiments are on the
rise, with chefs using unpredictable ingredients brought back from fishing expeditions.
Visitors rave about "mirrored cod," a fish with a reflective sheen that seems to display
shifting images of the past as it cooks, and "ember prawns," which crackle like embers
in the mouth, warming the eater from the inside out.
Not all Weirded dishes are for the faint-hearted. Some visitors have reported
temporary transformations—skin taking on a sea-green hue or hair shifting to
translucent strands—after indulging in certain seafood platters. Others claim that
some meals whisper strange thoughts, leaving them wondering whether the food was
truly meant for mortal consumption. Adventurous diners flock to Fiskmark for the
thrill of tasting the unknown, though many establishments still offer traditional fare
for those who prefer to avoid the Weirding’s influence.
Waterfront Leisure and the Sport of Utfordring
The waterfront of Fiskmark is more lively than ever, with visitors booking
fishing trips, dolphin rides, and harbor tours. Yet, even leisurely strolls along the
docks come with a touch of the unexpected—boats sometimes appear in the harbor
without ever setting sail, and phantom figures are spotted boarding vessels only to
vanish upon closer inspection. Some adventurous souls rent boats in search of
underwater Weirding zones, hoping to catch rare aquatic phenomena or witness
undersea rifts firsthand.
Living and Adapting in Fiskmark
Fiskmark remains a tight-knit community, though life here now requires a
measure of caution and adaptation. Locals have grown used to the peculiarities of the
Weirding, treating them with a mix of humor and wariness. Children playing on the
docks sometimes chase echoes of themselves—faint, translucent versions of moments
yet to happen. Street performers integrate the strange occurrences into their routines,
making illusions out of real-time distortions, much to the amusement of tourists and
townsfolk alike.

Though merchants and fishermen continue to do business as usual, many now
carry charms and wards against Weirded disruptions. Superstitions have taken hold—
sailors refuse to cast off on certain tides known to overlap with Weird zones, and
taverns display weirdstones to ward off malignant influences. Despite these
challenges, the people of Fiskmark remain resilient and resourceful, viewing the
Weirding as just another obstacle to overcome.
A Place of Thrills, Trade, and Transformation
The Fiskmark District stands at the crossroads of tradition and transformation,
its vibrant markets and thriving waterfront infused with the unpredictable magic of
the Weirding. Here, every meal might offer more than just nourishment, every fishing
expedition a glimpse into another reality, and every sport a test not just of skill, but of
adaptability. Visitors come not only for the seafood and sport but for the thrill of the
unexpected, knowing that Fiskmark offers experiences found nowhere else in Eveltoft.
For those who embrace the chaos and wonder of the Weirding, Fiskmark
promises not just entertainment and excitement—but a journey into the strange and
unknown. Whether you seek delicious food, thrilling competitions, or a brush with the
bizarre, Fiskmark remains the place where commerce and magic meet, inviting all who
visit to taste the unpredictable tides of this ever-changing world.
Heibury District
Heibury District
Day passes or proper identification required for entry
Named for the legendary shield wall that once stood in defense of the city, the
Heibury District remains the military heart of Eveltoft. Its barracks, armories, and
training grounds continue to forge the fiercest warriors in Ryndor, but in the age of the
Weirding, Heibury has become more than just a bastion of tradition. Unpredictable
phenomena now weave their way through even the most rigid of drills, leaving warriors
to grapple not only with blades and bows but also with the chaos of altered reality.
Training Amid the Unpredictable
Heibury’s warriors train relentlessly, though their routines now include
unexpected disruptions caused by the Weirding. Training grounds shift underfoot,
forcing recruits to adapt mid-spar. Mock battles are interrupted by strange flickers of
time, leaving participants suddenly on opposite sides of the fight or resetting
moments they can’t quite remember. Some soldiers develop strange abilities—**their
reflexes heightened** as if guided by unseen hands or weapons glowing faintly with
residual energy—but these gifts come at a cost. Too much exposure to the Weirding
has led to soldiers reporting fractured memories or a sense of being watched by things
unseen.
Adventurers and visitors are still welcome to participate in mock battles, but they
must be prepared for anomalies in the sparring arena. Illusions of past battles
sometimes manifest without warning, and those unprepared for these phantom
encounters may find themselves fighting alongside forgotten warriors—or against the

shadows of their own memories.
Craftsmanship in an Altered Reality
The blacksmiths and weapon makers of Heibury continue their tradition of
exquisite craftsmanship, though now even their forges are touched by the Weirding.
Blades hum with strange vibrations, shields seem to repel more than physical attacks,
and some armor responds to invisible forces—becoming lighter or heavier at
unpredictable intervals. Visitors to the workshops may witness artisans using new
techniques, channeling unstable magic into steel in ways previously thought
impossible. However, these innovations come with risks—**some weapons develop
minds of their own**, refusing to be wielded by those they deem unworthy.
Despite the strangeness, Heibury’s weapon makers remain proud of their craft.
They continue to offer tours and demonstrations, and visitors can commission
custom-made swords or enchanted armor—though the final product might bear
unforeseen quirks. Some Weirded weapons have become prized in underground
markets, though official military orders forbid their use in service, wary of what
unintended effects they might unleash on the battlefield.
Mercenary Work and Bounty Boards
Heibury remains a gathering place for adventurers, mercenaries, and bounty
hunters, though the jobs posted now carry far stranger risks. Bounty boards offer
contracts to track creatures touched by the Weirding, escort caravans through areas
affected by time distortions, or close small rifts that open unpredictably along trade
routes. Mercenaries must navigate not just enemies but shifting landscapes, as paths
change mid-mission and beasts from other planes slip through cracks in reality.
Some adventurers have begun to specialize in Weirding-related jobs, developing
expertise in recognizing anomalies and handling creatures altered by the strange
magic. These specialists are in high demand but tread carefully—too many encounters
with the Weirding have left veterans haunted by dreams that feel too real or
fragmented memories of places they’ve never been.
Living in Heibury: Adaptation and Vigilance
Life in Heibury now demands discipline and adaptability, as even the most
familiar routines are affected by unpredictable phenomena. Guards and soldiers
patrol not only for criminal activity but also to contain sudden Weirded occurrences.
Strange rifts sometimes open in alleyways, and phantom warriors from longforgotten wars wander the streets before dissolving into mist. The people of Heibury
are accustomed to unexpected challenges, meeting each new disruption with the same
determination and precision that defines their military heritage.
The great shield wall, though long fallen, remains a symbol of resilience—a
reminder that Heibury’s people stand firm, no matter how strange or unstable the
world becomes.
A District of Tradition and Transformation
The Heibury District remains a vital part of Eveltoft, even as it navigates the

challenges of the Weirding’s encroachment. Its warriors train harder, its blacksmiths
innovate boldly, and its adventurers embrace the unpredictable. Heibury’s identity—
rooted in tradition, honor, and strength—has become more complex, as its people
learn to adapt to a world in flux without losing sight of who they are.
In Heibury, the past and present merge, and discipline meets uncertainty. The
district is a place where swords and shields still matter, but where sharp minds and
quick reflexes are just as essential. For those who call Heibury home, the Weirding is
not something to fear—it is just one more challenge to conquer, another battlefield on
which to prove their worth.
Gullborg District
Gullborg District
Timeless Splendor Suspended
Once the pinnacle of luxury and opulence, Gullborg District now lies frozen in
time, held captive by the enigmatic forces of the Weirding. From the outside, the
district appears untouched by the years that have passed since the slow-time anomaly
first took hold. Visitors observe only days-old celebrations and freshly stocked
storefronts, but for those outside, years have passed without seeing their loved ones, or
conducting trade inside the district.
A Glimpse Through the Curtain of Time
To the outside world, Gullborg looks unchanged. The grand markets bustle as
they did on the day the slow-time anomaly emerged, musicians play in courtyards, and
half-finished meals linger on tables. The illusion is almost comforting.
Few dare to enter Gullborg unless absolutely necessary. Merchants waiting for
goods trapped in the district have given up hope of retrieving them, and many who
tried to venture in for rescue missions are now trapped within, just as bound by the
slow-time anomaly as the original residents. Only two individuals have ever escaped
the district since the Weirding began—both returned disoriented, younger than their
children trapped outside the zone, and haunted by the sense that they left something
behind.
An Uncertain Future
City officials and the Crystal Scholars have yet to find a way to neutralize the
slow-time anomaly that holds Gullborg in its grasp. Efforts to seal the rift or
recalibrate the temporal flow have failed, and some fear that the anomaly may spread,
consuming more of Eveltoft if left unchecked. Yet the allure of Gullborg’s wealth keeps
some desperately seeking solutions. If the anomaly can be controlled, they reason, the
mastery of time itself could become the city’s greatest asset.
But for now, the district remains both a treasure trove and a trap, suspended on
the edge of reality, where luxury lasts forever—and so does regret. Those trapped
inside may live out their days in comfort and splendor, but whether they will ever
escape to enjoy it in the outside world remains unknown. The question on everyone’s
mind is: if time moves differently inside Gullborg, what becomes of the soul when the

years no longer align?
Kieferden District
Kieferden District
A Tranquil Oasis Beneath the Veil of the Weirding
Once known as a peaceful retreat within the bustling city of Eveltoft, Kieferden
District has been touched by the unpredictable influence of the Weirding. Though its
lush greenery, spas, and Ferden Pool still draw visitors, the serenity that once defined
the district now carries a subtle sense of unease. Strange phenomena ripple beneath
the surface, and those who visit leave wondering if the tranquility they experienced was
real—or a carefully woven illusion.
The Strange Stillness of Ferden Pool
At the heart of Kieferden lies the Ferden Pool, a natural hot spring once famous
for its healing properties. Now, under the effects of the Weirding, the pool exhibits
strange behaviors. Water levels shift inexplicably, with the pool draining one moment
and brimming over the next. Mineral deposits shift in color, sometimes glowing faintly
at night, and ripples appear on the surface even without wind—as though something
unseen stirs from beneath. Some visitors claim the water warps time, making a few
moments of immersion feel like entire days. Others whisper that entering the pool can
alter memories, leaving bathers unsure whether their experiences are real or imagined.
Legends about the Sev’rinn sorcerer who first summoned the pool have
resurfaced, with new rumors suggesting that the spring’s magic has been awakened by
the Weirding. Some believe the Ferden Pool is now a conduit between worlds, drawing
energy from Nebernoria. Strangely, objects left by the water’s edge sometimes vanish
overnight, only to reappear in entirely different parts of Eveltoft—or not at all.
Spas and Wellness Centers: Healing or Hallucination?
Kieferden’s spas and wellness centers continue to offer treatments and
therapies, but those who seek relaxation within the district now risk strange side
effects. Massages may trigger fleeting visions, as if memories from other lives bleed
through. Aromatherapy sessions leave participants feeling oddly disconnected from
time, while herbal teas brewed with local plants produce dreams that feel startlingly
real—and sometimes impossible to forget.
A growing number of apothecaries in the district have begun experimenting with
Weirded herbs, despite warnings from the Crystal Scholars. Some concoctions are said
to enhance magical abilities, while others temporarily grant strange insights, though
at the cost of disorientation or paranoia. The herb shops in Kieferden now attract
adventurers and scholars eager to unlock the secrets of these new remedies, though
the risks are ever-present.
Art, Music, and Performance in a Warped Reality
The district’s arts and culture scene has also been transformed by the Weirding.
Musicians claim that their instruments play notes unbidden, as though guided by

invisible hands, and painters report visions that compel them to create works far
beyond their original intent. Art galleries have begun showcasing pieces that change
subtly over time—portraits blink or shift expression, and landscapes display different
seasons depending on the time of day. Performers speak of strange occurrences during
shows, such as props moving of their own accord or audiences seeming to forget entire
performances midway through.
Ferden’s theaters and music venues now host performances influenced by the
district’s weirdness, featuring experimental compositions and illusion-based
spectacles. Some acts claim to invoke Nebernorian energies, creating mesmerizing
experiences that blur the line between reality and fantasy. Audiences leave entranced
but unsettled, uncertain whether they witnessed art or some fragment of another
realm.
Rumors of Secret Societies and Cults
The dark rumors surrounding Ferden Pool have only deepened under the
influence of the Weirding. Some say that the pool serves as a meeting place for secret
societies seeking to harness the rift’s energy. Others believe that a cult devoted to
Nebernoria has emerged, conducting rituals by moonlight in the district’s hidden
groves. The Crystal Scholars have launched investigations into these rumors, but no
conclusive evidence has been found—though the disappearance of several
investigators has fueled suspicions that something is lurking beneath Kieferden’s
surface.
A Haven, with a Touch of Madness
Despite the unease the Weirding brings, Kieferden remains a place of beauty and
wonder. Visitors still come to immerse themselves in the Ferden Pool, seek rare herbs,
or indulge in the district’s renowned spas and performances. Yet beneath the peaceful
veneer, the influence of the Weirding pulses—subtle, persistent, and impossible to
ignore. Every breeze through the district’s trees seems to whisper secrets, and every
ripple in the pool suggests that another world lies just out of reach.
Those who visit return changed, whether they realize it or not. Some leave with
newfound clarity or strange insights, while others report a lingering sense of
disconnection from time and place. What Kieferden offers in peace, it takes in
certainty—for in this oasis touched by the Weirding, nothing is ever truly what it
seems.

### DM Tools — Eveltoft

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | An astral shadow detaches from a random party member and begins mimicking their actions one round late. It lasts 1 hour before dissolving; frightened creatures treat it as hostile. |
| 3–4 | A nearby bridge pivots 90 degrees, redirecting foot traffic to an unintended district. The party must spend an extra 30 minutes navigating back to their destination. |
| 5–6 | A canal reverses direction for 1 minute. Any vessel or swimming creature is pushed 60 feet upstream. After 1 minute the flow snaps back to normal. |
| 7–8 | A rogue enchantment seizes one random magical item among the party — it floats, spins, and hums for 1 minute. While airborne, the item cannot be used or retrieved. |
| 9–10 | A mundane object nearby — a clock, a chair, a lantern — briefly awakens with simple intelligence, speaks one cryptic sentence in a language of the DM's choosing, then goes permanently inert. |
| 11–12 | A Weird Zone pops up in a 30-foot radius around the party. For 1 minute, spell attack rolls are made with advantage but saving throws against spells are also made with advantage. Then it collapses. |
| 13–14 | A magical storm erupts overhead. Any character caught outdoors must succeed on a DC 12 Strength saving throw or be pushed 10 feet in a random direction and knocked prone. |
| 15–16 | A planter or park nearby erupts with astral flora. Any character who touches a flower must succeed on a DC 13 Constitution save or have disadvantage on their next Wisdom check. |
| 17–18 | A Rift Reverberation ripples out from Central District. A portal flickers open for 6 seconds, through which a confused astral creature stumbles. Roll d6: 1–3 the creature is harmless and frightened; 4–6 it is hostile. |
| 19–20 | The streets align perfectly. For the next 4 hours the party moves through Eveltoft without navigational difficulty — locals are cooperative, shortcuts appear obvious, and no further Weirdings occur in that window. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **Rift Reverberation Crisis.** The nullification fields in Central District fail — a five-minute portal tears open, drawing astral creatures into the streets. City Hall engineers recruit nearby fighters. The party has ten minutes to repel the creatures or evacuate civilians before the portal closes.
- **Sealed House (Chipping-Gong).** A Weirdwood building has locked itself shut with three occupants inside. It is frightened, not hostile. Persuasion DC 14 (spoken aloud, knocking gently) or Animal Handling DC 13 can coax it open. Forced entry causes walls to tighten and floors to buckle.
- **The Vanishing Merchant (Dogun).** A trader the party just transacted with vanishes mid-exchange — stall, goods, and coin all gone. Arcana DC 14 or Perception DC 16 finds an astral residue trail leading two streets over to a temporary Weird Zone where the merchant crouches, confused and terrified.
- **The Singing Catch (Fiskmark).** A fisherman drags in a bioluminescent eel that begins singing in Nebernorian. It sings for three minutes, then dies. Arcana DC 15 identifies the language; History DC 16 yields a partial translation — a prophecy connected to something the party is already pursuing.
- **The Reluctant Weapon (Heibury).** A blacksmith's newly forged sword refuses its buyer — humming discordantly and glowing red when touched. The smith hires the party to negotiate. The sword is sentient, arrogant, and wants a worthy wielder. Charisma and Insight encounter; the sword cannot be destroyed unless a Weirding changes it.

#### Travel Options

- 🏙️ **On Foot Through the Districts (variable).** Roughly 30 minutes per district. DC 10 Perception in unfamiliar areas — failure means a wrong turn into an adjacent district.
- 🚤 **Canal Boat (fast, unreliable).** Canal boats cross in minutes when waterways behave. Roll a d6 at departure: on a 1, the canal reverses during transit and the party must disembark early or arrive at the wrong terminus.
- 📜 **Heibury Day Pass (required for district entry).** Obtained from City Hall. Valid identification is sufficient; a party member with a criminal record must succeed on Persuasion DC 14 or Deception DC 12 with a forged document. Single-use.
- ⚠️ **Gullborg (effectively inaccessible).** The slow-time anomaly prevents safe entry. Crystal Scholars sell anti-anomaly amulets for 200 gp each, with no guarantee they hold for more than one hour. Attempting entry without one risks being frozen in the anomaly indefinitely.
- 🌿 **Kieferden Hidden Paths (fast, risky).** Grove shortcuts halve travel time to the eastern districts. Each use carries a 1-in-6 chance of an unplanned encounter with Nebernoria devotees in the hidden groves.

#### Landmarks

- **Eveltoft City Hall & Fenchong Falls** — *30 min · 200 XP.* The seat of city government sits directly above Fenchong Falls, drawing its nullification power from the water below. Arcana proficiency and one minute of concentration near the hydro engines — DC 14 check — reveals the current Rift stability and whether a Reverberation is imminent.
- **The Ferden Pool** — *Kieferden · 1 hour · 150 XP.* The famed natural hot spring. Immersion for ten minutes requires a DC 13 Constitution save — on a failure, one hour passes unnoticed. On a success, the character gains the benefits of a Short Rest and removes one level of exhaustion.
- **The Utfordring Arena** — *Fiskmark · 1 hour · 100 XP.* An underwater aquatic competition venue. A bout requires DC 15 Athletics — a win earns 25 gp and 150 XP; a loss earns 5 gp and the permanent affectionate nickname "Drowned One" among Fiskmark locals.
- **The Weirdwood Market** — *Chipping-Gong · 1 hour · 100 XP.* Exclusively Weirdwood goods, priced 50% above standard. Items have a 1-in-20 chance of being mildly sentient. Carpenter's Tools or Woodcarver's Tools proficiency allows a DC 12 appraisal check to haggle down the premium.
- **The Amber Vaults** — *Gullborg, visible from outside · 0 XP.* Clearly visible through the anomaly — doors open, coin untouched, attendants frozen. Thieves have tried. None returned. Crystal Scholars offer 500 gp for a single intact ledger page as proof of a viable new method to breach the anomaly.

#### Guilds of Eveltoft

Each district of Eveltoft has a guild that player characters may join. Membership grants a mechanical benefit in addition to social and narrative access.

- **The Rift Wardens' Compact** *(Central District)* — A joint body of Crystal Scholar volunteers and City Hall officials who monitor the Rift and coordinate emergency response to Rift Reverberations. They maintain exclusive access to the nullification engine rooms and the only official log of portal activity. *Benefit: Gain proficiency in Arcana (expertise if already proficient). Once per long rest, spend 1 minute attuning to local Rift energy — for the next hour you sense the presence and direction of any active portal or Weird Zone within 300 feet.*
- **The Weirdwood Wrights** *(Chipping-Gong)* — Master craftspeople and foresters who have made a trade of Weirdwood's unpredictability. The Wrights are the first call whenever a structure in Chipping-Gong misbehaves — which is increasingly often. *Benefit: Gain proficiency with Carpenter's Tools. Once per long rest, spend 1 minute touching any wooden structure or object to learn one piece of its history — its last owner, a significant event, or whether it has been altered by Weirding energy.*
- **The Shifting Bazaar Consortium** *(Dogun)* — An informal network of merchants and astral-goods dealers who profit from Dogun's chaos, sharing intelligence on vanishing stalls, transforming wares, and the locations of overnight astral vendors. *Benefit: Advantage on Persuasion checks in marketplaces and trade negotiations. Once per day, when you fail a Deception or Persuasion check during a commercial exchange, immediately reroll it and take the higher result.*
- **The Tidebound Fellowship** *(Fiskmark)* — A brotherhood of fishermen, maritime traders, and Utfordring competitors united by the sea and the increasingly strange things that come out of it. The cumulative effect of Fiskmark's Weirded seafood has left all members with subtle aquatic affinities they can no longer fully explain. *Benefit: Gain proficiency with water vehicles and Survival checks near bodies of water. Once per long rest, consuming a piece of Fiskmark's strange seafood grants you the ability to breathe underwater for 1 hour.*
- **The Ironveil Order** *(Heibury)* — Eveltoft's military elite, overseeing the district's shifting training grounds and its Weirded arsenal. Membership requires surviving a sparring session on ground that will not stay still. *Benefit: Once per short rest, when a creature hits you with an attack, use your reaction to reduce the damage by 1d10 + your proficiency bonus. You must be wearing medium or heavy armour.*
- **The Amber Circle** *(Gullborg)* — Financiers and agents who operate from outside Gullborg's frozen borders, keeping the district's business interests alive while funding research into breaking the anomaly — and profiting handsomely from the uncertainty in the meantime. *Benefit: Your guild connections generate 10 gp per week in passive income. Advantage on Intelligence (History) checks and Intelligence-based checks to appraise the monetary or magical value of an object.*
- **The Veil Tenders** *(Kieferden)* — Healers and herbalists who harvest Kieferden's strange medicinal plants and tend the Ferden Pool, walking a careful line between legitimate wellness practice and the cult activity spreading through the district's hidden groves. *Benefit: Gain proficiency with an Herbalism Kit. Once per long rest, spend 10 minutes applying Veil Tender techniques to a willing creature, removing one level of exhaustion. Cannot remove exhaustion caused by magical compulsion or curse.*

## Dollow Canyon

Dollow Canyon
A Verdant Weird
Dollow Canyon, stretching between Mt. Bannockwyrm and Benard Peak, is an
anomaly in Ryndor's otherwise cool and rugged landscape. While much of the
surrounding region is defined by volcanic rock and harsh winds, Dollow Canyon bursts
with jungle overgrowth, a lush and humid paradise where nature thrives unchecked.
Warm air currents funnel into the canyon, making it one of the warmest places in

Ryndor, where tropical flora and fauna have flourished unnaturally. Yet, beneath its
vibrant beauty, the effects of the Weirding make this jungle treacherous—a place where
life grows too fast, and the rules of nature twist unpredictably.
A Jungle That Defies Time and Logic
The jungle of Dollow Canyon is a living maze. Paths open one day and close the
next under walls of vines and flowering canopies. Plants bloom, wither, and regrow
within hours, creating a surreal rhythm of life and decay that challenges both memory
and navigation. Some adventurers speak of entire groves of trees that migrate through
the canyon, forcing travelers to rely on instinct and luck to find their way. Fruit trees
bear strange, luminous fruit that grants unusual effects—visions of the future or bursts
of strength—but sometimes exact a hidden toll in return, such as sudden fatigue or
strange compulsions.
The Weirding makes the jungle even more dangerous. Some plants exhibit
behaviors that mimic animals, while animals take on plant-like qualities, such as vines
that lash out like serpents or beetles that root themselves into the soil like weeds. Time
passes strangely here—**what seems like a day within the canyon might only be
moments outside**, and some explorers return with memories of events they cannot
explain, as if they experienced multiple timelines within a single journey.
The Creatures of Dollow Canyon
The creatures of Dollow Canyon are equally unusual, their biology warped by the
Weirding. Gigantic predatory plants, such as flytraps the size of carriages, lurk in the
undergrowth, their glowing tendrils exuding a hypnotic scent. Insect swarms shimmer
with iridescent wings, shifting colors as they move, and serpents with bioluminescent
scales weave through the jungle’s branches, casting eerie patterns of light in the
twilight beneath the canopy.
Perhaps the most dangerous inhabitants are the jungle trolls, twisted by time and
magic. These creatures are cunning and fast, capable of blending into the environment
with chameleon-like skin. Some trolls seem to exist outside the normal flow of time,
blinking in and out of reality or appearing in multiple places at once. The Weirding has
made these trolls nearly impossible to predict or fight—they seem to learn from future
encounters, making them deadlier with each confrontation.
A Tropical Oasis for the Bold and the Foolish
Despite its dangers, Dollow Canyon attracts both scholars and treasure hunters
eager to unlock the secrets of the jungle. Rare herbs and plants with powerful medicinal
properties grow only here, including flowers that glow under moonlight and mosses
that heal wounds instantly—though some claim these plants come at a hidden cost.
Potions brewed from Dollow’s plants are said to grant immense power or strange
dreams, but prolonged use can blur the lines between reality and hallucination, leaving
the drinker untethered from time.
Travelers seeking hidden ruins within the canyon hope to discover remnants of
ancient civilizations or artifacts affected by the Weirding. However, finding such
treasures is no small feat—many who enter the canyon become hopelessly lost within
the shifting jungle or fall prey to the predatory life forms that thrive within it.

## An Ever-Changing Labyrinth

The environment within Dollow Canyon shifts so frequently that it is almost
impossible to map. New rivers appear overnight, flowing through the jungle only to dry
up the next morning. Waterfalls cascade from seemingly nowhere, only to vanish as
quickly as they arrive. The heat and humidity are oppressive, causing illusions and
mirages that blend with the Weirding’s natural effects.
Those who enter the canyon must rely on their instincts, for even the most
detailed maps become obsolete within hours. Some say the jungle is alive, responding to
the thoughts and emotions of those within it. Paths seem to open for those with pure
intentions, while others close off abruptly for travelers whose hearts are weighed down
by greed or fear.
A Risk for the Brave, a Trap for the Unwary
The lure of wealth and mystery draws many into Dollow Canyon, but only a few
emerge unscathed. Some return with treasures or strange plants in hand, but others
come back with fractured minds, speaking of visions they saw in the jungle’s depths—
visions of futures that may never come to pass, or encounters with creatures that
seemed to know them before they had even met.
Despite the dangers, the canyon has become a pilgrimage site for Sev'rinn
mystics and adventurers, who believe that surviving its challenges brings
enlightenment and strength. However, many are lost within the jungle, their stories
swallowed by the ever-changing wilderness. Jungle paths close behind them, and the
forest forgets.
Dollow Canyon stands as a paradox—**a place of life, yet filled with death; a
realm of beauty, but home to terror**. Those who dare to venture into its depths must
tread carefully, for here, even the plants have memories, and time itself seems to play
tricks on the mind. Will you find the treasures you seek—or become just another lost
soul among the verdant maze, swallowed by the tangled grip of the Weirding?

### DM Tools — Dollow Canyon

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | Time slips outward. The party emerges from the canyon to find several hours have passed in the outside world — enough to miss a meeting, lose daylight, or alarm anyone waiting for them. |
| 3–4 | A path seals itself. A wall of dense vines grows across the route ahead within seconds. Hacking through requires ten minutes and a DC 13 Athletics check, or the party must backtrack. |
| 5–6 | A plant blooms, withers, and regrows directly underfoot within one minute. Any character in the affected area must succeed on a DC 12 Dexterity save or be restrained until the start of their next turn. |
| 7–8 | The canyon responds to intent. One character carrying stolen goods, harbouring a secret betrayal, or acting under false pretences finds their path closing while companions' paths open. The DM chooses who and need not explain why. |
| 9–10 | Hypnotic spore cloud. A flytrap-sized plant releases golden pollen. All characters within 20 feet must succeed on a DC 14 Constitution save or be charmed for 1 minute — convinced the canyon is safe and beautiful, unwilling to leave or take hostile actions. |
| 11–12 | A new river appears. An entirely new waterway cuts across the party's path, knee-deep and fast-moving. Crossing requires a DC 11 Athletics check; failure sweeps the character 30 feet downstream. |
| 13–14 | Bioluminescent cascade. The serpents in the canopy illuminate simultaneously, bathing the party in eerie blue-green light for one minute. Stealth checks are made with disadvantage during this time. |
| 15–16 | A jungle troll blinks into reality beside the party for one round — aware, watchful, and clearly evaluating them — before vanishing again. Whether it acts on what it observed is the DM's decision. |
| 17–18 | Healing moss erupts underfoot. A patch of the rare instant-heal moss blooms beneath one character's feet. They regain 1d8 hit points — then the moss withers to dust within seconds. |
| 19–20 | The canyon opens. A clear, straight path appears through otherwise impenetrable undergrowth, leading directly toward the party's destination. It remains open for one hour before the jungle reclaims it. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Flytrap Ambush.** A carriage-sized predatory plant conceals itself as a flowering clearing. Characters must succeed on a DC 14 Wisdom save upon entering or spend their first action moving closer. The plant attacks when a character is within 10 feet. Burning the root cluster (AC 12, 30 HP, vulnerability to fire) collapses the trap.
- **The Troll That Learns.** A time-Weirded jungle troll has encountered the party before — in a future they haven't lived yet. It anticipates one character's fighting style and opens with a perfect counter, adapting in real time. Defeating it requires improvisation.
- **Lost Herbalist.** A potion-maker has been wandering the canyon for what they believe was two days — context clues suggest far longer. They carry half-finished notes on three rare plants and are beginning to hallucinate. Getting them out safely requires navigating at least two Weirdings without losing them to another time slip.
- **The Iridescent Swarm.** A vast swarm of Weirded insects descends, drawn to magical energy. Any active spell effect or magical item attracts them; they begin dismantling enchantments. The party must extinguish their magical signature or outrun the swarm before items are temporarily drained.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **On Foot Through the Canyon Floor (variable).** DC 12 Survival each hour; failure loses the path and adds 1d4 hours. A character with Nature proficiency can assist, granting advantage.
- 🌿 **Following the Canopy Line (faster, exposed).** Aviari or climbers move through the upper canopy, bypassing sealed ground paths — travel time halved. Each hour requires a DC 11 Perception check to avoid disturbing a bioluminescent serpent nest.
- 🌊 **River Route (unreliable).** When a navigable river exists — which changes day to day — following it downstream is fast and clear. Roll a d6 at the start of each hour: on a 1 the river vanishes or reverses, forcing the party ashore.
- 🧪 **Herbalist's Guide (reliable).** A local potion-maker or Dollow regular who knows the canyon's rhythms can lead the party without triggering path closures. DC 13 Investigation in the nearest settlement to find one; they charge 5 gp per day.
- ✨ **Magical Transit (unreliable).** Teleportation within the canyon requires a DC 16 spellcasting ability check. On a failure, the caster and all targets arrive at a random location within the canyon chosen by the DM.

#### Landmarks

- **The Flytrap Grove** — *2 hours · 150 XP.* A cluster of carriage-sized predatory plants occupying a wide clearing thick with golden hypnotic spores (DC 14 Constitution save on entry). Between the plants, half-digested gear from previous victims yields a potion of growth and a waterproof satchel worth 40 gp — DC 13 Perception to spot.
- **The Moonbloom Field** — *3 hours · 100 XP.* A rare open patch of glowing moonbloom flowers. DC 13 Nature and thirty minutes of careful work yields enough material for two potions of healing. Failing the check by 5 or more triggers confusion (as the spell) for 1 minute.
- **The Vanishing Falls** — *4 hours · 200 XP.* A waterfall that appears and disappears on no discernible schedule. When present, immersion for one minute in its pool restores 2d6 hit points from the healing moss on every submerged stone.
- **The Troll's Clearing** — *5 hours · 250 XP.* A wide, suspiciously clear area littered with objects the time-Weirded troll has collected from future encounters — items that won't exist for weeks, belonging to people who haven't arrived yet. A DC 15 Arcana or History check can identify one and infer its implied origin.
- **The Old Cartographer's Camp** — *1 hour · 100 XP.* The ruins of a surveyor who tried and failed to map Dollow Canyon. Dozens of contradictory maps pin a rotting frame. DC 14 History (twenty minutes of study) extracts the approximate location of one landmark of the DM's choosing, valid for the next 24 hours.

## Hurstwold Forest

Hurstwold Forest
Deep, dark mysteries in the trees
Hurstwold Forest has long been a place of legend, but the Weirding has twisted its
mysteries into something far more perilous. The forest itself seems only half tethered to
the material world. Trails appear and disappear at will, leading travelers in circles for
days or dropping them into places they never intended to visit. What was once a
beautiful and mystical woodland has become a place where the boundary between
reality and dream flickers and folds—and where those without pure intentions risk
more than just getting lost.
Dense trees loom overhead, their trunks seemingly breathing with strange
patterns of light and shadow, as if absorbing the Weirding's influence. The air is heavy
with a cool, shifting mist that dampens both sound and senses, making it impossible to
know how far one has traveled—or whether they are still within the same moment they
began. Moss glows faintly underfoot, shifting colors in response to emotions or

thoughts, as though it is alive and aware. This eerie, sentient landscape confounds even
experienced travelers.
A Home for Warped Beings
The magical creatures that once called Hurstwold home—**faeries, sprites, and
unicorns**—have been irrevocably altered by the Weirding. Some have become
fragmented versions of themselves, flickering in and out of existence as though trapped
between realities. Others are more powerful and unpredictable, their behavior now far
more dangerous. Faeries weave illusions of past lives or alternate futures, confusing
travelers into making deals that bind their souls. Sprites appear as doppelgängers of lost
loved ones, luring wanderers deeper into the forest's ever-changing heart.
More troubling are the new creatures birthed from the Weirding’s touch—twisted
forms of animals and beings that defy classification. Some are harmless and strange,
like a fox with eyes that glow like stars. Others are incredibly dangerous, such as
shadow-stags whose antlers seem to absorb light and energy, draining the life force of
those who stand too close.
The Heart of Hurstwold: A Grove Lost to Time
At the heart of the forest lies the legendary sorcerer’s grove, though the Weirding
has altered its reality beyond recognition. The sorcerer’s grove, once rumored to hold a
portal to any place in the world, is now said to be a doorway to nowhere and everywhere
—a place where those who step through disappear from all known realms, their fates
left to drift across the multiverse.
Those few who claim to have reached the grove tell incoherent tales of swirling
stars and endless voids—or offer visions of strange, otherworldly cities built upon
impossible architecture. It is rumored that only those with pure intentions may still
reach the grove’s center, but the definition of "pure" has become dangerously fluid
under the Weirding’s influence.
Traps and Curses of the Forest
The Weirding has twisted more than the creatures of Hurstwold; it has also
altered the very terrain. Paths once navigable by locals now shift without warning,
dropping travelers into deadly pitfalls or endless mazes of thorny brambles. Some areas
are rumored to loop time infinitely, leaving wanderers to experience the same moments
over and over—until they slowly lose their grip on reality.
Those who stray too far from the known trails may encounter malevolent spirits
warped by the forest’s strange energies. These specters are believed to be the remnants
of lost souls who fell victim to the Weirding’s pull, forever trapped in fractured
moments of fear and regret. Locals warn that to meet your reflection in the forest is a
terrible omen, as it means that the forest intends to keep you—and leave your true self
behind.
Living in Harmony with Chaos
Despite its dangers, some creatures and beings have adapted to the new reality of
Hurstwold Forest. Witches, druids, and renegade Sev’rinns have taken refuge deep

within its heart, learning to bend the Weirding’s effects to their will. These practitioners
of ancient magic embrace the chaotic nature of the forest, wielding the strange currents
of time and space like tools. They live in hidden enclaves, their communities cloaked in
illusions that only the truly initiated can see through.
Even so, life here is precarious. The witches speak in riddles, claiming that the
forest whispers truths from futures that may never come. Some villagers on the
outskirts of the Hurstwold believe these witches can grant visions of other timelines—
but at a steep price: memories, years of life, or even names.
Locals who know the forest well have adapted simple customs to avoid its worst
traps. They carry charms carved from Hurstwold wood and leave offerings to the forest
spirits to ensure safe passage. These offerings often consist of candles or personal
tokens, placed at the entrances of the forest. Without such rituals, even a short journey
can result in a lifetime of wandering through warped realities.

### DM Tools — Hurstwold Forest

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | The trail loops. The party walks for an hour only to return to their starting point. DC 14 Survival to break the loop; each failure costs another hour. Leaving a personal offering before attempting grants advantage. |
| 3–4 | The moss turns red beneath one character's feet — the forest responding to a fear or guilt they carry. The DM chooses who and what it reflects. That character has disadvantage on Wisdom saving throws for the next hour. |
| 5–6 | A faerie weaves an illusion of an alternate future. DC 13 Wisdom save or the character is stunned until the end of their next turn, unable to look away. |
| 7–8 | A sprite takes the face of one character's deceased or absent loved one and beckons them deeper. DC 14 Insight to recognise the deception; on a failure the character must be physically restrained or they move toward it on their next turn. |
| 9–10 | A shadow-stag crosses the path. Its antlers leach light, dropping the area into magical darkness in a 15-foot radius for 1 minute. Any character who ends their turn in the darkness takes 1d6 necrotic damage. |
| 11–12 | The trunks breathe. A low rhythmic pulse moves through every tree in sight. All Perception and Investigation checks are made with disadvantage for the next 10 minutes. |
| 13–14 | The threshold requires a toll. A ring of moss and burned-down candles blocks the path ahead. Any character who crosses without leaving something personally valued is silently deposited 100 feet back with no memory of crossing. |
| 15–16 | The mist thickens. Visibility drops to 10 feet for 10 minutes — darkvision does not penetrate it. Separated characters must succeed on DC 12 Perception each minute or lose track of the group entirely. |
| 17–18 | A Weirded unicorn appears, its form stuttering between solid and translucent. It regards the party for one round, then vanishes. Any character of demonstrably pure intent gains advantage on their next Charisma check made within Hurstwold. |
| 19–20 | The grove points the way. For one hour the moss on the north-facing side of every tree glows brighter than usual, creating a navigational guide. No Survival checks are required for forest travel during this window. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Faerie's Bargain.** A faerie offers something the party genuinely needs — directions, a lost item, information about the sorcerer's grove. The price sounds reasonable. DC 15 Insight reveals a secondary clause: the faerie has worded it to claim a soul, an undefined future favour, or a memory the character cannot name until it is gone. Negotiation is possible; refusing outright makes the faerie hostile.
- **The Doppelgänger Sprint.** Sprites simultaneously take the forms of loved ones belonging to different party members, beckoning each in a different direction. Resolution requires either a group DC 13 Insight check to see through all illusions at once, or tracking down and confronting each sprite individually.
- **Shadow-Stag at the Waterhole.** A shadow-stag stands over a wounded traveller. It is not feeding — it appears to be guarding. Its darkness aura makes close approach dangerous (1d6 necrotic per round). DC 14 Animal Handling reveals the traveller struck it first and the stag is waiting for an apology it cannot ask for.
- **The Witch's Price.** A witch who has made Hurstwold her home offers shelter, healing, and directions. Her price is always small and specific — a childhood memory, the sound of a particular laugh, the ability to recall a certain face. What she takes is gone permanently.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **On Foot (unreliable).** DC 13 Survival each hour. On a failure the trail loops or deposits the party somewhere unintended — add 1d4 hours. Leaving an offering at the forest entrance grants advantage on the first check.
- 🕯️ **The Offering Path (one guaranteed passage).** A traveller who leaves something genuinely valued — not coin, something personal — at the forest threshold is permitted one unimpeded passage through Hurstwold. This works once per person; the forest remembers.
- 🧚 **Faerie Escort (fast, binding).** A faerie guide halves travel time but will propose a deal. The DM should prepare the terms carefully — the faerie honours the letter of any agreement, not the spirit.
- 🌿 **Druid or Witch Guide (reliable).** Finding one requires DC 14 Investigation at the forest edge or prior knowledge. They ask for nothing immediately — but they will remember the favour.
- 🦅 **Above the Canopy (partial).** Aviari or mounted flyers can navigate by landmarks above the treeline, avoiding trail-based Weirdings. The forest's mist rises above the canopy at night, removing this advantage entirely after dusk.

#### Landmarks

- **The Sorcerer's Grove** — *6 hours · 400 XP.* The legendary doorway to nowhere and everywhere, deep in Hurstwold's heart. Stepping through is one-way. Spells cast in the grove are maximised, but saving throws against them are also made with advantage. DC 17 Arcana (one hour of study without entering) yields one fact about a specific plane of the DM's choosing.
- **The Offering Gate** — *30 min · 75 XP.* The forest threshold hung with burned candle stubs, knotted ribbon, and carved tokens. Leaving an offering before entering grants advantage on the first Survival check inside. Taking any existing offering triggers an immediate hostile reaction from the nearest Weirded creature.
- **The Whispering Moss Hollow** — *3 hours · 175 XP.* A depression blanketed in glowing moss that responds to thought and emotion. Ten minutes of stillness and a DC 13 Wisdom check receives a genuine fragment — a truth, a clue, or a warning. On a failure, the same fragment arrives but the character cannot trust whether it is real or a faerie's invention.
- **The Shadow-Stag's Waterhole** — *4 hours · 200 XP.* A clear pool where the water reflects the forest as it was before the Weirding — ordinary trees, daylight, familiar stars. Drinking from it (DC 14 Constitution save) either clears one condition affecting the character or triggers a vision of Hurstwold as it once was.
- **The Witch's Refuge** — *5 hours · 150 XP.* An impossibly tidy cottage that should not exist this deep in the forest. The witch serves tea that removes one level of exhaustion and bread that tastes like whatever the eater is most homesick for. Her collection of taken memories fills dozens of small glass vials on the shelves. Her price is named after the party has accepted her hospitality.

## Innerstifla Sound

Innerstifla Sound
A Rift-Touched Passage
The Innerstifla Sound, separating Leighmore from the ancient Hurstwold Forest
and the coastal town of Norwycke, has become a place of unpredictable beauty and
danger, deeply influenced by the Weirding. Named for the ice that once reliably coated
its surface in winter, the sound now shifts unpredictably between frozen stillness and
turbulent chaos, as though time itself ebbs and flows through its waters. According to
ancient legend, the great frost giant Hrimnir carved the sound with his enchanted staff,
smashing the ice to open a deep channel. Now, the strange forces unleashed by the Rift
to Nebernoria have warped both the waters and the creatures that inhabit them,
creating a place where reality is never quite stable.
Waters in Flux
The waters of Innerstifla pulse with unpredictable energies—at times calm and
crystalline, reflecting the heavens above, and at others boiling with strange currents
that seem to defy the natural laws. Ice forms overnight even in summer, only to crack
and melt within moments. Sailors navigating the sound describe encounters with
phantom storms that appear and vanish within minutes, leaving behind strange debris
—**barnacled artifacts and bones not of this world**. Occasionally, entire stretches of
the sound become mirrors of other places or timelines, revealing alternate versions of
the ships that sail them, or showing glimpses of Nebernoria’s shimmering astral
waters.
The Creatures of Innerstifla Sound
The magical creatures that once called Innerstifla Sound home have been
profoundly altered by the Weirding.
- Mermaids, once beautiful but perilous guardians of the sound, have become
twisted by the strange energies. Their songs now echo across time, creating eerie
harmonies that seem to linger in the minds of those who hear them, even after they

leave the water. Those who listen too long may find themselves unable to distinguish
between dreams and reality. Some say that these mermaids phase between worlds,
slipping between Ryndor and Nebernoria, and that their voices are fragments of lost
souls drifting across dimensions.
- The sea serpents, already feared by sailors, have become even more monstrous.
Their scales shimmer unnaturally, shifting in hue with the light and leaking strange
phosphorescence into the water. Some serpents appear impossibly large, as though
their bodies stretch into another plane, their eyes flickering with the eerie glow of astral
fire. Sailors tell tales of serpents emerging from nowhere, vanishing in the blink of an
eye, and entire ships swallowed by the strange folds of reality that surround these
beasts.
Navigating the Sound: Peril and Profit
Though the Innerstifla Sound is fraught with danger, it remains an essential trade
route between Leighmore, Norwycke, and the Hurstwold. Brave merchants and sailors
still traverse the sound, though few return without tales of the strange happenings they
encountered along the way. Some traders have reported cargoes inexplicably altered
mid-journey—barrels of wine turned to saltwater, or fish caught in the net transformed
into stone. Others swear that the journey takes longer than it should, as if time stretches
and warps within the sound’s waters.
The most daring captains seek to profit from the Weirding’s influence. Certain
weirded artifacts and rare astral materials have surfaced from the depths, valuable to
collectors and scholars alike. Yet every expedition into the sound carries immense risk
—some sailors return marked by the experience, claiming to have seen themselves
from another timeline, or insisting that something unseen followed them back to shore.
A Rift Below the Waters
The Crystal Scholars suspect that the sound is connected to a submerged rift, a
secondary faultline leading to Nebernoria. Faint currents of astral magic weave through
the water, disrupting the natural rhythms of the sea and creating anomalies that even
the most experienced navigators struggle to explain. Scholars have detected pockets of
slowed time beneath the surface, where objects and creatures become frozen for years
or even decades before re-emerging. Some abandoned ships drift silently beneath the
water, their crews long gone, preserved as ghostly remnants of an earlier age.
Strangely, the currents beneath the sound seem to respond to emotion. Those
who sail the waters in fear often encounter hallucinations or temporal echoes, as
though the sound draws from their anxieties to manifest illusory threats. Others report
feelings of profound déjà vu, as if they’ve sailed these waters in another life—or are
doomed to sail them again.
A Place Caught Between Worlds
The Innerstifla Sound is more than just a dangerous stretch of water—it is a
liminal space, balanced between Ryndor and the astral plane. Every journey across it
carries the risk of crossing into another reality, or of becoming lost in time’s

unpredictable currents. Those who return from the sound speak of impossible things—
**familiar landmarks that shift**, strange lights that flicker beneath the water, and the
eerie feeling of being watched by something just out of sight.
Despite the risks, the people of Leighmore and Norwycke depend on the sound for
their livelihood, and the Fishermen’s Guild continues to organize regular crossings. The
Keepers of the Rift maintain a watchful presence along the shores, fearing that the
influence of the Rift could spread further if the sound is not kept under control. Yet even
they admit that the waters are unpredictable, and that one day, something too large to
contain may rise from its depths.
Sailing the Shifting Waters
The Innerstifla Sound has become a place where fortunes are won and lost in the
blink of an eye. Sailors, smugglers, and adventurers alike are drawn to its eerie beauty,
hoping to glimpse something extraordinary beneath its shifting surface. But every
voyage comes with the knowledge that the sea does not forgive easily, and that those
who dare to sail these strange waters may find themselves caught between realities,
with no way home.
For those brave enough to attempt the crossing, the sound offers both peril and
possibility, a glimpse into a world where nothing is certain, and even the stars may not
shine as they should.

### DM Tools — Innerstifla Sound

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | Ice forms without warning. Water around the vessel freezes solid, halting all movement for 1d6 minutes. Anything dropped overboard during that window is locked beneath it. |
| 3–4 | A phantom storm erupts from clear sky and lasts exactly three minutes before vanishing. Barnacled artifacts and otherworldly bones rain down. Roll a d6: on a 5–6, one item is genuinely useful (DM's choice). |
| 5–6 | A stretch of the water turns reflective as glass, showing the party's vessel in a different timeline — same hull, different crew, different damage. The mirror lasts one minute. |
| 7–8 | A mermaid's song reaches the vessel. DC 14 Wisdom save or carry a fragment of the melody for 24 hours — disadvantage on Perception checks as attention keeps drifting toward it. |
| 9–10 | A sea serpent surfaces nearby. Its phosphorescent scales suppress any magic item within 30 feet for 1 minute (items only, as *antimagic field*). The serpent dives again after two rounds. |
| 11–12 | The submerged rift pulses. Characters in contact with the vessel must succeed on a DC 12 Constitution save or take 1d8 psychic damage from a flash of Nebernorian imagery. |
| 13–14 | Time reverses locally. The vessel is pushed 300 feet back along its own wake — exactly where it was three minutes ago. No damage, no warning; only position changes. |
| 15–16 | A barnacled artifact rises and bobs against the hull. It radiates faint magic (Arcana DC 13 to identify the school). Its actual function is the DM's to determine. |
| 17–18 | The ice sings. A sheet of ice forms briefly and produces a clear, resonant tone before shattering. A DC 14 Arcana check identifies the note as identical to frequencies recorded near the main Rift in Eveltoft. |
| 19–20 | The waters calm completely. For the next two hours, the sound is glassy and still — no Weirdings, no serpents, no phantom weather. The Fishermen's Guild pays 10 gp for advance notice of when these windows occur. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Mirrored Ship.** The party's vessel encounters its own timeline reflection sailing the opposite heading. If they communicate, they learn something about where their current course leads. Boarding the reflection (DC 15 Arcana to stabilise the crossing) gives ten minutes before it dissolves.
- **The Mermaid's Warning.** A mermaid sings directly at the vessel — not a lure, but an alert. DC 15 Arcana or DC 16 Insight to translate fully: the submerged rift is destabilising and something has started moving toward the surface. One hour until it arrives.
- **Serpent at the Trade Lane.** A Weirded sea serpent has coiled around the primary crossing lane, suppressing all magic within its aura. Three Guild vessels are stranded. The Guild offers 150 gp to move it — but it cannot be killed without triggering a Rift pulse, as the Keepers of the Rift will make emphatically clear.
- **Keepers' Recruitment.** A Keepers patrol vessel intercepts the party, having observed their reaction to a Weirding. They offer information, safe passage, and a retainer — in exchange for a single unspecified favour to be called in later.

#### Travel Options

- ⛵ **Fishermen's Guild Crossing (standard, organised).** Regular crossings timed around known calm windows. 2 gp per person. Guild crews are experienced with Weirdings but are not fighters; their contracts do not cover serpent encounters.
- 🧊 **Ice Bridge (rare, temporary).** When the sound freezes over completely, the ice is thick enough to walk across in under an hour. A DC 12 Nature check at the shore determines whether it will hold for the full crossing.
- 🌊 **Private Vessel (faster, unescorted).** Skips the Guild schedule but means no experienced Weirding crew. Each hour requires a DC 11 Water Vehicles check; failure triggers a random Weirding.
- 🔱 **Mermaid Escort (fast, conditional).** A mermaid who trusts the party can guide a vessel across in half the normal time, steering clear of active rift zones. They will not escort anyone they judge to be acting against the sound's interests.
- 🦅 **Aerial Crossing (safest).** Avoids all water-based Weirdings. Phantom storms still affect aerial travellers — DC 12 Acrobatics check to stay on course if one erupts mid-crossing.

#### Landmarks

- **The Rift Faultline** — *Open water · 300 XP.* The suspected submerged secondary rift, marked on Keepers charts with a red cross. Diving within 30 feet and succeeding on a DC 16 Arcana check confirms the rift's existence and estimates its stability — information the Crystal Scholars pay 100 gp to receive.
- **The Debris Shelf** — *Shore of Norwycke · 1 hour · 150 XP.* A stretch of shore where phantom storms deposit otherworldly debris regularly. Locals leave it alone. DC 13 Investigation over one hour recovers one barnacled artifact that always radiates detectable magic.
- **The Mirror Stretch** — *Mid-crossing · 200 XP.* A section roughly a mile from Leighmore's shore where timeline reflections occur most frequently. DC 14 Arcana (ten minutes of study) extracts one piece of information about an alternate version of events relevant to something the party is pursuing.
- **The Keepers' Watch Station** — *Leighmore shore · 30 min · 75 XP.* A fortified stone post maintaining the most complete log of Weirding activity on the water. The station holds two sending stones linked to the Eveltoft chapter house — the Keepers will loan one to a party they trust.
- **The Serpent's Coil** — *Open water · 250 XP.* A semi-permanent formation of churned water and phosphorescent foam where a Weirded serpent rests near the surface. Approaching within 60 feet reveals the serpent phases partially into another plane on each breath. A DC 15 Arcana check suggests it is being slowly pulled through the faultline and may not survive the week.

## Inverlinn Coast

Inverlinn Coast
The Volcanic Lands
The southeastern coast of Ryndor, known as Inverlinn, is a desolate volcanic
expanse, a place where fire and earth meet in perpetual unrest. Its name, drawn from
the ancient Nordica words for fire and mountain, perfectly reflects the volatile
landscape—a region shaped by eruptions, lava flows, and seismic upheaval. Long ago,
the Nordica people believed that powerful spirits and magical forces dwelled within
these mountains, and rituals to appease and harness their power were performed under
the shadow of the Great Volcano. Today, with the spread of the Weirding, the ancient
energies of Inverlinn have become even more unstable, transforming the region into a
place of chaotic magic and unpredictable danger.
A Land of Fire, Magic, and Mutation
Inverlinn remains largely abandoned, with only a few small, reclusive
communities scattered across the volcanic coast. Those who live here are hardy
survivalists, using ancestral magic and newfound Weirded abilities to endure the harsh
environment. Magma drakes, fire elementals, and lava spiders still stalk the craggy
terrain, but these creatures, too, have changed—**fused with strange energies** from
the Weirding. Some lava spiders spin webs that shimmer like starlight, while fire
elementals pulse erratically, their flames flickering with colors unseen in ordinary fire.
Locals report sightings of phantom beasts—creatures that shift in and out of existence,
leaving no trace but scorched footprints and an uneasy hum in the air.

Even the volcanoes themselves seem affected. Some erupt with no warning, while
others that have been dormant for centuries now rumble with strange patterns, as if
alive and listening. Occasionally, magma rivers twist into impossible shapes, flowing
uphill or spiraling into glowing whirlpools. The air above the volcanic craters
sometimes shimmers with an ethereal mirage, reflecting visions of other realms or
alternate futures, though it’s impossible to say if these sights are real or illusions born
of the Weirding.
The Magic of the Inverlinn People
The people of Inverlinn possess unique magical abilities, shaped both by their
ancient traditions and the strange energies of the Weirding. It is said that those born
under the shadow of the volcanoes inherit elemental magic—their blood infused with
the power of flame and stone. However, these abilities come with a heavy cost, as
overuse of magic in Inverlinn can awaken dormant anomalies in the landscape, causing
time distortions, cracks in reality, or wild magical storms. Local practitioners have
learned to balance their magic carefully, using just enough to survive without triggering
disastrous changes.
Rumors spread of individuals who have embraced the Weirding, gaining powerful
but unstable abilities. These mages, known as Ashborn, are said to channel both fire and
astral energy, becoming living conduits for the chaotic magic of the land. However, they
are also feared, for their power often draws dangerous anomalies—rifts that open
suddenly, unleashing creatures from other realms or causing matter to dissolve and
reform unpredictably.
A Haven for Scholars and Adventurers
Despite the risks and strangeness, the Inverlinn Coast draws adventurers and
scholars from across Ryndor, eager to unlock its mysteries. The Great Volcano, long
thought to contain ancient relics or forgotten knowledge, has become a subject of
fascination, though few who enter its depths return unchanged. Those who survive
speak of chambers filled with glowing obsidian, fire spirits whispering ancient
prophecies, and pools of magma that reflect not the present but distant futures or
alternate possibilities.
Even the ruins of ancient Nordica temples, scattered across the coast, offer only
cryptic clues. Some temples appear to shift locations, defying all attempts to map them,
while others reveal new chambers overnight, as if awakened by unseen forces. Scholars
seeking to study these ruins must navigate both the volatile terrain and the
unpredictable magic, all while avoiding the creatures that lurk in the shadows, their
forms twisted by the Weirding.
Life in Inverlinn: Thriving on the Edge of Chaos
For those who choose to live in Inverlinn, life is harsh, but resilience is woven
into their very bones. The small communities scattered across the volcanic coast rely on
agriculture, hunting, and magic to survive, though even the crops behave strangely.
Some plants grow hot to the touch, while others emit faint glows under moonlight, and

a few release clouds of ash-like spores that cause vivid, prophetic dreams. Rituals to
maintain harmony with the land are performed regularly, though even these customs
have begun to evolve under the Weirding’s influence.
Visitors are welcome in these isolated communities, but they are expected to
respect the old ways and honor the spirits of the land. Outsiders often struggle to
understand the delicate balance that the locals maintain—one misstep could disrupt the
tenuous harmony, inviting disaster or awakening dormant threats. The people of
Inverlinn may be few in number, but they possess a deep understanding of the forces
around them, both magical and mundane. Community bonds are strong, and each
member plays a vital role in ensuring the survival of their neighbors.
A Land of Mystery, Danger, and Opportunity
Inverlinn remains a place of great mystery and wonder, but now it is also a land of
unpredictable chaos. Adventurers seeking glory are drawn to the coast, hoping to
discover lost relics or new forms of magic, but many return only with fragmented
memories—or not at all. Scholars come hoping to unravel the secrets of the Weirding,
only to find that the land resists easy understanding. The magma flows shift, the
creatures mutate, and the Great Volcano rumbles with ancient intent, as if it holds
knowledge not meant to be uncovered.
For those bold enough to venture into Inverlinn, each step is a gamble. The
Weirding makes no promises, and what one finds beneath the ashen skies and glowing
