rivers may be treasure or torment. Yet, despite the dangers, the allure of discovery
persists, and those who understand the balance between risk and reward may find their
greatest opportunities waiting within the fire and shadow of Inverlinn.

### DM Tools — Inverlinn Coast

#### Weirdings (d20)

| d20 | Effect |
|-----|--------|
| 1–2 | An eruption without warning. Every character within 60 feet must succeed on a DC 13 Dexterity save or take 2d6 fire damage from ejected rock and ash. The vent goes quiet within one minute. |
| 3–4 | Magma flows uphill. A lava river reverses course and climbs a slope, cutting off the party's route. They have two rounds to cross before the channel is impassable for ten minutes. |
| 5–6 | A fire elemental pulses erratically through colours never seen in ordinary fire — violet, white, deep blue. A DC 12 Arcana check identifies one hue as Nebernorian in origin. |
| 7–8 | Starlight webs. A lava spider's shimmering web drops across the path. Contact deals 1d4 psychic damage and briefly fills the character's mind with images of deep space. |
| 9–10 | A phantom beast passes through. Scorched footprints appear beside the party — visible and audible, but belonging to nothing present. The hum it leaves behind lasts one minute. |
| 11–12 | The volcano listens. A low rhythmic vibration rolls through the ground. Every character in contact with the earth succeeds on a DC 11 Wisdom save or feels certain something vast and ancient is aware of their presence. |
| 13–14 | Magma spirals into a glowing whirlpool for thirty seconds. A DC 13 Arcana check reveals a shape at its centre corresponding to a symbol found elsewhere in Ryndor's history — the DM decides which. |
| 15–16 | A magma drake circles overhead, its Weirded state causing erratic flight. It will not attack unless provoked, but each round it remains there is a 1-in-6 chance it loses control and dives. |
| 17–18 | Ash memory. A volcanic ash cloud drifts through the party. DC 12 Constitution save or experience a thirty-second vivid hallucination of a Nordica ritual performed at this exact location, possibly centuries ago. |
| 19–20 | The spirits are appeased. The ground steadies, lava slows, and the hum drops to silence for one hour. Weirdings do not occur during this window and native creatures are non-hostile. |

#### Encounter Ideas

- **The Fused Drake.** A magma drake partially incorporeal from the Weirding — its attacks pass through armour on a 19–20. A DC 14 Arcana check reveals the Weirding energy can be disrupted by targeting the violet seam along its spine.
- **The Reclusive Community.** A settlement refuses to evacuate before an imminent eruption, insisting the correct ritual will protect them. The ritual requires components scattered across three dangerous locations and they are too few to gather them in time.
- **The Lost Relic Seeker.** An adventurer returns from the Great Volcano alive but non-verbal, with fragmented memories and a relic they cannot describe finding. It radiates unstable Weirding energy. They will not release it voluntarily.
- **Spirit Appeasement.** A Nordica descendant community hires the party to perform a ritual at a volcano vent. The ritual is real — but the Weirding has altered the spirits' expectations. Each step goes slightly wrong, requiring improvisation (Arcana DC 13, Religion DC 12, or Performance DC 14) without breaking the sequence.

#### Travel Options

- 🥾 **Overland Through the Lava Fields (slow, hazardous).** DC 13 Survival check each hour. On a failure, a new lava flow forces a detour — add 1 hour. Failure by 5 or more leads into a Weirding encounter.
- 🏘️ **Guided by Locals (reliable).** Reclusive coastal communities guide travellers through safe corridors for 3 gp per day. They know lava flow patterns, creature territories, and which vents are due to erupt.
- ⛵ **Coastal Vessel (fast, exposed).** Avoids the lava fields but keeps the party within range of eruptions landing in the water — each creates a scalding steam burst (DC 12 Dexterity save, 1d6 fire damage) in a 30-foot radius. Roll for eruptions once per hour.
- 🦅 **Aerial (fastest, drake risk).** Clears the terrain entirely. Each hour of aerial travel has a 1-in-6 chance of attracting a Weirded magma drake, which will pursue beyond the coast's edge.
- ✨ **Magical Transit (unreliable).** Volcanic Weirding energy interferes with teleportation. DC 15 spellcasting ability check; on a failure the caster and targets arrive at a random location in the lava fields.

#### Landmarks

- **The Great Volcano** — *2 days · 400 XP.* The dominant peak of Inverlinn, deeply changed by the Weirding. Each hour inside requires a DC 14 Constitution save or gain one level of exhaustion. Characters who reach the lower chambers find Nordica inscriptions — DC 15 History reveals a piece of Ryndor's pre-Weirding past the DM has held in reserve.
- **The Nordica Ritual Site** — *6 hours · 200 XP.* A ring of blackened standing stones on a stable plateau. The Weirding has made the site active again. A ten-minute ritual and DC 13 Religion check grants the effects of a short rest and advantage on saving throws against fire damage for 24 hours.
- **The Starlight Web Warren** — *8 hours · 250 XP.* A network of lava tubes colonised by Weirded lava spiders whose webs are worth 50 gp a strand to the right collector. Harvesting one (DC 13 Sleight of Hand) risks psychic contact with the spider's consciousness — 1d6 psychic damage on a failure. Three previous collectors are desiccated here.
- **The Magma Whirlpool** — *4 hours · 175 XP.* A self-sustaining Weirding loop where magma spirals indefinitely. A DC 14 Arcana check confirms it is stable magical energy. Disrupting it releases a burst of raw magical force equivalent to a *fireball* centred on the whirlpool.
- **The Phantom Footprint Trail** — *3 hours · 150 XP.* A line of scorched footprints — always fresh, never accumulating — crossing a stretch of cooled black rock near the coast. Following it (DC 12 Survival each hour) leads toward the Great Volcano. A DC 15 Arcana check at the origin detects a recurring Weirding signature: something passes here on a consistent schedule that no one has yet identified.

## Isles of Holmea

Holmea
The Misty Island
Off the northeastern coast of Ryndor, beneath the shadow of the Bannockwyrm
Mountains, lies the floating island of Holmea, now suspended within a powerful Weird
Zone. Once a formidable stronghold of the Sev’rinn Rebellion, Holmea now drifts
through swirling mist above violent fjords. This strange elevation, a side effect of the
Weirding, has made the island even more remote and enigmatic.
The Sev’rinn Council, formed after their victory over the Ullac Regime, governs
magic from Holmea, where they established a prestigious school of magic to teach
young practitioners to harness their abilities responsibly. The island’s natural defenses,
bolstered by enchantments and now affected by unstable magical currents, have made
it an ideal sanctuary for magical beings and creatures, offering them protection from
persecution.
Holmea also harbors a vast preserve for magical creatures, managed by skilled
Sev’rinns to ensure their survival amidst the Weirding’s chaotic influence. Strange
mutations among the fauna are closely monitored, as the creatures respond to the
island’s shifting energy.
Holmea has become more than just a school or preserve—it is a symbol of

resilience and hope for those marginalized for their magical gifts. Though floating
adrift in an ever-changing Weird Zone, its community thrives, offering refuge and
inspiration to those seeking a place where magic is not just accepted, but celebrated.
The island’s influence radiates across Ryndor, and its people remain among the most
respected and powerful figures in the realm.
Life on Holmea
Life on the floating island of Holmea is as mystical as it is unpredictable, with its
elevation suspended by the chaotic forces of a powerful Weird Zone. The constant mist
that shrouds the island deepens the sense of mystery, shifting with astral energies that
make navigation treacherous. Holmea’s natural defenses—enhanced by enchantments
and strange anomalies—protect its thriving community of magical beings and
practitioners, creating a sanctuary where magic is not only celebrated but protected
from persecution.
The Sev’rinn Council governs magic across Ryndor from Holmea, maintaining
balance despite the unpredictable effects of the Weirding. Their prestigious school of
magic, one of the finest in the region, draws young magical beings eager to master their
abilities. Yet, even the students and Sev’rinn masters are not immune to the Weirding’s
influence—**spells behave unpredictably**, and the school must constantly adapt its
teaching to account for the strange new properties of Primordial Resonance.
The island’s preserve for magical creatures, managed by skilled Sev’rinns, has
also been affected by the Weirding. Creatures mutate, gaining new abilities or exhibiting
odd behavior patterns, and habitats twist into unfamiliar shapes. The Sev’rinn
caretakers work tirelessly to understand and mitigate these changes, ensuring the
preserve remains a safe haven amid growing instability.
Life on Holmea requires self-sufficiency and cooperation. The isolation caused by
its floating elevation forces its inhabitants to rely on one another, with resources
carefully managed to ensure prosperity. Navigating the mist and shifting landscapes
poses challenges for visitors and residents alike—many have become lost in its depths,
their paths twisted by astral interference.
Despite these difficulties, Holmea remains a beacon of hope, knowledge, and
sanctuary, where magic is protected and practiced freely. It stands as a symbol of
resilience, proving that even in an era reshaped by the Weirding, unity, adaptability,
and wisdom can forge a path forward.

## Lake Polshaw

Lake Polshaw
A Cradle of the Weirding
Lake Polshaw is a place where the influence of The Weirding is palpable, warping
reality and bending nature in unsettling ways. The lake’s dark waters are said to reach
unfathomable depths, appearing as a reflection of nothingness, as if the world itself
stops beneath its surface. Strange currents swirl unpredictably, and at times, entire
sections of the lake shift position, leaving familiar landmarks displaced. The eerie
silence is only interrupted by the discordant cries of twisted ravens with too many

wings and serpent-like creatures that coil beneath the water, their forms flickering
between states of being.
The forest surrounding Lake Polshaw has mutated, its gnarled trees growing
inward toward the water, as if drawn by an unseen force. The trees appear to pulse
slowly, as if breathing, and their branches shift unnaturally, creating shadowy figures
that seem to stalk the lake’s edge. Strange, glowing fungi sprout intermittently,
releasing spores that float in still air, unmoved by the wind, leaving travelers with an
uneasy sense that they are being watched by something unseen.
The House on Stilts: An Echo of the Past
Suspended precariously over the shifting waters, an abandoned house still clings
to its rotting stilts—**a relic caught between worlds**. Locals claim that the house is
not always present, appearing and disappearing unpredictably. Sometimes, the
structure looks old and crumbling, other times, it is eerily pristine, as though
untouched by time. Time moves differently within the house, with visitors reporting
hours passing inside while only moments elapse outside, or vice versa.
Legends say that the family who once lived there was lost to an unknown curse
brought on by the lake’s strange energies. Their fate has become intertwined with
temporal echoes that loop endlessly, replaying fragments of memories through ghostly
apparitions that drift between moments. Those who enter the house might encounter
the family in various states of distress, as if pulled from different points in their final
moments, trapped in an eternal loop of despair.
Only a few have ventured inside and returned, each claiming to have seen
impossible reflections of their own future or past selves, or to have had conversations
with versions of people they have yet to meet. One survivor reported that every door in
the house opens into a different reality, some serene, others terrifying. The walls seem
to whisper riddles, as if the house itself is alive, eager to trap intruders in its tangled
web of timelines.
The Deep League’s Ambitions and the Weirded Waters
Despite its dangers, the League of the Deep has expressed interest in using Lake
Polshaw for the next Utfordring Championship, intrigued by the unique challenge posed
by the lake's unpredictable reality shifts. However, the proposal has sparked
controversy, as few believe it is possible to hold a fair competition in waters tainted by
the Weirding. Competitors could become trapped in time loops or fall through rifts into
other realms.
The League has begun experimental training sessions in the lake, though reports
from participating athletes are troubling—some claim to have swum for hours, only to
resurface back at the starting point as if they had never moved. Others report strange
encounters beneath the surface: glowing, fish-like creatures that vanish the moment
they are touched, and visions of alternate selves urging them to abandon the race.
A handful of athletes have refused to participate, citing nightmarish
hallucinations and missing memories that plague them after leaving the water. Yet, the
allure of such a unique playing field persists, and whispers among the elite teams

suggest that the League may already be developing weirded tactics to navigate the
lake’s strange currents and temporal distortions.

Mt. Bannockwyrm

Mt. Bannockwyrm
The Dragon Mount
Mt. Bannockwyrm stands as one of the most imposing and enigmatic landmarks
on Ryndor's northeastern coast, towering near the floating island of Holmea. Since the
onset of the Weirding, the mountain’s mysteries have deepened, and reality itself seems
to warp along its jagged cliffs and hidden trails. Time, space, and even magic twist in
unpredictable ways around the mountain, creating an atmosphere both exhilarating
and perilous.
The summit of Mt. Bannockwyrm, once thought to be unreachable, now
shimmers with strange currents of energy, making traditional navigation impossible.
Paths may lead travelers to places they never intended to go, while others seem to
vanish altogether, only to reappear days or even weeks later. The Weirding's influence
manifests in fluctuating weather patterns, where sudden thunderstorms or bursts of
freezing wind can occur without warning.
A Haven of Weirded Creatures
Mt. Bannockwyrm is home to many rare and mystical creatures—some native to
the mountain, others transformed by the Weirding’s unpredictable magic. Among them
is the Thunderbird, a storm-beast whose feathers crackle with lightning, now
appearing only when the Weirding currents align. Alpine Unicorns, once a rare sight,
now seem to exist in multiple places simultaneously—glitches in reality that make it
impossible to know whether you're encountering the same unicorn or several versions
of the same creature.
Deeper within the mountain, the fire elementals have become unstable, their
flames flickering between realities. It is said that a single elemental can appear in two
places at once, making them impossible to trap or fight. Wind Witches, believed to
control the region’s weather, have become something more—they now tap directly into
the Weirding itself, their powers unpredictable and terrifying. It is whispered that the
strongest among them no longer age, existing out of time and seeing visions of possible
futures.
The Labyrinth of Shifting Caverns
Mt. Bannockwyrm has always been a place of labyrinthine caves, where
smugglers and treasure hunters sought refuge. However, the Weirding has transformed
these passages into ever-changing corridors, where even seasoned explorers can lose
their way. Maps drawn within the caves are useless—passages twist back upon
themselves or lead to places that should not exist. Some areas appear frozen in time,
while others are ravaged by bursts of time dilation, where days pass in moments or
moments stretch into years.
Rumors persist that somewhere within the caves lies an ancient treasure hoard,

guarded not only by traps but by the unpredictable tides of the Weirding. Some
adventurers claim to have glimpsed phantom artifacts—objects that flicker in and out
of existence—suggesting that the treasures of the mountain may exist simultaneously
across multiple dimensions.
The Hidden Forces Within
Despite the Weirding’s chaos, some factions actively seek to harness the
mountain's untapped power. The Wind Witches, long believed to guard the summit, are
said to have formed pacts with astral entities beyond Nebernoria, using the Weirding to
strengthen their control over the elements. Nullification wards—powered by enchanted
springs within the caves—attempt to contain the worst of the Weirding’s effects,
though cracks in the wards suggest the containment is slowly failing.
Treasure hunters and smugglers still risk the caves, despite the warnings. Many
seek mythical relics from the early Sev'rinn rituals, believing they hold the key to
stabilizing the Weirding. Others seek forgotten weapons, hoping to use the mountain’s
unstable magic to gain an advantage in Ryndor’s dangerous political landscape. Some
whisper that the Custodians of Prosperity, housed in nearby Ban Mynydd, have already
begun secret experiments with artifacts retrieved from Bannockwyrm’s depths.
The Mountain of Possibilities—and Peril
Mt. Bannockwyrm is a place where reality bends to the will of magic, memory,
and myth. Every step on its winding paths is a step into the unknown—**a place where
treasure and ruin wait in equal measure**. The descendants of Runa’s children believe
the mountain is testing them, and those who survive its trials emerge changed, with
glimpses of futures yet to come.
Yet, for all its beauty and majesty, Mt. Bannockwyrm remains treacherous. Those
who climb its heights must be prepared to face twisting time, fractured realities, and
creatures born of magic and madness. For every adventurer who returns with tales of
strange wonders, another vanishes into the mountain’s depths, forgotten by the world
outside.
To climb Mt. Bannockwyrm is to embrace the Weirding fully, accepting the
uncertainty it brings. Whether brave, foolish, or desperate, all who seek the mountain's
secrets must confront a simple truth: nothing on Mt. Bannockwyrm stays the same for
long.

## Nebernoria

Nebernoria
Nebernoria, a strange and volatile realm within the astral plane, has always been
home to bizarre landscapes and mysterious beings. However, the advent of The
Weirding has disrupted both realms, creating mutual chaos that flows between Ryndor
and Nebernoria. As energy spills through the Rift, Ryndor’s reality fractures—but the
effects do not stop there. The Weirding has taken root within Nebernoria, altering its
creatures and shifting its landscapes even further.
Astral Constructs, already unstable beings formed from raw astral energy, now

mutate unpredictably, changing shape and nature in ways even the native entities
cannot anticipate. Some creatures exhibit behaviors never seen before—**hulking
beasts turn ephemeral without warning**, while formerly insubstantial beings become
aggressive, solid forms. Whole regions dissolve and reconstitute in entirely new shapes,
defying reason with each passing moment.
Crossing between Ryndor and Nebernoria has become more treacherous than
ever. The Keepers of the Rift, charged with safeguarding the portal, must now contend
with the unpredictable surges of The Weirding flowing both ways. As travelers step
through the Rift, they find themselves in constantly shifting environments where even
time cannot be trusted. Explorers returning from Nebernoria carry not just artifacts but
strange astral afflictions—some come back physically intact but mentally broken, while
others seem out of sync with reality, slipping between timelines.
The connection between the two realms has become a source of both power and
instability. While artifacts pulled from Nebernoria offer unimaginable potential, each
object risks spreading Weirding phenomena further into Ryndor. Adventurers seeking to
unlock the Rift’s secrets must navigate both the chaos of Nebernoria and the growing
instability of their own world, knowing that the Weirding flows in both directions—and
neither realm will ever be the same.

## Norwycke

Norwycke
Gateway to the Sea
The remote coastal town of Norwycke stands on the threshold between the
known and the unknowable, where the mystical Hurstwold Forest and the relentless sea
meet. Steep cliffs surround the small bay, and the rolling hills beyond hint at ancient
power. While life in Norwycke once followed predictable rhythms of fishing and
agriculture, The Weirding has rewritten the rules of existence here. Now, strange events
bleed through the cracks between worlds, complicating the town’s already rugged
lifestyle.
Though hardy and self-sufficient, the people of Norwycke now live on edge,
navigating temporal surges, strange visions, and twisted realities that arise without
warning. Visitors brave enough to explore the Hurstwold are warned of paths that shift
overnight and trails that loop back on themselves—or worse, disappear entirely,
trapping wanderers between moments.
Norwycke remains a paradox: a quiet town filled with echoes of things that never
were, where fishermen haul in impossible catches and farmers’ crops bloom out of
season or rot overnight. Even so, the community has learned to adapt to the
unpredictable nature of their home, welcoming those who respect their way of life, but
cautioning everyone that not all who come to Norwycke ever leave.
A Haunted History and Evolving Realities
Norwycke’s long history, steeped in the legends of Viking settlers and enchanted
forests, now bends under the weight of the Weirding’s influence. Locals say the town no
longer sits fully within one reality—**it drifts at the edges of time and space**,

occasionally pulling in fragments from distant worlds. The once-thriving market of
Norwycke has transformed into a surreal bazaar where objects age and un-age within
moments, and mysterious trinkets appear for sale without any memory of who placed
them there.
The Hurstwold Forest, long believed to be home to fairies, elves, and ancient
magical creatures, has changed dramatically. Trails flicker in and out of existence, and
travelers report seeing themselves walking ahead or behind on parallel paths. Pockets of
altered time flow within the forest, causing some adventurers to emerge years later
while believing only hours have passed. Others never return at all, or reappear strangely
changed—speaking languages no one recognizes or carrying artifacts from places that
exist only in dreams.
Life in a Weirded Town
Daily life in Norwycke has become a delicate dance between the familiar and the
unpredictable. The fishermen cast their nets knowing that some catches glow with
unnatural light, and crops are planted with the understanding that the seasons may not
follow. Temporal shifts ripple through the town, causing some days to stretch endlessly
while others vanish before noon. The locals have become accustomed to lost time and
strange visions—figures moving in reflections, or phantom animals stalking the forests
around them.
The townspeople are fiercely protective of each other, even more so in the face of
the Weirding’s strange influence. Community events have evolved into rituals of
grounding and protection, meant to anchor Norwycke to reality for as long as possible.
Town meetings serve not only to govern, but also to share sightings of strange
anomalies and offer support to those who have returned from time slips or strange
encounters in the forest.
Despite its unsettling environment, Norwycke's spirit endures. Fishing and
farming remain at the heart of daily life, though the harvests are often unpredictable,
and the waters of the bay hold secrets from other realities. For relaxation, the
townspeople gather at the local café, but many conversations drift to discussions of
strange phenomena and rumors of new Weirding pockets forming in the Hurstwold.
Outdoor activities such as hiking and fishing remain popular, though they carry a
higher risk—**venturing too deep into the woods or bay can mean slipping into an
alternate reality, or worse, never returning.**
Navigating the Unknown
While some visitors come to Norwycke in search of the beauty of the Hurstwold
Forest or the serenity of the coast, others arrive seeking answers about the Weirding’s
influence. Researchers, adventurers, and mystics are drawn to the town, hoping to
uncover its mysteries or harness the strange powers at work. The locals, however, warn
these outsiders: the Weirding does not follow mortal logic, and curiosity often leads to
ruin.
The town is also a hub for those fleeing other Weirded zones, offering temporary
refuge for those looking to escape the chaos elsewhere in Ryndor. But even here, safety

is relative—many who stay too long in Norwycke find it increasingly difficult to leave.
Some claim the town itself has grown sentient, deciding who may come and go,
trapping unlucky souls in its ever-shifting reality. Only a few have managed to escape
once the Weirding takes hold, though none emerge unchanged.

## Surreymouth

Surreymouth
The Current of the Isle
Surreymouth, once a thriving trade hub on the southern coast of Ryndor, now
stands transformed by The Weirding’s unpredictable influence. Though it remains the
center of commerce on the isle, the city’s fortunes rise and fall with the strange
phenomena that emanate from both The Rift to Nebernoria and the sea. Water travel is
still preferred over land routes, as the terrain warps unpredictably, storms appear
without warning, and strange beings emerge from places where they should not exist.
The Surreymouth Port Authority continues to oversee trade, managing both
legal commerce and fending off rampant black-market operations. However, The
Weirding has only emboldened criminal enterprises, as weirded artifacts, enchanted
cargo, and illicit goods slip between realms, complicating oversight. The city’s
underworld has flourished, with organized crime families adapting to the new reality,
taking advantage of the strange twists of fate that now define Surreymouth’s chaotic
landscape.
Life in a Weirded Port
The harbor is a kaleidoscope of strange vessels and altered ships—some
ordinary, others twisted by the Rift’s influence. Fishermen, merchants, and sailors
navigate waters that shift currents unnaturally, as entire ships have been known to
disappear for days and return as if no time had passed at all. Sailors whisper of strange
lights beneath the waves, silent voices that beckon from the deep, and phantom ships
appearing alongside real ones—ghostly copies that vanish before the break of dawn.
Even seasoned traders must prepare for the unexpected, as cargoes occasionally warp
or change mid-journey, arriving as completely different goods than when they were
loaded.
Despite the unpredictability, the bustling markets of Surreymouth remain
vibrant, offering goods both mundane and bizarre. Traders from across Ryndor still
flock to Surreymouth’s bustling quayside, where fishmongers sell strange, glowing
catches from the deep, and street vendors peddle weirded trinkets rumored to carry
curses or blessings. Merchants tread carefully, knowing that even innocuous
purchases might contain hidden magic or strange energies that follow buyers home.
The city's famous inns and taverns, once hubs of camaraderie, have also become
places of suspicion and intrigue. Whispers fill the air, and patrons exchange tales of
near misses with temporal echoes or eerie visions experienced at sea. Some travelers
report having spoken to future or past versions of themselves, leaving them deeply

unsettled. Bartering with time-warped merchants has become a new risk, as deals
made today might not come to fruition for years—or hours.
Port Authority in the Shadow of The Weirding
The Surreymouth Port Authority, once a beacon of structure and control,
struggles to maintain its grip on the city’s chaotic waters. Their attempts to monitor
trade have become fraught with strange incidents, as entire manifests rewrite
themselves during inspections, and customs officials are forced to navigate goods that
sometimes vanish only to reappear days later in another district. Their Coast Guard
patrols often encounter phantom ships or vessels caught in time loops, making piracy
more difficult to track.
Smuggling rings have adapted, using the cover of strange weather patterns and
disruptions caused by the Weirding to move illicit goods, including weirded artifacts
that are highly sought after in black markets across Ryndor. Corruption has grown
rampant, with some customs officers rumored to be trading in time-warped goods
themselves, profiting from the Rift’s influence. The organized crime families of
Surreymouth thrive under this new uncertainty, offering protection and predictability
to those willing to pay.
The Deep League: Utfordring’s New Frontier
The Deep League of Surreymouth, once renowned for its mastery of the aquatic
sport Utfordring, now finds itself in uncharted waters. Weirded phenomena affect the
competitions, as currents within the underwater arenas shift unpredictably, and
merfolk athletes experience temporal anomalies mid-game. Players sometimes
emerge from a match only to discover that days have passed above the surface. Though
the league has officially banned weirded artifacts and influence from the sport, rumors
persist of athletes dabbling with strange charms to gain an edge.
Spectators continue to flock to the matches, captivated by the unpredictability of
the Weirding’s influence. Each game is a gamble—not just for the players but also for
the fans, who might leave the arena to find entire seasons have passed while they
watched a single match. Some players, frustrated by the unpredictable disruptions,
have called for the Deep League to officially incorporate weirded elements into the
sport, believing that the chaotic nature of the Weirding represents the future of
Utfordring.
A City Suspended Between Realities
Surreymouth’s identity is now tied to the unpredictable pulse of the Rift and the
sea. Life in the city is defined by risk and reward—those who can navigate the twists of
fate stand to gain great wealth, but every venture carries the threat of being caught in a
loop or lost to the shifting tides of reality.
The port, the markets, and even the criminal underworld have all been shaped
by the Weirding, forcing the people of Surreymouth to adapt or perish. Time flows
strangely here, creating opportunities for the bold and leaving the unprepared
stranded. Fortune smiles briefly, and disaster strikes without warning, as the Rift and

the sea dance together in an unpredictable ballet of chaos.
Yet, through it all, the people of Surreymouth endure, drawn by the thrill of the
unknown and the promise of prosperity. For every trader that vanishes beneath the
waves, another arrives to take their place. In Surreymouth, the line between success
and ruin is as thin as a whisper—and every venture is a bet against the capricious
nature of the Weirding itself.

## Wenport

Wenport
The Seabreeze Harbor
The town of Wenport, perched along the rugged coastlines of Ryndor, is best
known for its fishing, shipping, and maritime charm. But in recent years, as the
influence of The Weirding spreads across the land, even this picturesque harbor town
has begun to experience strange phenomena. Wenport's small fleet of fishing boats
still ventures into the nearby seas, but the waters have grown increasingly
unpredictable. Fishermen speak in hushed tones of shifting currents, glowing
creatures, and fish that seem to shimmer with unnatural colors—and not all catches
are safe to eat anymore. Some say the sea remembers things it shouldn’t, and that
what comes from the depths now carries hints of ancient forces best left undisturbed.
At the heart of Wenport lies its picturesque harbor, where brightly colored
fishing boats bob on gentle waves, though some mornings, the water moves without
wind, as if pulled by unseen hands. The old lighthouse, long a beacon of safety for
sailors, now emits an occasional pulse of light that some claim reveals glimpses of
distant shores—or forgotten memories. Locals whisper that ships sometimes arrive
with no sign of their crews, the decks covered in salt-encrusted barnacles, though the
journey had only been a few days. Despite these unsettling events, the rhythm of life in
Wenport persists, the town adapting to the strangeness around it with the same
resilience and humor that has kept it afloat through storms and misfortune.
A Changing Port and New Tides
Wenport’s small port and warehouses remain essential hubs for shipping goods
between coastal towns, though trade routes have grown more erratic. Goods arrive in
unexpected quantities or disappear mid-journey, only to reappear days later—**damp
and untouched**. Some merchants swear their cargo was tampered with by ghostly
hands during transport, and odd trinkets—barnacle-covered coins, bits of driftwood
carved with incomprehensible symbols—sometimes find their way into shipments. A
few traders have begun avoiding Wenport altogether, worried that whatever touches
the port is marked by the Weirding.
Still, the fishing industry clings to tradition, and the local market bustles with
activity. Fishermen proudly sell their catches, though some now wear protective
charms—fishhooks twisted into spirals, believed to ward off the sea’s influence.
Travelers from neighboring towns and wandering merchants still pass through, and
Wenport benefits from taxes and fees, though there is a growing unease about what the
tides might carry next.

Even Wenport’s small tourist trade has taken on a new edge. Visitors arrive
drawn not only by the town’s charm but by rumors of strange happenings—they hope
to witness the strange lights of the lighthouse or catch sight of odd creatures lurking
beneath the water’s surface. The local artisans, though wary, now offer curious
trinkets inspired by the Weirding—pieces of driftwood shaped like ancient sea gods,
bottles filled with glowing sand, or paintings that shift slightly when no one is
watching.
Life in Wenport: Resilience Against the Unknown
Life in Wenport remains tight-knit, though the strangeness of the Weirding
presses at the edges of daily life. The townsfolk remain welcoming and warm, carrying
on their maritime traditions with pride, but the laughter at the local tavern is now
accompanied by furtive glances at the door. Fishing is still a way of life, but some
fishermen have begun marking their boats with runes, believing it keeps them safe
from whatever moves in the water now.
The annual Seabreeze Festival, once a simple celebration of the sea’s bounty, has
taken on new meaning. Some say it appeases whatever strange forces stir in the
water, though the festival remains joyful—**fishing competitions, boat races, and
seafood tastings** still draw crowds from far and wide. A new event has even emerged:
The Lantern Drift, where townspeople release glowing lanterns into the harbor, hoping
their lights will guide lost sailors or appease restless spirits.
The maritime museum now hosts strange artifacts found along the shore—
**driftwood with unfamiliar carvings**, pieces of barnacle-crusted jewelry, and
scraps of sailcloth from ships that never docked. Visitors to the town’s art gallery find
that some paintings seem to move subtly, shifting as though alive, their colors echoing
the strange lights beneath the waves. Life in Wenport remains simple yet uneasy, with
the townspeople determined to weather the changes—just as they’ve weathered every
storm before.
The Harbor on the Edge of the Unseen
While the people of Wenport continue their work, not everything is as it seems.
Ships sail into port carrying cargo from places no sailor remembers visiting, and some
fishing nets return empty, filled only with odd pieces of kelp that seem to whisper
when the wind blows through them. The lighthouse keeper, an elderly man who has
tended the light for decades, swears that something watches the town from the waves
—though whether it is protector or predator remains unclear.
The Weirding’s influence lingers just beneath the surface—in the water, the
waves, and the wind that blows through the cliffs. Some say the sea itself has become a
conduit for the Weirding, a reflection of unseen realms and forgotten stories. And yet,
the people of Wenport endure, welcoming travelers with hearty meals and open arms,
knowing that change is inevitable but determined to face it together. Here on the coast,
where sea and strangeness meet, the people of Wenport stand ready to ride the tides of
the unknown, just as they have always done.

## Wulfricton

The Traveller’s Rest
The last stop before ascending the hilltops to Eveltoft, Wulfricton lies nestled
within a valley surrounded by rolling hills and dense, whispering forests. Though the
town has stood for generations, The Weirding’s influence now flickers at its edges,
casting a shadow over its peaceful reputation. Named after Wulfric, the legendary
warrior who defended the town from invaders long ago, Wulfric’s Trading Post is still
the heart of the town, bustling with merchants, travelers, and craftsmen. However,
strange artifacts and odd trinkets—subtly affected by the Weirding—now circulate
through the market, tempting buyers with unpredictable potential.
The market hums with the familiar sound of bargaining and laughter, yet an
undercurrent of unease lingers in the air. Merchants murmur tales of shifting trade
routes—paths that move or vanish overnight, leading traders hopelessly astray. Some
swear that coins sometimes turn to dust or change into odd currencies after being
exchanged, leaving both buyers and sellers questioning what is real. Despite the
creeping strangeness, the people of Wulfricton are resilient, refusing to allow the
unpredictable world to disrupt their long-held traditions.
A Town in Transition
Wulfricton's central square remains the town’s focal point, where seasonal
festivals and celebrations continue as they always have. In the spring, ribbons and
flowers still adorn the streets to mark the renewal of life, but weird blooms—glowing
petals or plants that change color—have begun appearing among the usual decorations.
During the harvest season, the marketplace fills with bounties from the land, but some
crops behave strangely, sprouting far beyond their season or growing with unnatural
vigor. Farmers have reported wheat fields that seem to sing with ethereal voices under
moonlight, and harvesters have begun to wear protective charms to avoid attracting
unwanted attention from the Weird.
Craftsmen in the town continue to specialize in woodworking, metalworking,
and leatherworking, though their materials are not always what they seem. Wood from
nearby forests sometimes refuses to be carved, shifting its shape mid-project, and
metal ingots hum with strange resonance, requiring artisans to develop new
techniques to manage them. Despite these challenges, Wulfricton’s craftsmen have
embraced creativity and adaptability, making the town renowned for unique and finely
crafted goods—some of which carry subtle magical effects, even when unintended.
Life in Wulfricton: Enduring the Unknown
Though Wulfricton’s taverns and inns still serve hearty meals—stews, roasts,
and fresh bread baked with local ingredients—rumors of strange visitors traveling
through the hills have made their way into nightly conversations. Some travelers report
time shifts, arriving in town only to realize that days, or even weeks, have passed
without them noticing. Others claim to have seen ghostly figures—perhaps echoes of
past festivals or ancient travelers lost to time—lingering at the town's borders, just
beyond the firelight.

The people of Wulfricton have learned to live alongside these oddities, adopting
protective practices passed down through generations. Charms and wards hang over
doorways to guard homes against wandering spirits, and locals carry small stones
from the nearby streams, believing them to offer protection from the Weirding’s
effects. Life in Wulfricton remains simple and grounded, though even the oldest
families, whose roots run deep in the valley’s soil, acknowledge that the land is not the
same.
Community in the Shadow of Change
Despite the unpredictable world beyond their borders, the people of Wulfricton
maintain a strong sense of tradition and community. Families continue to share
stories passed down from generation to generation, though these tales have begun to
twist and evolve, reflecting the changing nature of the world. Long-time residents
warn travelers to stay vigilant, advising them to follow only familiar paths and avoid
wandering alone at dusk, when the boundaries between the real and the strange feel
thinnest.
The spirit of resilience that has always defined Wulfricton endures. The
townspeople take pride in their ability to adapt, meeting the challenges of the Weirding
with ingenuity and determination. They welcome travelers with the same warmth and
hospitality that has always defined the town, though a watchful eye follows every
stranger. Beneath the surface of laughter and merriment, there is an unspoken
understanding that change is inevitable—and that the quiet hills and forests
surrounding Wulfricton hold secrets waiting to awaken.
In Wulfricton, life continues much as it always has—though now, every step
forward feels like balancing on the edge of the unknown.

## Wyrmbost

Wyrmbost
Home of the Dragon Farms
Wyrmbost has always been a modest city compared to the bustling centers of
Eveltoft and Surreymouth, but its role within Ryndor is indispensable. Nestled at the
fringes of the Weirding’s growing influence, Wyrmbost is both shielded and touched
by the strange energies creeping across the land. It has existed under Eveltoft’s
protection since the days of Destin, thriving as the breeding ground for beasts and
magical creatures. Yet now, with the emergence of the Weirding, unpredictable
anomalies have begun to affect the animals, dragons, and crops that define life here.
Wyrmbost serves as the caretaker of native crops—one of the few places where
agriculture remains somewhat stable in Ryndor. However, the land is restless. Crops
sometimes shift color mid-season, growing with unsettling speed or twisting into
unfamiliar forms. Farmers tread cautiously, unsure whether their harvest will yield
bountiful food or strange, unrecognizable plants. Despite these oddities, the town’s
focus remains on its Dragon Farms, where miniature hybrid Fire Wyrms—favorites for
labor and protection in the mines of Ban Mynydd—are bred. Yet even the dragons are

not immune to the Weirding. Hatchlings have been known to flicker between shapes,
some breathing fire that burns cold, while others develop second pairs of wings that
disappear at dusk.
Breeders from Norwycke and Leighmore still arrive to retrieve bear cubs and
thick-haired horses, but they come with superstition and hesitation, wary of what
might have changed since their last visit. Some animals bred in Wyrmbost now display
unsettling behaviors, such as staring into space for hours or emitting sounds that
seem to echo from another place entirely. Visitors leave with their purchases but often
return whispering rumors that their beasts now dream strange dreams or vanish
briefly, only to reappear hours later without explanation.
The Dragon Farms
The Dragon Farms of Wyrmbost remain the town’s pride and joy, raising
dragons for companionship, protection, and work. The people of Wyrmbost have
always held a deep reverence for these creatures, viewing them not only as tools but as
sacred partners in their daily lives. However, the Weirding has complicated this longstanding relationship. Some dragons raised in Wyrmbost now absorb residual Weirding
energy, giving them unpredictable abilities. Hatchlings born under strange stars have
been known to vanish and reappear miles away, and others have shown signs of
sentience far beyond their years.
The people of Wyrmbost remain determined to care for their dragons, learning
new ways to manage their strange quirks. Some breeders now train their dragons to
respond to the changes in their nature, developing innovative techniques to harness
the unpredictability rather than fear it. A few dragons, touched by the Weirding, seem
to be able to navigate strange anomalies—walking through warped spaces or
temporarily resisting the pull of time distortions. Though these abilities are not fully
understood, the dragons are more than willing companions in the town's efforts to
thrive in uncertain times.
Life in Wyrmbost: Adapting to the Weirding
Daily life in Wyrmbost revolves around the Dragon Farms and seasonal
agriculture, though neither is as straightforward as it once was. Many families raise
personal dragons as companions and guardians, though some now display unsettling
behaviors—their eyes glowing faintly at night, or their fire leaving runes scorched into
the earth. These quirks are met with stoic acceptance, with the people of Wyrmbost
saying,
“Even the land must learn to dream differently now.”
Farmers continue to grow wheat, barley, and root vegetables, though they must
monitor their fields closely. Some crops sing strange lullabies under moonlight, while
others seem to resist being harvested—binding themselves to the soil as if unwilling to
leave. Harvesters wear charms and perform rituals to avoid upsetting whatever forces
now touch their land. In the face of these challenges, Wyrmbost’s people remain closeknit and grounded, finding strength in their traditions and relationships with the land
and their beasts.

Wyrmbost’s artisan community also endures, crafting handmade goods from

leather, fur, and wool—materials that have, on occasion, taken on odd properties.
Some items seem to shift subtly in shape or texture when left unattended, while others
hum with a low vibration, as if touched by an unseen force. These goods, despite their
oddities, remain highly valued in the markets of the four sister cities. Travelers passing
through Wyrmbost often stop to buy charms or enchanted accessories, hoping they
will offer protection from the Weirding’s influence.
Tradition and Resilience
Wyrmbost may not be as wealthy or influential as Eveltoft or Ban Mynydd, but it
thrives on its own terms. The main square, dominated by a statue of Destin, stands as
a reminder of the town’s proud history and enduring spirit. An ancient stone bridge,
still in use today, serves as both a landmark and symbol of Wyrmbost’s ability to
weather the changes brought by the Weirding. The people of Wyrmbost believe deeply
in the bond between themselves and their dragons, knowing that no matter how
strange the world becomes, they can adapt together.
Visitors to Wyrmbost are always welcome, but they are expected to respect the
town’s customs and acknowledge the partnership between beast and person that
defines life here. Travelers who underestimate the dragons or treat them merely as
tools soon find themselves unwelcome. The people of Wyrmbost are fiercely protective
of their way of life and have little patience for those who refuse to adapt to the new
reality.
A Future Forged in Strangeness
While the Weirding presents new challenges, it also offers unexpected
opportunities. Some breeders have begun experimenting with Weirded dragons,
exploring their unique abilities and how they might benefit the people of Ryndor. A few
visionaries in Wyrmbost believe the Weirding is not a curse, but a gift waiting to be
understood. However, these experiments remain carefully managed, as the town
recognizes that not every change should be embraced.
As the Weirding deepens its hold on Ryndor, Wyrmbost stands as a testament to
resilience in the face of uncertainty. Whether through dragonfire, clever
craftsmanship, or sheer determination, the people of Wyrmbost remain steadfast,
ready to face the future no matter how strange it may become. In this evolving
landscape, Wyrmbost will endure, knowing that even in the most unpredictable times,
the bond between person and dragon remains unbreakable.

## Unmapped Lands

The Unmapped Lands of Ryndor
Beyond the well-charted regions of Eveltoft, Ban Mynydd, and Holmea lies the
unmapped expanse of Ryndor—places so remote, dangerous, or transformed by the
Weirding that no mapmaker dares attempt to chart them. These lands are not just
unexplored; they seem to resist exploration entirely. What one explorer encounters may
never be seen by the next, as shifting landscapes and strange phenomena erase trails,

twist memories, or change the very nature of the terrain.
Traveling the unmapped lands is a perilous endeavor, for here the Weirding is
unchecked and unpredictable. Rifts to other realms open and close seemingly at
random, temporal loops trap wanderers, and new ecosystems bloom overnight. Some of
these regions appear placid and inviting, only to reveal themselves as illusory or
treacherous, while others teem with creatures born of chaos and magic, remnants of
the Rift to Nebernoria’s expanding influence.
What Lies Beyond?
The Unmapped Lands provoke endless speculation. Some say these places are
portals to forgotten civilizations, their knowledge locked away beneath ancient ruins.
Others believe that entire cities have been swallowed by the Weirding and now exist
only in fragmented moments, blinking in and out of reality. The strange rumors
include:
- Floating forests, islands of tangled roots and canopy that drift lazily across the
sky, untethered from the ground.
- Inverted cities—entire metropolises buried underground, only accessible when
the Weirding turns reality inside-out.
- Endless rivers, flowing in spirals and loops, where time moves slower as the
water rushes faster.
- Behemoths of unknown origin, creatures so large they appear as moving
landscapes, slowly traveling across the horizon.
Lost Expeditions and Forgotten Discoveries
Many expeditions have attempted to traverse these lands, but few return. Those
that do bring back fractured memories and strange artifacts, their accounts riddled
with contradictions. An explorer might swear to have encountered a tower that rose
from nowhere, only to discover upon revisiting the location that nothing remains but a
pool of water. Some tales speak of vast underground caverns, brimming with ancient
machines humming with arcane energy, or plants that whisper secrets to those who
listen closely enough.
The Sev’rinn Council has long maintained that the unmapped regions hold
forgotten ley lines, powerful sources of Primordial Resonance, but even their bravest
members are reluctant to delve too far. For every new discovery, there are whispered
warnings of phenomena too dangerous to confront—villages where the dead walk
alongside the living or valleys where gravity runs sideways, leaving travelers stranded
on invisible walls.
Legends of Lost Cities and Hidden Powers
Some claim that entire lost cities thrive within the unmapped expanse, their
people surviving in realms fractured by the Weirding. Rumors abound of a city of glass
that only appears under moonlight, and a fortress of stone that moves locations with
every new moon. Mythical beasts—dragons, hydras, and creatures from nightmares—
are said to roam these lands freely, warped by time and magic.
The Black Orchid, an elusive magical flower believed to grant unimaginable
power, is said to grow in a hidden valley beyond the reach of any map. Others claim that

a Nebernorian gate exists far within the unmapped regions, an unstable portal that
pulls entire landscapes into the astral plane, forever lost to the material world.
Navigating the Unmapped
For those determined to brave these unpredictable regions, navigation is a
maddening ordeal. Compasses spin wildly, paths shift from moment to moment, and
landmarks seem to appear and vanish at will. Travelers must rely on instinct, luck, and
perhaps even divinatory magic, for traditional tools and maps are utterly useless. Some
guides swear by magically charged stones or enchanted objects, which they believe can
sense areas of stability amidst the chaos.
Others place their trust in dreams and visions, believing that glimpses of the
unmapped regions can be found within the subconscious. This practice is fraught with
peril, however, as the Weirding seems to feed upon intention—the more you search for
something specific, the less likely it is to be found.
Warnings from Those Who Returned
Those few who have survived journeys through the unmapped regions often
emerge deeply changed. Some are aged beyond their years, while others return young
and vibrant but plagued by visions of futures that never happened. Many claim to have
lost parts of themselves—memories, emotions, or even their shadows—left behind in
places where time and reality blurred beyond recognition.
The Sev’rinn mystics warn that the unmapped lands are not merely wilderness
but places where the boundaries between worlds have unraveled, leaving all who enter
vulnerable to the strange tides of other realms and fragmented timelines. Whether
these are places where possibility reigns or where reality has come undone remains a
mystery—one that only the most daring adventurers might solve, though at great cost.
Adventuring in the Unmapped Lands
For those brave enough to explore these regions, the rewards can be immense—
but the risks are greater still. Magical artifacts of untold power, rare ingredients for the
most potent potions, and lost knowledge from ancient civilizations are just some of the
treasures rumored to lie hidden within the unmapped lands. Yet for every explorer who
returns with riches, countless others vanish without a trace.
Will you uncover the truth behind the legends of the unmapped lands? Will you
risk everything to find the lost cities and forgotten treasures? Or will you become
another story told around the fire—a warning to those who dream of taming the
unknown?
In the unmapped regions of Ryndor, nothing is certain. Reality shifts, paths
dissolve, and time itself becomes an unreliable guide. Here, even the bravest
adventurers are as likely to find madness as fortune. Will you risk stepping beyond the
edges of the map? And if you do, will you return whole—or at all?

# Notable Figures

Brun Furlow
Brun Furlow
Of Roots and Ruin, Episode 1: Weird Rumors
Medium humanoid (human), Neutral Good
Armor Class: 13 (leather armor)
Hit Points: 22 (4d8 + 4)
Speed: 30 ft.
Abilities
STR | 13 (+1)
DEX | 14 (+2)
CON | 12 (+1)
INT | 10 (+0)
WIS | 15 (+2)
CHA | 11 (+0)
Saving Throws: Dexterity +4, Wisdom +4
Skills: Perception +4, Survival +5, Vehicles (Water) +6
Tools: Navigator’s tools, Cartographer’s tools
Senses: Passive Perception 14
Languages: Common, Elvish
Traits
Experienced Navigator. Brun Furlow can’t get lost except by magical means.
When making checks related to navigating waterways, he has advantage.
Quick Reflexes. If Brun takes the Dodge action, he can move up to 10 feet without
provoking opportunity attacks.
Actions
Shortsword. Melee Weapon Attack: +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.
Hit: 6 (1d6 + 2) piercing damage.
Throw Net. Ranged Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, range 5/15 ft., one target.
Hit: The target is restrained. A creature can use its action to make a DC 10
Strength check, freeing itself or another creature within reach on a success.
Background & Personality
Brun Furlow is a seasoned boat captain who has spent most of his life navigating
the dangerous waters of the Innerstifla Sound. Practical, calm under pressure, and
fiercely protective of his crew, Brun has weathered countless storms and strange
encounters on the sound. He carries the stories of lost sailors and strange creatures of
the deep with a mix of reverence and humor. While not particularly flashy, Brun knows

how to get the job done—he values action over words and trusts his instincts over most
people.
Brun hides a soft heart beneath his gruff exterior, and those who earn his trust
will find a loyal ally. However, with rumors of strange phenomena growing on the
sound, even his resolve is beginning to waver.

## Ardella Lentris

Ardella Lentris
Of Roots and Ruin, Episode 1: Weird Rumors
Medium humanoid (half-elf), Lawful Neutral
Armor Class: 15 (studded leather armor)
Hit Points: 65 (10d8 + 20)
Speed: 30 ft.
STR DEX CON INT WIS CHA
12 (+1) 16 (+3) 14 (+2) 18 (+4) 15 (+2) 12 (+1)
Saving Throws: Int +7, Wis +5
Skills: Investigation +7, Animal Handling +5, Nature +7, Insight +5, Perception
+5
Senses: Darkvision 60 ft., Passive Perception 15
Languages: Common, Elvish, Draconic, Sylvan
Abilities & Traits
- Field Experience. Ardella can identify magical creatures and plants with a DC 12
Nature check. She also knows how to administer antidotes or stabilize creatures
poisoned by exotic flora or fauna.
- Calm Mind. Ardella has advantage on saving throws against being frightened or
charmed.
- Spellcasting. Ardella is a 5th-level spellcaster. Her spellcasting ability is
Intelligence (spell save DC 15, +7 to hit with spell attacks).
Spells Prepared (slots 4/3/2):
- Cantrips: Mending, Prestidigitation, Message
- 1st Level: Identify, Feather Fall, Cure Wounds
- 2nd Level: Lesser Restoration, Detect Thoughts
- 3rd Level: Dispel Magic
Actions
- Quarterstaff. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.
Hit: 6 (1d8 + 2) bludgeoning damage.
- Commanding Voice (Recharge 5-6). Ardella issues a firm order to a creature
she can see within 30 ft. It must succeed on a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw or follow the
command on its next turn (as the command spell).
Personality & Roleplay Notes

Ardella is methodical and calm under pressure, often serving as the voice of
reason in chaotic situations. She takes great pride in her role within the Society and sees
fieldwork as more than just a job—it is her calling. Ardella is respected for her wisdom
and experience but isn’t afraid to get her hands dirty when necessary. She is patient
with apprentices and expects professionalism from her colleagues.
Mannerisms:
- Adjusts her spectacles when thinking.
- Frequently takes notes on a small enchanted notebook.
- Speaks in precise, deliberate tones but softens when addressing creatures in
distress.

## Halric Emreth

Name: Halric Emreth
Of Roots and Ruin, Episode 1: Weird Rumors
Neutral, Medium Humanoid (any), Commoner
Armor Class: 12
Hit Points: 11 (2d8 + 2)
Speed: 30 ft.
STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA
10 (+0) | 15 (+2) | 12 (+1) | 11 (+0) | 14 (+2) | 13 (+1)
Skills
- Stealth +4
- Insight +4
- Deception +3
- Perception +2
Senses: Passive Perception 12
Languages: Common, Thieves’ Cant
Abilities
Observant and Paranoid. Halric has advantage on Insight checks to determine if
someone is lying.
Slip Away. Halric can take the Disengage or Dash action as a bonus action once
per short rest.
Sly Talker. Halric uses Deception to hide his true intentions and gathers
information while appearing harmless.
Actions
Dagger. Melee Weapon Attack: +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.
Hit: 4 (1d4 + 2) piercing damage.
Personality and Motivation
Halric is a suspicious and streetwise townsman, navigating the gray areas of
Norwycke’s social circles. He’s resourceful but not a fighter, relying on wit and stealth.

Halric discovered the Ullac connection when Feddel’s shipments didn’t align with the
rising green fungus incidents, and he’s been gathering clues ever since. Desperate to
find allies, he assumes the worst about strangers—especially anyone connected to the
salve supply—and only opens up if persuaded.
Halric is motivated by survival and exposing the suppliers before the fungus
overtakes the town. He’s not a hero but knows the streets well enough to assist the
party.

# The Reliquary

The world of Ryndor is home to an abundance of treasures, both common and
wondrous, that adventurers can discover during their travels. Some of these treasures
have been passed down through generations, while others were created by ancient
civilizations that no longer exist. Whatever their origin, these treasures hold great
power and value that can change the course of an adventurer's journey.
The treasures of Ryndor come in many forms - gold, gems, magical artifacts, and
more. Some of them are simply objects of beauty, while others have practical uses or
possess mystical properties. However, they all have one thing in common: they are
highly sought after by adventurers, treasure hunters, and villains alike. This chapter
will explore the many treasures that can be found in Ryndor, from the smallest trinkets
to the most powerful artifacts, and provide insights into their histories and significance
in the world of Ryndor.
## Magic Items
The world of Ryndor is filled with magic, and many of its ancient civilizations
have left behind powerful items that still hold mystical properties. These artifacts range
from simple trinkets to legendary weapons, each with its own unique history and power.
Adventurers who seek to uncover the secrets of Ryndor will find that magic items are
essential tools in their journeys. They provide aid in battle, protection from harm, and
even the ability to traverse great distances. However, these items are not easily found,
and many are fiercely guarded by powerful creatures and ancient guardians.
### Uncommon Items
These magical treasures are not as legendary as the artifacts of Ryndor, but they
are still highly sought after by adventurers and collectors alike. These items possess
unique properties and abilities that can give adventurers an edge in their journeys, or
unlock new paths to power. From enchanted weapons to magical trinkets, each of these
items has its own story and history, waiting to be discovered by those brave enough to
seek them out. In this section, we will explore a few of the many uncommon magic
items that can be found in the world of Ryndor.
#### Ichor of Runes
Uncommon Potion
This viscous, greenish liquid contains the essence of ancient runes, imbuing the
drinker with a powerful connection to magic.
Drinking the Ichor of Runes grants the following benefits for one hour:
- The drinker has advantage on all Intelligence (Arcana) checks.
- The drinker can cast one 1st-level spell of their choice that they do not have
prepared, using their spellcasting ability. Once this spell is cast, this feature can't be
used again until the next dawn.
Additionally, when the effects of the potion end, the drinker must succeed on a
DC 15 Constitution saving throw or suffer one level of exhaustion.
#### Spite Mantle
Uncommon item, requires attunement

The Spite Mantle is a cloak made of a black, rough fabric that seems to repel light.
When worn, the user gains resistance to necrotic damage.
Additionally, once per short rest, the user can use the cloak to cast the spell Hex
(save DC 14) on a creature they can see within 60 feet. The spell lasts for 1 hour or until
the target drops to 0 hit points.
Finally, while attuned to the Spite Mantle, the user has disadvantage on all
Wisdom (Insight) checks as the cloak seems to feed on negative emotions and thrives on
causing strife.
#### Jar of Invocation
Uncommon magical item
This small glass jar is filled with a swirling mist that seems to glow with an inner
light. When opened, the mist pours out and takes the form of a humanoid figure made of
pure energy.
While the figure is present, it can be commanded to perform a single task or
action, such as delivering a message or attacking an enemy. Once the task is completed,
the figure dissipates and the mist returns to the jar.
The jar can be used once per day, and the figure has a duration of 1 hour or until
the task is completed.
Properties:
- As an action, the jar can be opened to release the mist, which takes the form of a
humanoid figure made of pure energy.
- The figure can be commanded to perform a single task or action.
- The figure has a duration of 1 hour or until the task is completed.
- The jar can be used once per day.
Weight: 1 lb.
#### Azure Urn
Uncommon Item
This small azure-colored urn is made of a rare crystal and is adorned with
intricate silver engravings.
When the urn is filled with any type of liquid, the liquid will never spill, no matter
how the urn is tilted or shaken, and the urn will always remain cool to the touch.
Once per day, the urn can be used to cast the spell Purify Food and Drink on up to
one gallon of liquid inside.
#### Fruit of Nightmares
Uncommon item
The Fruit of Nightmares appears as an unassuming piece of fruit, resembling an
apple or pear, but with a sickly grayish-purple hue.
\pagebreakNum
Once consumed, however, the fruit transforms into a writhing, tentacled
creature, resembling something out of a Lovecraftian horror. This creature is loyal to its
consumer and will follow their commands to the best of its ability.
While the creature is alive inside the body of the consumer, the consumer gains
advantage on Intimidation checks. However, the creature has a limited lifespan and will

eventually dissolve into a sticky, acidic residue, leaving behind only the pit of the fruit.
The pit can be passed and then re-planted to produce more Fruit of Nightmares.
#### Neberbloom
Uncommon plant
This rare and valuable plant is known for its ability to absorb and store magical
energy. When consumed or used in alchemical concoctions, it can enhance the potency
of spells and imbue the user with magical power. However, due to the difficulty of
extracting and handling it, neberbloom is a highly prized and expensive commodity.
Effects:
When consumed, the user gains advantage on their next spell attack or spell save
DC.
When used in an alchemical concoction, the user can add an additional 1d4 to the
spell's damage or healing.
Neberbloom can be used to craft potions of magic absorption, which grant
temporary resistance to magic damage.
Drawbacks:
The extraction process is dangerous and requires specialized knowledge, with a
risk of failing and losing the plant's magical properties.
Overuse can lead to magical instability and unpredictable results, including wild
magic surges or spell failures.
Neberbloom is highly addictive, and prolonged use can lead to physical and
mental deterioration.
### Rare Items
The rare magic items of Ryndor are whispered about in hushed tones and legends
of their power have spread far and wide. These are items of immense power, coveted by
adventurers and rulers alike, and their histories are often shrouded in mystery and
danger. Only the most courageous and cunning of adventurers can hope to obtain these
treasures and unlock their full potential. From ancient artifacts to powerful relics, each
of these rare items holds immense power and potential. In this section, we will delve
into the world of rare magic items, and explore the stories and legends behind some of
the most powerful treasures in all of Ryndor.
#### Tranquility Feather
Rare magical item, requires attunement
This feather is a calming and peaceful presence, seemingly imbued with the
gentle breeze of the world. When held, the feather gives a feeling of serenity and
tranquility to the user.
While attuned to the Tranquility Feather, the user gains the following benefits:
- The user gains advantage on Wisdom (Insight) checks.
- The user gains resistance to psychic damage.
- The user can cast the spell Calm Emotions (without expending a spell slot) once
per long rest.
In addition, the Tranquility Feather has 3 charges. The user can spend 1 charge to
cast the spell Sleep (without expending a spell slot) targeting a single creature. The spell

has a range of 60 feet and does not require concentration. The spell does not affect
creatures with an Intelligence of 4 or less, constructs, or undead. The Tranquility
Feather regains all charges at dawn.
This rare magical item is often sought after by healers, diplomats, and anyone
who seeks peace and serenity in their lives. It is said that the feather was once owned by
a powerful druid who had the ability to calm even the wildest of beasts.
#### Insanity Mirror
Rare magical item, requires attunement
This small hand mirror has a silver frame and a polished obsidian surface. When
you gaze into it, you see your own reflection but with subtle distortions and shadows
that seem to flicker and twist unnaturally.
While attuned to the Insanity Mirror, you gain the following benefits:
Distorted Reflection When you take the Dodge action on your turn, you can
choose to shift your reflection into an alternate dimension, gaining partial concealment
until the start of your next turn. You have advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks and
gain resistance to non-magical damage from ranged attacks.
#### Invisible Box
Very Rare, artifact
This small, unassuming wooden box is completely invisible, even to detect magic
spells. It weighs 1 pound and measures 6 inches in length, 4 inches in width, and 2
inches in height. The Invisible Box has the following properties:
Invisibility. The Invisible Box is completely invisible and cannot be detected by
any means, including detect magic and true sight.
Storage Space. Despite its small size, the Invisible Box can store up to 100 pounds
of material, or up to 20 cubic feet of material.
Opening and Closing. To open or close the Invisible Box, the user must speak the
command word "Aethis" in Dwarvish. Once the command word is spoken, the Invisible
Box will become visible for 1 minute, allowing the user to open or close it. After 1
minute, it will become invisible again.
While the Invisible Box is a powerful item for storing and transporting valuable
items, its invisibility also makes it easy to lose or forget. Additionally, it cannot be used
to hide living creatures, as any creature inside the box will suffocate due to lack of air.
#### Nebernite
Wondrous item, rare
This rare, glowing blue mineral can only be found in the otherworldly realm of
Nebernoria. Nebernite is highly sought after by mages and enchanters for its powerful
magical properties. When properly attuned, it can enhance the abilities of magical items
and imbue them with additional enchantments.
While holding or wearing a magical item that is not already attuned to Nebernite,
you can spend 8 hours attuning it to
\pagebreakNum
this rare mineral. Once attuned, the magical item gains a +1 bonus to its magical
properties. Additionally, you can expend a spell slot of 2nd level or higher to imbue the

item with an additional enchantment of your choice from the following list:
Elemental Fury The item deals an additional 1d6 damage of a chosen elemental
type (acid, cold, fire, lightning, or thunder) on a hit.
Forceful Impact The item grants the wielder the ability to knock back an
opponent they hit with it. The target must make a Strength saving throw (DC = 8 + your
proficiency bonus + your spellcasting ability modifier) or be pushed back 10 feet.
Empowering Presence The item grants the wielder advantage on Charismabased checks and saving throws.
Once you have expended a spell slot to imbue the item, you cannot do so again
until the next dawn. Additionally, Nebernite attunement lasts for 30 days, after which it
fades and the item loses the bonus and additional enchantment.
### Legendary Items
The legendary magic items of Ryndor are the stuff of legends, whispered about in
awe and wonder by adventurers and common folk alike. These are items of unparalleled
power and enchantment, capable of feats beyond the imaginations of mortals. They are
objects of great beauty, imbued with arcane energies that sing through their every fiber.
Each wondrous item is unique and remarkable, bearing the stamp of the ancient
wizards and artisans who created them. In this section, we will explore the world of
wondrous magic items, and delve into the legends and stories behind these mystical
treasures.
#### The Everlasting Quill
Legendary, artifact
The Everlasting Quill is an ancient artifact with a gold and silver feathered body
and a nib made of a rare gemstone that constantly shimmers and changes color. The
quill is imbued with powerful magic that allows its user to create and manipulate reality
through the written word. Its ink never runs dry, and it is said that the quill has the
power to write the destiny of those who wield it.
Reality Shaping The user can use the Everlasting Quill to write new realities into
existence. This can include creating new creatures, objects, or even entire locations. The
effects of the writing are immediate and permanent, but the user must have a clear idea
of what they wish to create, as vague or incomplete ideas will not work.
Destiny Writing The quill has the power to write the destiny of a creature or
object. When the user writes the destiny of a creature or object, it becomes a selffulfilling prophecy, and the written destiny will come to pass. The user must be careful
with this power, as the destiny they write may not always be what they intend.
Ink of Power The ink used by the Everlasting Quill is infused with powerful
magic. The user can use the ink to cast spells, as long as they have the appropriate
components and the spell is written down.
Limited Use The Everlasting Quill has limited charges, and once its charges are
expended, it becomes a mundane quill until its charges are restored.
Cursed The Everlasting Quill is a powerful artifact, but it also comes with a
terrible curse. The user of the quill is forever bound to it, and their destiny becomes
entwined with that of the quill. The quill will always call to its user, and they will feel a

constant urge to write with it. If the user ever loses the quill or tries to destroy it, they
will suffer from terrible nightmares and visions until they are reunited with the quill.
Additionally, the quill will corrupt the user over time, slowly turning them into a being
of pure magic.
### Soulstone of the Ancients
Legendary Item, requires attunement
This small, polished stone emits a soft glow and seems to pulse with an
otherworldly energy. The Soulstone of the Ancients is said to contain the souls of
ancient and powerful beings from a time long forgotten.
While attuned to the Soulstone of the Ancients, the user gains the following
benefits:
- The user gains proficiency in Arcana and History if they don't already have it.
- The user can communicate telepathically with any creature within 60 feet of
them, as long as the creature understands a language.
- The user can cast one 9th-level spell of their choice once per day. The spell
must be a divination or enchantment spell and cannot be changed once chosen.
Additionally, the user can choose to release the souls within the Soulstone of the
Ancients to perform a powerful magical effect. Doing so requires the user to spend an
action and make a DC 25 Wisdom saving throw. On a success, the souls within the stone
are released, causing the following effects:
- All creatures within 60 feet of the user must make a DC 25 Wisdom saving
throw. On a failure, they are stunned for 1 minute.
- The user can cast one 9th-level spell of their choice as part of this action. The
spell must be a divination or enchantment spell and cannot be changed once chosen.
- The user's maximum hit points are doubled for 1 hour.
The souls within the Soulstone of the Ancients take time to recharge after being
released, and the user must wait 1 week before being able to use this effect again. If the
user dies while attuned to the Soulstone of the Ancients, their soul is absorbed into the
stone, and they cannot be resurrected by any means.

## Weirded Objects

Echo Flask
A silver drinking flask that whispers back whatever was last said around it.
- Effect: When a creature speaks within 10 feet of the flask, it records their words
and repeats them 1d6 minutes later in the same voice and tone.
- Quirk: It sometimes plays the whispers at unsettling times, like during stealth
missions or negotiations.
- Rumor: It’s said some echo flasks record words from past owners, causing
strange or cryptic messages to surface unexpectedly.
Lightless Lantern
A lantern that gives off complete darkness.
A black-iron lantern etched with spiraling, eye-like runes. When activated, the
glass panes seem to fill with inky, fluid shadow rather than light.

Effect: When lit, the lantern emits an aura of magical darkness in a 30-foot radius.
This darkness overrides non-magical light and prevents darkvision from
functioning within its area. Only effects such as see invisibility, truesight, or devil’s
sight allow vision through the lantern’s veil.
Quirk: The darkness subtly bends and flows around living creatures within it.
Observers outside the radius see brief glimpses of strange silhouettes that shouldn’t
be there—shapes that don’t match anyone inside.
Complication: The lantern affects memory—creatures who remain in its darkness
for more than 10 minutes must succeed on a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or forget
the last minute of conversation or movement made within the veil.
The Itchy Blanket
A perfectly ordinary wool blanket that causes a slight itching sensation, even when not
in use.
- Effect: When carried, the owner occasionally feels phantom itches and has a
compulsion to scratch. If used to sleep, the user gains no benefits from a short rest
unless they succeed on a DC 10 Constitution saving throw.
- Quirk: Washing the blanket does not remove the effect, and it always smells
faintly of wet wool.
- Weirding Twist: When someone else sleeps under the blanket within 10 feet of
the owner, both individuals will share each other’s dreams.
Endless Sock
A single, long sock that never seems to have a pair.
- Effect: When unfolded, it keeps extending until it becomes a 10-foot-long tube.
It always returns to its original size after 24 hours.
- Quirk: If torn or cut, the sock repairs itself overnight, albeit slightly
mismatched in color.
- Rumor: Some believe this sock can capture and imprison mischievous spirits by
turning them inside out within the tube.
Stone of Forgetting
A smooth river stone that causes momentary lapses in memory when held tightly.*
- Effect: If a creature holds the stone for more than a minute, they forget the last
1d6 minutes unless they succeed on a DC 12 Intelligence saving throw.
- Quirk: It’s often found in people’s pockets, with no memory of how it got there.
- Weirding Twist: The stone sometimes whispers fragments of lost memories to
its owner in moments of silence.
Weathered Map
A map that changes depending on the weather conditions.
- Effect: The locations depicted shift based on the current weather. For example,
towns only appear when it’s sunny, rivers move with rainfall, and roads vanish during
storms.
- Quirk: In areas affected by The Weirding, the map often displays impossible or

forgotten landmarks.
- Complication: Relying on this map for travel can be dangerous, as it may
mislead travelers into nonexistent locations.
Compass of Reluctance
A brass compass whose needle refuses to point north unless coerced.*
- Effect: The needle can only be made to point north if the owner hums a song for
at least 10 seconds. It sometimes insists on pointing to seemingly random locations
instead.
- Quirk: If placed near magical objects, the needle begins to vibrate violently.
- Weirding Twist: On rare occasions, the compass points toward places of
significance from its wielder’s past or dreams.
Raincap
A felt hat that drips water when worn, regardless of the weather.*
- Effect: The hat releases small drops of water every few seconds, as if soaked
