with sacred auras. Their unwavering faith and dedication make them formidable
defenders of their draconic heritage and the causes they hold dear.
#### Drakarim Traits
Ability Score Increase Your Strength score increases by 2, and your Charisma
score increases by 1.
Age Drakarim mature at the same rate as humans, but can live up to 120 years.
Alignment Drakarim tend to be strong-willed and individualistic, but their
alignment can vary widely depending on their upbringing and personal beliefs.
Size Drakarim are medium-sized creatures, standing between 6 and 7 feet tall
and weighing between 200 and 300 pounds.
Speed Your base walking speed is 30 feet.
Languages You can speak, read, and write Common and Drakarim.
Draconic Ancestry You have draconic ancestry. Choose one type of dragon from
the Draconic Ancestry table in the Player’s Handbook. You gain a breath weapon and
resistance to a damage type associated with your dragon ancestry.
Draconic Resistance You have resistance to the damage type associated with your
draconic ancestry.
Breath Weapon You can use your action to exhale destructive energy. Your
draconic ancestry determines the size, shape, and damage type of the exhalation. Once
you use your breath weapon, you can't use it again until you complete a short or long
rest.
Tail Swipe You can use your tail to make a melee attack against a creature within
5 feet of you. The attack deals 1d6 + your Strength modifier bludgeoning damage.
Khuzud
Khuzud
The Khuzud are an ancient and reclusive race of dwarves, born from a few
hundred individuals who rejected their kin's expansion to the surface and remained
deep within the earth. While all modern dwarves are descendants of the Khuzud,
modern dwarves bear little resemblance to their ancient ancestors. The Khuzud may be
rare among the dwarves, but their kingdoms are the most expansive, filled with ancient
halls and tunnels carved deep into the earth.
Khuzud Lore
When the Khuzud saw their people push further and further to the surface, a few

hundred stood apart in scornful distaste. They remained below, and became the ancient
ancestors of the Dwarves factions that split upon the surface.
The Ancient Folk. Direct descendants of the ancient Dwarves. All modern
Dwarves are descended from the Khuzud, but bear little to no resemblance to their
ancient ancestors. They are the smallest in population by far, but have the most
expansive kingdoms of all the Dwarves. Ancient, echoing halls built deep into the stone
of the deepest places, the kingdoms of the Khuzud are often empty for hundreds of
miles.
The Soul Forge
Modern dwarves like to say that their souls were birthed in the same ancient
forge in which the Khuzud now forge their finery and weapons. Dwarves life began
deep, in fact the deepest reaches of Onidor are the most ancient. When the first few
Dwarven souls sparked into existence, it was in pure darkness. It was the god Moradin
who sparked the Soul Forge, which flared to life and thus the Dwarves were birthed in
flame and shadow. Moradin, the Soul Forger knew not what creatures he just created,
but looked upon them with awe and admiration as they emerged from fire and rock.
With fresh awareness, contemplating awareness itself, they found each other. Sightless
as they were, the ancient Dwarves began to communicate through sound, and
discovered they could detect the world around them with an extra sense that was only
present when they clicked their tongues or tapped their limbs against the hard stone
surrounding them. Before the Dwarves had homes or names, they invented Inglishmek,
the echolocative sign language that is now used only by the lingering Khuzud.
As the Dwarves grew in number, they expanded their territory and began to delve
deeper into the earth, uncovering vast veins of precious metals and gems. It was during
this time that the Khuzud separated from their kin, choosing to remain in the deep,
dark places of the earth. They continued to develop their own unique culture and
society, utilizing their echolocation and Inglishmek to communicate and trade with
each other.
Despite their separation, the Khuzud remained a respected and revered faction
among the Dwarves. The ancient kingdoms they built, such as Milgalor, were
considered to be hallowed ground and were visited by Dwarves from all over the world.
The Khuzud were known for their unparalleled skill in metalworking, and their weapons
and armor were highly sought after by Dwarves and non-Dwarves alike.
Today, the Khuzud are a dwindling race, with their numbers far fewer than the
other Dwarven factions. However, their legacy lives on in the magnificent halls and
cities they left behind, as well as in the skilled craftsmanship that they passed down to
their descendants. To the Dwarves, the Khuzud are a reminder of their ancient past and
the depths from which they came.
Solitary Spirits
The Khuzud are solitary, aloof, standoffish, and eccentric. They are more often
amused than excited, and slow to make friends and enemies. Khuzud commonly spend
most of their life alone, interacting with other members of their race only several times.

While they are quick to obsession with discovery and invention, they are disinterested
in social development and conservation. The Khuzud are not an adventurous race, as
most of the world beneath has been explored and documented, and the world of the
surface is too dangerous a place for their less evolved bodies.
But when they are pursuing a goal in philosophy or invention, they can be focused
and relentless. The Khuzud are also not a violent race, but are more than capable of
holding their own in combat. Although, since the separation of the Dwarves, the Khuzud
have not been violent within their own race and have actually struck a very peaceful
balance in their own kingdom.
Deep Ones
Khuzud stand between 4 and 5 feet tall, and are very broad and compact, usually
weighing between 200 and 300 lbs. Their skin has no pigmentation, and appears
translucent in direct light. Their skin is so thin and fragile in appearance, that most
believe if they were to step into direct sunlight, they would immediately turn to stone.
Khuzud have no eyes, as there is no need for sight in a lightless world. Khuzud are
completely hairless, except for sensitive whiskers that extend the height and width of
their body that they use for sensing their surroundings. The only distinguishable
characteristics between male and female Khuzud is that these whiskers grow from the
chin and upper lip of the males, and from the temples and tops of the occipital bone of
the females. These whiskers can vary in color, but generally range from dark grey to
pale silver.
Given their slow and efficient metabolisms, Khuzud Dwarves require little
sustenance, and live between 300 and 400 years. The gestation period for a Khuzud is
about 19 months, and a female Khuzud will bear only one child in her lifetime. Most
believe that this limited reproductive cycle is due to limited availability of habitat, as
the Khuzud have discovered as much of the deep reaches of the world as is inhabitable.
Clicks and Gestures
Their primary method of communication is a hybrid between tongue clicks
intonations and a type of sign language called Inglishmek that they can sense with their
hyper developed echolocation system. The clicks help them "see" the signs and symbols
formed utilizing their extrasensory ability to "see" using Echolocation. The Khuzud
cannot speak the language of the other races, as they do not have vocal chords, but they
are known to learn to read and write Common.
Inglishmek Gestures
Raising your right hand with the palm towards your face, thumb and two fingers
forming a circle, one finger fully clenched and one finger fully stretched is a gesture
that is used after a fortunate event and is meant to cause it to prolong or repeat.
Raising your left hand with the palm towards the sky, two fingers crossed and
three fingers half clenched is a gesture that is used to strengthen an agreement similar
to making a promise.

Holding your left hand, with the palm towards the sky, two fingers crossed, two
fingers fully stretched and the last one fully clenched, against your right hand with the
palm towards the side, thumb and one finger forming a circle and three fingers fully
stretched is a gesture that expresses the equivalent of 'stop, do not move'.
Holding your left hand, with the palm towards someone else, two fingers fully
stretched and three fingers half clenched, against your right hand with the palm
towards someone else, one finger fully stretched, one finger half clenched and the other
three fully clenched is a gesture that expresses you're not serious about what you're
saying.
Reclusive
Khuzud maintain an ancient grudge from before the separation of the races, but
have come to rely on the supplies and discoveries of the surface folk to improve their
own ways of life. Because of their extended lifespan, they remain aloof of close bonds
with most of the other races, but strong friendships and lifelong alliances have been
forged through out the ages.
As a reclusive and rarely seen race, the Khuzud have historically had limited
interaction with other races. However, when they do come into contact with humans
and elves, their unique abilities to communicate and trade can be valuable assets. Their
ability to understand sign language through their echolocation system, combined with
their ability to read and write in Common, can allow them to overcome language
barriers and communicate effectively with other races.
In terms of trade, the Khuzud's skill in mining and crafting makes them valuable
partners for the production of metalwork and gems. Their efficient metabolism also
means they require less food and resources than other races, which can make them less
burdensome as trade partners.
<img
src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/Se635cI.png'
style='position:absolute; bottom:-10px;; right:-70px;; width:520px;;' />
<div style='footnote'>Artist Credit | Maxdebrabander</div>
However, their limited reproductive cycle and small population may limit their
ability to engage in long-term or large-scale trade agreements.
While the Khuzud may prefer to live in underground or dimly-lit environments,
co-habitation with other races is still possible. Cities and settlements that are built into
mountains or underground caverns may be suitable environments for the Khuzud to
live alongside humans and elves. Additionally, their unique abilities may make them
valuable members of society, especially in situations where their echolocation system
can be utilized for practical purposes, such as navigating through dark or cluttered
environments.
Hallowed Lands
The ancient kingdoms of the Khuzud are the birthplace of the Dwarves race, and
so are hallowed ground for all Dwarves. They lie deep beneath the stony faces of the

mountains, where they mine precious gems and metals and forge items of wonder.
Whatever wealth Khuzud can't find in their vast mountains, they gain through trade.
Expansive systems of underground railways and waterways allow enterprising
merchants of the different races to conduct trade between the regions. Some of the
railways and waterways even extend between the continents, under deep ocean reaches
built ages ago.
Though it is not impossible, Khuzud in surface kingdoms is extremely rare, as it
is believed that a Khuzud cannot survive in direct sunlight.
Devout Worshipers
The Khuzud have a unique religion that is deeply connected to their origins and
their environment. Their beliefs are centered around the worship of their patron god,
Moradin, the Soul Forger, who is credited with creating the first Dwarves from the fire
and rock of the earth.
For the Khuzud, Moradin is not only the creator of their race but also the god of
crafting and industry, and they hold him in high regard. They believe that everything
they create, from weapons to jewelry, is a tribute to their god, and they strive to perfect
their craft in his name. Many Khuzud follow a monastic lifestyle, dedicating their lives
to the perfection of their craft and the worship of Moradin.
Additionally, the Khuzud also have a deep connection to the earth and the
underground environment that they call home. They see the earth as a living entity that
must be respected and protected. Therefore, they are keen to protect the earth from any
harm and take great care when mining or excavating their underground cities.
The Khuzud also recognize other deities, particularly those of other Dwarven
pantheons, such as Dumathoin, the god of mining and underground exploration, and
Abbathor, the god of greed and wealth. They believe that these gods, alongside Moradin,
can help guide them in their lives and provide them with the strength and wisdom they
need to succeed.
The First Adventurers
Retiring the peak of the industrial age in the time before history, popular
professions now tend towards philosophic, and scientific ventures, with minor dabbling
in the arts. They are still the most legendary metal craftsman and jewelers in the world,
and are responsible for the crafting of every wondrous artifact to ever reach popular
lore.
Fighter Khuzud are known for their physical prowess and are often portrayed as
great warriors. They are naturally tough and durable, which makes them well-suited to
the Fighter class. They have a slow metabolism and require little sustenance, allowing
them to engage in prolonged battles without worrying about food or water.
Rogue Despite their size and strength, Khuzud are also agile and quick. They rely
heavily on their echolocation system and Inglishmek to navigate their world, which
could make them skilled scouts or thieves. Their lack of eyesight could also lend itself
well to sneaking around in the dark.
Cleric The Khuzud are known for their strong connection to their ancestors and

the earth. This could make them excellent Clerics, who draw power from their faith and
the divine. Khuzud Clerics might specialize in domains like Earth or Ancestors.
Artificer The Khuzud are expert craftsmen and are skilled at mining and
metalworking. An Artificer would be a good fit for a Khuzud character who wants to use
their talents to create magical items or constructs.
Khuzud Traits
Age The maximum age of Khuzud is 400. They are considered young until age 60.
Speed Khuzud base walking speed is 25 feet, and is not reduced by wearing heavy
armor.
Alignment Khuzud tend towards neutrality, focusing their time on invention,
discovery, and advancement. Some are drawn towards Good. Khuzud are rarely Evil.
Sunlight Sensitivity
Khuzud prefer dark and stony places, always underground. Khuzud often suffer
damage when exposed to sunlight for too long.
Ancient Ancestry
Khuzud have an innate sense of their surroundings when underground, and
underground is always treated as favored terrain. When you make an Ability or Skill
check related to your favored terrain, your proficiency bonus is doubled if you are using
a skill that you’re proficient in.
While traveling for an hour or more in your favored terrain, you gain the
following benefits:
- Difficult terrain doesn’t slow your group’s travel.
- Your group can’t become lost except by magical means.
- Even when you are engaged in another activity while traveling (such as
foraging, navigating, or tracking), you remain alert to danger.
- If you are traveling alone, you can move stealthily at a normal pace.
- When you forage, you find twice as much food as you normally would.
- While tracking other creatures, you also learn their exact number, their sizes,
and how long ago they passed through the area.
Blind
Having lived underground for millennia, Khuzud never developed eyes. They have
superior hearing, and can be skilled in combat despite their blindness because of their
unique echolcation skill. Khuzud can perceive their surroundings without relying on
sight within a specific radius.
Language
Khuzud generally only communicate through Inglishmek and Echolocation. They
rarely learn the written language of other races, but it is possible.
Leoporin
Leoporin
Leoporin are a race of rabbit-like humanoids known for their speed and agility.
They are skilled hunters and gatherers, and often live in small, tight-knit communities
in the forest.

Leoporin are known for their quick reflexes, and are often sought after as
messengers or scouts. They have excellent hearing and vision, making them skilled at
tracking prey and detecting danger. They also have a natural ability to burrow, which
they use to create underground homes and tunnels for their communities.
In historical events, Leoporin have been known to play a crucial role in helping
their allies win battles by relaying vital information and providing support. Some
Leoporin tribes have even been known to create underground tunnels and traps to
defend their communities against invaders.
Leoporin Lore
The history of the Leoporin race is shrouded in myth and legend, passed down
through generations of their small, tight-knit communities. According to their ancient
tales, the Leoporin were once ordinary rabbits, inhabitants of the vast forests of Ryndor.
But their fate took a remarkable turn when they encountered a powerful magical artifact
known as the Swiftstone.
Legend has it that a group of rabbits stumbled upon the Swiftstone deep within a
hidden grove. As they approached, the stone emitted a radiant light and bestowed upon
them the gift of sentience and humanoid form. Overnight, the rabbits transformed into
the first Leoporin, with their physical characteristics resembling a blend of rabbits and
humans.
With their newfound intelligence and dexterity, the Leoporin quickly adapted to
their new form and embraced their enhanced abilities. They honed their skills in
hunting, gathering, and burrowing, becoming masters of survival in the forest. Over
time, the Leoporin formed small, close-knit communities, valuing cooperation and
harmony with nature.
As the centuries passed, the Leoporin continued to evolve both physically and
culturally. Their keen senses and agility became more refined, making them unrivaled
hunters and scouts. They developed a rich oral tradition, passing down stories,
knowledge, and ancestral wisdom through storytelling and songs.
Throughout history, the Leoporin proved invaluable allies to other races in times
of conflict. Their speed and agility allowed them to act as messengers, delivering vital
information with unmatched swiftness. Their keen senses helped their allies detect
ambushes and navigate treacherous terrains. Many battles were won and lives were
saved thanks to the crucial role played by the Leoporin.
The Swiftstone
The discovery of the Swiftstone is a tale of both wonder and transformation in the
history of the Leoporin. It is said that a young Leoporin hunter named Liria was tracking
a particularly elusive prey deep within the heart of the forest. As she followed the trail,
she stumbled upon a hidden grove, concealed by a dense thicket of foliage.
Curiosity piqued, Liria cautiously ventured into the grove, her senses heightened
with anticipation. It was there, bathed in a soft, ethereal glow, that she discovered the
Swiftstone. The stone emanated a radiant energy, pulsating with an otherworldly
power. Intrigued by its mesmerizing aura, Liria reached out and touched the stone.

In an instant, Liria felt an immense surge of energy coursing through her body.
The Swiftstone's magic suffused her being, awakening latent potential and granting her
a deeper connection to the natural world. Her senses sharpened, her reflexes quickened,
and a newfound clarity of thought enveloped her.
Word of Liria's encounter with the Swiftstone spread throughout the Leoporin
community, filling them with a mixture of awe and hope. Recognizing the potential
benefits this magical artifact held for their entire race, a group of Leoporin elders set
out on a journey to retrieve the Swiftstone and bring it back to their community.
The return of the Swiftstone marked a turning point for the Leoporin. With its
presence, the Leoporin's natural abilities were enhanced, granting them unparalleled
speed, agility, and keen senses. They became even more proficient in their roles as
hunters and gatherers, able to secure food and resources with greater efficiency. The
stone's magical influence also deepened their connection with the forest, allowing them
to communicate with animals and plants on a profound level.
The Swiftstone became a revered object within the Leoporin society, symbolizing
their unity and shared destiny. It was carefully guarded and kept within a sacred grove,
where the Leoporin held ceremonies and rituals to honor its power. The stone's
influence reached beyond the physical realm, permeating their culture and traditions,
guiding their choices, and shaping their way of life.
With the Swiftstone as a catalyst, the Leoporin flourished as a race, thriving in
the forests and establishing their close-knit communities. They developed a profound
respect for the natural world, seeking harmony with the creatures and plants that
shared their habitat. The discovery of the Swiftstone became a cornerstone of their
identity, a testament to their unique evolution and connection to the mystical forces of
Ryndor.
Beauty is Speed
The Leoporin people embody the spirit of agility and grace. They possess a lean
and lithe physique, perfectly adapted for swift movement and nimble actions. Their
bodies are covered in soft, velvety fur that ranges in color from earthy browns and
greens to vibrant shades of orange and gold, blending harmoniously with their forested
surroundings. Their large, expressive eyes reflect their keen awareness and sharp
instincts, capturing the essence of their curious and observant nature.
Renowned for their speed, the Leoporin are gifted with exceptional reflexes and
dexterity. Their nimble feet are designed for quick movements, and their powerful hind
legs allow them to bound effortlessly through the forest undergrowth.
Whether it's leaping from tree branch to tree branch or navigating treacherous
terrains, their agile movements make them formidable hunters and acrobatic explorers.
Along with their physical prowess, the Leoporin possess acute senses, with keen
hearing that allows them to detect even the faintest rustle of leaves and a sharp vision
that can spot the smallest prey from a distance.
Community and cooperation form the cornerstone of the Leoporin society. They
live in close-knit groups, forming small communities nestled amidst the forest's
embrace. Each individual contributes their unique skills and talents for the betterment

of the group, fostering a strong sense of camaraderie and interdependence. The
Leoporin value the wisdom of their elders, drawing upon their guidance and experience
to make important decisions. They hold a deep reverence for nature, believing in the
interconnectedness of all living beings and the importance of maintaining a
harmonious balance within their environment. The Leoporin embody a spirit of
adaptability and resilience, always finding innovative solutions to overcome challenges
and navigate the ever-changing world around them.
Small and Mighty
The Leoporin possess a distinct and charming physical appearance. Standing at
an average height of around 4 to 4.5 feet (120-135 cm), they have a slender and agile
build that allows for swift movements. Their lightweight frames contribute to their
exceptional speed and agility, enabling them to navigate their forested habitats with
ease.
The Leoporin are covered in a soft and velvety fur that varies in color, ranging
from earthy browns, grays, and greens to vibrant shades of orange and gold. This
natural camouflage helps them blend seamlessly into their surroundings. The fur is
dense and plush, providing insulation during colder seasons and protection against
thorny undergrowth. Some Leoporin may also exhibit unique patterns or markings on
their fur, which serve as individual identifiers within their communities.
In terms of gender differences, male Leoporin tend to have slightly larger builds
than females, with more pronounced muscle definition. Males often have broader
shoulders and thicker limbs, emphasizing their physical strength. Females, on the other
hand, possess a slightly more slender and graceful appearance, emphasizing their
agility and nimbleness.
The average lifespan of a Leoporin is around 60 to 70 years, with some
individuals exceeding this range through the blessings of a healthy and harmonious
lifestyle. The Leoporin's longevity can be attributed to their deep connection with
nature, their physical resilience, and their ability to adapt to the challenges of their
environment.
Cautious Harmony
The Leoporin have unique relationships with various races, shaped by their
interactions and shared experiences in the world of Ryndor.
Drakarim: The Leoporin and Drakarim have a complex relationship. While
initially wary of each other due to their differing lifestyles and temperaments, they have
developed a mutual respect over time. The Leoporin admire the Drakarim's strength
and discipline, and the Drakarim appreciate the Leoporin's agility and resourcefulness.
They often find common ground in their shared love for nature and the desire to protect
their respective territories.
Aviari: The Leoporin and Aviari have a harmonious relationship based on mutual
admiration. The Leoporin appreciate the Aviari's grace in flight and their deep
connection with the skies. The Aviari, in turn, admire the Leoporin's agility on the
ground and their knowledge of the forest. They often collaborate in hunting and

gathering, exchanging information and resources to ensure the well-being of both
communities.
Cervar: The Leoporin and Cervar share a symbiotic relationship rooted in their
shared respect for the natural world. The Leoporin appreciate the Cervar's gentle nature
and their ability to navigate the forest with grace. The Cervar, in turn, benefit from the
Leoporin's knowledge of edible plants and the protection they offer against potential
threats. The two races often coexist peacefully, occasionally assisting each other in
times of need.
Humans: The Leoporin have a cautious but generally positive relationship with
humans. While they recognize that not all humans may share their respect for nature,
they appreciate those who demonstrate an understanding of the balance between
civilization and the natural world. The Leoporin may assist humans in hunting or act as
guides through treacherous terrain, fostering a level of trust and camaraderie.
Elves: The Leoporin share a deep affinity with the elves, as both races have a
profound connection to the forests. They understand each other's perspectives on the
importance of preserving nature and maintaining the balance of the world. The
Leoporin and elves often exchange knowledge and skills, fostering a sense of unity and
cooperation.
Dwarves: The Leoporin's relationship with dwarves is one of mutual respect for
each other's unique abilities. While their lifestyles and habitats differ, they recognize
the strength and craftsmanship of the dwarves and appreciate their expertise in mining
and stonework. The Leoporin may seek assistance from the dwarves in creating durable
tools or structures, and in return, offer their knowledge of the natural world.
Verdant Kingdom
Nestled deep within the verdant heart of Ryndor, lies the revered realm of
Aelurin. This ancestral land of the Leoporin embodies the essence of natural beauty and
tranquility. Lush and vibrant forests, known as Sylvarith, stretch as far as the eye can
see, with ancient trees like the towering Eldergrove, enveloping the land in a majestic
embrace. The landscape is adorned with crystal-clear, babbling streams and
shimmering ponds, like the Serenewaters, offering a haven for diverse wildlife. The air
is crisp and fragrant, carrying the sweet scent of blossoms from the Blossomthorn
Grove and the earthy aroma of the Forest Floor Haven.
Aelurin, the land of the Leoporin, is a patchwork of dense woodlands and rolling
meadows, interwoven with a network of hidden trails and secret burrows known as
Earthkin Hollows. These cleverly concealed burrows serve as both homes and
sanctuaries, providing the Leoporin with shelter and protection. The land is alive with
the vibrant energy of nature, and the Leoporin have a deep spiritual connection with
their surroundings. They live in harmony with the flora and fauna, respecting the
delicate balance of the ecosystem and ensuring its preservation for future generations.
Aelurin is not just a physical space for the Leoporin, but a reflection of their
values and way of life. It is a place of community and kinship, where Leoporin families
gather and celebrate the cyclical rhythms of nature. The lands hold countless stories
and legends passed down through generations, weaving together a rich tapestry of their

cultural heritage. Here, in Aelurin, the Leoporin find solace, strength, and inspiration,
embracing their role as stewards of the land and guardians of its delicate equilibrium.
Songs of Mouth
The Leoporin language is a symphony of soft, melodic tones, combining
harmonious sounds with a musical quality that resonates with the natural world. The
phonetic structure of their language is characterized by gentle, flowing vowels and
delicate consonants. The vowels are reminiscent of the rustling leaves in a gentle
breeze, with sounds like "ee," "oh," and "ah" that glide smoothly from one to another.
Consonants are subtle and lyrical, producing soft and soothing sounds, such as "s," "l,"
and "m."
The Leoporin language is melodically enchanting, resembling a serenade of
nature's chorus. The rising and falling intonations of their speech mimic the rhythm of
a tranquil stream, with phrases that ascend and descend like the graceful flight of birds.
The language is adorned with subtle inflections, creating melodic patterns that mimic
the cadence of a woodland symphony. Conversations among Leoporin are like a dance of
melodies, blending harmoniously and creating a tranquil aura that resonates with the
world around them.
"May the forest guide you."
This phrase might be used when bidding farewell to someone who is embarking
on a journey or adventure, expressing the hope that the forest's guidance and
protection will be with them.
"The stars shine upon us."
This phrase could be spoken during a celebration or gathering under the night
sky, acknowledging the beauty and influence of the stars on the moment.
"The song of the wind..."
Usually an quiet utterance, this phrase is used to describe the sound of wind
rustling through trees, invoking a sense of tranquility or to express the calming effect of
a gentle breeze.
"Quick hands, quick deeds."
Usually used when teaching younger Leoporin the importance of completing
tasks quickly, by doing it adeptly.
By the Moon
The Leoporin hold a deep reverence for nature, and their spirituality is intricately
woven into their daily lives. Their religion, known as Luminarism, is centered around
the belief in the divine essence that flows through all living things. They see the world
as a sacred tapestry, where every creature, plant, and element is a thread
interconnected in a grand cosmic design. The Leoporin believe that by honoring and
respecting this interconnectedness, they can attain harmony with the natural world and
find spiritual enlightenment.

Central to Luminarism is the concept of the Luminar, the divine energy that
permeates the universe. The Leoporin believe that the Luminar is embodied in the
celestial constellations that adorn the night sky. These celestial bodies are seen as
guiding lights, each representing different aspects of life and nature. The Leoporin pay
homage to these celestial beings through rituals and ceremonies, seeking their
blessings and wisdom.
The Leoporin religious practices often involve communal gatherings in sacred
groves, where they offer prayers and perform rituals to express their gratitude and seek
spiritual guidance. They also have shamans, known as Luminari, who serve as
intermediaries between the physical and spiritual realms. The Luminari are highly
respected members of the community, possessing deep knowledge of herbal lore,
divination, and healing arts. They guide the Leoporin in their spiritual journeys,
interpreting celestial signs and providing counsel in times of need.
In essence, Luminarism is not merely a religion for the Leoporin, but a way of life
that instills a profound sense of reverence, harmony, and interconnectedness with
nature. It shapes their actions, fosters a deep appreciation for the world around them,
and guides their pursuit of spiritual enlightenment and oneness with the cosmic
tapestry of existence.
Driven by Curiosity
Leoporin may be driven to seek adventure by their innate wanderlust and
curiosity, a quest for knowledge and discovery, a desire to protect nature and confront
threats to the environment,
the pursuit of diplomatic alliances and understanding, or a personal journey of
growth and mastery. Each Leoporin's motivation may be unique, but their shared
yearning for exploration, learning, and personal fulfillment propels them beyond their
ancestral lands into the wide world of adventure.
Ranger The Leoporin's hunting and gathering skills make them natural
candidates for the Ranger class. Their keen senses and connection with the natural
world allow them to excel as skilled trackers, archers, and survivalists. The Leoporin
Rangers often form deep bonds with the creatures of the forest and use their knowledge
of the wilderness to protect their ancestral lands.
Rogue The Leoporin's speed, agility, and natural stealth make them ideal
candidates for the Rogue class. Their quick reflexes and keen senses allow them to
navigate through tricky situations with ease. Leoporin Rogues often serve as scouts,
infiltrators, and thieves, utilizing their natural abilities to gather information, disarm
traps, and strike swiftly from the shadows.
Druid With their close connection to nature, the Leoporin are well-suited to the
Druid class. They possess a deep understanding of the natural world and can tap into its
primal forces. Leoporin Druids often specialize in shapeshifting into animal forms,
harnessing elemental powers, and healing through the power of nature. They act as
guardians of the land, preserving its balance and using their abilities to commune with
the spirits of the forest.
Monk The Leoporin's natural agility and dexterity make them adept Monks. Their

disciplined mindset and focus on martial arts enable them to unleash lightning-fast
strikes and perform acrobatic feats. Leoporin Monks often follow a path that combines
their physical prowess with their spiritual connection to the Luminar, using their
abilities to defend their kin and maintain harmony within their communities.
Leoporin Traits
The Leoporin are a unique race in Ryndor, known for their quickness and agility.
They are a small, furry humanoid race that have adapted to their environment by
developing powerful legs that allow them to run at incredible speeds.
Ability Score Increase Your Dexterity score increases by 2, and your Wisdom
score increases by 1.
Age Leoporin reach maturity at the age of 15 and can live up to 60 years.
Alignment Leoporin have a tendency towards neutrality but can be of any
alignment.
Size Leoporin stand between 4 and 5 feet tall, and they have a slender build. Your
size is Small.
Speed Your base walking speed is 35 feet.
Languages You can speak, read, and write Common and Leoporin. Leoporin is a
language of soft, melodic tones and has a musical quality to it.
Swift Feet Your long, powerful hind legs make you incredibly fast. When you take
the Dash action, your speed is tripled instead of doubled.
Keen Senses You have proficiency in the Perception skill.
Burst of Speed As a bonus action, you can move an additional 10 feet. You can use
this feature a number of times equal to your Wisdom modifier (minimum of once) and
regain all expended uses after finishing a long rest.

# Where It All Started

Here are some backgrounds that reflect the history, culture, and mysteries of
Ryndor. Each background provides new roleplay opportunities, skills, and unique
benefits, helping players align their characters with the setting’s lore.
Sev’rinn Initiate
Sev’rinn Initiate
You were chosen at a young age to receive elemental attunement under the guidance
of the Sev’rinn. Whether you completed your training or abandoned the path, the spark of
elemental essence still lingers within you.
Skill Proficiencies: Arcana, Insight
Tool Proficiencies: Herbalism kit
Languages: One of your choice (reflecting cultural exposure during training)
Equipment: A small crystal vial containing remnants of a failed elemental ritual,
simple robes, a scroll with notes on elemental theory, a pouch with 10 gp
Feature: Elemental Echoes
Once per long rest, you can subtly influence the environment with elemental
essence (a breeze stirs the air, a small spark flares, or nearby water ripples unnaturally).

This effect is minor but can influence NPCs or hint at your connection to the elements.
Suggested Characteristics:
Sev’rinn Initiates often display an air of mysticism and intensity, carrying the
weight of their elemental bond. Some embrace their connection, while others are
haunted by the power they never fully mastered.
Ban Mynydd Miner
Ban Mynydd Miner
Raised in the deep tunnels of Ban Mynydd, you are accustomed to dark, cramped
spaces and dangerous work. Whether you still toil in the mines or left the tunnels behind, the
skills you gained underground never left you.
Skill Proficiencies: Athletics, Perception
Tool Proficiencies: Smith’s tools
Equipment: A small piece of raw ore, miner’s tools, sturdy boots, and a pouch
with 5 gp
Feature: Tunnel Instincts
You have advantage on Survival checks made to navigate underground or find
your way in labyrinthine environments. You also have a knack for locating weak points
in stone structures.
Suggested Characteristics:
Miners from Ban Mynydd are known for their resilience and no-nonsense
demeanor. They tend to form tight bonds with companions, treating them as family
forged through shared hardship.
Skywatcher of Holmea
Skywatcher of Holmea
Trained among the high spires and floating sanctuaries of Holmea, you are familiar
with the interplay of astral magic and the celestial movements. You spent your formative
years tracking constellations, unraveling star maps, or communing with otherworldly beings.
Skill Proficiencies: Arcana, Religion
Tool Proficiencies: Cartographer’s tools
Languages: Celestial or Deep Speech
Equipment: A star chart of constellations visible only from Holmea, a small
telescope, a set of common clothes, and a pouch with 8 gp
Feature: Starborn Wisdom
Once per long rest, you can ask the GM a yes-or-no question about events or
locations connected to the astral plane. The answer may come as a cryptic hint or vision
during the next long rest.
Suggested Characteristics:
Skywatchers are often philosophical and introspective, driven by a thirst for
understanding. Some feel out of place on the material plane, always gazing upward
toward the stars or lost in deep thought.
Ghost Whisperer of Dollow Canyon

## Ghost Whisperer of Dollow Canyon

The twisted growth of Dollow Canyon is teeming with unnatural spirits, and you’ve
learned to interact with these lingering souls. Whether you act as a guide for lost spirits or a
trickster who manipulates them, the ghosts know your name.
Skill Proficiencies: Deception, Religion
Languages: One of your choice (often tied to ancient rituals or necromancy)
Equipment: A simple lantern, a ritual dagger, a journal of ghost stories, and a
pouch with 10 gp
Feature: Whispered Guidance
Once per long rest, you can call upon the spirit of a minor ghost to assist you. It
provides brief, vague information about a place, person, or event you inquire about.
Suggested Characteristics:
Ghost Whisperers often have a haunted air about them, their mannerisms
reflecting long exposure to restless spirits. Some see themselves as guides for the dead;
others use their knowledge for personal gain.
Kigan Uldar Champion
Kigan Uldar Champion
You've trained for years to compete in Kigan Uldar, a brutal competition where skill,
endurance, and quick thinking are the only things standing between victory and injury.
Whether you’re a decorated champion or a newcomer aiming to make your mark, your
experience on the field has shaped your character.
Skill Proficiencies: Athletics, Intimidation
Tool Proficiencies: One type of gaming set (representing Kigan Uldar miniatures
or strategy tools)
Languages: One of your choice
Equipment: A token of victory (like a medal, whistle, or cloth strip from your
team), a set of athletic clothes, a waterskin, and a pouch with 12 gp
Feature: Fame of the Field
Your reputation as a Kigan Uldar player grants you recognition. People familiar
with the sport may offer you shelter, food, or basic supplies. You can also gain access to
competitive events and secure audiences with high-status individuals who enjoy the
sport.
Suggested Characteristics:
Kigan Uldar champions tend to be confident, driven, and relentless in pursuit of
their goals. They enjoy challenges and thrive under pressure, often displaying a friendly
bravado—or ruthless aggression.
Utfordring Diver
Utfordring Diver
Utfordring is not just a sport; it is a way of life beneath the water’s surface. You’ve
spent your life training to be agile and strategic in the depths, either as part of an official
league or in unsanctioned competitions.
Skill Proficiencies: Acrobatics, Sleight of Hand

### Tool Proficiencies: Navigator’s tools or water vehicles

Equipment: A diving mask or trinket related to Utfordring, a small waterproof
pouch with 10 gp, a game token awarded from a match, and a set of lightweight clothing
Feature: Aquatic Agility
You are adept at moving in water. When underwater, you gain advantage on
Dexterity (Acrobatics) checks to avoid hazards or escape grapples. Additionally, other
athletes and fans of Utfordring may recognize you, granting you favors or information.
Suggested Characteristics:
Utfordring divers are agile and cunning, using both finesse and strategy. They
often embrace risk and have a deep love for the water, sometimes struggling to feel
grounded on land.
Weirding Refugee
Weirding Refugee
The Weirding has displaced many from their homes, driving them to unfamiliar lands.
You are one of the survivors of a Weird Zone disaster, carrying the scars—mental or physical
—of that experience.
Skill Proficiencies: Insight, Stealth
Tool Proficiencies: Alchemist’s supplies or herbalism kit
Languages: One of your choice
Equipment: A shard of strange glass from your home, a set of plain clothes, a
small journal with scribbled memories, and a pouch with 5 gp
Feature: Touched by the Weirding
Your exposure to the Weirding has left you with an eerie sensitivity. Once per long
rest, you can make a Wisdom (Insight) check to predict how an unfamiliar creature or
person might react. You also have advantage on checks to understand or resist
environmental anomalies caused by Weird Zones.
Suggested Characteristics:
Weirdling refugees tend to be cautious and observant, often haunted by their
past. Some cling to hope for restoration, while others embrace the chaos the Weirding
has brought into their lives.
Hurstwold Warden
Hurstwold Warden
You have walked the paths of the ancient Hurstwold forest, learning to navigate its
treacherous terrain and to coexist with its mystical inhabitants. Whether as a guide, scout, or
guardian, the forest has become your second home.
Skill Proficiencies: Nature, Stealth
Tool Proficiencies: Herbalism kit
Languages: Sylvan
Equipment: A wooden charm from the forest, a hunting knife, a cloak made from
enchanted leaves, and a pouch with 10 gp
Feature: Friend of the Forest

You have an innate understanding of natural magic and the spirits within
Hurstwold. You can move through difficult terrain in the forest without penalty, and
creatures native to the forest are less likely to see you as a threat.
Suggested Characteristics:
Wardens of Hurstwold are often calm, patient, and observant. They are deeply
connected to nature and tend to be wary of cities and large crowds, preferring the
solitude of the forest.
Surreymouth Trader
Surreymouth Trader
You grew up navigating the bustling markets and docks of Surreymouth, learning to
haggle, bargain, and move goods with ease. Whether your trade is legal or illicit, you’ve
mastered the art of negotiation.
Skill Proficiencies: Deception, Insight
Tool Proficiencies: Vehicles (water) or one type of gaming set
Languages: One of your choice
Equipment: A ledger of trade contacts, a set of fine clothes, a satchel with small
samples of exotic goods, and a pouch with 15 gp
Feature: Marketplace Connections
You know how to find the best deals—or bend the rules—when dealing with
merchants. Once per long rest, you can secure a discount or locate a rare item (subject to
GM approval). You can also use your contacts to gather rumors and information.
Suggested Characteristics:
Surreymouth traders are opportunistic, quick-witted, and resourceful. They are
always looking for the next deal and know that every connection has

# A Class of Your Own

Masters of Their Own Fate – The Classes of Ryndor
In Ryndor, the path an individual takes is not just a matter of skill or heritage—it
is an expression of their place in a world teetering between tradition, magic,
technology, and chaos. From the disciplined fighter honing their technique on the
battlefields of the Ardal Plains to the elusive rogue navigating the shadows of
Surreymouth's underbelly, the classes in Ryndor reflect the diverse ways people have
learned to thrive, survive, and shape their world.
Every class in Ryndor is more than a collection of abilities; it is an identity shaped
by the land’s intricate balance between the natural, the arcane, and the strange. Those
who live by the sword are as respected as those who wield magic, and innovation can
come from either faith or steel. Yet, the introduction of The Weirding—that chaotic rift
between worlds—has reshaped what it means to follow these paths. Some individuals
find strength in tradition, upholding ancient customs that once guided their ancestors.
Others embrace the change, twisting strange magic and technology to forge a new
future for Ryndor.
In this chapter, we present the classes as they exist within the world of Ryndor,
detailing how each class not only survives but thrives in a setting where magic pulses

unpredictably, faith provides both hope and power, and technology competes with
the old ways for dominance. Whether your character follows the way of the sword,
spell, or spirit, their journey through this world will be shaped by choices—choices that
will ripple outward, affecting not only their own fate but the fate of Ryndor itself.
Each class finds new dimensions within the world of Ryndor. Clerics of the Skola
in Holmea channel celestial energy through ancient texts and crystal lenses, while
warlocks bargain with beings that linger too close to the rift to Nebernoria. Fighters
serve as bodyguards to nobles vying for control in Eveltoft’s council chambers, and
druids guard the last untouched pockets of wilderness from Weirded corruption. Rogues
and bards whisper in back alleys and taverns, spreading rumors or secrets that can
topple kingdoms.
The paths of Kigan Uldar and Utfordring are reflected here, as well—those who
train not only for battle but for spectacle, pushing their bodies and minds to the limit in
feats of athleticism and daring that inspire entire communities. In a world where
physical prowess is admired as much as arcane mastery, adventurers may find
themselves facing challenges that demand both cunning and strength.
The power of choice and the consequence of action lie at the heart of every class
in Ryndor. Will your character uphold the traditions of their ancestors, seeking to
restore what was lost? Will they delve into the secrets of the Weirding, seeking
knowledge at any cost? Or will they carve their own path, defining their role in a world
that offers both danger and possibility at every turn?
The classes of Ryndor offer infinite possibilities, each tied to the forces that
shape the land. It is up to you to decide which of these forces your character will wield—
and how they will face the challenges that await.
Barbarian
Barbarian: The Untamed Spirit of Ryndor
Barbarians in Ryndor are more than warriors—they are primal forces bound to
the land, embodying the wild, unyielding spirit of the world itself. In a land where
nature’s fury shapes the very culture, barbarians are revered and feared in equal
measure. They are living tempests, forces of pure instinct and will, drawn from the
deepest roots of Ryndor’s wilds and mystical forces. Whether shaped by the crashing
waves along Surreymouth's harbors, the raging fires within Ban Mynydd’s forges, or
the howling winds of the Bannockwyrm peaks, Barbarians in Ryndor are unpredictable
forces, unleashed to conquer or protect.
Origins of the Barbarian Spirit
Every barbarian in Ryndor carries with them a story of survival. Many have grown
up in the untamed expanses of Hurstwold Forest or the dangerous Dollow Canyon,
where the land itself tests one’s mettle daily. Others trace their rage to ancient
ancestors who defied oppression, especially those who fought in the Sev’rinn
Rebellion, their fury echoing through generations as a legacy of resistance. Some
barbarians are wanderers, shaped by a nomadic existence and a deep connection to the
natural and spiritual forces of the world.

While they may come from vastly different regions and backgrounds, all

barbarians share an affinity for raw emotion—a connection to the world not through
logic or study, but through feeling, instinct, and rage. They understand that the
delicate balance between creation and destruction that defines Ryndor must
sometimes be disrupted to achieve change.
Barbarians and the Weirding
Barbarians have a complex relationship with the Weirding, the strange and
unpredictable phenomenon born from the friction between Ryndor and Nebernoria. For
some, the Weirding is an unwelcome curse that disrupts their control, as time shifts
unpredictably or landscapes dissolve before their eyes. For others, it is a gift—another
chaotic force to harness and channel through their rage. Stories tell of barbarians who
have wandered into Weird Zones and returned altered, their very essence marked by the
phenomena—time-scarred warriors who fight with unnatural precision or power that
shifts like a storm on the horizon.
Some clans, especially those in remote areas, revere the Weirding as an
extension of the natural world, seeing it as proof that the land is alive and evolving.
These barbarians often experiment with strange relics and artifacts, willing to risk
corruption for a taste of the Weirding’s potential. Others serve as protectors against its
dangers, confronting beasts twisted by the Weirding and guarding settlements near
unstable zones.
The Role of Barbarians in Ryndor’s Society
Barbarians are often outsiders to the cities and organized powers of Ryndor.
Many hail from regions where Kigan Uldar and Utfordring competitions are more than
sport—they are tests of survival, where strength and cunning are honored above all
else. In places like Norwycke or the Ardal Plains, a barbarian’s rage is seen as a tool of
justice, a way to protect the weak and mete out vengeance against oppressors.
Some barbarian clans serve as guardians of sacred places, like the ancient groves
of Hurstwold or the treacherous jungle depths of Dollow Canyon. Others act as
mercenaries or bounty hunters, employed by guilds in Surreymouth or Ban Mynydd to
hunt down dangerous prey. While the cities of Ryndor may view barbarians with
caution, they are also respected for their unwavering resolve, often called upon in
times of crisis when brute force is needed to protect against invading forces or
unnatural threats.
Paths Unique to Ryndor
Barbarians in Ryndor are shaped not only by their innate rage but by the worlds
they inhabit. Many follow primal paths unique to their regions, their powers reflecting
the environment or forces that shaped them. Whether they embody the unstoppable
fury of nature, the essence of ancient storms, or even tap into the chaos of the
Weirding, each barbarian is a reflection of the wild, untamed heart of Ryndor.
These warriors stand apart from organized military orders, refusing the
constraints of laws or rulers. Instead, they act with the freedom of those who answer

only to their instincts, embodying the principle that power lies in action, not in words.
In a world as unpredictable and volatile as Ryndor, where change is inevitable and
survival is hard-won, barbarians are the primal answer to a simple truth: strength, in
all its forms, endures.
Path of the Howling Tempest
Barbarian: Path of the Howling Tempest
Barbarians who follow the Path of the Howling Tempest draw their rage from the
elemental winds and storms that surge across the jagged terrain of Ryndor. These
warriors embody the unpredictable fury of the storm—violent, swift, and relentless. In
their rage, they move like a tempest, their attacks accompanied by bursts of wind and
thunder. The Howling Tempest barbarians harness the essence of the storm not only
for destruction but to protect allies caught in nature’s fury. Their presence on the
battlefield is heralded by gales that buffet their foes and empower their comrades.
Path of the Howling Tempest Features
Stormbound Rage
3rd-level Path of the Howling Tempest feature
When you rage, the winds howl around you and carry your fury across the
battlefield. While raging, your movement speed increases by 10 feet, and whenever you
move at least 10 feet toward a creature and hit it with a melee weapon attack, the target
takes an additional 1d6 thunder damage. This damage increases to 2d6 at 10th level and
3d6 at 14th level.
Additionally, while raging, the area within 10 feet of you becomes difficult terrain
for your enemies. The winds swirl at your command, slowing their movement.
Gale's Reprieve
6th-level Path of the Howling Tempest feature
The storm carries you out of danger. When a creature within 30 feet of you makes
an attack against you or an ally, you can use your reaction to cause a powerful gust to
push you or your ally 10 feet in any direction. This movement does not provoke
opportunity attacks.
You can use this feature a number of times equal to your Constitution modifier
(minimum of 1). You regain all expended uses when you finish a long rest.
Tempest's Embrace
10th-level Path of the Howling Tempest feature
Your rage channels the raw fury of storms. While raging, you gain resistance to
lightning and thunder damage. Additionally, whenever you take damage from a creature
within 10 feet of you, the storm lashes back—forcing the creature to make a Strength
saving throw (DC = 8 + your proficiency bonus + your Constitution modifier). On a failed
save, the creature is pushed 15 feet away from you.
Eye of the Storm
14th-level Path of the Howling Tempest feature

You learn to calm the storm within yourself, creating a protective aura in the heat
of battle. As an action while raging, you can summon the Eye of the Storm, a 20-footradius aura centered on you that lasts for 1 minute. While in this aura:
- You and friendly creatures have advantage on Dexterity saving throws.
- All ranged weapon attacks against you and friendly creatures have
disadvantage.
- You and friendly creatures gain resistance to lightning and thunder damage.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you finish a long rest.
Bard
The Bard: Weavers of Fate and Song
In Ryndor, the Bard is more than just a performer—they are storytellers,
historians, diplomats, and conduits of ancient truths. In a world balanced precariously
between the forces of the natural, the arcane, and the Weirding, bards wield the power
of expression to bridge divides, stir emotions, and shift the tides of fate itself. Whether
inspiring warriors on the battlefield, spreading subversive tales in noble courts, or
chronicling the strange phenomena of The Weirding, bards stand at the nexus of magic
and influence.
The Role of Bards in Ryndor
Every bard in Ryndor embodies the idea that knowledge, creativity, and music
are forces capable of shaping reality. In the great halls of Eveltoft, bards serve as
advisers, spinning intricate webs of words to influence political decisions and
manipulate shifting alliances. In the black markets of Surreymouth, clever bards weave
tales of fortune and caution to sway deals in their favor. Some serve as emissaries,
traveling between the major cities—**Norwycke**, Ban Mynydd, and Wyrmbost—
using their charisma and wit to build fragile peace between factions.
With the emergence of The Weirding, bards have taken on new responsibilities—
and dangers. Strange melodies and half-forgotten songs now echo in unpredictable
patterns, seemingly drawn from the rift to Nebernoria. Some bards have begun to
explore these eerie harmonies, crafting new spells and performances to harness the
Weirding’s unstable energies. Yet the cost is high. Bards who channel the Weirding too
deeply often return altered or afflicted, with new songs in their repertoire—along with
haunting memories they can never quite escape.
Traditions of Performance and Lore
Not all bards seek out the strange energies of the Weirding. Many uphold the
ancient tradition of the Skalds, who once traveled Ryndor, chronicling battles and
memorializing heroes through epic poems and ballads. These Skaldic bards find power
in recalling Ryndor’s oldest legends—some believe the act of retelling these stories
strengthens the land itself, preventing further destabilization from the Weirding.
Kigan Uldar and Utfordring games have also created new paths for bards, as they
turn arenas into theaters of spectacle and sport. Arena Bards are celebrated as much for
their charisma as for their spellwork, their stirring songs becoming an integral part of

the competitive atmosphere. Victory in the Deep League is marked by both physical
prowess and the brilliance of the accompanying performance, creating heroes who are
immortalized in song across the land.
The Bardic Styles of Ryndor’s Races
- Humans: Bards among the human population blend diverse influences,
mastering both ancient storytelling techniques and cutting-edge performance magic.
Human bards often serve as political advisers or wandering troubadours, using their
versatility to adapt to any audience.
- Elves: Elven bards focus on elegant, intricate melodies that weave illusion and
charm into their performances. Their songs are often seen as subtle spells, with magic
hidden in every harmony and poetic verse. Elves are particularly skilled at manipulating
Primordial Resonance, allowing their music to harmonize with the natural world.
- Dwarves: Dwarven bards prefer epic tales accompanied by booming chants and
percussion. Their performances honor ancestral heroes, and their songs contain
powerful evocations that inspire allies to stand firm even in the direst of battles.
- Sev’rinns: Sev’rinn bards explore the intersections between magic and
emotion, focusing on the essence of memory and transformation. Their songs can
evoke lost dreams or reshape a listener’s perspective, reflecting their deep connection
to the ever-changing forces of Ryndor.
- Cervar: Cervar bards emphasize movement and dance, using their
performances to mimic the fluidity of nature. Their songs are often playful, imitating
the sounds of forests and rivers, yet layered with hidden meanings and insights.
Weirding-Touched Bards
Some bards in Ryndor have begun to explore The Weirding’s strange echoes,
discovering how unstable resonance patterns can create powerful, albeit unpredictable,
magic. These Weirding-Touched bards are considered both geniuses and outcasts—
**capable of shaping reality with unsettling melodies**, but often at the cost of their
own sanity. Instruments exposed to the Weirding hum with chaotic energy, shifting in
shape or producing dissonant, otherworldly tones.
A new subset of spells has emerged among these bards, tapping into the essence
of change, memory, and temporal distortion. Some Weirding-Touched bards have even
learned to weave their spells into conversations, allowing them to alter time and
perception during moments of diplomacy, interrogation, or combat. However, using
such magic is fraught with risk, and those who delve too deeply into the Weirding are
often left scarred by the experience.
Becoming a Bard in Ryndor
To become a bard in Ryndor is to embrace the dual role of artist and storyteller,
historian and magician. It is to know that every performance, every song, and every
tale carries the potential to shift the fate of the world. As a bard, your words are both
shield and sword, and your magic lies in the belief that the world can be remade by
those brave enough to imagine it.

You may choose to follow traditional paths, embracing the ancient ways of the
Skalds or the intricate arts of diplomacy. Alternatively, you might walk the untrodden
paths of the Weirding, unraveling the strange melodies hidden beyond the Rift,
knowing that every note you play is both a gift and a curse.
What will you leave behind in Ryndor’s story? Will your songs inspire nations or
awaken old terrors? Will your art bring unity or discord? In Ryndor, the power to shape
the world rests not only in what you say—but in how well you say it.
College of Lanterns
College of Lanterns
The College of Lanterns draws its power from more than mere light. These bards
harness the strange energies of the Weirding, using their lanterns to part the veil
between what is seen and what truly is. Through the soft glow of their enchanted
lanterns, the deceptions of the world melt away, exposing hidden truths, illusions, and
the eerie fingerprints of the Weirding.
Lantern Bards are trusted guides in uncertain times, revealing the true nature of
people, objects, and places. They tread the line between known reality and the twisted
influence of the Weirding, offering clarity where others see confusion. To follow the
path of the Lantern is to embrace the unknown—and to illuminate it for others.
College of Lanterns Features
Guiding Light
3rd-level College of Lanterns feature
When you join the College of Lanterns at 3rd level, you gain the ability to summon
a magical lantern infused with the light of the Weirding. As an action, you can summon
a Weirdlight Lantern that floats near you and emits bright light in a 30-foot radius and
dim light for an additional 30 feet. This lantern lasts for 1 hour or until you dismiss it
(no action required).
While the lantern is active, you and your allies gain the following benefits:
- Revealing Glow: Inside the lantern’s bright light, illusions falter, and any
shape-shifting creatures or magically disguised objects revert to their true forms.
- Whispers of the Weirding: When a creature or object influenced by the
Weirding is within the bright light, it glimmers with a spectral outline, and you have
advantage on Wisdom (Insight) checks to understand its purpose or origin.
- Illuminated Path: Creatures of your choice in the light gain advantage on
Wisdom (Perception) checks and cannot be surprised.
You can use this feature a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, and
you regain all expended uses when you finish a long rest.
Lantern of Clarity
6th-level College of Lanterns feature
Your lantern gains the power to cut through the mental fog created by the
Weirding. While your Weirdlight Lantern is active, you and your allies gain the following
benefits:

- Pierce the Veil: When inside the bright light, creatures have advantage on
saving throws against fear, charm, and confusion effects.
- Unmask the Twisted: You can use a bonus action to reveal one hidden magical
or weirded influence on a creature, object, or area within 30 feet of the lantern’s light.
The influence becomes visible, outlined by eerie flickering light until the end of your
next turn, granting advantage on any Arcana or Investigation checks to understand or
dispel it.
Additionally, while your lantern is active, you can cast detect magic or identify
once without expending a spell slot. You regain the ability to cast these spells in this
way after finishing a long rest.
Radiant Lantern of the Weirding
14th-level College of Lanterns feature
At 14th level, your lantern becomes a powerful conduit for the Weirding’s strange
energy, revealing not only hidden truths but the deeper, unsettling nature of reality
itself. When you summon your Weirdlight Lantern, you can choose for it to gain the
following additional properties:
- Weirdlight Surge: Creatures of your choice within the bright light must succeed
on a Wisdom saving throw (DC = your spell save DC) or become dazed until the end of
their next turn, overwhelmed by visions of their true selves and hidden fears.
- Lantern of Duality: Inside the light, weirded objects or creatures temporarily
revert to their pre-weirded state, and any curse or twisted influence is temporarily
suspended. This effect lasts while the creature or object remains inside the lantern’s
bright light and ends immediately when they leave its radius.
- Weirding Resonance: Whenever a creature inside the bright light takes damage
from a spell or magical attack, it takes additional psychic damage equal to your
Charisma modifier (minimum of 1).
Once you activate these abilities, you can’t do so again until you finish a long rest.
Role of the College of Lanterns in Ryndor
In a world reshaped by the Weirding, the College of Lanterns has become more
important than ever. Lantern Bards travel to places touched by the Weirding, using their
magic to reveal the truth beneath the twisted surface. They are called to investigate
strange occurrences, guide expeditions into weirded zones, and uncover the origins of
mysterious artifacts and beings.
In Eveltoft, Lantern Bards are often found at the Rift to Nebernoria, helping
scholars decode astral phenomena and determine the true nature of recovered objects.
Many also accompany adventurers deep into wild and weirded lands, where reality
shifts and lies may take shape. They serve not only as performers and storytellers but
also as guides through the blurred edges of reality, ensuring that the light of
understanding prevails against the Weirding’s dark distortions.
Lantern Bards are sought after for both practical and spiritual counsel, using
their gifts to provide clarity, wisdom, and hope in uncertain times. But theirs is not an
easy path—they are called to illuminate truths that others may prefer to leave hidden.

Following the way of the lantern is a promise to reveal, no matter how unsettling the
truth may be.
Cleric
The Cleric Class in Ryndor
"The gods speak through song, through silence, and sometimes through storms. What
matters is not just listening—but knowing how to respond."
Clerics in Ryndor are powerful conduits of divine will, individuals who wield the
blessings of gods and cosmic forces to shape the world around them. In a land where the
Weirding disrupts both physical and spiritual realities, the role of a cleric has never
been more vital—or more complex. Whether calling upon ancestral spirits, channeling
astral resonance, or wielding divine fire, clerics walk a path that demands unwavering
faith, quick thinking, and a heart willing to face the unknown.
The Nature of Divinity in Ryndor
The people of Ryndor worship a wide array of gods, spirits, and cosmic entities—
some ancient, others born from the chaos of the Weirding itself. Faith in Ryndor isn't
always about reverence alone; it’s about alignment with a greater purpose. Clerics see
their power as both a gift and a responsibility, their actions rippling outward in ways
that alter reality itself. As guardians of both the physical world and spiritual realms,
clerics serve on the front lines against both mundane threats and supernatural
phenomena.
Some clerics strive to restore order and stabilize regions affected by the Weirding,
while others delve into its chaotic potential, believing disruption is the first step toward
creation. Regardless of their path, every cleric must tread carefully, as even divine
power can falter or mutate in ways that defy understanding.
Faith and the Weirding
The Weirding has added new challenges—and opportunities—for clerics. Some
regions of Ryndor have become spiritually fractured, and divine magic behaves
unpredictably within the Weird Zones. In some cases, prayers are answered with
strange, unintended consequences, or visions come from long-forgotten gods who stir
in the rift between planes. Clerics attuned to these disturbances may develop strange
new abilities—or encounter beings who demand dangerous bargains in exchange for
power.
For many clerics, maintaining faith has become a daily struggle, as the cosmic
forces they serve are no longer as stable or predictable as they once seemed. The faithful
must learn to adapt, becoming both guides and protectors in a world that now teeters
between planes of existence.
Role of Clerics in Ryndor’s Society
Clerics hold unique positions of influence in Ryndor. In cities like Eveltoft, they
serve as advisors, healers, and judges, helping to resolve disputes and maintain balance
within society. Rural communities often rely on clerics as spiritual leaders and
protectors, offering guidance through both divine teachings and practical magic.

However, not all clerics are celebrated—**distrust** and superstition linger in areas
where the Weirding has caused divine magic to behave unpredictably, leaving some
wary of the clergy’s intentions.
In some regions, particularly those touched by the Sev’rinn influence, clerics
combine their religious teachings with elemental magic to enhance their abilities,
crafting strange rituals that call upon both divine and natural forces. Others ally
themselves with powerful city-states or guilds, wielding their magic in exchange for
influence, wealth, or knowledge.
Clerics and the Weirding Conflict
Clerics play a pivotal role in the battle against the Weirding. In regions where the
Weird Zones blur the lines between planes, clerics must use their magic to stabilize the
area—or risk becoming part of the chaos themselves. Some clerics form alliances with
scholars and wizards to study the effects of the Weirding, hoping to unlock its
mysteries and tame its power. Others, more cautious, warn that meddling with such
forces invites ruin.
Not all clerics agree on how to confront the Weirding. Some see it as a test of
faith, sent by the gods to challenge Ryndor’s people. Others believe the Weirding is
evidence of divine imbalance, requiring new rituals and practices to restore cosmic
harmony. Whatever their perspective, clerics must navigate not only the dangers of the
physical world but also the shifting spiritual landscape that the Weirding has left in its
wake.
Adventuring as a Cleric in Ryndor
Many clerics feel called to adventure, drawn to restore order where the Weirding
has brought chaos—or spread their influence to regions in need. Some embark on
personal quests, seeking answers from the gods or searching for ancient relics hidden
within the ruins of fallen civilizations. Others become reluctant wanderers, carried by
fate to places where their magic is needed most.
When playing a cleric in Ryndor, consider:
- What is your relationship with the gods? Do you serve willingly, or out of duty,
fear, or personal ambition?
- How does the Weirding affect your faith? Do you see the chaos as a threat to be
overcome, or a force to be harnessed?
- What role do you play in your community? Are you a healer, a warrior, a
teacher—or something more mysterious?
- What are your goals as an adventurer? Do you seek knowledge, redemption,
power—or something altogether unknown?
Domain of Resonance
Domain of Resonance
“All things vibrate with meaning—some in harmony, others in discord. The faithful
walk the path between both.”
Clerics of the Resonance Domain are attuned to the magical frequencies that

ripple through the planes, especially the material and astral realms. They believe in the
delicate balance between order and chaos, working as guides who help align the world’s
vibrations, or disrupt them when needed. The Weirding has heightened the influence of
this domain, as the collision of planes distorts magical resonance, leaving clerics of this
path both revered and feared for their insight into unstable forces.
Resonance Domain clerics are equal parts musicians, mystics, and spiritual
scientists, using their magic to attune energies, influence emotions, and uncover
hidden truths. They are often sought after for their ability to stabilize wild magic zones
and dispel strange phenomena. However, their power comes with the risk of drawing
the attention of unpredictable astral beings.
Domain Features
| Cleric Level | Feature |
|:------------:|:--------|
| 1st | Domain Spells, Vibrational Insight |
| 2nd | Channel Divinity: Amplify Vibration |
| 6th | Harmonic Surge |
| 8th | Divine Strike (Thunder) |
| 17th | Cosmic Resonance |
Domain Spells
Clerics of the Resonance Domain learn spells that align with their role as
manipulators of sound, energy, and perception.
| Cleric Level | Spells |
|:------------:|:-------|
| 1st | Dissonant Whispers, Thunderwave |
| 3rd | Shatter, Calm Emotions |
| 5th | Dispel Magic, Hypnotic Pattern |
| 7th | Greater Invisibility, Freedom of Movement |
| 9th | Modify Memory, Wall of Force |
Vibrational Insight (1st Level)
At 1st level, you gain proficiency in either Performance or Arcana. In addition,
you can cast Detect Magic at will, but only as a ritual. When you use this feature, you hear
subtle vibrations that reveal the aura or intent of a magical item or being.
Channel Divinity: Amplify Vibration (2nd Level)
Starting at 2nd level, you can use your Channel Divinity to manipulate the energy
around you. As an action, you create a resonant pulse in a 30-foot radius around you for
1 minute.
- Resonant Pulse: All spell damage within this area increases by 1d6 thunder
damage. Additionally, the next enemy to fail a saving throw within the pulse must
succeed on a Constitution saving throw or become dazed (incapacitated until the end of
its next turn).
- You can end the effect early as a bonus action.

## Harmonic Surge (6th Level)

You can manipulate the flow of magic around you to increase its resonance. When
you or an ally within 30 feet casts a spell, you can use your reaction to grant one of the
following effects:
- Harmonic Boost: Add 1d8 thunder damage to the spell's effect.
- Resonant Echo: After the spell is cast, it echoes for a moment. If the target
moves within the next turn, it takes 1d8 psychic damage as the energy reverberates.
You can use this feature a number of times equal to your Wisdom modifier
(minimum of 1), and regain all uses after a long rest.
Divine Strike (8th Level)
At 8th level, you can infuse your attacks with the energy of sound waves. Once on
each of your turns when you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can deal an
additional 1d8 thunder damage. When you reach 14th level, this extra damage increases
to 2d8.
Cosmic Resonance (17th Level)
At 17th level, your connection to magical resonance allows you to maintain
harmony—or disrupt it—with overwhelming power. You gain the following abilities:
- Resonant Field: As an action, you create a 60-foot-radius sphere centered on
yourself that lasts for 1 minute. While active, the field enhances magic:
- Allies’ spell attacks and save DCs increase by 2.
- All enemies in the field have disadvantage on saving throws against thunder or
psychic damage.
- Planar Feedback: If an enemy fails a saving throw inside the field, they become
vulnerable to thunder damage until the end of your next turn.
You can use this feature once per long rest.
Roleplaying a Resonance Domain Cleric
Clerics of the Resonance Domain walk the fine line between stability and chaos.
Some see themselves as protectors of harmony, ensuring that magic and natural
energies flow in balance. Others revel in discord, believing that disruption is necessary
for progress and change.
These clerics are often sought after in regions affected by the Weirding, as they
are uniquely suited to stabilize (or harness) its influence. However, their affinity with
chaotic energies sometimes makes them outsiders among other religious figures, who
view their methods as too unpredictable.
When playing a Resonance Domain Cleric, consider:
- How do you view magic? Is it a gift to be carefully cultivated or a chaotic force
to embrace?
- What role do you play in the Weirding? Do you seek to restore order to areas
disrupted by the Weirding, or do you tap into the chaos to enhance your abilities?
- How do you interact with sound and music? Do you use instruments or singing
to channel your divine magic, or do you listen to the hidden vibrations of the world to

guide you?
Resonance Domain Clerics in Ryndor
In Ryndor, the Resonance Domain is associated with the subtle vibrations
between the material and astral planes. These clerics are often connected to the
Sev'rinn Council or specialized orders dedicated to stabilizing astral energy. Their
abilities are highly sought after in the chaotic regions touched by The Weirding, where
strange distortions in time and space require delicate manipulation.
Resonance Domain clerics are also deeply involved in musical and magical
traditions, often participating in or leading rituals that blend faith with music. Some
clerics even use their abilities to craft strange and beautiful instruments that echo with
arcane power, leaving traces of music that linger in the air long after the performance
ends.
Druid
Druid Class in Ryndor
"The land speaks, and I answer. The skies shift, and I change. The Weirding spreads,
and I become the bridge."
Druids in Ryndor are the guardians of nature, but in a world shaped by the
Weirding, they are more than just protectors of forests and fields—they are
intermediaries between the natural and the unnatural. The strange influences that have
emerged across the land challenge the very balance they have sworn to protect. As
beings of both tradition and transformation, druids must adapt to the ever-changing
nature of Ryndor. They embrace cycles—of life and death, magic and nature, and now,
stability and chaos—seeking harmony amid the strange.
The Role of Druids in Ryndor
The druidic tradition in Ryndor stretches back to ancient times, predating the rise
and fall of empires. Many druids act as shamans, guides, and advisors, respected for
their wisdom and understanding of nature’s cycles. However, the spread of the
Weirding has unsettled them. Some druids resist these changes, trying to maintain the
old ways, while others embrace the strangeness as part of nature’s evolution.
Druids in Ryndor often serve as watchers of boundaries: between life and death,
order and chaos, and material and astral realms. They interact with ancient forests,
volcanic landscapes, hidden groves, and now, weird zones, understanding that balance
must be found in transformation.
Druidic Traditions in Ryndor
- Ancient Guardians: Some druids uphold the oldest traditions, protecting
ancient forests like Hurstwold or Arvanthwaite Woods. They are wary of the Weirding
and seek to isolate these places from its influence.
- Wayfarers and Guides: These druids walk the wilds of Ryndor, helping travelers
survive treacherous terrain and avoid strange phenomena. They understand that
balance requires movement and change.
