- Weird-Touched Mystics: A growing number of druids now study the
Weirding’s effects on natural phenomena. They explore strange groves and mutated
ecosystems, seeking ways to harness the unpredictable forces of this new world.
Druids in Daily Life
Druids rarely reside within cities, preferring to live on the fringes of civilization
or within natural sanctuaries. However, they are often welcomed as healers, herbalists,
and wise advisers by rural communities. The people of Wyrmbost, for example, rely on
druids to maintain the health of the beasts they breed. Druids also serve as mediators
between settlements and the land itself, ensuring that communities respect natural
cycles and avoid overexploiting resources.
In Eveltoft, druids play a quieter but essential role, ensuring that the city’s
interaction with the Weirding is carefully monitored. Some act as emissaries between
the Crystal Scholars and the wilderness beyond, negotiating for harmony in a world
shifting between order and chaos.
Themes for Druid Characters in Ryndor
- Guardians of the Old Ways: Does your character believe in protecting the
ancient traditions, resisting the strangeness of the Weirding to maintain balance?
- Weird-Touched Wanderers: Does your druid explore the fringes of strange
ecosystems, fascinated by the new creatures and phenomena that the Weirding has
introduced?
- Advisors and Mediators: Do you serve as a spiritual guide or negotiator
between communities, seeking to balance human ambition with the land’s needs?
- Transformative Shapeshifters: How has your ability to transform and adapt
been influenced by the Weirding? Have your forms changed in ways you do not yet
understand?
Playing a Druid in Ryndor
As a druid in Ryndor, you bridge the gap between tradition and transformation.
Whether you resist the Weirding or embrace it, you must navigate a world in flux. Your
magic draws from the forces of nature, but those forces are no longer predictable. A
druid of Ryndor is more than just a protector of nature; they are a guide through
uncertainty, a weaver of cycles, and a witness to the strange evolution of the land.
Character Inspiration Questions
1. What is your relationship with the Weirding? Do you view it as a curse or an
opportunity for growth?
2. What is your connection to nature’s cycles? Are you a strict traditionalist, or
do you believe in adapting to new influences?
3. How do you interact with other characters? Do you prefer solitude, or do you
see yourself as a teacher and guide?
4. Where do you call home? Are you tied to a specific forest, mountain, or stretch
of land, or do you wander in search of understanding?
5. What creatures do you revere or fear? How do you interact with the strange

beasts introduced by the Weirding?
Circle of the Weird
Circle of the Weird
"The threads of the Weirding are tangled and frayed, and we are the ones who weave
them anew."
Druids who join the Circle of the Weird embrace the chaotic and unstable
energies that flow between the material and astral planes, drawn to the strange
phenomena brought about by the Weirding. These druids believe that the natural world
and the realms beyond are interconnected in ways that defy understanding, and they
seek to uncover the secrets hidden within these blurred boundaries. As a member of the
Circle of the Weird, you embody the unpredictable nature of the Weirding, using its
chaotic influence to reshape the battlefield, adapt to bizarre forms, and reveal hidden
truths that lie beneath reality’s surface.
Features of the Circle of the Weird
Circle Spells
Your connection to the Weird grants you access to unique magic that pulls from
strange planes of existence. At certain levels, you gain access to spells that reflect the
chaotic influence of the Weirding.
| Druid Level | Circle Spells |
|:-----------:|:--------------------------------:|
| 3rd | Mirror Image, Misty Step |
| 5th | Blink, Hypnotic Pattern |
| 7th | Greater Invisibility, Confusion|
| 9th | Mislead, Passwall |
These spells count as druid spells for you, and you always have them prepared.
Weird Shape
2nd-level Circle of the Weird feature
When you tap into your Wild Shape, your form fluctuates with the chaotic
energies of the Weirding. As a bonus action, you can expend a use of your Wild Shape to
assume the form of a Weirded Beast—a creature shaped by the unstable forces of the
Weirding.
- While in your Wild Shape, your form becomes unpredictable and mutable. You
may roll once on the Weird Shape Mutation table below at the start of each of your turns
to determine a bonus or effect for that turn.
| d6 | Weird Shape Mutation |
|:--:|----------------------|
| 1 | Your limbs stretch unnaturally—**+10 ft. reach** for melee attacks this
turn. |
| 2 | Your body flickers—**+2 AC** as you momentarily phase out of reality. |
| 3 | Illusions swirl around you—enemies attacking you must succeed on a DC 13

Wisdom saving throw or have disadvantage. |

| 4 | You generate heat or frost—**1d6 fire or cold damage** to creatures that hit
you with melee attacks. |
| 5 | Your senses sharpen—**advantage on Perception checks** until the start of
your next turn. |
| 6 | Your voice twists—**advantage on Intimidation checks** and creatures
that hear you speak take 1d6 psychic damage. |
This feature offers new and unpredictable utility with each transformation,
making you a dynamic presence in combat.
Revelation of the Real
6th-level Circle of the Weird feature
You can cast Light at will, but when cast through this feature, the light reveals
the true nature of creatures and objects affected by the Weirding.
- Creatures hidden by illusions, shapeshifting, or invisibility become briefly
revealed within the light for 1 round.
- Objects disguised or enchanted appear as they truly are, granting you insights
into curses, enchantments, or magical traps.
Additionally, when you concentrate on a spell that creates light (such as Daylight
or Faerie Fire), creatures illuminated by the spell have disadvantage on saving throws
against your druid spells.
Twist the Unseen
10th-level Circle of the Weird feature
The Weirding allows you to bend reality in unpredictable ways. When you use
your Wild Shape, you may choose one of the following effects instead of assuming an
animal form:
- Flicker Between: You shift between realities, gaining resistance to all damage
and moving through creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. This effect
lasts for 1 minute, or until you are incapacitated.
- Illusory Echo: You create an illusionary duplicate of yourself, which moves as
you do. Creatures must succeed on an Intelligence saving throw (DC 15) to tell the
difference between you and your echo. If they fail, they cannot target you directly until
the start of your next turn.
Weird Manifestation
14th-level Circle of the Weird feature
At the height of your power, you can pull unstable forces directly from the astral
rift into the material plane. As an action, you can unleash a Weird Manifestation that
affects all creatures within a 30-foot radius centered on you. Choose two effects from
the list below, or roll randomly:
| d8 | Weird Manifestation Effect |
|:--:|------------------------------------------|
| 1 | Time slows—affected creatures cannot take reactions for 1 minute. |

| 2 | Gravity shifts—creatures within the area are either pushed 10 ft. away from
you or pulled 10 ft. toward you (your choice). |
| 3 | Voices of unseen entities whisper—creatures must make a Wisdom save (DC
16) or be Frightened until the end of their next turn. |
| 4 | Colors invert—affected creatures have disadvantage on attack rolls for 1
minute. |
| 5 | The ground warps—**difficult terrain** spreads throughout the area for 1
minute. |
| 6 | Objects levitate—non-attended objects within the area float freely, up to 10
feet off the ground. |
| 7 | Healing anomaly—each creature in the area regains 2d8 hit points. |
| 8 | Ethereal surge—**invisible creatures** within the area are forced into
visibility for 1 minute. |
Once you use this feature, you must finish a long rest before using it again.
Playing a Circle of the Weird Druid
The Circle of the Weird offers a blend of unpredictability, utility, and danger. As
a member of this circle, your abilities reflect the chaos and transformation inherent in
the Weirding. Your character might see themselves as a mediator between the natural
and unnatural worlds, using chaos as a tool to heal or disrupt as needed.
Roleplaying Considerations
- How do you interpret the Weirding? Do you believe it is a blessing, a curse, or a
puzzle to be solved?
- How does unpredictability shape your worldview? Do you embrace change, or
struggle to control the forces you wield?
- What led you to the Circle of the Weird? Was it curiosity, necessity, or an
encounter with a strange force you could not ignore?
Fighter
The Fighter Class in Ryndor
Fighters are the steadfast warriors of Ryndor, trained in the art of combat from a
young age. Whether fighting on the ground, commanding an airship crew, or mastering
ancient weapon techniques, Fighters bring skill, strategy, and strength to every
battlefield. They are found in all corners of the land—guarding the cities, exploring the
wilderness, or engaging in competitions of strength and prowess in the arena. Fighters
in Ryndor are as diverse as the regions they come from, with their techniques shaped by
the land, sky, and strange forces like The Weirding.
Warriors of Every Kind
Fighters in Ryndor adopt countless roles, from disciplined knights sworn to
protect the realm, to bold adventurers carving their path through the unknown. Some
serve as mercenaries or soldiers, while others become champions in the Kigan Uldar
Games, where the most daring and skilled combatants compete for glory. Many
Fighters also dedicate themselves to causes—whether defending communities from

Weirded creatures, mastering ancient martial traditions, or unearthing the lost combat
knowledge of Nebernoria.
The Weirding and Fighters
The Weirding has drastically altered both the landscape of Ryndor and the
techniques of combat itself. Some Fighters have adapted to these strange changes,
incorporating elements of Weirded environments into their tactics. Warriors who brave
Weird Zones learn to expect the unexpected, mastering fast reactions and strange
combat strategies to outlast supernatural effects. However, others are more cautious,
relying on tradition and discipline to remain grounded amidst the chaos.
In this new age, even the most skilled Fighters must stay alert—every battlefield
may shift beneath their feet, and every opponent could harbor unforeseen dangers..
Role in the World
Fighters play an essential role in Ryndor’s society. In Eveltoft, they serve as
guards, soldiers, and gladiators in the city’s many competitions. In more rural regions,
Fighters act as protectors, defending towns and villages from marauding beasts or rival
factions. Ban Mynydd's deep mines rely on Fighters to clear out dangerous creatures
lurking underground, while airship crews value skilled Fighters to fend off airborne
raiders. Those Fighters who venture into the Weirded wilderness face immense danger
but often return with stories and treasures beyond imagining.
Fighters are also key figures in the Kigan Uldar and Utfordring competitions.
Their mastery of weaponry and tactics makes them crowd favorites, and many seek
fame and fortune through victory in these grand events. However, with the Weirding
creeping into more parts of the world, Fighters are finding their skills tested in ways
they never expected.
Fighters in Society
Each culture within Ryndor views Fighters differently. Some regions treat them
as noble defenders, while others see them as mere mercenaries-for-hire. In Eveltoft,
Fighters trained in the Heibury District are respected for their discipline, while the
warriors of Ban Mynydd carry the weight of tradition. Many rural Fighters serve as both
hunters and defenders, protecting their homes from wild beasts and strange threats.
In Ryndor’s ever-shifting power dynamics, Fighters may align with different
factions—mercenary guilds, royal armies, or shadowy organizations. Some use their
skills to protect the realm, while others pursue personal gain or follow their own moral
code. Regardless of their allegiance, Fighters are always at the forefront of conflict,
ready to face whatever challenges the world throws their way.
Creating a Fighter in Ryndor
When creating a Fighter in Ryndor, consider where your character learned their
craft. Were they trained by a formal academy, like those in the Heibury District, or did
they learn their skills through hardship and survival in the wilderness? Did your Fighter
compete in the Kigan Uldar Games, or do they dream of commanding an airship as a
Skybound Captain? Perhaps your Fighter has adapted to life within a Weirded zone,

learning to fight in strange and unpredictable conditions.
Questions to Consider:
- What motivates your Fighter? Honor, wealth, revenge, or something else?
- Does your Fighter embrace tradition, or are they an innovator on the
battlefield?
- How has the Weirding impacted your Fighter’s journey? Do they fear it, or have
they adapted to thrive within it?
Skybound Captain
Skybound Captain
A Fighter Archetype for DnD 5e
"The skies do not forgive the careless. To command an airship is to command fate
itself."
Skybound Captains are tactical masters of both combat and airship command.
These fighters are experts at maneuvering through unstable environments, making
lightning-fast decisions, and inspiring their crew to greatness. Whether serving as
daring explorers, military officers, or even cunning sky-pirates, they thrive in the chaos
of aerial combat, blending leadership, agility, and strength.
Skybound Captain Features
Airship Command
When you choose this archetype at 3rd level, you become proficient in
navigator’s tools and vehicles (air) if you do not already have them. Your experience as
a captain gives you tactical insight and battlefield leadership.
- Sky Orders: As a bonus action, you can give a tactical order to an ally within 30
feet of you who can hear you. That ally gains advantage on the next attack roll, ability
check, or saving throw they make before the start of your next turn. You can use this
ability a number of times equal to your proficiency bonus, regaining all expended uses
after a long rest.
Master of the Skies
At 3rd level, you excel in unstable environments like airships or moving
platforms. You gain the following benefits:
- Steady Ground: You have advantage on saving throws to avoid being knocked
prone or moved against your will while on a moving surface or in flight.
- Acrobatic Proficiency: You gain proficiency in Acrobatics, or if you already
have it, you gain expertise (doubling your proficiency bonus for Acrobatics checks).
7th Level: Windborne Maneuvering
You move with precision, striking while on the move.
- When you take the Dash action, you can make one melee or ranged weapon
attack as part of that action.
- You ignore non-magical difficult terrain, and you can move through the space
of friendly creatures during your turn without expending extra movement.

10th Level: Captain’s Aura
Your command presence bolsters your allies. You project an aura of leadership in
a 10-foot radius around you. While in this aura:
- Allies add your proficiency bonus to initiative rolls.
- Allies operating vehicles (air or water) add your proficiency bonus to skill
checks related to navigation or control.
This aura expands to 30 feet at 18th level.
15th Level: Eye of the Storm
You thrive in chaos, always finding opportunity in adversity.
- When you roll initiative, you can swap your initiative result with that of a
willing ally within 30 feet.
- If an ally within 10 feet of you must make a saving throw, you can use your
reaction to grant them advantage on that saving throw.
18th Level: Stormlord’s Wrath
At the height of your mastery, you channel the power of the storm and command
both ship and crew with unparalleled skill.
- Once per long rest, you can summon an electrical storm to rage around your
airship or platform, lasting for 1 minute. During the storm:
- Enemy creatures have disadvantage on ranged attacks against your crew.
- All movement speed for your airship or platform increases by 10 feet.
- You and your allies within 30 feet deal an extra 2d8 lightning or thunder
damage on one weapon attack per turn.
Additionally, while aboard an airship, you and your allies within 30 feet gain
resistance to lightning and thunder damage.
Roleplaying the Skybound Captain
Skybound Captains are natural leaders with experience navigating perilous skies.
Whether you are an honorable officer, a fearless pirate, or an independent adventurer,
your tactical abilities and airship expertise are central to your story. These captains can
take on diverse roles, from fleet commanders defending against aerial threats to
explorers charting new frontiers in Ryndor’s skies, including the Weirded zones.
Skybound Captain Combat Tactics
- Use Sky Orders strategically to give allies the edge in critical moments.
- Take advantage of Windborne Maneuvering to stay mobile, strike effectively,
and escape difficult situations.
- In larger battles, your Captain’s Aura ensures your party strikes fast and
navigates hazardous encounters with ease.
- When facing overwhelming odds, Eye of the Storm can rearrange initiative and
turn the tide in your favor.
- Stormlord’s Wrath can devastate your enemies with lightning-imbued attacks,
while enhancing your ship’s speed and defense.
Monk

## Monk Class in Ryndor

Introduction
The Monks of Ryndor are disciplined warriors who channel both the physical and
metaphysical into perfect harmony. Drawing from traditions rooted in elemental
balance and the philosophical ideals of ancient practitioners, Ryndorian Monks seek
inner enlightenment while mastering the energy around them. Some Monks live in
isolated sanctuaries, perfecting their craft far from civilization, while others wander the
land, seeking to balance forces thrown into disarray by the Weirding.
Monastic Traditions
Monks in Ryndor are shaped by their origins and the focus of their training. While
they all possess extraordinary martial prowess, each monk tradition specializes in a
different path, blending combat with unique spiritual or elemental disciplines. From
mountain sanctuaries to bustling districts of Eveltoft, these traditions thrive,
connecting body, mind, and the shifting energies of the land.
Elemental Influence
The Weirding has left its mark on many of the monasteries of Ryndor. Monks
attuned to these new energies develop unique abilities tied to specific elemental
principles—such as water’s flow, earth’s resilience, or time’s subtle shifts. This
infusion of strange energies enhances their martial arts, allowing them to manipulate
the environment and wield powerful ki techniques in unexpected ways.
Life as a Monk
Monks in Ryndor can be found meditating in ancient sanctuaries, serving as
wandering sages, or even acting as protectors for communities plagued by instability.
Many Monks embrace simple living, wearing garments reflecting both ancient
traditions and practical modern adaptations—often inspired by the Norse-Chinese
blend that permeates Ryndorian fashion. Their clothing incorporates wraps, loose
robes, and intricate knot patterns, sometimes marked with subtle glyphs representing
the flow of ki.
Unique Monastic Orders
Monasteries across Ryndor have developed distinct philosophies and techniques
to adapt to the challenges of the land and the Weirding. Some focus on elemental
balance, integrating the natural forces into their martial discipline, while others delve
into metaphysical arts, harnessing the strange energies of time or space to enhance
their agility or insight. Here are some examples of orders you may encounter:
- Order of the Flowing Tide: Monks of this order embody fluidity, adopting
water’s adaptability to avoid harm and strike with precision.
- Order of the Stalwart Stone: Focused on resilience, these monks absorb
punishment and redirect force like immovable stone.
- Order of the Shattered Hourglass: These monks explore temporal shifts, using

strange time-based ki techniques to strike faster than the eye can follow.
- Order of the Empty Sky: Masters of air and space, they leap vast distances and
control their environment with astounding grace.
Monks and the Weirding
The Weirding has led some monks to unlock abilities thought impossible—such
as phasing through solid walls or slowing an opponent’s perception of time. These
powers often come at a price, as monks walk the delicate line between balance and
chaos. While they attempt to master the Weirding’s influence through meditation and
discipline, not all survive the mental strain of dealing with this unpredictable force.
Role in Ryndor
Monks serve diverse roles throughout Ryndor, acting as mediators, explorers,
warriors, and sages. Many find themselves drawn to places affected by the Weirding,
seeking to restore balance or unravel mysteries. Some offer guidance to those lost in
spiritual turmoil, while others use their skills to combat supernatural threats emerging
from the Rift to Nebernoria. The versatility and wisdom of Ryndorian monks make them
invaluable allies in any adventuring party, and their pursuit of mastery ensures they are
always evolving.
Way of Shifting Powers
Way of Shifting Powers
Monks who follow the Way of Shifting Powers learn to channel and manipulate
the volatile resonance that flows through Ryndor. These monks see themselves as
vessels for elemental energy, allowing it to ebb and flow through them. Practitioners
master how to adapt their techniques in harmony with shifting resonances—whether
tapping into fire’s destructive surge or the calm, healing energy of water. They focus
not on control, but on embracing change, riding the currents of magic that permeate
the world.
Features of the Way of Shifting Powers
3rd Level: Resonant Strike
When you make an unarmed strike, you can infuse it with shifting resonance.
Choose an energy type (fire, cold, thunder, or radiant) when you strike. Your attack
deals an additional 1d6 damage of the chosen type. You can change the energy type each
time you hit with an unarmed strike.
6th Level: Flux Step
You can tap into the unstable energies of Ryndor to teleport short distances. As a
bonus action, spend 1 Ki point to teleport up to 20 feet to a location you can see. When
you reappear, creatures within 5 feet of you must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw
(DC equal to 8 + your proficiency bonus + your Wisdom modifier) or take 2d6 force
damage as a burst of energy surges around you.
11th Level: Elemental Confluence

At the start of each of your turns, you attune yourself to a different elemental
resonance: fire, air, water, or earth. Depending on your attunement, you gain the
following benefits:
- Fire: Your attacks ignite enemies, dealing an additional 1d8 fire damage.
- Air: You gain advantage on Dexterity (Acrobatics) checks and can move an extra
10 feet.
- Water: You can heal yourself or an ally within 10 feet for 1d8 HP as a bonus
action.
- Earth: You gain temporary hit points equal to your Wisdom modifier at the start
of your turn.
You can change your attunement at the start of each of your turns without
spending an action.
17th Level: Avatar of Resonance
You unleash the full force of resonance within you. As an action, spend 5 Ki points
to enter a state of perfect harmony with the elements for 1 minute. While in this state:
- You gain resistance to all damage types except psychic.
- Each time you take the Attack action, you can switch your elemental resonance
mid-attack, gaining the benefits of different elements for each hit.
- You can teleport up to 30 feet as a bonus action, leaving a blast of energy in your
wake that deals 3d8 force damage to creatures within 5 feet.
You can use this ability once per long rest.
The Way of Shifting Powers emphasizes adaptability and magical resonance,
blending the physical prowess of monks with the elemental forces of Ryndor. These
monks are agents of change, flowing with power that reflects the unstable, shifting
energies of the Weirding, giving them a unique role both on and off the battlefield.
Paladin
The Paladin in Ryndor
Paladins in Ryndor are champions of conviction, wielding magic through their
sheer force of belief. Whether pledging themselves to gods, ideals, or cosmic forces,
they are defenders of justice, hope, and order in a land often twisted by the Weirding’s
chaotic influence. These warriors exemplify the duality of power—righteous protectors
or dangerous zealots—depending on the oaths they swear and the causes they uphold.
Paladins and the Weirding
The nature of a Paladin’s oath is particularly vulnerable to the Weirding. A broken
oath can corrupt a Paladin’s powers, twisting them into a perversion of their original
ideals. Some Paladins embrace these changes, believing the Weirding is a test of their
resolve, while others struggle against the transformations within. Weirded oaths lead to
strange powers—blessings altered in unforeseen ways or auras that shift unpredictably.
The Role of Paladins in Ryndor’s Struggles
In a realm torn by ambition, elemental shifts, and astral rifts, Paladins are often

more than just fighters. They serve as arbiters, emissaries, and warriors of faith,
safeguarding the balance between order and chaos. Many have become leaders in
Eveltoft and Ban Mynydd, standing as symbols of hope or as feared enforcers of harsh
justice. Paladins also find themselves as mediators between mortals and strange beings
from Nebernoria, using their divine magic to negotiate or protect.
Oaths in Ryndor
The choice of oath is deeply personal in Ryndor. Some Paladins swear Oaths of
Redemption, seeking to heal the land ravaged by the Weirding, while others pursue
Oaths of the Vanguard, vowing to guard Ryndor against Nebernoria’s creeping
influence. Unique oaths tied to the land’s elemental magic or to the enigmatic
Custodians of Prosperity have also emerged, influencing how Paladins interact with the
world and their powers.
Auras of Stability
The Paladin’s aura magic is highly sought after, particularly in regions heavily
affected by the Weirding. These auras can provide sanctuaries from chaotic shifts,
anchoring reality for allies. Some orders train Paladins specifically to patrol unstable
zones, offering respite for the people struggling with strange phenomena.
Champions of Ideal and Cause
Paladins are found throughout Ryndor, aligned with cities, councils, or elemental
orders. Some follow ancient codes rooted in the lore of Ban Mynydd, while others swear
modern oaths to protect Eveltoft and its people from emerging threats. Whether as
wandering knights or leaders of powerful sects, these Paladins channel the divine or
cosmic resonance to shape the future of the land.
Oath of Resonance
Oath of Resonance
Paladins who swear the Oath of Resonance pledge themselves to maintain the
delicate harmony between the forces of Ryndor. Whether it’s balancing elemental
magic, protecting the stability of reality from the Weirding, or acting as a bridge
between opposing ideals, these Paladins serve as guardians of equilibrium. They are
warriors of alignment—working not to impose rigid order or chaos but to preserve the
balance that keeps the world whole.
Tenets of Resonance
Paladins who follow this path live by the following principles:
- Balance in All Things: Recognize that both light and shadow, creation and
destruction, have their place in the world. Maintain the balance.
- Resonance with Others: Seek to understand others’ beliefs and actions, even
when they seem opposed. Harmony can only be achieved through empathy.
- Ward Against the Unnatural: Protect the world from forces that would distort it
—especially those from Nebernoria or unstable Weirding zones.
- Flow Like Water, Stand Like Stone: Be adaptable in times of change, yet

immovable in your values when faced with corruption or imbalance.
Oath Spells
Starting at 3rd level, you gain the following oath spells:
Level Spells
3rd Detect Magic, Sanctuary
5th Calm Emotions, Warding Bond
9th Dispel Magic, Protection from Energy
13th Aura of Purity, Guardian of Nature
17th Wall of Force, Greater Restoration
Channel Divinity
At 3rd level, you gain the following Channel Divinity options:
- Resonant Strike: As a bonus action, infuse your weapon with elemental energy.
On your next hit, choose a damage type (fire, cold, lightning, or radiant) to deal an
additional 2d10 damage and push the target 10 feet away.
- Field of Alignment: As an action, create an aura within 10 feet of you for 1
minute. While inside, creatures can reroll saving throws against effects that impose
conditions (such as fear or charm).
Aura of Equilibrium (7th level)
You radiate an aura that calms chaotic forces. Within 10 feet of you, any time a
creature rolls with advantage or disadvantage, they treat both rolls as equal to the
higher of the two values. At 18th level, the range of this aura increases to 30 feet.
Resonant Reflection (15th level)
When targeted by an elemental effect (fire, cold, lightning, etc.), you can use your
reaction to absorb the energy. You take half damage, and the next melee attack you
make within 1 minute deals the absorbed damage type as extra damage.
Avatar of Balance (20th level)
As an action, you can become a beacon of cosmic harmony for 1 minute. While in
this form:
- You gain resistance to all damage.
- Creatures within 30 feet of you cannot have advantage or disadvantage.
- You can change the damage type of any attack you make to one of the following:
fire, cold, radiant, or necrotic.
Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you finish a long rest.
Oath of Discord
Oath of Discord
The Oath of Discord attracts Paladins who revel in chaos, destruction, and the
unraveling of societal or cosmic harmony. These paladins reject balance and order,

embracing entropy as the true state of existence. Whether seeking power through
destruction or serving a malevolent force, Paladins of Discord sow conflict wherever
they go, uniting only to tear down the status quo.
Tenets of Discord
These paladins thrive in chaos and follow these principles:
- Spread Chaos: Instability is power. Disrupt any force that seeks control or
harmony.
- Foster Betrayal: Trust is a weakness; manipulate others to turn on each other
for your benefit.
- Revel in Ruin: Destruction fuels growth—create conflict and thrive in its
aftermath.
- Embrace Power: Seize power by any means, and show no mercy to those who
stand in your way.
Oath Spells
At 3rd level, you gain access to the following spells:
Level Spells
3rd Cause Fear, Bane
5th Crown of Madness, Shatter
9th Bestow Curse, Fear
13th Greater Invisibility, Confusion
17th Cloudkill, Dominate Person
Channel Divinity
When you take this oath at 3rd level, you gain the following Channel Divinity
options:
- Agony’s Touch: As a bonus action, curse a creature you can see within 30 feet.
For 1 minute, they take an additional 1d8 necrotic damage whenever they take damage.
- Seed of Discord: As an action, choose two creatures within 30 feet. They must
succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or be compelled to attack one another for 1 minute,
as if under the compelled duel spell.
Aura of Strife (7th level)
Your presence fuels conflict. Creatures within 10 feet of you cannot benefit from
temporary hit points, and whenever a creature in the aura makes a melee attack, it deals
extra damage equal to your Charisma modifier (minimum of +1). The aura increases to
30 feet at 18th level.
Harbinger of Betrayal (15th level)
You gain resistance to psychic damage, and you can use your reaction when an
ally within 10 feet of you makes a saving throw. The ally automatically fails the saving
throw, and you gain 2d8 temporary hit points.
Avatar of Chaos (20th level)

As an action, you can awaken the full power of discord within you for 1 minute.
While in this state:
- Creatures within 30 feet of you have disadvantage on saving throws.
- Whenever a creature takes damage within your aura, another creature of your
choice within range also takes half that damage.
- Once per turn, when you hit with a weapon attack, the target becomes
frightened until the end of your next turn.
After using this feature, you cannot do so again until you finish a long rest.
The Oath of Discord paladins live for conflict, wielding chaos as both weapon and
shield. They leave ruin in their wake, reveling in betrayal and thriving in the crumbling
remains of peace.
Ranger
Ranger Class in Ryndor
In the vast and unpredictable landscape of Ryndor, Rangers stand as masters of
survival, navigation, and reconnaissance. They are adept at thriving in both the
untamed wilderness and urban sprawl, moving with quiet precision through dense
forests, shifting sand dunes, and bustling markets. Rangers in Ryndor blend ancient
traditions with new techniques—many learn the ways of both elemental resonance and
primal intuition, making them uniquely attuned to the Weirding that affects the land.
Themes of the Ranger Class in Ryndor
- Guardians of the Frontier: Rangers serve as scouts, trackers, and protectors,
often patrolling dangerous borders or maintaining the safety of remote settlements.
Whether guarding the trade routes of Surreymouth or the dense Hurstwold Forest, they
are always on the move.
- The Resonance of Nature: Many Rangers develop a strange attunement to the
elements of Ryndor. They can sense shifts in weather patterns, the strange pulses of
Weirded zones, and track the subtle flow of life in regions affected by elemental
resonance.
- Wanderers and Guides: Rangers rarely stay in one place for long. Their journeys
through the wildlands or the decaying remnants of ancient cities make them invaluable
guides, often employed by scholars, merchants, and adventurers alike.
Subcultures and Regional Roles
- The Greenhearts of Hurstwold: These Rangers are deeply in tune with nature’s
primal forces, making them exceptional trackers and guardians of wildlife.
- Voidstriders of Ban Mynydd: Masters of stealth and exploration, these Rangers
navigate dangerous mines, Weird zones, and dimensional rifts to scout for threats and
ancient artifacts.
- Seawatchers of Surreymouth: Coastal Rangers who patrol the shores and trade
routes. They specialize in managing maritime dangers like storms and sea monsters.
The Ranger and the Weirding

The Weirding presents a unique challenge—and opportunity—for Rangers. Some
develop strange abilities from exposure to Weirded zones, granting them limited
powers of foresight or the ability to sense hidden pathways. Others choose to guard the
land from the harmful influence of the Weirding, hunting down dangerous anomalies
that threaten Ryndor’s fragile balance.
Archetypes Unique to Ryndor
- Skyward Stalkers: Rangers attuned to the skies who ride giant birds and patrol
trade winds.
- Echo Wardens: Rangers who track resonant anomalies caused by the Weirding,
wielding elemental forces in subtle ways.
- Lantern Guides: Operating primarily in Eveltoft, these Rangers specialize in
urban navigation, using the lights of enchanted lanterns to reveal hidden pathways and
creatures.
Rangers in Ryndor embody resilience, adaptability, and loyalty to their chosen
path. Whether traversing ancient ruins or standing guard against unseen forces, they
are the first line of defense—and often the last hope—against the ever-shifting dangers
of the Weirded Lands.
Arcane Mechanist
Ranger Archetype: Arcane Mechanist
The Arcane Mechanist is a Ranger who merges nature’s mastery with the
technological ingenuity of Ryndor. These Rangers are experts in using and maintaining
the realm’s advanced tools, airships, and mechanical companions. Rather than drawing
power solely from primal forces, the Arcane Mechanist taps into technology to enhance
their abilities, making them invaluable guides, scouts, and saboteurs. Whether
calibrating intricate gadgets or adapting machinery to strange environments, these
Rangers are masters of innovation and resourcefulness.
Arcane Mechanist Features
3rd Level: Tinker’s Tools & Tech Sense
You gain proficiency with Tinker’s Tools. Additionally, you develop a sixth sense
for machinery and arcane devices. As an action, you can detect magical or technological
traps, contraptions, and energy sources within 60 feet. You can also identify how to
disable or manipulate them with a successful Intelligence (Investigation) check.
3rd Level: Mechanical Companion
You build a mechanical companion, a small automaton (choose a form: bird,
spider, or fox). Your companion acts on your turn and can use the Help action or deliver
a simple ranged attack (1d6 piercing damage, range 30/60 ft). If it is destroyed, you can
repair it over a short or long rest.
7th Level: Deployable Devices
You invent small gadgets to aid in exploration and combat. You can prepare two

devices each day, choosing from the following:
- Smoke Bomb: Creates a 10-foot-radius cloud of smoke for 1 minute. All
creatures inside are heavily obscured.
- Shock Dart: Launches a small projectile. On a hit, the target takes 2d8 lightning
damage and can’t take reactions until the start of its next turn.
- Spring Trap: Sets a hidden mechanical trap that deals 2d6 piercing damage and
restrains the first creature to trigger it (Strength save to escape).
11th Level: Overclock
You push your devices beyond their intended limits. Once per short or long rest,
you can activate Overclock Mode. For 1 minute, your mechanical companion gains an
additional action per turn and advantage on all attack rolls. Additionally, you can use
two deployable devices as a bonus action during Overclock.
15th Level: Arcane Infusion
Your understanding of technology allows you to imbue magic into your
inventions. You can now store a spell of 3rd level or lower into your mechanical
companion or any deployable device. Once the spell is triggered (such as when the trap
activates or the companion attacks), the stored spell takes effect. You regain the use of
this ability after a long rest.
The Arcane Mechanist thrives in Ryndor’s technologically advanced landscapes,
making them essential allies on airships, within arcane laboratories, and when
navigating Weirded zones. With an arsenal of gadgets and a mechanical companion by
their side, they harness both nature and technology in perfect harmony.
Rogue
Rogue Class in Ryndor
In Ryndor, Rogues are not merely thieves and tricksters; they are adaptive
survivors, master infiltrators, and cunning strategists. The evolving complexities of the
Weirding have only sharpened their talents. Rogues serve as spies, treasure hunters,
black market operators, and saboteurs, blending stealth, wit, and an innate ability to
manipulate environments—whether in a bustling city or Weirded wilderness. They are
the ones who find opportunities where others see barriers, navigating dangerous trade
routes, crime networks, and political intrigue with unmatched expertise.
Masters of Deception and Strategy
Rogues thrive within Ryndor’s labyrinthine politics and dangerous trade
networks. They may operate behind the scenes in Surreymouth’s black market, gather
intelligence on behalf of Eveltoft’s Crystal Scholars, or serve as elite operatives hired by
the Custodians of Prosperity. From the back alleys of Gullborg to the untamed depths of
the Weirded Hurstwold Forest, these agents are everywhere, unseen but always
watching. Their subtle manipulation of events makes them invaluable, though many
question their loyalty.

## Stealth in the Weirded Lands

The unpredictable forces of the Weirding provide both challenge and opportunity
for Rogues. With a knack for improvisation, they exploit the strange physics and hidden
pathways caused by Weird Zones. Many Rogues have perfected the art of blending their
skills with the weirding’s unpredictable effects, mastering the ability to vanish from
sight or slip through dimensional gaps.
Whether avoiding the scrutiny of the Keepers of the Rift, smuggling Weirded
artifacts from Nebernoria, or deceiving magical creatures drawn to the Rift’s strange
energy, Rogues in Ryndor have learned to thrive in a world where nothing is certain,
and everything can be used to their advantage.
Subtle Yet Deadly
The Rogue’s toolkit includes stealth, lockpicking, sleight of hand, and the ability
to read people and situations at a glance. They rely on finesse over brute strength, using
poison-tipped blades, hidden weapons, and traps. In the Weirded Lands, Rogues favor
mundane objects imbued with strange quirks—items whose effects are unpredictable
but highly effective in the right hands.
The Rogue class embodies the unpredictable nature of Ryndor itself—always
adaptable, always two steps ahead. These agents, thieves, and tricksters may serve
noble or selfish causes, but in a world ruled by uncertainty, they are the ones best
equipped to thrive.
Riftstalker
Riftstalker
Archetype Overview:
Riftstalkers are Rogues who have mastered the art of moving between
dimensions, exploiting strange anomalies and spatial quirks caused by the Weirding.
These nimble operatives thrive in areas destabilized by the Rift to Nebernoria, slipping
through folds in space, vanishing at a moment’s notice, and reappearing where they are
least expected. Whether acting as smugglers, spies, or covert agents, Riftstalkers bend
space to their advantage, becoming elusive hunters in a world filled with instability.
Features of the Riftstalker Archetype
3rd Level – Dimensional Step:
You learn to momentarily shift between spaces. As a bonus action, you can
teleport up to 15 feet to an unoccupied space you can see. This ability can be used a
number of times equal to your proficiency bonus per long rest.
9th Level – Anomaly Sense:
You develop an instinct for detecting disturbances in space. You have advantage
on Perception (Wisdom) and Investigation (Intelligence) checks to detect hidden
portals, dimensional anomalies, or creatures affected by spatial magic.
13th Level – Rift Ambush:

After using your Dimensional Step, you can add your sneak attack damage even if
you don’t meet the usual conditions, as long as you appear adjacent to your target.
17th Level – Fractured Self:
You can summon alternate versions of yourself from nearby timelines. As an
action, you create 1d4 illusory duplicates that last for 1 minute. These duplicates mimic
your movements, imposing disadvantage on all attack rolls targeting you.
The Riftstalker Rogue embodies the unpredictability of the Weirding and the
dangers lurking between realms. Whether working as a treasure hunter or shadowy
operative, they are the masters of the unseen paths, always one step ahead—or several
steps away—when trouble finds them.
Sev’rinn
UNDER CONSTRUCTION
