Figure out the elemental charge rules as per the shift ability
Figure out multi-classing to other attunements
Build an example PC for each attunement - add to “Faces and the Souls Within”
Sev’rinn: Elemental Warriors of Ryndor
Class Overview
The Sev’rinn are not mere spellcasters; they are living conduits of elemental
power, capable of summoning the primal forces of nature in the heat of battle.
Elemental mastery is woven into their identity—whether they conjure fire to engulf
their weapons, invoke gusts of wind to evade attacks, or summon stone armor midbattle. A Sev’rinn commands elemental magic with instinct rather than study, adapting
moment by moment to the demands of combat. However, every spark of power drawn
from the elements risks opening a doorway to the Weirding, a chaotic influence that
changes the battlefield in unpredictable ways.
Sev’rinn use Elemental Techniques—swift invocations and battle actions
powered by Elemental Charges, rather than traditional spell slots. These warriors blur
the line between martial combatants and arcane masters, making them a force to be
reckoned with on the battlefield.
Class Features Summary
| Level | Features | Elemental Charges | Techniques Known | Weirding Surge DC
|
|------------|--------------------------------------|---------------------|---------------------|------------------------|
| 1st | Elemental Attunement, Combat Techniques | 2 | 3 | 10 |
| 2nd | Elemental Shift, Weirding Surge | 3 | 4 | 11 |
| 3rd | Comabt Technique | 3 | 4 | 11 |

| 5th | Channel Power | 4 | 6 | 12 |
| 7th | Combat Technique | 4 | 6 | 12 |
| 9th | Resonant Flow | 5 | 8 | 14 |
| 10th | Combat Technique | 5 | 8 | 14 |
| 13th | Weirding Infusion | 6 | 9 | 15 |
| 17th | Elemental Avatar | 8 | 10 | 17 |
Core Class Features
Hit Points
- Hit Dice: 1d10 per Sev’rinn level
- Hit Points at 1st Level: 10 + Constitution modifier
- Hit Points at Higher Levels: 1d10 + Constitution modifier per Sev’rinn level
Proficiencies
- Armor: Light armor, medium armor
- Weapons: Simple weapons, martial weapons
- Tools: None
- Saving Throws: Constitution, Wisdom
- Skills: Choose two from Arcana, Athletics, Nature, Perception, and Survival
1st Level: Elemental Attunement
At 1st level, you attune yourself to one of five elemental forces—**Fire, Water,
Air, Stone, Nature, Light or Soul**—which grants unique effects that enhance your
combat prowess. Your Attunement also determines the bonus effect when you use
certain Techniques. You can choose the benefits of a new attunement with each new
level of Sev’rinn. For example, your first level of Tideborn, you can choose from the
Tideborn combat techniques. At your second character level, you choose to take a level
in Emberclad. You would choose from the Emberclad combat techniques, since it’s your
first level in Emberclad.
1st Level: Combat Techniques
You learn three Elemental Techniques at 1st level from the Sev’rinn technique
list. You can use a Technique by spending 1 Elemental Charge. Techniques are bonus
actions or reactions, making them ideal for battle. You regain all spent Charges at the
end of a short or long rest.
3rd Level: Elemental Shift
At 2nd level, Sev’rinn gain the ability to tap into the raw, transformative power of
their elemental attunement through Elemental Shift. This power enables them to
embody the essence of their chosen element temporarily, gaining dynamic benefits that
change as the shift progresses.
Activation
Action:
You activate
Elemental Shift

as a
bonus action
.
Duration:
The shift lasts for
1 minute
or until you end it as a
free action
on your turn.
Uses:
You can use
Elemental Shift
a number of times equal to your
proficiency bonus
. All expended uses are restored when you complete a
long rest
.
Choosing an Elemental Effect
Once Elemental Shift is active, you can either roll 1d6 or choose one effect from
the Elemental Shift Tablecorresponding to your attunement.
Rolling:
If you roll at the start of your shift, you receive the effect indicated by the dice roll,
which applies immediately.
Locking:
Alternatively, at the time of activation, you may lock in one of the six effects listed
in your Elemental Shift Table. If locked, the effect does not change for the shift’s full
duration.
Changing the Elemental Effect
At the
start of each of your turns
, you can choose to:
Roll the
1d6
again to determine a new effect for the remainder of that turn.
Maintain the effect from the previous turn without re-rolling.
If you roll,
the new effect overrides the previous one until the start of your next turn or another
roll.
2nd Level: Weirding Surge
Whenever you use a Combat Technique, roll a d20. On a natural 1, a Weirding
Surge occurs. Weirding Surges cause strange and chaotic effects to manifest, warping

reality around you. The DC to resist or control the Surge increases as you level.
Weirding Surge Table (Roll 1d6):
| d6 | Weirding Effect |
|--------|------------------------------------------|
| 1 | A rift briefly opens, summoning a random creature for 1 minute.
| 2 | Gravity reverses in a 10-foot radius around you for 1 round.
| 3 | A harmless glowing orb follows you for the next 10 minutes.
| 4 | The terrain around you shifts, creating difficult terrain for 1 round.
| 5 | Your voice echoes unnaturally, imposing disadvantage on Charisma checks.
| 6 | Time flickers—your next action repeats itself automatically.
5th Level: Channel Power
At 5th level, you unlock the ability to unleash powerful elemental bursts tied to
your current Attunement. As an action, you can spend 2 Elemental Charges to activate
one of the following bursts:
- Fire (Emberclad): Release a 20-foot cone of flame. Creatures within the area
must make a Dexterity saving throw or take 6d8 fire damage (half on success).
- Water (Skycaller): Heal yourself and allies within 10 feet for 3d8 hit points.
- Air (Voidstrider): Create a powerful gust that pushes creatures within 15 feet
back (Strength save to resist).
- Stone (Lithomage): Gain resistance to all damage until the start of your next
turn.
- Nature (Greenheart): Vines erupt in a 15-foot radius, restraining enemies
(Strength save to escape).
- Time (Chronomancer): You and one ally within 30 feet take an additional action
on your next turn.
- Space (Voidstrider): Instantly teleport 30 feet to a point you can see.
- Soul (Eidolon): Reduce the movement speed of creatures within 20 feet by half
for 1 minute (Wisdom save ends).
- Light (Luminor): Unleash a burst of radiant energy. Creatures within 15 feet
must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or be blinded for 1 minute (repeat save at
the end of each turn).
9th Level: Resonant Flow
At 9th level, you become adept at maintaining a steady flow of elemental energy.
Once per turn, when you spend an Elemental Charge, you can immediately regain 1
Charge by rolling a natural 18-20 on an attack or ability check.
17th Level: Elemental Avatar
At 17th level, you can fully embody an elemental force. For 1 minute, you gain
resistance to all damage and can change your Attunement at the start of each turn
without using a charge. Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you finish
a long rest.
Tideborn

## Water Attunement Techniques – The Tideborn

Water attunement flows with adaptability, patience, and relentless force. As a
Tideborn, you embody the essence of the tides: gentle and nurturing one moment,
overwhelming and unstoppable the next. Your techniques control the battlefield, heal
allies, and manipulate the environment through currents, mists, and frost.
Elemental Shift: Water Attunement – Shift Table
When you activate your Elemental Shift ability to Tideborn, you channel the fluid
and adaptable power of water, transforming yourself into a being of aquatic force. Roll
1d6 and consult the table below to determine the shift’s effect. You can roll each turn
that the shift is active or choose to lock in a specific effect for its duration.
| d6 | Shift Effect |
|:---:|:--------------|
| 1 | Tidal Surge – Your movement increases by 15 feet, and you can move
through enemy spaces without provoking opportunity attacks. You leave behind a
slippery trail, making the spaces you exit difficult terrain for enemies. |
| 2 | Riptide Grasp – When you hit a creature with a melee weapon attack, you
can pull it 10 feet toward you. If the creature fails a Strength saving throw (DC 8 + your
proficiency bonus + Wisdom modifier), it is knocked prone. |
| 3 | Mistform Cloak – Your form becomes partially insubstantial. You have
resistance to non-magical weapon damage, and attacks made against you from more
than 10 feet away are made with disadvantage. |
| 4 | Icy Flow – At the start of each of your turns, you create a sheet of ice beneath
your feet, spreading in a 10-foot radius. The ice persists for 1 minute, turning the area
into difficult terrain for all creatures except you and allies. Enemies that move through
it must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or fall prone. |
| 5 | Healing Current – At the start of each of your turns, an ally within 15 feet
regains hit points equal to 1d8 + your Wisdom modifier. If no allies are within range, you
instead gain temporary hit points equal to your Wisdom modifier. |
| 6 | Crashing Blow – Your melee weapon attacks crash with the force of a wave.
When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can deal an additional 1d10
bludgeoning damage and push the creature 10 feet back. |
Description of Shift Effects
- Tidal Surge: Water grants fluidity, allowing you to weave through enemies and
disrupt their footing.
- Riptide Grasp: The power of riptides pulls enemies to you, disorienting them
and giving you the advantage.
- Mistform Cloak: Just as mist evades touch, you become elusive and harder to
harm.
- Icy Flow: The chilling force of water forms ice at your feet, turning the
battlefield into a trap for your foes.
- Healing Current: Water’s nurturing side flows through you, empowering you or
your allies to recover from injuries.

- Crashing Blow: The might of crashing waves flows through your strikes,
making each hit a powerful impact that knocks enemies off-balance.
This table brings versatility to the Water Attunement's Elemental Shift ability,
emphasizing its dual nature: both fluid and crushing, nurturing and relentless.
1st Level Techniques
Misty Veil
Effect: You conjure a light mist around a target area (10 ft. radius) for up to 1
minute. While in the mist, creatures have partial cover and disadvantage on ranged
attack rolls against them. Allies can move freely, but enemies treat the mist as lightly
obscured.
Usage: Bonus Action
Flavor: "A cloak of mist gathers, hiding you from prying eyes."
Surging Flow
Effect: You enhance an ally’s speed with water's fluidity. The target gains an extra
10 feet of movement and can ignore difficult terrain until the end of their next turn.
Usage: Reaction when an ally moves
Flavor: "Like a river’s current, you carry them forward effortlessly."
3rd Level Techniques
Crashing Wave Strike
Effect: When you hit a creature with a melee attack, you can unleash a surge of
water that forces the target to make a Strength saving throw (DC equal to 8 + your
proficiency bonus + your Constitution modifier). On a failure, the target is pushed 10
feet away and knocked prone.
Usage: 1/Short Rest
Flavor: "Water crashes down with the force of a storm, sweeping all in its path."
Icy Embrace
Effect: You summon a burst of frigid water around a target within 30 feet. The
target must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or be restrained by ice for 1 minute.
They may repeat the saving throw at the end of each of their turns.
Usage: 1/Long Rest
Flavor: "Frozen tides encircle you, locking you in place."
7th Level Techniques
Riptide Step
Effect: You teleport up to 30 feet to a space you can see, leaving behind a whirlpool
of water. Creatures within 5 feet of the starting point must make a Strength saving
throw or be pulled 10 feet toward the origin point.
Usage: 2/Short Rest
Flavor: "You vanish with a splash, and the water drags others in your wake."
Healing Waters
Effect: You create a restorative pool in a 10-foot radius. Allies in the pool regain hit
points equal to 1d8 + your Wisdom modifier at the start of their turns for up to 1 minute.

Usage: 1/Long Rest

Flavor: "The water soothes and mends, washing away wounds and weariness."
10th Level Techniques
Torrent Shield
Effect: As a reaction to being hit by an attack, you summon a barrier of water
around yourself or an ally within 10 feet. The barrier absorbs damage equal to 1d12 +
your Wisdom modifier before dissipating.
Usage: 3/Long Rest
Flavor: "The water forms a shield, softening the blow before vanishing."
Floodgate Surge
Effect: You unleash a massive wave in a 30-foot cone. All creatures within the area
must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failure, they are knocked prone and take 3d8
bludgeoning damage. On a success, they take half damage and are not knocked prone.
Usage: 2/Long Rest
Flavor: "A wall of water crashes forward, overwhelming everything in its path."
14th Level Techniques
Tide of Renewal
Effect: You create a healing surge that spreads in a 20-foot radius. All allies within
the radius regain 2d10 hit points, and one condition of their choice (such as poisoned or
frightened) is removed.
Usage: 1/Long Rest
Flavor: "The tide washes away not just wounds, but fear and despair."
Whirlpool Prison
Effect: You summon a massive whirlpool centered on a point within 60 feet. The
whirlpool is a 10-foot radius and 20-foot tall cylinder. Any creature that starts its turn
inside must make a Strength saving throw or be restrained and pulled to the center. A
restrained creature may attempt the saving throw at the end of its turn. The whirlpool
lasts for 1 minute or until you dismiss it.
Usage: 1/Long Rest
Flavor: "The waters spiral into a powerful vortex, dragging all into its embrace."
--#### 18th Level Techniques
Ocean’s Dominion
Effect: You summon the power of an oceanic storm, creating heavy rain and
strong winds in a 60-foot radius for 1 minute. While active, creatures of your choice
have advantage on Dexterity and Strength saving throws. Enemies treat the area as
difficult terrain, and ranged attacks within the storm are made with disadvantage.
Usage: 1/Long Rest
Flavor: "The storm follows your command, hindering foes and empowering your
allies."
Tsunami Strike
Effect: You unleash a massive wave that sweeps across a 60-foot line. Creatures

caught in the wave must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failure, they take 8d10
bludgeoning damage and are swept 20 feet away. On a success, they take half damage
and remain standing.
Usage: 1/Long Rest
Flavor: "You call upon the fury of the sea, leaving devastation in your wake."
--These techniques give Water-attuned Sev’rinns the ability to balance offense,
defense, healing, and battlefield control. They emphasize the fluid adaptability of
water, while also granting the devastating potential to overwhelm opponents when
needed.
Skycaller
Skycaller (Air Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
When activating Elemental Shift as a Skycaller, you harness the volatile and
unpredictable power of air currents. Roll 1d6 to determine the nature of the shift and the
elemental effect for the duration of the shift.
| d6 | Effect | Description |
|:---:|--------------------------------------|-------------|
| 1 | Cyclone's Touch | You gain 10 feet of additional movement, and opportunity
attacks against you are made with disadvantage. |
| 2 | Whisper of Winds | You can cast Silent Image or Message at will without using
a spell slot. |
| 3 | Shockwave Burst | As a reaction, you can push enemies within 10 feet of you
back 5 feet whenever you take damage. |
| 4 | Gale Guard | You create swirling winds around you, gaining +2 to AC until
your next turn. |
| 5 | Zephyr Step | You can move through enemy spaces without provoking
opportunity attacks. Your movement does not provoke reactions. |
| 6 | Tempest Strike | When you hit with a melee attack, you can knock the target
prone or push them 10 feet back. |
Skycaller Combat Techniques
These techniques allow a Skycaller to manipulate air currents in battle, striking
with speed and unpredictability.
- Wind Dance
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
Your movements flow with the winds. As a bonus action, you can Dash, and until
the end of your turn, you ignore difficult terrain.
- Air Slash
Prerequisite: 5th Level
When you make a weapon attack, you can extend your strike with a sharp gust of
wind. Make a ranged weapon attack (30 ft.). On a hit, it deals your weapon damage type
plus 1d8 slashing damage.
- Storm's Wake

Prerequisite: 7th Level

When you successfully land an attack, your target is surrounded by a gust of wind.
Until the start of your next turn, the target’s movement is halved.
- Flight Mastery
Prerequisite: 10th Level
You learn to ride the winds effortlessly. You gain a flying speed of 30 feet for 1
minute, once per long rest.
- Howling Strike
Prerequisite: 14th Level
When you make a melee weapon attack, you can choose to summon a thunderous
boom. The attack deals an extra 2d6 thunder damage, and creatures within 5 feet of the
target must succeed on a Strength saving throw (DC = 8 + your proficiency + your
Dexterity) or be pushed 15 feet away.
Lithomage
Lithomage (Stone Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
When activating Elemental Shift as a Lithomage, you channel the immense,
grounding power of stone. Roll 1d6 to determine the nature of the shift and the effect it
grants for the duration.
| d6 | Effect | Description |
|:---:|--------------------------------------|-------------|
| 1 | Granite Skin | You gain temporary hit points equal to your level +
Constitution modifier. |
| 2 | Earthen Anchor | Your movement becomes immune to being reduced, and
you cannot be knocked prone. |
| 3 | Stonegrasp | As a bonus action, you can make the ground beneath a creature
grasp them. The target must succeed on a Strength saving throw (DC 8 + your
proficiency + Strength modifier) or be restrained until the end of your next turn. |
| 4 | Seismic Aura | Every enemy that starts their turn within 5 feet of you must
succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or be pushed 5 feet back. |
| 5 | Fortress Stance | You gain a +2 bonus to AC, and allies within 5 feet of you
gain half cover. |
| 6 | Boulder Step | When you move, the ground quakes. Creatures you move past
must make a Dexterity saving throw or fall prone. You can move through enemy spaces
without provoking opportunity attacks. |
Lithomage Combat Techniques
The Lithomage wields the steady, unyielding force of the earth in combat,
fortifying themselves while disrupting their enemies.
- Stoneguard
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
As a reaction to being hit by an attack, you can reduce the damage by 1d8 + your
Constitution modifier. You can use this feature a number of times equal to your

proficiency bonus, regaining uses on a long rest.
- Pulverizing Strike
Prerequisite: 5th Level
When you land a melee weapon attack, you can channel stone energy to deal an
additional 2d6 bludgeoning damage. The target must make a Strength saving throw or
be knocked prone.
- Rock Wall
Prerequisite: 7th Level
As a bonus action, you summon a wall of earth 5 feet high and 10 feet long within
30 feet of you. The wall provides half cover to creatures behind it and lasts until the start
of your next turn.
- Tectonic Shift
Prerequisite: 10th Level
You cause the battlefield to tremble. As an action, every creature within 20 feet of
you must make a Dexterity saving throw or be knocked prone. Structures or objects
within range take 2d8 bludgeoning damage.
- Pillar Strike
Prerequisite: 14th Level
When you hit with a melee weapon, you can create a 10-foot stone pillar beneath
your target. The target is launched upward, taking 4d6 bludgeoning damage and falling
prone. You can use this ability once per short or long rest.
Greenheart
Greenheart (Nature Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
Channeling the energy of life itself, the Greenheart attunes to the thriving forces
of nature. Roll 1d6 to determine the manifestation of your Elemental Shift.
| d6 | Effect | Description |
|:---:|---------|-------------|
| 1 | Thornskin | You sprout thorned vines along your skin. Any creature that hits
you with a melee attack takes 1d6 piercing damage. |
| 2 | Verdant Cloak | You blend with nature, gaining advantage on Dexterity
(Stealth) checks and partial cover in foliage-heavy areas. |
| 3 | Rooted Resilience | As a bonus action, you root yourself in place. You can’t be
knocked prone or moved against your will. |
| 4 | Bloom of Renewal | When you are healed, you regain additional hit points
equal to your proficiency bonus. Nearby allies within 10 feet gain half this bonus. |
| 5 | Venomous Bloom | As an action, you can release a poisonous spore cloud.
Creatures within 10 feet must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or become
poisoned for 1 minute. |
| 6 | Symbiotic Regrowth | When an ally within 10 feet of you is healed, you
recover hit points equal to your Constitution modifier. |
Greenheart Combat Techniques
The Greenheart embodies the adaptive strength of nature, turning environmental

advantages and living forces to their benefit. They grow, heal, and entangle, turning the
battlefield into an extension of themselves.
- Bramble Snare
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
When you hit a creature with a melee weapon attack, vines lash from the earth,
restraining the target (Strength save to resist). You can use this ability a number of
times equal to your proficiency bonus, regaining uses after a long rest.
- Pollinating Strike
Prerequisite: 5th Level
When you land a melee hit, you can cause pollen to burst, blinding the target. The
creature must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or be blinded until the end of its
next turn.
- Nature’s Sanctuary
Prerequisite: 7th Level
As a bonus action, you create a 15-foot radius of flourishing plants around you.
Allies inside the radius have advantage on death saving throws and recover 1d4 hit
points at the start of their turn. The sanctuary lasts for 1 minute or until you are
incapacitated.
- Adaptive Bloom
Prerequisite: 10th Level
As a reaction when you take damage, you absorb some of the impact. You reduce
the damage taken by 1d10 + your Constitution modifier. You also sprout blossoms,
granting temporary hit points to an ally within 10 feet equal to half the damage you
negated.
- Thornwood Avatar
Prerequisite: 14th Level
You summon a living armor of vines and thorns. For 1 minute, your AC increases
by 2, and any creature that hits you with a melee attack takes 3d6 piercing damage.
Once you use this feature, you must finish a long rest before using it again.
Chronomancer
Chronomancer (Time Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
The Chronomancer bends the flow of time itself, manipulating seconds as
weapons and shields. When you use Elemental Shift, roll 1d6 to determine how your
temporal influence manifests.
| d6 | Effect | Description |
|:---:|---------|-------------|
| 1 | Temporal Blur | You gain +2 AC as your form flickers between moments,
making you harder to target. |
| 2 | Speed Surge | As a bonus action, you can take the Dash or Disengage action.
Your movement does not provoke opportunity attacks this turn. |
| 3 | Frozen Time | You can freeze a small object (no larger than 1 cubic foot) in
time for 1 minute, making it immune to damage and decay. |
| 4 | Rewind Strike | When you miss with a melee or ranged attack, you can reroll

the attack. You must use the second roll. |
| 5 | Echo of Action | As a reaction, you can duplicate an ally's movement from
their last turn, moving the same distance in the same direction. |
| 6 | Lingering Moment | At the start of your turn, regain a spell slot of 3rd level
or lower that you expended in the previous round. |
Chronomancer Combat Techniques
The Chronomancer warps the battlefield with unpredictable shifts in time,
disorienting enemies and giving their allies the advantage. Their techniques reflect the
power to delay, accelerate, or rewrite moments in combat.
- Time Spike
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
As a reaction to an enemy entering your melee range, you can trap them in a
temporal distortion. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or be
restrained for 1 round as time locks their movements.
- Temporal Reversal
Prerequisite: 5th Level
As a bonus action, you rewind the last 6 seconds. Choose one creature within 30
feet to restore hit points equal to half the damage they took since the end of your last
turn. This ability can be used once per long rest.
- Time Sink
Prerequisite: 7th Level
You create a 10-foot radius time dilation field for 1 minute. Enemies inside the
field have their speed halved, and attacks they make are rolled at disadvantage. Once
used, this ability recharges after a long rest.
- Parallel Future
Prerequisite: 10th Level
You glimpse a possible outcome of an action. After rolling a d20 for an attack or
ability check, you can roll again and choose either result. This ability recharges after a
short or long rest.
- Time Avatar
Prerequisite: 14th Level
You take on the form of a time-warped being for 1 minute. During this time, you
gain the following benefits:
- You take two turns in each round of combat.
- If you are reduced to 0 hit points, you rewind to 1 hit point instead (this occurs
once).
Once you use this feature, you can’t use it again until you complete a long rest.
Voidstrider
Voidstrider (Space Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
As a Voidstrider, you manipulate space itself, bending the battlefield to your will.
When you activate Elemental Shift, roll 1d6 to determine the effect.
| d6 | Effect | Description |

|:---:|---------|-------------|
| 1 | Gravity Surge | Choose a point within 30 feet. Creatures in a 10-foot radius
must succeed on a Strength saving throw or be pulled 10 feet toward the point. |
| 2 | Void Slip | As a reaction to an attack, teleport 10 feet to an unoccupied space
you can see. This ability nullifies the triggering attack if you move out of range. |
| 3 | Planar Echo | Leave an illusionary duplicate in your space. The duplicate lasts
until the start of your next turn, distracting enemies and giving the first attack against
you disadvantage. |
| 4 | Gravitational Anchor | For 1 minute, you cannot be moved or knocked prone
by any means. |
| 5 | Void Blink | As a bonus action, teleport up to 15 feet. You can use this
movement to pass through solid objects but cannot end your turn inside them. |
| 6 | Singularity Shield | A swirling void protects you for 1 minute. Gain +2 AC,
and ranged attacks against you are rolled with disadvantage. |
Voidstrider Combat Techniques
Voidstriders excel at battlefield mobility, controlling space to confuse enemies
and protect allies. They are masters of unpredictable movement and spatial
manipulation.
- Spatial Displacement
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
As a bonus action, swap places with a willing ally within 30 feet. Both you and the
ally gain +2 AC until the start of your next turn.
- Warping Step
Prerequisite: 5th Level
Once per turn, when you move at least 15 feet, your next melee attack deals an
extra 1d8 force damage as spatial energy tears through your target.
- Zone of Entropy
Prerequisite: 7th Level
You create a 10-foot radius zone within 60 feet that lasts for 1 minute. Inside this
zone, creatures have disadvantage on attack rolls, and all ranged projectiles are
absorbed into the void. Recharges after a long rest.
- Gravity Well
Prerequisite: 10th Level
As an action, you generate a field that pulls creatures toward a point of your
choosing. Creatures within 30 feet of the point must succeed on a Strength saving throw
or be dragged 20 feet toward it. Once used, this ability recharges on a short or long rest.
- Void Mastery
Prerequisite: 14th Level
For 1 minute, you gain the following abilities:
- You can teleport up to 30 feet as a bonus action.
- Attacks against you automatically miss if you teleport after being targeted.
- If you teleport through a creature, that creature takes 2d8 force damage.

## Emberclad

Emberclad (Fire Attunement) Elemental Shift Table
As an Emberclad, you wield the relentless fury of flame. Your power turns heat
into both a weapon and a shield. When you activate Elemental Shift, roll 1d6 to
determine the fiery effect.
| d6 | Effect | Description |
|:---:|---------|-------------|
| 1 | Blazing Aura | Flames surround you for 1 minute. Creatures within 5 feet take
1d6 fire damage at the start of their turns. |
| 2 | Ignite | As a bonus action, set a flammable object or surface within 30 feet on
fire. A creature hit with this effect takes 1d8 fire damage. |
| 3 | Inferno Step | When you move at least 10 feet, leave behind burning embers.
Any creature that enters the space takes 1d6 fire damage. |
| 4 | Searing Touch | Your melee attacks deal an additional 1d6 fire damage for 1
minute. |
| 5 | Smoke Veil | You summon a thick smoke cloud around you, heavily
obscuring your space for 1 minute. Creatures inside must make a Constitution saving
throw or be blinded until the start of their next turn. |
| 6 | Explosion of Flames | As an action, release a wave of fire. All creatures
within a 15-foot radius must make a Dexterity saving throw or take 2d8 fire damage. On
a success, they take half damage. Recharges on a long rest. |
Emberclad Combat Techniques
The Emberclad embodies destruction, relentless aggression, and fiery endurance.
Their combat techniques allow them to scorch the battlefield and overwhelm foes with
heat and flame.
- Scorching Dash
Prerequisite: 3rd Level
When you Dash, fire trails in your wake. Creatures you pass within 5 feet of take
1d6 fire damage and must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or catch fire, taking 1d6
fire damage at the start of their turn.
- Immolating Strike
Prerequisite: 5th Level
As a bonus action, your weapon erupts in flame. Your next attack deals an
additional 2d8 fire damage. If the target is flammable, it ignites and continues burning
for 1 minute, taking 1d6 fire damage at the start of each of its turns.
- Blazing Vortex
Prerequisite: 7th Level
You summon a vortex of fire in a 10-foot radius centered on yourself. Creatures in
the area must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 3d6 fire damage. This vortex
lasts 1 minute or until you dismiss it as a bonus action.
- Molten Core
Prerequisite: 10th Level

Your body radiates intense heat. For 1 minute, any creature that hits you with a
melee attack takes 2d6 fire damage. If a creature grapples you, it must succeed on a
Constitution saving throw or take 3d6 fire damage each round it maintains the grapple.
- Inferno Mastery
Prerequisite: 14th Level
You can unleash a devastating inferno. As an action, release fire in a 30-foot cone.
Creatures in the area must make a Dexterity saving throw or take 8d8 fire damage, or
half as much on a success. Once used, this ability recharges after a long rest.
Eidolon
Eidolon Elemental Shift Table
d6 Soul Shift Effect
1 Haunting Echo: The target becomes disoriented, suffering disadvantage on
their next attack roll.
2 Soulbond: You create a fleeting connection with an ally within 30 feet. You may
swap places with them as a reaction until the end of your next turn.
3 Draining Touch: When you deal damage, regain hit points equal to half the
damage dealt.
4 Ethereal Step: You phase into the ethereal plane until the end of your next turn,
gaining movement through creatures and objects.
5 Spectral Veil: Shadows cloak your form. Gain +2 AC and advantage on Dexterity
(Stealth) checks until the start of your next turn.
6 Phantasmal Assault: Your attack evokes terrifying illusions. The target must
succeed on a Wisdom saving throw (DC = 8 + proficiency + Charisma modifier) or be
frightened until the end of its next turn.
Eidolon Combat Techniques
- Soulflame Strike (Level 3+): When you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you
can expend a use of Elemental Shift to ignite your weapon with ethereal fire. Deal an
extra 2d8 psychic damage. This damage increases to 3d8 at 11th level and 4d8 at 17th
level.
- Echoing Will (Level 6+): As a reaction, when an ally within 30 feet takes
damage, you may absorb part of the pain. Reduce the damage taken by 1d10 + your
Charisma modifier and take the same amount.
- Wraith Dance (Level 10+): You vanish and reappear in a flurry of ghostly
movement. As a bonus action, teleport to an unoccupied space you can see within 60
feet and make a melee attack.
- Bound by Spirit (Level 14+): You can tether your soul to an enemy for 1 minute.
While tethered, any damage the enemy deals to others is halved, but you take the other
half as unavoidable damage. You may end this effect as a reaction.
- Eidolon’s Ascendance (Level 18+): As an action, for 1 minute, you become a
spectral entity. Gain resistance to all damage except force and psychic, and advantage
on all saving throws against being charmed or frightened. Additionally, enemies within

10 feet have disadvantage on Wisdom saving throws.
Luminor
Luminor Elemental Shift Table
d6 Light Shift Effect
1 Blinding Flash: A burst of light erupts from you. One creature of your choice
within 30 feet must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or be blinded until the end
of its next turn.
2 Radiant Burst: When you deal damage, deal an extra 1d8 radiant damage. This
increases to 2d8 at 11th level.
3 Sunlit Step: Your movement leaves glowing footprints, and you ignore difficult
terrain until the start of your next turn.
4 Beacon’s Call: Choose an ally within 60 feet. That ally gains temporary hit
points equal to 1d10 + your Charisma modifier.
5 Shadowbane: Any illusion or magical darkness within 15 feet of you is
immediately dispelled.
6 Solar Ward: You gain resistance to radiant and fire damage until the start of
your next turn.
Luminor Combat Techniques
- Blazing Strike (Level 3+): When you hit a creature with a melee weapon attack,
you can expend a use of Elemental Shift to engulf your weapon in searing light, dealing
an extra 2d10 radiant damage. This damage increases to 3d10 at 11th level and 4d10 at
17th level.
- Illuminate Path (Level 6+): As a bonus action, you emit a guiding light for 1
minute. Allies within 30 feet of you have advantage on saving throws against being
frightened or blinded.
- Brilliant Form (Level 10+): As an action, you transform into a glowing avatar of
light for 1 minute. While in this form, your weapon attacks deal an extra 1d6 radiant
damage, and enemies that start their turn within 10 feet of you must succeed on a
Constitution saving throw or be blinded until the end of their next turn.
- Daybreak’s Blessing (Level 14+): As a reaction, when an ally within 30 feet
drops to 0 hit points, you can expend an Elemental Shift to heal them for 4d10 hit points
and lift them to their feet. They also glow with radiant light, gaining +2 to AC until the
start of your next turn.
- Eternal Glow (Level 18+): For 1 minute, you become a living beacon of light. You
gain resistance to radiant, fire, and necrotic damage. Your presence causes magical
darkness to dissipate in a 30-foot radius, and creatures within the aura cannot benefit
from invisibility. Enemies within 10 feet have disadvantage on attack rolls against
anyone other than you.
Sorcerer
The Sorcerer Class in Ryndor

## Awakened by the Rift

Sorcerers are a new phenomenon in Ryndor, emerging only since the Rift to
Nebernoria tore open reality. Unlike Sev’rinns, who align with elemental forces, or
Wizards, who bend resonance through study, Sorcerers draw their magic directly from
the chaotic energies of the Rift. Their power is unpredictable, alien, and often
misunderstood, creating fear and awe wherever they appear. These individuals are
conduits for the instability between worlds, and their magic resonates with the
strangeness of Nebernoria.
Magic from the Unknown
Sorcerers’ abilities are inherently tied to the Rift’s influence. Their magic
manifests without study or training—it flows through them naturally, like an extension
of their will. Each Sorcerer’s connection to the Rift is personal, shaped by their exposure
to its strange energies. Some are born with this power, while others develop it after
direct contact with the Rift. This gift, however, comes with a price: it leaves a mark on
both their body and mind, as they channel forces not meant for the material world.
A Blessing and a Burden
Communities often struggle to understand Sorcerers, viewing them with a mix of
wonder and suspicion. While their abilities can be useful, the nature of their power is
dangerous and unreliable. A seemingly simple spell might ripple into unintended
consequences, altering the fabric of reality or awakening lingering influences from
Nebernoria. Some Sorcerers are celebrated as heroes for harnessing their abilities to
protect others, while others are ostracized, accused of bringing chaos wherever they go.
Shaping Reality
The strength of Sorcerers lies in their adaptability. With no need for external
study, they can twist their magic instinctively, shaping it through raw emotion and
sheer will. Their access to Metamagic allows them to manipulate spells in ways that
others can’t match—quickening spells in battle, extending durations, or casting with
subtle precision. Yet each spell cast brings them closer to the chaotic forces of the Rift,
making every use of magic a delicate balance between control and chaos.
Outcasts of the Rift
Though the Sorcerers are few in number, their existence raises questions about
the Rift’s ongoing influence on the world. Are they harbingers of something greater, or
the first wave of a deeper transformation? Many seek to understand their connection to
Nebernoria, while others fear what might happen if the Rift’s magic spreads unchecked.
Whether accepted or rejected, Sorcerers must navigate both the dangers of their power
and the suspicions of those around them, forging their own path in a world that fears
what it cannot understand.
In Ryndor, Sorcerers walk the line between creation and collapse. Each spell is a
reflection of the Rift’s strange potential, and each decision brings them closer to
unlocking the mysteries of the magic that flows through their veins—or succumbing to

the chaos that surrounds them.
Riftborn Origin
Riftborn Sorcerer
Sorcerous Origin Overview:
Riftborn Sorcerers are individuals whose very essence is intertwined with the
chaotic energies of the Rift to Nebernoria. Rather than drawing power from the natural
elements of the material world like Sev’rinns, Riftborn Sorcerers embody the
unpredictable magic that flows between dimensions. Their magic is unstable, potent,
and strange—sometimes enhancing their abilities and at other times bringing
unintended consequences. This connection to the Rift makes them both powerful and
dangerous, capable of bending reality to their whims, though always at the risk of
unraveling the threads of fate.
Features of the Riftborn Origin
1st Level – Chaotic Manifestation:
The magic of the Rift surges unpredictably through you. Whenever you cast a
sorcerer spell of 1st level or higher, roll a d6. On a 1, strange magic manifests around
you, determined by the Rift Surge Table (provided later). You can roll with advantage
on this table once per long rest.
1st Level – Dimensional Instincts:
Your exposure to dimensional anomalies gives you a heightened awareness. You
gain proficiency in Arcana and Perception, and you can detect nearby planar anomalies
and portals within 60 feet without requiring a check.
6th Level – Phase Step:
You learn to slip through the folds of space. As a bonus action, you can teleport up
to 30 feet to an unoccupied space you can see. You can use this feature a number of
times equal to your Charisma modifier per long rest.
14th Level – Rift Cloak:
A shroud of dimensional energy shields you from harm. As a reaction when you
are hit by an attack, you can shift out of phase, granting yourself resistance to all
damage until the start of your next turn and teleporting 10 feet away. You can use this
feature once per short or long rest.
18th Level – Tear Reality:
At great personal cost, you can rip open a temporary rift between dimensions. As
an action, you summon a 15-foot-radius vortex of unstable energy centered on a point
you can see within 60 feet. Creatures in the area must make a Dexterity saving throw
against your spell save DC, taking 12d12 force damage on a failed save or half as much
on a success. Once you use this feature, you can’t do so again until you finish a long rest,
unless you spend 10 sorcery points to use it again.
Rift Surge Table (Sample Effects)

d6 Surge Effect
1 Your spell casts twice. Choose a new target.
2 A glowing portal appears, revealing distant scenes.
3 Nearby objects hover 10 feet off the ground.
4 You gain resistance to all damage for 1 minute.
5 A random spell from the wild magic table triggers.
6 Time slows briefly—take an additional action.
The Riftborn Sorcerer is a volatile and powerful magic user, forever on the edge of
control. Whether they revel in the chaos or struggle to manage it, they wield energies
few can comprehend, making them both a boon and a threat to those around them.
Warlock
The Warlock Class in Ryndor
A Pact Across the Rift
Warlocks in Ryndor are not just wielders of magic—they are conduits, granted
power through binding pacts with entities from beyond the Rift. These patrons are
beings of immense and alien influence, existing in the astral chaos of Nebernoria. Some
patrons grant power in exchange for service, while others use Warlocks as vessels to
further strange, unknowable goals. Each pact comes with both gifts and burdens,
marking Warlocks as forever tied to the mysteries of the Rift.
The Influence of the Rift
Unlike other magic users, Warlocks’ abilities are not their own—they are
borrowed, channeled through the connection to their patron. This connection manifests
in both subtle and overwhelming ways. Some Warlocks find themselves influenced by
strange thoughts and compulsions, hearing whispers or seeing visions from the other
side. Others experience physical changes, like glowing eyes, shifting shadows, or
strange runes appearing on their skin. Regardless, the magic granted by their patron is
unpredictable and otherworldly, leaving a trace of the Rift’s influence in everything
they do.
Pacts and Power
Warlocks form pacts to gain access to extraordinary abilities, choosing paths that
reflect their bond with their patron. These powers are granted through unique gifts—
such as Eldritch Invocations, arcane boons that reshape reality, or mysterious familiars
summoned from across the Rift. Each Warlock builds a unique relationship with their
patron, often negotiating for additional power, though these bargains may come at
unforeseen costs.
Navigating Suspicion and Awe
Though Warlocks possess incredible abilities, they are met with suspicion by the
people of Ryndor. Their bond with beings from Nebernoria makes them objects of both
fear and fascination. Some view them as dangerous puppets of unknown entities, while
others admire them as visionaries walking the thin edge between worlds. Warlocks

often hide the true nature of their power to avoid scrutiny, but even in secrecy, they feel
the weight of their bond pressing down on them—a reminder that the Rift always
demands more.
Walking a Forbidden Path
Warlocks represent the untamed possibilities of Ryndor’s future. Their power
flows not from study or heritage but from the delicate web of trust, debt, and influence
binding them to patrons beyond the Rift. Whether driven by ambition, curiosity, or
desperation, Warlocks chart their own course through a world that does not yet
understand them, forever changed by the gifts and demands of their patron.
In Ryndor, Warlocks stand at the crossroads of power and peril, knowing that
every spell they cast echoes across the Rift—inviting the gaze of beings who see far
more than any mortal mind can comprehend.
Boons
Pact of the Planebinder
Pact Boon: Planebinder
Warlocks in Ryndor who enter the Pact of the Planebinder gain the ability to
tether fragments of otherworldly magic to the material world. Their bond with patrons
across the Rift grants them fleeting control over unstable realities, weaving together
dimensions for unpredictable, potent results.
Planebinder Features
- Dimensional Echo: As a bonus action, you summon a glimpse of another
timeline. The echo replicates a simple action (such as an attack or object interaction),
granting you advantage on your next ability check or attack roll. The echo dissipates at
the end of your next turn.
- Weave the Rift: When casting a spell, roll a d6. On an even result, your spell’s
potency surges—such as additional damage, increased range, or heightened saving
throw DC. On an odd result, unpredictable energy twists the spell, creating a minor
complication (DM’s discretion).
- Shiftstep: At 6th level, you can flicker between dimensions. As a reaction to
being targeted by an attack, you teleport 30 feet to a visible location. After using this
ability, you must complete a short or long rest to use it again.
The Pact of the Planebinder reflects the Warlock’s delicate grasp over the strange
forces from the Rift. They manipulate threads of reality itself, embracing both the
power and unpredictability of tethering planar energies to their will.
Patrons
Rift Patrons for Warlocks in Ryndor
The Rift has opened connections to entities that defy logic and understanding.
Warlocks who draw power from these patrons are irrevocably changed, their minds

brushed by the unfathomable. These are a few of the powerful entities that grant Riftbound Warlocks their abilities:
The Blighted Conductor
An ancient intelligence that manipulates resonance and sound, this being exists
as a chaotic symphony in a decaying dimension. Warlocks of the Blighted Conductor
control vibrations, soundwaves, and madness, sowing discord and confusion wherever
they go. Their spells hum with unsettling harmonies, causing pain and distorted
perceptions.
Expanded Spells: Dissonant Whispers, Shatter, Synaptic Static
Boons: Gain the ability to temporarily deafen or disorient foes with Rift-born
vibrations.
The Endless Dreamer
Existing in an astral realm of slumber, the Endless Dreamer offers knowledge
through visions but bends the line between waking and dreaming. Their Warlocks
become conduits of sleep magic, bending dreams into reality, and at times confusing
the two. Their powers manifest in strange, half-formed dreams that affect allies and
enemies unpredictably.
Expanded Spells: Sleep, Dream, Phantasmal Force
Boons: Once per long rest, turn reality into a dreamscape, causing attacks to
phase through you or objects to appear ephemeral.
The Shattered One
This patron is a fragmented deity, broken across infinite dimensions, whispering
from pieces scattered throughout the Rift. Warlocks of the Shattered One tap into these
fragments, gaining access to incomplete but potent bursts of power. However, they
experience fractured visions of other timelines, becoming increasingly aware of
alternate realities where every decision splinters.
Expanded Spells: Blink, Mirror Image, Dimension Door
Boons: Once per rest, reroll an ability check, attack, or saving throw, as if shifting
through timelines to find a better outcome.
The Hunger Between Stars
This entity is a vast, formless force of consumption, existing between the
dimensions of space and time. Warlocks who serve the Hunger siphon their patron’s
insatiable appetite, draining life, energy, or even memories from others. As their
influence grows, they become void-like conduits of entropy, consuming all that touches
them.
Expanded Spells: Arms of Hadar, Hunger of Hadar, Maddening Darkness
Boons: Once per rest, you may absorb a magical effect targeted at you, nullifying
it and gaining temporary hit points.
Each Rift patron brings not only power but an existential burden, leaving their
Warlocks forever altered by the strange forces they have invited into their lives. In

Ryndor, becoming a Warlock of the Rift means embracing the unpredictable, straddling
the line between understanding and madness, between creation and oblivion.
The Many Mouthed Mother
The Many-Mouthed Mother
The Many-Mouthed Mother is a patron of insatiable hunger and chaotic
creation, emerging from the most twisted depths of the Rift. She is said to be a colossal,
ever-changing being with countless mouths, each whispering promises, warnings, or
maddening truths. Her followers crave to consume—knowledge, power, emotions, or
flesh—and offer her tributes by spreading chaos and devouring everything in their
path, metaphorically or literally. Those who serve the Many-Mouthed Mother find their
own bodies and minds shifting, growing extra senses or physical changes, as they
slowly become part of her insatiable will.
Expanded Spells:
- Tasha’s Hideous Laughter
- Devour Life
- Confusion
- Phantasmal Killer
- Wall of Mouths
Boons of the Mother:
- Ravenous Maw: As an action, summon a gnashing mouth on your hand for 1
minute. The maw deals 1d8 + Charisma modifier in slashing or psychic damage on a hit.
It can consume simple objects, removing curses or corrupting them into Weirded
variants.
- Gift of Whispers: Gain the ability to speak with two voices simultaneously—one
sweet and persuasive, the other harsh and intimidating. Once per long rest, you can
force a creature to make a Wisdom save or act under an implanted compulsion for 1
minute.
Invocation of Endless Appetite: Your hunger becomes insatiable, granting you
temporary hit points equal to half the damage dealt each time you kill a creature. But
with each kill, a small mutation forms—an eye where one shouldn’t be, teeth beneath
your palm, or a whispered craving from deep within.
Serving the Many-Mouthed Mother brings both power and a curse—those who
follow her struggle to maintain their identity, slowly losing themselves to the endless
hunger of their patron. Every spell cast is an invitation to consume, to spread chaos, and
to nurture the Mother’s relentless desires.
Wizard
Wizards of Ryndor
In Ryndor, Wizards embody the relentless pursuit of knowledge. Their mastery
comes not from the innate gifts of the Sev’rinn or the otherworldly pull of the Rift but

from the study of the Primeval Resonance—the fundamental energy that hums
beneath all existence. They explore the ancient mysteries, analyze elemental
harmonics, and shape magic through deliberate craft and careful discipline.
Wizards in Ryndor view magic as a tool of precision, wielded with skill and
wisdom. They are scholars, inventors, and strategists—those who believe in mastering
reality through understanding and careful manipulation.
The Role of Wizards in Ryndor
Wizards often serve as advisors to rulers, members of arcane councils, or
archivists in magical academies. Some are wanderers, traveling Ryndor in search of lost
relics, ancient spells, or forgotten secrets of the Resonance. Others dedicate their lives
to the Crystal Scholars or align themselves with the Keepers of the Rift, hoping to
contain or explore the arcane anomalies created by The Weirding.
Power through Study
Unlike Sev’rinns, who wield elemental forces instinctively, Wizards must
immerse themselves in years of study. They learn to harness the Resonance’s frequency
patterns through written spells, incantations, and mathematical formulas. Their magic
is precise, demanding preparation and insight, but offers unparalleled flexibility in
return.
The Wizard’s Journey
Most wizards begin their journey by attending one of the many magical
institutions scattered across Ryndor, such as the Holmea Skola or the research enclaves
within Eveltoft. Others travel independently, joining secret orders or arcane societies.
However, all share a common goal: mastery of magic through knowledge. Wizards of
Ryndor are innovators, blending tradition with invention to craft spells that push the
boundaries of magic.
Specialization: The School of Harmonics
Unique to Ryndor is the School of Harmonics, a discipline focusing on the
resonance patterns that underpin existence. These wizards learn to manipulate
elemental frequencies, channeling spells like a composer guiding an orchestra. By
tuning into the hum of the Resonance, they can amplify their magic, disrupt opponents,
or align spells with specific elemental forces. Harmonics-trained wizards are rare and
highly sought after, capable of bending the arcane to create moments of breathtaking
power.
Wizards in Ryndor are symbols of reason and control in a chaotic world—a
reminder that even amidst the turmoil of The Weirding and the unpredictable magic of
the Rift, mastery through knowledge remains a powerful force.
School of Harmonics
Let’s build a new Wizard school for Ryndor centered around the Primeval

Resonance—the underlying mystical force that binds reality. This school, called the
School of Harmonics, focuses on the delicate manipulation of these elemental
frequencies, allowing wizards to align, amplify, or disrupt the natural patterns of
magic.
School of Harmonics
Wizards of this school become experts in the resonance of magic, learning to
perceive the ebb and flow of arcane frequencies. Through years of study, they learn to
tune into the hum of existence, using these harmonic patterns to bend magic to their
will. They don’t just cast spells—they weave them into the fabric of the world itself.
Features of the School of Harmonics:
2nd Level – Resonant Pulse:
You learn to emit bursts of harmonic energy. Whenever you cast a spell of 1st level
or higher, you create a Resonant Pulse. This pulse reverberates outward, giving allies
within 10 feet advantage on their next skill check or saving throw before the start of
your next turn.
6th Level – Tune the Arcane:
You become adept at shifting the resonance of your spells to suit the situation.
When casting a spell that deals damage, you can change the damage type to one aligned
with the core elements of Ryndor: fire, water, air, stone, light, or shadow. You can use
this feature a number of times equal to your Intelligence modifier per long rest.
10th Level – Harmonic Ward:
Your connection to the resonance protects you from magical interference. When
you are affected by a spell, you can use your reaction to force the caster to make an
Intelligence saving throw against your spell save DC. On a failure, the spell fizzles and
has no effect on you. You can use this feature once per short or long rest.
14th Level – Symphony of the Elements:
You master the ability to orchestrate a symphony of resonant magic. When
casting a spell of 5th level or lower, you can cast a second spell of equal or lower level as
part of the same action, provided both spells target different creatures or areas. This
ability can be used once per long rest.
The School of Harmonics represents not just a form of spellcasting but a
philosophy—one that treats magic as music and the wizard as a composer of unseen
symphonies. Wizards of this school are equally comfortable amplifying allies’ strength,
disrupting enemies’ magic, or bending the elements to their will through careful tuning
of arcane frequencies.

## Faces and the Souls Within

This chapter presents example characters built using both the familiar classes of the 5th

Edition Open Gaming License and the custom options unique to Ryndor. Each build
draws from the world’s shifting currents: Leoporin born of the Swiftstone’s pulse, bards
who carry lanterns of unreal clarity, sorcerers marked by dimensional rupture. These
examples are not archetypes, but invitations—to walk in strange footsteps, to ask
difficult questions, and to see yourself not as a trope, but as a fracture of the world’s
soul made flesh.
Whether you are a player seeking inspiration or a GM looking to seed your world
with evocative NPCs, the following entries offer fully realized characters with
backstory, mechanical build notes, and thematic resonance. They span across races and
roles, from haunted guides to starlit tricksters, from the scarred survivors of Weird
Zones to the forgeborn thinkers of the Khuzud deepways.
Here, you’ll find not only stats, but stories. Not only features, but flaws. Each of
these faces bears the marks of the Weirding. Each of these souls has reason to venture
forward into the dark.
Turn the page. The weird is waiting.
Isera Wyrgleam, Riftborn Sorcerer
Name: Isera Wyrgleam
Race: Leoporin
Class: Sorcerer (Riftborn Origin)
Background: Weirding Refugee
Alignment: Chaotic Good
Gender: Female
Age: 19
Height: 4’3”
Fur Color: Dappled silver and moss green
Eyes: Iridescent violet
Languages: Common, Leoporin, Sylvan

### BACKSTORY: Touched by the Rift, Bound to the Forest

Isera was born in the Earthkin Hollows beneath Blossomthorn Grove, a remote
corner of Wulfricton where the petals fall like snow and the trees sing softly in their
sleep. Like most Leoporin, her early life was full of forest games, song-hunting, and
morning burrow duties. Her people lived by rhythm and light: moonlit harvests, shared
meals, and the teachings of the Luminari.
But when she was twelve, the sky cracked.
A Weird Zone rupture tore open a seam in the fabric of the forest—not natural
magic, not Luminar, but something older, hungrier. It swallowed part of the grove,
warping trees into spirals, singing animals into dust, and tainting the Swiftstone’s
resonance for miles.
Isera barely survived. When she woke, she was alone, her fur threaded with white
streaks and her eyes shimmering violet. The others said she must have been marked,

that the Rift had tried to devour her—but changed its mind. Ever since, she’s heard the
humming of things that don’t belong, seen shapes in the leaves that flicker from this
world into the next.
The shard of strange glass she carries is from that day—found lodged in her paw
when she woke. It glows faintly when the stars move wrong.
Unable to stay, but too volatile to be fully trusted, Isera left Aelurin at seventeen.
The Luminari gifted her a rune-wrapped satchel and a whispered blessing: “Let the stars
be sharp, and the forest kinder than the sky.”
She’s wandered since—following rumors of leyline sickness, vanished scouts,
and unstable resonance sites. Most think her cursed, but the Holmean Magical Creature
Society saw potential. They sent her on low-risk missions to observe Weirding shifts—
until recently, when the green growth started to pulse with Rift-energy she could feel in
her teeth.
Now she walks the balance between memory and madness, nature and
unraveling.
And she wants to know why the forest bleeds green.

## Personality Traits

Quietly intense
: Isera doesn’t waste words, but every silence feels charged.
Obsessively curious
: She cannot leave a mystery untouched—even if it bites back.
Forest-sure
: She knows how to listen to roots, read wind, and follow moss.
Flaws
Fear of being “lost again”
: She hides signs of her magic’s instability.
Trust Issues
: Too many people have tried to “study” her. She flinches from authority.
Bonds
The Swiftstone
still whispers in her dreams. She believes it wants to heal.
She keeps a journal of strange dreams
, convinced they are memories of a world before the Rift.
Ideal
"Even broken things have patterns. Even chaos has echoes."
She believes that understanding the Rift might allow her to one day seal it—or even
reverse it.
Race
: Leoporin
Class
: Sorcerer, Riftborn Origin

## Background

: Weirding Refugee
Level

Tuurvak Clattersign, College of the Lantern Bard
Name: Tuurvak Clattersign
Race: Khuzud
Class: Bard (College of Lanterns)
Background: Ghostwhisperer of Dollow Canyon
Alignment: Neutral Good
Gender: Male
Age: 122
Height: 4’5”
Skin: Translucent gray-pale, faint veins visible
Whiskers: Matte silver, grown long from chin and jaw
Eyes: None (echolocation only)
Languages: Common (written only), Inglishmek, Deep Cant

## BACKSTORY: The Echo of Lost Lights

Born in the sleeping depths of Ban Mynydd, where the tunnels outnumber the
living and sound travels like breath through stone, Tuurvak learned early that silence
does not mean safety. The child of artisan philosophers, he was trained in tonal
mapping and lithosonic resonance—Khuzud arts that use echolocation to shape tunnels
and tune stone.
When he was still young by Khuzud reckoning, his curiosity led him upward—too
far, too fast. He breached into a collapsed cavern near Dollow Canyon, where strange
spirits hummed through shattered crystals and half-melted glyphs. There, among the
ghosts of failed rituals, a voice found him. It spoke not in Inglishmek, but in forgotten
breath. Since then, he has not slept in true silence.
He emerged altered. Not cursed, his kin insisted—attuned. His old tonal lantern
now flickers with spectral hues, and ghosts follow him like echoes. Among surface folk,
this made him an outcast. Among the College of Lanterns, it made him a candle in the
void.
Tuurvak joined the College to understand what the ghosts want—and what the
Weirding has taken. His voice is a quiet drone, his gestures methodical. His songs are
felt more than heard: pulse-beats in the bones, shimmerings in the dark. His lantern
cuts illusions not with flame, but with frequency.
He does not fear the Weirding.
He fears forgetting what came before it.

## Personality Traits

Stone-Slow and Precise:
Tuurvak processes everything before reacting. His silence is weighted, not empty.
Speaks Through Echo:
Often uses Inglishmek even among those who can’t read it, expecting the world to
keep up.
Mildly amused by death.
He’s seen too many ghosts to take the end seriously.

## Flaws

Sunlight-averse:
Exposure to daylight is disorienting and painful.
Dismisses surface emotions:
Sees most other races as emotionally fragile or overly impulsive.
Can’t let a spirit rest if it speaks to him first.
Compelled to solve or resolve the unfinished.

## Bonds

The
ghost who found him
in Dollow still follows him—and has never revealed its name.
He hums the
first tonal phrase
ever spoken by Moradin, passed through ancestral dreaming.
Keeps a pebble from the cavern where he first saw ghostlight. He believes it hums
only for him.

## Ideal

"Light is not the opposite of shadow. It is its memory."
He believes the Weirding is not chaos, but memory misaligned, and seeks to realign it
through resonance and ritual.

Varkos "Tempest-Born" Drayden
Race: Human
Class: Barbarian, Path of the Howling Tempest
Background: Kigan Uldar Champion (Thunderbolts, Skyfire League)
Alignment: Chaotic Good
Gender: Male
Age: 34
Height: 6’3”
Build: Muscular, broad-shouldered, built for impact
Eyes: Lightning blue
Skin: Deep tan, scarred knees and forearms
Hair: Shaved sides, long silver topknot
Languages: Common

## BACKSTORY: The Storm Leaves the Arena

Varkos Drayden once ruled the skies of the Skyfire League as the Thunderbolts’
premier striker—a blur of motion and muscle known across Ryndor as “TempestBorn.” His signature play, Vault Spiral into Slam Dive, earned him records,
endorsements, and the love of a thousand chanting crowds.

But that was before the Weirding touched the game. A rogue planar rift surged
mid-finals, warping the orb and disfiguring two players in front of thousands. Varkos
ripped off his armband and left the field before the match ended. “You can’t cage the
storm without courting lightning,” he muttered—and disappeared.
Now he walks Ryndor as a wanderer and a weapon, the storm still alive inside
him. What once delighted crowds now terrifies monsters and bandits. He still wears his
Thunderbolts gear, weather-worn and blood-smeared, and he hasn't forgotten how to
move like a strike of lightning and hit like the echo.

## Personality Traits

Charismatic Swagger:
Varkos treats most interactions like a pre-game interview—confident, wry, and
brimming with presence.
Storm Seeker:
He goes wherever chaos brews, like wind chasing pressure drops.
Flaws
Addicted to Speed:
Still chases the rush of movement, of making the winning play—even if the game's
long over.
Authority Issues:
He distrusts uniforms and emblems—even ones he used to wear.
Bonds
The Thunderbolts:
They're still his team, even if he walked out. He'd bleed to protect their legacy.
The Skyfire Flame:
A trophy from his first league win, hidden in his pack, burned into his memory.
Ideal
"A real storm doesn’t need permission to arrive."
He believes might and motion must serve purpose, not glory. If there's danger ahead,
he’ll hit it head-on.
CHARACTER BUILD: Level 1 Human Barbarian (Tempest Path at 3rd)

A former sports legend now turned wandering warrior, Tuurvak blends
showmanship and sheer power. He channels his fury like a controlled weather event—
flashy, brutal, impossible to ignore.
