## Of Roots and Ruin

UNDER CONSTRUCTION
Of Roots and Ruin
No players allowed beyond this point—Dungeon Masters only! Spoilers abound
here, revealing the full arc of the campaign and what awaits the heroes.
Welcome to the campaign that will carry your characters from humble beginnings
to uncovering a web of corruption buried beneath the surface of Ryndor’s seemingly
perfect society. In Of Roots and Ruin, adventurers embark on a journey shaped by hard
truths, shifting power, and ethical dilemmas—where magic and nature are on the brink
of annihilation
The campaign begins at Level 1 and progresses with each completed episode. At
the end of each episode, characters will gain a level, culminating in an epic
confrontation by Level 5. This design ensures the pace remains fast, and players stay
engaged, with challenges scaling alongside their growing abilities.
Whenever a creature, NPC, or item appears in bold, it indicates the name is listed
in the appendix. This is your cue to consult the appendix for detailed stats and abilities,
helping keep your session running smoothly and maintaining the campaign’s rhythm.
Episode Guide
Episode 1: Follow the Rumors
The adventurers start small, following strange reports of missing animals and
unsettling occurrences with unknown origins in Norwycke and near the Hurstwold.
Players will encounter clues—fragmented stories from locals, mysterious symbols, and
strange traces of creatures and plants corrupted by something other than the
Weirding. Right as they’re getting close to something, a mysterious figure makes it
clear they aren’t welcome in Norwycke, and they especially aren’t welcome to be poking
around where they don’t belong.
Episode 2: Uncover the Dead Creatures
As the heroes delve deeper, they discover remains of magical beings—unicorn
horns, mermaid scales, and other remnants harvested with surgical precision. Who is
responsible for these atrocities, and how far do they reach?
Episode 3: Discover the Technology
The adventurers stumble upon new, unsettling technology—a mix of Ullac
Regime machinery and Weirded enchantments. This twisted innovation uses magical
creatures as fuel, destabilizing the environment and sowing chaos in nearby
settlements.
Episode 4: Find the Thread of the Ullac
Tracking the remains of this operation leads the adventurers closer to the heart of
the Ullac Regime’s last vestiges. Strange allies and dangerous enemies stand in their
way, and decisions must be made—whether to destroy or co-opt this powerful but
deadly technology.
Episode 5: Encounter the Baddies, Make Your Choice

In the climactic final encounter, the adventurers face Ullac loyalists—individuals
corrupted by both their beliefs and the Weirding’s influence. Do they dismantle this
dark enterprise entirely, or do they wrest control and attempt to reshape it for the
better?

## Story Overview

Episode 1: Going Green
Summary
The adventure begins at the Holmean Magical Creature Society’s headquarters
in Wyrmbost. During a morning meeting, Ardella Lentris is interrupted by a ranger who
brings in a farmer covered in invasive green growth. As the Society investigates, the
characters are sent to Norwycke, where rumors of the same growths persist. They travel
across the Innerstifla Sound under the guidance of captain Brun Furlow. Upon arrival
in Norwycke, the players find a town struggling against the overwhelming spread of
green growths, discovering hints that a mysterious Greensalve temporarily halts the
infection.
As the players go in search of Greensalve of their own, they discover signs that
Feddel, the proprietor of Feddel APothecary, has gone missing under suspicious
circumstances. While snooping around, a hooded figure enters the apothecary and
suspects the players are the suppliers of the Greensalve. After they clear the air and
convince the figure to trust them, he introduces himself as Halric, and reveals his
suspicion that the green growth is no accident - the Greensalve suppliers have done it
on purpose, to profit from their own cure.
The clues to track down the suppliers are very limited - just a strange symbol in a
ledger, and the last place Halric saw Feddel.
There’s Green…. on Everything
The green growth is a side effect of the Ullac Regime’s machine, which is
designed to extract raw magical essence from specific creatures. The machine relies on
harvested magical components like unicorn horns, pixie wings, and other potent
organic sources. However, the residual energy released from this process—an unstable
blend of natural magic and Weirding energies—escapes into the environment, causing
the uncontrolled fungal growth.
The growth acts like a magical parasite, spreading rapidly and infusing with
resonance energy, corrupting the land and destabilizing the local ecosystem. This
unintended consequence threatens to unravel nature’s delicate balance, while the
remnants of the Ullac cabal disregard the danger in their quest for power. This link
becomes clearer as the players piece together clues, revealing that the fungal spread
isn’t just an anomaly—it’s a symptom of the cabal’s sinister, ongoing work hidden deep
within the Hurstwold.
An Unusual Meeting

The day begins like any other at the Holmean Magical Creature Society’s

headquarters, with sunlight filtering through stained-glass windows. The compound
hums with activity: caretakers feed enchanted creatures, apprentices study under
experienced Sev’rinns, and researchers debate strange reports from the field.
As the characters gather for their morning meeting, the usual bustle of the
Holmean Magical Creature Society is interrupted by a loud commotion at the front
gate. Ardella pauses, narrowing her eyes as the noise grows louder—shouts, hurried
footsteps, and the low hum of unfamiliar magic.
At the head of the room, Ardella Lentris (Notable Figures, pg. X) the lead field
coordinator, leans over her notes, adjusting her spectacles. “All right, everyone, quiet
down. We’ve got a packed day—new reports came in overnight.”
She taps a list on the board. “Routine habitat inspections, a few rescue missions,
and—”
Just as she starts to unroll a scroll from a metal receptacle, a disheveled ranger
patrol officer bursts into the room, dragging in a half-collapsed farmer. The farmer’s
clothes are tangled with green tendrils, green fungus creeping up his arms. He gasps,
struggling to speak, “It’s… growing on everything… the houses, the fields… even… on
us.”
The ranger turns to Ardella, panting, “Something’s not right—this stuff is
spreading fast, and it’s moving like it has a mind of its own.”
As you’re watching, you can see the fungus growing up the farmer’s arms, and
growing where it drops to the ground or on the ranger’s clothes. (DC5 perception)
Ardella snaps into action, pulling a small stone from her pocket. Speaking into it:
“We’re going to need containment in the main conference room. Bio flora - unknown
origin.”
If the players don’t immediately react, the ranger urges them to help stabilize the
farmer or contain the spreading growths. Ardella throws them a pack containing gloves,
enchanted shears, and vials of solvent designed to neutralize rogue flora.
- Skill Challenge Options:
- Medicine (DC 10): Try to slow the fungal growth on the farmer’s body.
- Nature (DC 12): Identify the fungus and its strange properties.
- Arcana (DC 13): Detect the lingering presence of unknown magical energy.
As the characters act, the fungus spreads further, covering the farmer’s face and
choking his breathing.
Players must decide quickly whether to cut the tendrils loose, contain them with
solvents, or retreat to a safer location. Every moment of hesitation risks more spread.
The farmer, overwhelmed by the fungus, jerks violently before turning still. The
green tendrils pulse with eerie light as he mutates into a strange hybrid of man and
plant. His body twists, eyes glowing with an unsettling emerald hue—he is no longer
entirely human. But he remains completely still.
When the immediate crisis is contained, Ardella barks quick orders to secure the
room and assigns the players to investigate. “You’re going to Norwycke,” she says, “We
need to figure out what caused this before it spreads.”

The ranger, now in shock, can only mutter, “It’s in the soil. In the wind…”
Making arrangements to leave, the ranger will meet the players before they head
out. He will meet them in Norwycke, he has something to attend to first.
Crossing the Sound
To reach Norwycke, the players must first travel to Leighmore, a small fishing
village on the southern edge of the Innerstifla Sound. Known for its wary seafarers and
stubborn independence, Leighmore provides the only practical route across the
treacherous waters to Norwycke.
The scent of brine and fish oil clings to the air as you step onto Leighmore’s
weathered dock. Salt-encrusted fishing boats bob lazily in the cold water. A gruff
ferryman named Brun Forlow (Notable Figures, pg. X) greets you with a skeptical look.
“Going across the Sound, eh? Can’t say I recommend it this season—but coin’s coin.”
His boat, the Stone Current, awaits your boarding, rocking with the restless tide.
Brun hauls up the anchor with practiced ease, and the boat begins to glide across
the surface of the Sound. The cold wind bites at your skin as mist rolls in, swallowing
the shoreline behind you.
If the players make conversation with Brun during the crossing, he has the
following talking points to share:
- “It’s been getting worse out there.”
– Brun mentions that he’s heard unsettling talk from other sailors and
merchants about strange occurrences beyond the usual.
- “The trees aren’t right, neither is the air.”
– He describes the atmosphere near the forest as heavy and unnatural, like it’s
watching you.
- “Folks say green tendrils are showing up in places they shouldn’t—wrapping
around barns, crawling across fields.”
– He shares gossip that the green fungus seems to grow unnaturally fast,
creeping into places overnight.
- “Some say it’s the Weirding. Some say it’s worse.”
– Brun doesn’t hide his unease, hinting that the rumors are spooking even
experienced locals.
- “A couple of boats went missing last month. Never came back from their route
across the Sound.”
– He adds that strange disappearances have increased, including boats vanishing
in calm waters.
- “I heard the folk in Norwycke don’t sleep much these days. Say something’s
moving through the trees at night.”
– Brun shares unsettling rumors of strange sounds and sightings in the forest,
making it hard for people to sleep.
- “Used to just be stories. Now, there’s no one laughing about it.”
– He expresses that what was once a local joke has turned into a genuine cause

for fear.
The boat ride turns into an unexpected challenge, where the players must take
control of the situation after the ferryman, Brun Forlow, becomes incapacitated.
The mist thickens, and Brun leans forward, squinting as he steers the boat
through narrow channels. Just as you begin to relax, something catches the old
ferryman off guard. His eyes widen in fear, and with a sudden shout, he stumbles,
falling hard against the side of the boat. His head strikes the wooden railing with a
sickening thud, and he slumps to the deck, unconscious.
For a moment, the boat wavers—and you feel the sharp tug of the current pulling
you dangerously off course.
Player Challenges:
Players must now step in to steer the Stone Current and keep it afloat as obstacles
arise. Several tasks can be divided among the party members.
1. Navigating the Sound:
A player needs to grab the rudder and attempt to guide the boat.
- Check: Wisdom (Survival) DC 14 to steer the boat properly.
- Consequence: On failure, the boat scrapes against rocks, taking 10 damage, and
a leak begins to form (see Plug the Leak).
2. Rowing the Boat:
Another player can row to fight the shifting currents.
- Check: Strength (Athletics) DC 12 to keep the boat steady.
- Consequence: On failure, the boat drifts further off course, adding another
obstacle to the journey.
3. Plug the Leak (if caused):
The boat takes on water after scraping rocks.
- Check: Dexterity (Sleight of Hand) DC 13 to stuff cloth into the cracks and slow
the flooding.
- Consequence: Without successful patching, players will have to keep bailing
water (Dexterity DC 10 every round)
Somehow, through luck or teamwork, you manage to keep the boat afloat and on
course. As the mist begins to thin, the distant cliffs of Norwycke come into view.
Though battered and soaked, you’ve made it—just as the old ferryman stirs with a
groggy groan.
Brun squints at you, rubbing his head. “That… must’ve been one hell of a ride,
huh?” he mutters. “Better you than me on that rudder, though.”
After hours of tense sailing, the cliffs of Norwycke loom out of the fog—dark and
foreboding. The harbor is eerily quiet. The lanterns hanging from weather-worn posts
flicker weakly in the wind, casting long, wavering shadows on the dock.
The locals you spot seem reluctant to speak, glancing nervously toward the edge
of Hurstwold Forest, which presses close against the town like a watchful beast.
Something’s Not Normal in Norwycke

As the players arrive in Norwycke, the town teeters on the edge of panic,
blanketed in the unsettling green growths they saw on the farmer. Tendrils coil up the
sides of homes, slowly consuming walls, roofs, and pathways. A few, very few, people
can be seen on the streets—vendors open stalls, fishermen haul nets—but every
movement is labored, hindered by creeping vines and spreading spores that twist
through doors, clog machinery, and trap livestock. The streets are nearly vacant, only a
few solitary souls scrubbing, scraping, and slicing at green fungus. Yet, despite their
best efforts, the green infestation grows faster than it can be removed.
In the marketplace, wooden stalls groan under the weight of vines. Green tendrils
snake along cobbled paths, slowing traffic as carts get stuck or livestock become
entangled. Stray animals behave strangely, avoiding the growths and circling the
town’s edges with anxious whines.
As they watch, a man hurriedly crosses the street, covered in a waxy substance.
He cuts green growths away from the neck of his tunic with one hand, while another
fetches a large glass bottle from his bag. Cutting the growths, he unstopped the bottle
and pours more waxy substance around his neck. The growths seem to visibly recoil,
and their growth slows to nearly a stop. He stoppers the bottle and places it back in his
bag, making eye contact with the nearest player, then turning away to continue his
work.
In Norwycke, the townspeople have adapted to the green growth’s peculiar
pattern—the fungus spreads most aggressively at twilight and just before dawn. The
players have arrived just before sunset. During these hours, citizens retreat indoors. The
safest times to be outside are midday and deep into the night. Inside buildings,
residents rely on Greensalve to protect doorways, windows, and cracks in the floor from
encroaching tendrils.
As the sun begins to dip behind the hills of Norwycke, the green tendrils
writhing along the streets seem to quicken, creeping up walls and curling through
cracks. Just as the players take in this unsettling sight, Oln Trevis, the innkeeper of The
Bleeding Bark, spots them from across the street. He waves urgently, his voice low but
tense.
“Hey! You there—get inside, quick! Twilight’s coming!”
The players hear the low hum of strange growth around them, twisting and
tightening as if sensing the shift in the sun’s light. Oln stands at the inn’s doorway,
waving them in. Tendrils stretch along the ground toward the players, and Oln’s
frantic gestures only grow more urgent.
“If those vines get hold of you now, you’ll wish you stayed on that boat!”
Once inside, Oln slams the door shut and douses the frame with a smear of waxy,
greenish salve from a glass jar. The vines outside writhe against the wood but stop
short of crossing the threshold. Oln sighs with relief, then turns to the players.
“You lot better have some Greensalve on you—or know where to get it. That
stuff keeps the growths at bay, but it’s in short supply these days. If you’re out, you’d
best pay a visit to Old Feddel’s Apothecary—assuming there’s still any left. The way
things are going, even Feddel might run dry soon.”

- Ask about the Greensalve: Oln reveals that Feddel’s Apothecary controls the
town’s stock. He hints that something feels off—as if the apothecary always has just
enough supply no matter how bad the infestation grows.
- Offer to help: Oln gladly accepts, mentioning that some homes ran out of salve
this morning. The players might decide to assist townsfolk in getting salve or tracking
its distribution.
- Inquire about the growth: Oln explains that twilight and dawn are the worst
times for the growth. He advises staying indoors and only traveling at night or during
the day.
Rapid Expansion
The players will need Greensalve at some point in order to survive in Norwycke
and the surrounding areas.
When the players reach Feddel’s Apothecary, they discover that something has
gone terribly wrong. The once bustling shop stands eerily silent, its windows cracked
and green tendrils creeping along the walls, as if trying to break inside. The front door
is slightly ajar, rocking back and forth with the breeze, a faint smear of Greensalve
visible along the door frame and along the windows—just barely holding the fungal
growths at bay.
- Feddel is nowhere to be found, but there is a sign on the door that says “Out for
lunch, back at midday.”
- Feddel’s notebook, lying on the counter, is a ledger of shipments and signatures
for sales. The last sale made from the shop was the day before yesterday.
All of the entries in the ledger of shipments of Greensalve are marked with a
cryptic symbol—a circle with three jagged lines, and no name or supplier contact, like
the other entries have.
- Behind the counter area, a door in the floor is left open, leading to an
underground storage area. Inside, half the salve supply is unboxed, the other still
boxed, and the growth of the fungus is visible even here.
While the players are exploring the storage cellar below Feddel’s apothecary,
faint footsteps creak across the floorboards above them.
- If the players succeed on a Perception (DC 10) check, they can hear muttering in
a low voice—just a few words:
“…they’ll be back… must be quick…” “find the ledger…”
- Options for Action:
The players can either sneak back upstairs, confront whoever is there, or try to
remain hidden to listen further. They’ll catch sight of a hooded figure crouched over
the counter, quickly flipping through the ledger, and writing on another scrap of paper.
- If the players interrupt, the visitor bolts for the exit, but the players catch the
figure before they can escape.
- They deny knowing anything but are clearly nervous and suspicious.
- A successful Insight check (DC 12) reveals they are lying and terrified of
something—
The hooded figure stumbles backward, pulling their cloak tighter. Their voice

wavers with fear and accusation:
- “Y-You’re with them, aren’t you? The ones spreading this cursed stuff…
Thought you’d fool us, come to check if it’s spreading fast enough?”
- “Did you come to make sure we stay hooked on your damned salve? We know
what you’re doing—spread the plague, sell the cure, and watch us crawl back for
more!”
- “I saw Feddel meet with you… He’s missing now, isn’t he? What have you done
with him?”
To convince the hooded figure they aren’t the suppliers:
Here’s a list of skill checks the players can attempt to convince the hooded figure
they aren’t connected to the Greensalve suppliers:
1. Insight (DC 10): Recognize that the hooded figure is acting out of fear rather
than aggression. A calm, empathetic approach might help ease their panic.
2. Persuasion (DC 10): Appeal to the figure’s sense of reason, explaining that the
players are also here to investigate the strange growth and need help finding the truth.
3. Deception (DC 10): If the players pretend to have some authority over the
situation (e.g., posing as investigators from the Society), they might reassure the figure
enough to cooperate.
4. Investigation (DC 10): A player who analyzes the ledger and points out that
they arrived only recently (after the last sale) can use it as proof that they aren’t
involved.
Once the supplier situation is all sorted out, the hooded figure feels a lot more
comfortable with the players.
The hooded figure introduces himself as Halric (Notable Figures, pg X)
The hooded figure takes a step closer, their voice filled with bitterness:
“It’s all too neat, too perfect—the problem and the solution wrapped in one
dirty package. But never ENOUGH of the solution. Just enough to keep us paying.
That’s how they’ve got us by the throat.”
They glance nervously at the windows, as if expecting someone to burst through.
“The shipments always arrive after the growth spreads—like clockwork. And Feddel?
He knew. He knew, but kept taking their money. Now he’s gone of course, probably
gone to save his own skin.”
“If you’re really not with them, listen. Feddel was meeting someone dangerous
—those Greensalve shipments don’t just fall out of the sky. Whoever gave it to him
knew exactly what they were doing.”
After the encounter with Halric in the apothecary, as the players are piecing
together Halric’s discoveries about the Greensalve suppliers, a distant but unmistakable
rumble shakes the walls. The fungal growth around them quivers, and Halric’s face goes
pale as he mutters, “It’s happening again.”
Rushing outside, the party witnesses a chilling sight: thick waves of green fungus
visibly spreading along the ground, advancing like a creeping tide. Townsfolk,
recognizing the signs of an “expansion,” scramble to retreat indoors, slathering
Greensalve along windows and door frames in a desperate attempt to protect their

homes.

As the players and Halric gather outside, the tremor intensifies, sending
vibrations through the ground and buildings around them. The villagers begin to
murmur nervously, their eyes fixed on the edge of town where the green fungus seems
to be gathering in thick clusters.
A sudden, chilling silence falls over Norwycke as every creature, every person
seems to hold their breath. Then, as if responding to an unheard signal, the green
growth surges forward in a wave, faster and more aggressive than ever before. Tendrils
twist and coil over each other, stretching like reaching hands as they push past the
town’s edge, encroaching upon the homes and shops.
Villagers scream, rushing indoors and frantically slathering Greensalve around
windows and doorframes. Children are dragged inside, animals flee, and doors slam
shut as the invasive green tendrils spread like a living creature, overtaking streets and
alleyways.
As the fungal expansion violently surges through Norwycke, Halric and the
players are separated in the chaos. Tendrils slam down between them, buildings creak
under the pressure, and a thick wall of green cuts off visibility.
Halric shouts through the rising growth, his voice distant and warped:
“If you make it out—meet me at the hollow stone! Old druid marker—east
edge of the Hurstwold trail!”
Then he’s gone—swallowed in a blur of mist and reaching vines.

## Episode 2: Creeping Death

Summary
Following the expansion wave, players investigate the origin of the fungal surge,
leading them into the edge of the Hurstwold Forest. There, they find a secluded glade
corrupted by vibrant but decaying magic. Embedded in the fungal blooms are bones,
horns, feathers, and scales—remains of magical beings who have been drained, not
killed in battle. In the shadows of twisted trees and in the crumbling ruins of a forgotten
outpost, the party uncovers the first undeniable signs that the green growth is no
natural phenomenon—and no accident.
Locating the Hollow Stone
The player’s are trying to locate the hollow stone.
Ask Oln Trevis (innkeeper of the Bleeding Bark):
“That hollow stone’s not far, but no one walks that path anymore. Too many
things growing wrong. Why would you want to go there?”

He can:

Give the players a
rudimentary map
to the stone circle.
Offer
leftover Greensalve
and warn it won’t last forever.
Suggest they
travel by midday
—the fungus is weakest then.
Search the Library or Local Records (Investigation Option)
If the players search Feddel’s Apothecary or a dusty shelf in The Bleeding Bark’s
common room, they can uncover:
An old surveyor’s map
with faintly marked druid sites—one circled in charcoal.
Investigation (DC 13)
to piece together that the hollow stone is aligned with leyline crossing points.
Arcana (DC 14)
reveals leyline energy may amplify or distort magic nearby.
Nature-Based Divination
If the party includes a druid, ranger, or nature-focused caster:
Speak with Plants or Animals
:
Nearby trees or moss will “remember” the stone. The stone “hums when the
forest listens,” but lately it’s been
weeping green
.
Druidic Marks
:
Nature (DC 12)
or
Survival (DC 14)
uncovers
carved sigils on trees
near town, pointing toward the hollow stone.
Magical Detection
Casting
Detect Magic
near Greensalve-treated areas may reveal a
resonance pulse leading outward
—a thread of ambient magic drawn toward the Hollow Stone, which serves as a
magical anchor or conduit.

The Hollow Stone lies at the edge of the Deep Hurstwold, a place where the normal
canopy breaks into a clearing flooded with green light, even at twilight. It rests in a
liminal zone—not quite inside the most corrupted part of the forest, but touched by its
breath. The air hums faintly, like a wine glass on the edge of shatter.
The clearing is accessed via a barely-visible trail marked by carved bark sigils,
reachable only after a steep descent down a moss-slippery ravine and through a tunnel
of arching, fungus-laced roots.
Skill check options:
Arcana (DC 13)
: The stone resonates like a tuning fork—it’s not a portal, but a
magical amplifier
, tuned to ley energy.
Religion (DC 12)
: This is a
watching place
, where druids once
communed with the Weald
to ask permission to harvest from the forest.
History (DC 15)
: The glyphs match pre-Ullac resistance symbolism—this was once a
secret meeting site
.
No matter how long they wait, Halric is not there.
Investigation Options
The party can explore the surrounding area:
Perception (DC 13):
A thin trail of broken twigs and green residue leads away from the clearing, as if
someone left in a hurry.
Survival (DC 14):
Partial boot tracks—adult-sized, erratic—heading deeper into the Hurstwold, away
from the ring. You count one set, maybe two.
Insight (DC 10):
Halric planned to meet you here. If he didn’t show, it means something
prevented
him—not a betrayal, but an interruption.
Player Choices
At this point, the party faces a choice:
Follow Halric’s Trail
(recommended):
This leads toward the abandoned outpost where the first Ullac extraction device
was tested (next scene).
Return to Norwycke
:

Doing so risks losing Halric entirely, but allows for regrouping and rest.
Attempt Magical Tracking
:
Locate Creature
,
Sending
, or similar spells may reach Halric—if he’s still alive.
The Hollow-Bound Herd
After tracking Halric’s trail via Survival (DC 14) or magical means (Locate
Creature, Divination, etc.), the players descend deeper into the Hurstwold. The trees
grow closer, the canopy warps the light, and even the air tastes faintly of copper and
ozone.
The tracks wind toward a boggy hollow thick with ankle-deep green sludge.
Strange hoofprints churn the mud—but no deer run here now. From the far side
of the clearing, eyes gleam from between the trees.
Encounter: Twisted Elk
Creatures: 2–4 Spore-Touched Elks (modified Giant Elk or Dire Wolves for lower
levels)
These were once normal forest guardians, now warped by prolonged exposure to
magical pollution from the machine. Their bodies are overgrown with glowing fungal
plates and spore-vents along the ribs. Antlers have splintered into crown-like branches.
Stats (Sample for CR 2–3 party)
Use base stats of Giant Elk or Dire Wolf, with the following changes:
Spore-Touched Modifications:
AC
: +1 (fungal plating)
Spore Bloom (1/day)
: 10-ft radius burst when bloodied or killed
•
DC 13 Con save or be poisoned
for 1 minute.
- On a success, players resist the poison but are briefly disoriented (disadvantage on
next attack or check).
Aggressive Herding Instinct
: If two elks are within 10 ft of the same target, they gain advantage on attacks
against that target.
Fungal Sensitivity
: Vulnerable to fire and radiant damage.
Tactics

The herd is not feral, but

driven
—by instinct or by a larger force.
If one creature is bloodied and another is dead, the final elk attempts to flee (can be
tracked).
A player using
Speak with Animals
or
calming magic
(e.g.,
Animal Friendship
) hears a mental image:
Inspecting the elk corpses reveals
sickened organs
, fungal threads in brain tissue, and
traces of magical residue
consistent with leyline corruption.
Arcana (DC 13)
or
Medicine (DC 12)
confirms this is not a natural infection. It’s ambient damage from proximity to a
magical force pulling nature out of rhythm.
If tracked, the fleeing elk leads away from where Halric’s trail was leading
Extraction Site
Arrival
After tracking Halric—or the fleeing elk—the party descends into a damp gully
where the ground shifts underfoot like rotten sponge. Stonework juts from the forest
floor, overtaken by vines and fungus. Ahead, half-buried in the slope, is the skeletal
husk of a metallic outpost: rusted walls, fractured sigils, pipes that pulse green beneath
layers of moss and mycelium.
Layout (for reference)
The ruined structure has three chambers, all in various states of decay:
1. Collapsed Entry Bay
2. Resonance Extraction Room
3. Holding Cell / Drainage Pit
1. Collapsed Entry Bay
This space has crumbled ceilings and fungal growth erupting from cracks in the
stone. You can hear someone yelling for help from inside.
Investigation (DC 12):
Players find
drag marks
—Halric was pulled through here, unconscious or resisting.

Arcana (DC 13):

Lingering traces of teleportation or forced resonance manipulation.
Obstacle
: A thick fungal wall (10 ft wide) blocks access deeper inside.
Can be burned (fire), dispelled (radiant), or bypassed with
resonance tuning
(see below).
2. Resonance Extraction Room
This chamber is the corrupted heart of the site. Rusted scaffolding surrounds a
central plinth where magical creatures were once bound and drained. The yelling for
help is louder here.
A wide, low platform of dull metal gleams faintly. Coiled tubes hang like veins
from the ceiling, some still dripping ichor.
In the corner
, a shattered
crystal resonance chamber
is scorched from within—someone (Halric?) tried to destroy it.
Interactions
Arcana (DC 14):
The machine fed on magical biology—horns, feathers, wings—to distill raw
essence. This machine is powered by the tissue of living magical creatures.
Medicine (DC 13):
Fungal overgrowth here mimics
nerve tissue
—as if the structure itself has become semi-living.
Religion or Nature (DC 15):
Using druidic energy here creates feedback—
the Weald is actively resisting this place.
3. Holding Cell / Drainage Pit
A small antechamber houses a rusted cell, its bars bent outward. The stone
beneath is cracked, and a slick green fluid runs down into a dark hole at the back.
Inside the cell
is the shredded remains of a magical creature—likely a dryad or unicorn—its
essence long drained. And Halric, beaten badly but relieved to see you.
A broken piece of crystal
lies embedded in the corpse.
Optional Encounter
A Sporebound Husk (CR 2–3 solo undead/mutant) shambles from the drainage
hole if disturbed:
Once a worker or failed test subject, now fused with fungal growth.
Abilities

: Necrotic burst on death, grapple with fungal vines, can mimic voices.
How to Disable the Ullac Extraction Machine
Method 1: Overload the Leyline Conduit
Arcane Detonation
The machine is still connected to local leyline currents. Overloading it with too
much raw magical input causes a feedback loop that collapses the arcane circuitry.
How:
Cast
multiple high-level spells
into the crystal resonance core (e.g.,
Dispel Magic
,
Shatter
, or
Lightning Bolt
) OR channel a
magic item’s energy
into the control glyphs.
Arcana (DC 15)
reveals this possibility during inspection.
Optional: Locate a
resonance node override panel
hidden beneath the plinth (Investigation DC 14).
Consequence:
Violent backlash:
shockwave knocks everyone prone
, minor damage (e.g., 2d6 force).
All remaining energy pulses into the forest—
a brief spike in green growth
, followed by collapse and stillness.
Nearby fungal creatures become erratic or feral
for the next hour.
Method 2: Burn the Heart
Destroy the Ichor Core
A visible chamber beneath the platform contains pulsing green ichor, sustained
by semi-living tissues. If fire or radiant magic is used directly on the ichor, the parasite
can be destroyed.
How:
Crawl into the core chamber (requires
Athletics DC 12
or
Dexterity DC 14
to squeeze in).

Apply

fire damage
, or pour in radiant-infused liquid (like holy water, a sunbeam vial, etc.).
A
Nature (DC 13)
or
Medicine (DC 15)
check confirms that the ichor mimics fungal reproduction tissue—
it can be sterilized
.
Consequence:
Permanent shutdown.
However,
a poisonous fog vents from the cracked tubing
—the area becomes hazardous unless players act quickly to evacuate.
The burned ichor
taints the soil
—that patch of forest dies, leaving a
scarred, grey clearing
.
Method 3: Offer a Resonant Sacrifice
Ritual Unbinding
The machine is sustained by a binding glyph loop using druidic and arcane
weave. It can be unraveled by completing the binding backwards—but only with a
living source of magical resonance as a catalyst.
How:
Discover the original activation glyphs (Religion or Arcana DC 16).
Cast
Remove Curse
,
Greater Restoration
, or
Dispel Magic
at the glyphs while someone
channels attuned magic
into the stone circle (e.g., a druid using Wild Shape, or a sorcerer sacrificing sorcery
points).
Consequence:
The growth halts
completely
, and the land breathes again.
The character acting as the conduit is permanently affected
:

Loses a spell slot permanently.

Takes a mutation (e.g., bark-skin veins, moss hair, one glowing eye).
Optional Clue Delivery
Hidden logs in the holding cell describe
early containment attempts
and
failed overrides
.
A broken researcher journal in the crystal chamber has
ritual sketches and leyline maps
.
A faint ghost-memory (flavor scene, no mechanics) can show a test subject being
overloaded and the effect it had on the growth.
Clues and Evidence
By the end of this scene, the players should have discovered:
Some mysterious and powerful organization
designed this machine
to harvest raw magic.
The machine’s use
left behind unstable, parasitic energy
, which
feeds the green growth
now infecting the forest.
The site was
abandoned but not inactive
—leyline currents keep some systems passively charged.
Resolution: The Aftermath of the Machine
Once the machine is disabled (by any of the three methods), the entire ruin
groans as though exhaling. The green pulse in the pipes flickers, then fades. Somewhere
deep beneath the forest, an echo of that same pulse trembles outward—and dies.
Visuals and Effects (Based on Player Action)
Overload (Arcane Detonation)
:
Burn the Heart (Sterilization)
:
Ritual Unbinding (Resonant Sacrifice)
:
Halric’s Condition
Halric, if rescued, is bruised and burned from magical backlash. He can walk with
assistance, but he is rattled.
He insists they take the broken crystal embedded in the corpse—it contains a
residual arcane signature that can be used to trace other machines if studied by the
right people.

Players find:
A coded map
in the research logs, showing
multiple testing locations
deeper in the Hurstwold.

, burned into a steel plate—proof they’re still active.
A name
in a damaged journal entry:
“Ardella Lentris”
marked as

## Episode 3: The Machine Dreams Still

Summary
End of Episode 2: Decision Point
After disabling the Ullac extraction machine and rescuing Halric, the party discovers:
Proof that
Ardella Lentris
, a respected field coordinator from the
Holmean Magical Creature Society
, was overseeing the site.
Evidence that the machine’s purpose is not accidental—it’s part of a
deliberate, organized effort
.
Player Choices
Option 1: Confront Ardella Directly
“She needs to answer for this.”
What it means:
The party chooses to
seek out Ardella immediately
—through diplomatic channels, magical tracking, or by heading to the next
extraction site to cut her off.
This is the
bold, justice-forward
path. Risky, fast, and dramatic.
Leads into:
A chase structure
in Episode 3, possibly intercepting her or her agents at the next site.
Potential combat encounter with
loyalists or mercenaries
protecting her.

Possibly catching a

partial confession
—enough to use, but not the whole truth.

“The Society needs to know what’s happening inside its own walls.”
What it means:
Players believe in the HMCS and choose to
alert high-level members
—possibly sending Halric or a messenger while they continue forward.
This is the
institutionalist path
—hoping to
rally allies, reveal the corruption
, and turn the tide from within.
Leads into:
A slower Episode 3 start, but one that opens doors:
Messages from allies
Coded responses
Possibility of

, a base of operations, or new equipment.

Is there someone else in the HMCS they can trust?

“We can’t afford to stop. Not yet.”
What it means:
The party chooses to
continue pursuing the map of extraction sites
, hoping to
gather more evidence
before tipping their hand.
This is the
rogue investigation path
—prioritizing
exposure over confrontation.
Leads into:
Discovery of
a larger, operational extraction site
in Episode 3.
The
first glimpse of the cabal’s true nature
—a sigil, a named agent, or a ritual in progress.
Greater personal danger, but deeper knowledge gained.

### DM Guidance: Let the Players Split the Response

They might
send Halric
back to alert HMCS while continuing alone.
They might
try to magically contact
a trusted Society figure.
They might
plan to confront Ardella
, but discover she’s already several steps ahead.
Each option is valid and should lead into a custom Episode 3 hook based on their
choice.
Trail of Ash
Episode Entry: Modular Setup
Use the following to determine how the players arrive at this episode’s events:

### IF the players chose to Confront Ardella Directly:

Halric confirms her last known location matches the next extraction site on the
coded map. The party follows her trail west through the Hurstwold, reaching a
burned scouting camp and a shattered beacon post.
Proceed to Scene 1A: Burned Camp

## IF the players chose to Contact the HMCS:

After sending evidence and a copy of the coded map to the Society via Halric,
the players receive a magically encrypted reply. A field agent named Thalen
Dorr confirms suspicions about Ardella and relays her likely destination.
Proceed to Scene 1B: Message in the Flame

## IF the players chose to Investigate Alone:

Traveling deeper into the Hurstwold using the map, the players encounter
traces of an abandoned forward camp and leyline disturbance patterns that

mirror the ruined machine site.
Proceed to Scene 1C: Unquiet Trees

## Scene 1A: Burned Camp

“The trees here haven’t just burned—they’ve bled. The ash smells like old
spellfire, and the ground is littered with torn Society field kits.”
Investigation (DC 13):
Find a branded Society tool case—but the sigil is wrong. It’s not the HMCS, but a
forged version
using distorted script.
Arcana (DC 14):
Trace of a teleportation circle—destabilized and burnt out.
Survival (DC 12):
Discover tracks leading north toward an
overgrown ravine
—a shortcut to the next site.
Optional Combat:
Two Sporefang Stalkers—feral fey-beasts bred to track intruders.
(Use Shadow Mastiff stats with poison instead of fear.)

## Scene 1B: Message in the Flame

“As the campfire burns low, an ember rises unnaturally and spins in the air. A
voice—clear, deliberate—emerges from the heat.”
This is Thalen Dorr
, HMCS internal affairs mage. The message confirms:
Ardella has been under investigation in the past.
Thalen begs the players:
“Find proof. We’ll act if we can—but we need something irrefutable.”
Reward:
HMCS-Sanctioned Tracker Charm
(Advantage on Survival when following known magical signature)
Party is now being
watched

—NPC society watchers may appear later.

## Scene 1C: Unquiet Trees

“The wind stops. The leaves hang, frozen. Then one falls—but instead of
landing, it spins in place, caught in invisible breath.”
A corrupted
leyline wellspring
sits beneath a tree, pulsing with quiet resonance.
Detect Magic:
Reveals a flickering arcane trail, like static in the weave.

The trail leads to an unnaturally fast-growing fungal spire—
a signal post
used by Ardella’s handlers.
Inside the spire:
Fragments of messages—
code names, a schedule, an emblem
carved into the bark: a stylized
eye inside a spiral
.

## Shared Scene: Crossroads of Smoke

Regardless of entry, all stories reach the same encounter:
“The trail tightens through a ravine choked in fungal haze. Light bends wrong
here—refracted, smeared. And ahead… a figure. Cloaked, staff in hand.
Watching.”
The players meet Ilgen Durn, a soft-spoken elven ex-Society scholar who once
served with Ardella. He warns:
Mysterious figures are heading for the
Vault of Ashroot
, an ancient leyline convergence site hidden under the Weald’s roots.
Ilgen offers aid
only if the players commit to stopping the energy bleed into the forest:
Ilgen’s Gift:
A

## Resonance Disruptor Rod

– usable 1/day to
interrupt any machine’s pulse
for 10 seconds (enough to break a ritual or free a creature).
Vault of Ashroot
Description
The Hurstwold deepens—canopy thick as woven iron, air heavy with moss rot
and static tension. The forest opens not upward, but down—revealing a spiral
fissure lined with root-bridges and fungal shelves. At the bottom: the Vault of
Ashroot.
A sunken ruin, overgrown and humming with ley-resonance. What was once a
druidic convergence temple is now corrupted by a modified extraction device, buried
into its core like a tumor in a heart.

## Exploration Zones

1. Vault Entrance
Roots spiral down into a hollow dome
, half-ruined, slick with bioluminescent fungal runoff.
Perception (DC 13):
Hear the distant whine of a machine pulsing with rhythmic energy—like slow
breath.
Arcana (DC 12):
Trace lines of raw ley energy, pulled
against their natural flow
into the center chamber.
2. Outer Ring Chambers
Ruined chambers used long ago for
druidic rites
—now repurposed.
Players may discover:
A map
of extraction networks.
Memory fungus
that replays echoes of rituals once held here (flavor vision).
A
spent summoning circle

, burned out and twisted.
Optional Encounter:
Echoform Beasts – creatures that have bled partially into this reality from the
resonance pull (use Phase Spider stat block, reflavored with fungal-magic
effects).

## At the Vault’s Heart

“A crystal spire rises where the old altar once stood, wrapped in metal tubing
and humming green energy. Inside its glass: a massive pulsing creature—too
warped to name—being drained of essence.”
This is the Threshold Machine—larger, more refined, and actively testing portal
mechanics. It is not just drawing magic—it is testing boundaries between places. It is
utilizing resonance to open a new rift to Nebernoria.

## Choices / Interactions

Players may attempt:
Shut it down
(Resonance Disruptor Rod helps here)
Study it
(Arcana DC 16 reveals it’s
trying to form a “resonance bridge”
to somewhere else)
Free the creature
(Risky—may trigger machine instability)

## Optional Intel

One of the machine terminals contains a
holograph-style memory recording
of Ardella:
“Vessel Threshold Engine, target Coordinate: NBNR-Ax13. Begin parallel tests
at Vaults 5 and 7.

Tell the Ullac: Threshold viability is above 83%.”

If decoded, this reveals:
Ardella is no longer concerned with creatures—she’s using them as jump-starts
for
perpetual magical extraction
.

## Scene 4: Confrontation – Not Ardella… Yet

As the players make a decision, they’re not alone. A new figure enters—an Ullac
Agent, masked and cloaked.
Footsteps echo across the stone. A figure in bone-plated robes and fungalthreaded gloves steps forward. Their mask bears the Spiral’s eye sigil, carved
into a steel plate. Their voice distorts slightly, like they’re speaking through
resonance.

“It’s always the same. You see what we’re building and try to smash it. But
smashing the machine won’t unmake the need for it. You’ll see.”
Combat Option:
Ullac Agent + 2 Echoform Beasts
(Agent uses Warlock/Necromancer build with portal magic and voice mimicry)

## End of Episode 3: The Door Opens

During or after the fight, the Threshold Machine activates briefly, creating a stable
portal for 3 seconds. What’s on the other side is hard to perceive—but it’s not this
world.
If not stopped, the machine attempts a full bridge test in 72 hours. A full success
could mean a new rift to Nebernoria, and catastrophic magical consequences.

## Episode Rewards

Ley-anchored Resonance Core
(used to track machine tests)
Whispervine Charm

(lets players send 1-way messages through the Weald to known allies)
First clear symbol of the Ullac Regime’s return

## Story Summary & Next Steps

What the Players Might Do Next
Present the players with these options as rumors, messages, or decision points in
the aftermath of the Vault encounter:

### OPTION 1: Send Evidence to the Holmean Magical Creature Society

“The Society needs to know what’s being done in its name.”
Players may send encoded messages, fragments of glyphwork, or even the
resonance logs.
If done quickly, the Society may send
reinforcements or institutional support
by Episode 5.
Thalen Dorr may respond with new intel or request an in-person meeting.
Recommended if the players value justice, institutional change, or rallying
allies.

## OPTION 2: Track Ardella Directly

“If we stop her, the whole thing falls apart.”
The coded map shows a second active Vault site—
Vault 7
—farther east, near the collapsed ley crater of Duskwither.
Ilgen Durn offers to guide them part of the way, but won’t go farther.
Tracking her immediately may let them
intercept the next test or confront her
before the Spiral completes their calibrations.
Recommended if the players want a high-risk, high-reward pursuit arc.

### OPTION 3: Sabotage the Remaining Machines One by One

“We can’t fight them head on. But we can unravel their foundation.”
The players may strike from the shadows, using the map to find
Vaults 5 and 7
, dismantling them before Ardella reaches them.
This may draw the Spiral’s attention and paint targets on their backs.
However, successful sabotage may
slow or permanently destabilize the Rift geometry
.

Recommended if players favor tactical resistance, secrecy, or long-game

disruption.

## Appendices

A Detailed History
The Ullac Regime
The Ullac Regime emerged in the aftermath of the Torgarian War, during a time
when Ryndor was fractured and vulnerable. With the fall of the Sev’rinn royal family
and much of the realm in disarray, power-hungry factions vied for control. Into this
chaos stepped Knute Shun-Rote, who sought to restore order by establishing the Ullac
Regime, named for “law and discipline.”
Initially, the regime was welcomed as a stabilizing force. Knute and his allies
promised security through rigid governance, instituting a bureaucratic system that
emphasized law, punishment, and taxation. However, as the regime consolidated
power, it grew increasingly authoritarian, expanding its influence over every aspect of
Ryndorian life. The regime outlawed unsanctioned magic, seeing it as a threat to order.
Magical practitioners, especially Sev’rinns, were forced into hiding or pressed into
service under strict control.
The Ullac Regime’s strength lay in technology and discipline. Utilizing
advancements in anti-magical technology and surveillance, the regime created a
militarized state that curtailed magic use and crushed dissent. Political rivals were
swiftly dealt with, either through exile or execution, and the regime’s network of
nullification engines and automaton sentinels ensured there were few safe havens for
those who resisted.
Despite its authoritarian nature, the Ullac Regime expanded trade and
infrastructure, gaining support from wealthy merchants and cities like Ban Mynydd
that thrived under the regime’s rule. However, these advances came at the cost of
personal freedom, and over time, discontent simmered among the magical population.
What began as a necessary order following war soon evolved into a system of
oppression, setting the stage for the eventual Sev’rinn rebellion.
The Ullac Regime’s Treatment of Magical Creatures and Peoples
The Ullac Regime viewed magical creatures and practitioners not as individuals
but as potential threats to the state’s rigid control. The regime enacted policies of strict
containment and exploitation, regulating all magic-related beings.
Magical practitioners, including Sev’rinns, were forced to register with the
regime and were either pressed into servitude or imprisoned within nullification
zones, where their powers were neutralized. Those who refused were branded traitors
and hunted by automaton sentinels.
Magical creatures fared no better. Beasts such as elementals and minor drakes
were either enslaved for industrial use or exterminated. Wyrmbost’s smaller drakes
were captured to aid mining operations, their fire harnessed to power machinery. In
other cases, creatures considered too dangerous or untamable were eradicated outright.
The regime’s policies also extended to the severance of ancestral bonds—many
Sev’rinns were stripped of their heritage, forbidden to practice rites or rituals tied to

their magic. This cultural suppression aimed to disconnect magical beings from their
identities, reducing them to tools for the regime’s war machine. The result was a
population suffused with fear and resentment, leading to the first whispers of
rebellion that would eventually ignite the War of the Sev’rinns.
The Technological Marvels of the Ullac Regime
The Ullac Regime maintained dominance over the magical population of Ryndor
through a combination of cutting-edge technology and ruthless control. While Sev’rinn
magic relied on personal mastery, the regime’s technological infrastructure was
designed to be efficient, scalable, and brutally precise. Their innovations neutralized
magical threats, curtailed rebellion, and allowed them to exert control over vast regions
with minimal resistance.
--1. Nullification Engines
- The regime developed nullification engines, enormous devices capable of
creating anti-magical fields that could suppress magical abilities within a defined
radius. These engines were installed in key cities like Eveltoft and mounted on airships,
rendering magical attacks useless during battle.
--2. Automaton Sentinels
- Automaton Sentinels, mechanical soldiers powered by arcane cores, patrolled
the streets and guarded regime strongholds. These constructs were immune to magical
influences, making them ideal for tracking and capturing rogue Sev’rinns. Some were
enhanced with combat modules capable of detecting even the faintest traces of magical
energy.
--3. Precision Arc-Weapons
- The Ullac Regime’s arc-weapons used energy harnessed from crystalized rift
artifacts. These weapons could fire concentrated bursts of magical energy in controlled
forms—either lethal bolts of lightning or disruptive waves that disoriented spellcasters.
In combination with nullification fields, these weapons ensured battlefield superiority
over magical forces.
--4. Skyfleet: Airship Armada
- The regime maintained an armada of airships, allowing them to quickly deploy
forces across Ryndor. Some of these ships carried arcane dampeners that extended
nullification zones into enemy territory. Others served as flying prisons, where
captured Sev’rinns were shackled in enchanted cells designed to drain their powers.
--5. Surveillance Infrastructure
- The regime used scrying orbs and observation towers, powered by enchanted
machinery, to monitor rebel movements. A vast surveillance network covered Ryndor’s
cities and wilderness, tracking suspected dissidents and predicting rebel strategies. This
infrastructure gave the Ullac forces a tactical advantage, as they were often able to

intercept rebel plans before they were carried out.
--6. Rift-Enhanced Constructs
- The most dangerous innovation came from experiments with artifacts from
the Nebernorian Rift. These artifacts powered experimental constructs—monstrous
hybrids of technology and magic that acted as living weapons. Although volatile and
unpredictable, these constructs were unleashed in battles to devastating effect,
demoralizing rebel forces and leaving ruin in their wake.
--The Ullac Regime's technological supremacy gave it the edge needed to control
both magic and its practitioners, creating an overwhelming presence that stifled
resistance for decades. Their reliance on machines and surveillance, however, made
them blind to the subtleties of the Sev’rinn rebellion. As the rebels adapted, exploiting
the regime’s rigidity and weaknesses, the tide of the war began to turn—though not
without great sacrifice.
The Ullac Regime’s Harvest Technology: Recycling Life into Power
The Ullac Regime pushed its control beyond mere suppression, developing grim
technologies powered by the harvest of magical creatures and practitioners. These
machines, known as Arcane Recycling Engines, extracted vital elements from magical
beings and repurposed them to fuel the regime’s war machine. The process was both
brutal and efficient, transforming living magic into raw energy.
- Unicorn horns, symbols of purity, were ground into powder and used in
alchemical engines to stabilize nullification fields.
- Ember stones—crystals formed in the hearts of dragons—were extracted postmortem to power arc-weapons and airships. These stones produced immense heat,
making them invaluable for industry and combat.
- The blood of Sev’rinns, rich with magical potential, was distilled into potions
and combat serums. Regime soldiers injected themselves with this substance to gain
temporary magical resistance or heightened abilities during battle.
Captured Sev’rinns and magical creatures were imprisoned in draining
chambers, where their life force was slowly siphoned and converted into raw energy.
These machines, eerily precise, ensured nothing went to waste. Once drained of vitality,
the remnants of these beings were either discarded or burned, fueling the regime’s
conquest while snuffing out magical resistance.
This brutal cycle of harvesting and exploitation became a hallmark of the
regime’s technological supremacy. Entire ecosystems of magical beings were
devastated, while the regime’s weapons and engines hummed with stolen power. These
atrocities not only fed the war effort but also drove many neutral factions—including
the Keepers of the Rift—to align with the Sev’rinn rebellion, disgusted by the regime’s
desecration of life and magic.
War of the Sev'rinns
Timeline of the War of the Sev’rinns
---

1. The Seed of Rebellion (Year 0-2)
- Riven Trug and Ophelia establish Holmea as a stronghold for magical refugees,
rallying allies to resist the Ullac Regime. Smugglers, scholars, and underground guilds
pledge support, laying the foundation for the rebellion.
--2. Formation of Rebel Alliances (Year 3-5)
- Riven unites splintered factions, forging uneasy truces between merchants in
Surreymouth, rogue miners from Ban Mynydd, and disillusioned nobles from Eveltoft.
The Keepers of the Rift begin secret negotiations with the rebels.
--3. The Rift’s Appearance: A Turning Point (Year 6-7)
- The appearance of the Rift to Nebernoria in Eveltoft devastates morale within
the Ullac Regime. Immune to the regime’s nullification fields, the Rift proves the limits
of the regime’s technology. Astral storms and strange creatures spill into Ryndor,
spreading fear and chaos among both sides. Many regime soldiers desert, realizing that
their antimagic weapons are useless against the new threat.
--4. The Siege of Eveltoft (Year 7-8)
- Emboldened by the Rift’s arrival and the regime’s faltering control, the rebels
launch a full assault on Eveltoft. With support from Wyrmbost’s drakes and Mt.
Bannockwyrm’s elder dragons, the siege becomes a symbol of the rebellion’s rising
strength. Despite internal disputes, Ophelia’s leadership holds the movement together.
--5. The Rift Crisis and the Nebernorian Turn (Year 9)
- The regime’s attempts to weaponize artifacts from the Rift backfire, unleashing
astral anomalies across the battlefield. With the Keepers of the Rift now allied with the
rebellion, the astral incursions are sealed, preventing further disaster.
--6. The Fall of the Ullac Regime and the Rise of the Keepers (Year 10)
- The Ullac Regime collapses under the combined weight of internal rebellion and
external astral threats. The Nebernorian Accord is formalized, evolving into the
Keepers of the Rift, who take up the dual task of safeguarding the Rift and ensuring that
the horrors of the regime’s technology are never repeated.
--The appearance of the Rift marked a pivotal shift in the war, showing the limits of
technology and ushering in the fall of the Ullac Regime, as fear of the unknown
shattered their authority and emboldened the Sev’rinn rebellion.
The Seed of Rebellion on Holmea
Holmea, with its towering cliffs and perpetual mists, became the perfect refuge
for those seeking to escape the oppressive grip of the Ullac Regime. It was here, far from
the reach of prying eyes, that Riven Trug—descendant of Ysilpak Trug—established a
stronghold for magical practitioners and the exiled descendants of Torgar Shun-Rote.
Riven envisioned more than just a sanctuary; he sought to build a place where magic

could flourish once more, free from the restrictions imposed by the regime.
Holmea quickly became a hub for rebels and outcasts, attracting those who
refused to abandon their magical heritage. Wizards, alchemists, and Sev’rinns of every
lineage gathered under Riven’s banner, weaving together old traditions with new astral
knowledge gleaned from artifacts brought through the Rift. It was during this time that
Riven Trug met Ophelia, a powerful Sev’rinn from the bloodline of Celestia Tenk.
Ophelia’s charisma and mystical insight captivated Riven, and the two formed a bond
that would shape the future of the rebellion.
Ophelia had experienced firsthand the regime’s oppression and spoke not only of
revolution but of renewal—a vision of a world where magic could thrive in harmony
with order. Recognizing her potential as a leader, Riven entrusted her with the mantle
of Praetor Oracle, making her the symbolic heart of the movement. As Ophelia took on
this role, she began to develop the philosophical foundation of the rebellion,
emphasizing the importance of balance—both within magic and among the fractured
factions of Ryndor.
Together, Riven and Ophelia transformed Holmea from a haven into a thriving
rebel stronghold. The pair organized the first Council of Holmea, uniting disparate
magical factions under a single cause.
From Holmea, they coordinated covert missions across Ryndor, smuggling
supplies and spreading word of the rebellion. It was within the halls of Holmea’s hidden
libraries and enchanted forges that many of the tools and spells used in the rebellion
were crafted, blending ancient Sev’rinn magic with astral innovations.
The alliance between Riven and Ophelia solidified the rebellion’s purpose, setting
the stage for a movement that was not merely about survival but about reclaiming the
right to exist freely and powerfully. With Holmea as their sanctuary and Ophelia as their
figurehead, the rebellion’s leaders began to weave a strategy that would challenge the
Ullac Regime’s dominance and restore the pride of the Sev’rinn bloodlines.
Allies of the Rebellion: Political Maneuvers and Covert Operation
As the seeds of rebellion took root on Holmea, Riven Trug and Ophelia forged
critical alliances across Ryndor, employing both diplomacy and subterfuge to
strengthen their movement. These alliances extended beyond magic users, drawing in
merchants, scholars, rogue operatives, and sympathetic nobles who sought to
undermine the Ullac Regime’s oppressive control.
--Political Allies and Merchant Networks
- Surreymouth’s merchants were the first to pledge support. Riven promised
them protection from the regime’s crippling taxes in exchange for supplies and discreet
transport routes. The merchants established covert trade networks, funneling food,
weapons, and magical artifacts from coastal cities to Holmea.
- Ophelia’s influence reached Eveltoft’s council chambers, where disgruntled
officials began leaking vital intelligence to the rebels. Although some nobles acted out of
self-preservation rather than idealism, these betrayals provided the rebels with key
insights into the regime’s weaknesses.

--Covert Operations and Underground Guilds
- In the shadowy alleys of Ban Mynydd, Riven cultivated relationships with
smugglers and thieves' guilds, using their expertise to move people and artifacts
through hidden channels. These alliances proved invaluable, especially when the regime
began clamping down on public dissent.
- A faction of renegade Sev’rinns, exiled from the regime’s favor, joined the
movement. They established secret cells within urban centers, conducting sabotage
missions to disrupt the regime’s supply lines and infrastructure.
--The First Battles: Skirmishes and Resistance
- Early confrontations erupted along the roads between Ban Mynydd and
Eveltoft. Small bands of rebels ambushed regime caravans, seizing resources and
spreading fear among the Ullac troops. Though these skirmishes were minor, they
marked the beginning of a campaign to destabilize the regime’s control over trade and
transportation.
- Riven and Ophelia coordinated these operations from Holmea, using enchanted
scrying orbs to communicate across vast distances. This allowed them to strike swiftly
and retreat, keeping the regime off balance.
--Diplomatic Maneuvers and Fragmented Loyalties
- The rebellion faced challenges in maintaining unity. Riven’s efforts to unify
smugglers and noble sympathizers were often at odds with Ophelia’s desire to
maintain a clear moral vision for the movement. Yet, through deft diplomacy, Riven
ensured that ideological differences did not tear the alliance apart.
- Meanwhile, the rebels reached out to the Keepers of the Rift, who remained
neutral at the outset. Though reluctant, some Keepers began to share knowledge about
Nebernoria with the rebels, intrigued by Ophelia’s vision of a world where astral magic
could coexist with mortal rule.
--The Turning Point: Holmea as the Nexus
- Holmea evolved into both a strategic headquarters and a symbol of hope for
the rebellion. The island's workshops produced enchanted weapons, while its archives
became a repository of magical knowledge recovered from Nebernoria. Political
alliances deepened, as Ophelia and Riven pledged that Holmea would serve as the heart
of a new, liberated Ryndor, where magic would thrive beyond the regime’s reach.
These early alliances and operations formed the backbone of the rebellion, setting
the stage for larger battles to come. Every covert deal and small victory brought them
closer to their ultimate goal—**the fall of the Ullac Regime** and the restoration of
the Sev’rinn legacy.
The Alliance of Dragons: From Wyrmbost to Mt. Bannockwyrm
In the early days of the rebellion, Wyrmbost, known for breeding smaller drakes,
proved a valuable ally. These agile, fiery creatures served as scouts and couriers for the

rebels, delivering messages and performing hit-and-run strikes on regime supply lines.
However, Riven and Ophelia recognized that these drakes alone would not be enough to
shift the tide of the war.
It was through the trainers and beastmasters of Wyrmbost that the rebels
learned of the ancient dragons of Mt. Bannockwyrm, enormous and reclusive creatures
whose power had remained untapped for centuries. At first, attempts to contact the
larger dragons were met with silence, for the dragons of Bannockwyrm did not concern
themselves with mortal conflicts. Yet Riven knew that if these dragons joined the cause,
their sheer might could tip the balance of power.
Ophelia, wielding her knowledge of both astral magic and ancient Sev’rinn lore,
embarked on a diplomatic mission to Bannockwyrm. Accompanied by a group of
Wyrmbost beastmasters and several trusted rebel emissaries, she journeyed deep into
the volcanic caves of the mountain. There, the oldest and fiercest dragon, Xyntheras,
demanded not wealth but purpose—a reason to fight beyond mere human squabbles.
Ophelia’s vision of balance between magic and mortal life resonated with the
elder dragons, who saw the Ullac Regime as a threat to both freedom and the natural
order. She made a pact with Xyntheras and his brood, vowing that their ancient wisdom
would be honored and their domains protected in the new Ryndor. In return, the
dragons of Bannockwyrm pledged their strength to the rebellion, acting as powerful
allies during pivotal battles, laying waste to the regime’s fortresses, and instilling fear
in its armies.
The alliance between the smaller drakes of Wyrmbost and the massive dragons of
Bannockwyrm became a symbol of the rebellion’s unity—melding swift, guerrilla
tactics with overwhelming force. It was this partnership that would ultimately enable
the rebels to achieve decisive victories, bringing the dream of a liberated Ryndor ever
closer to reality.
The Heroes Who Brought Down the Ullac Regime: Targeting Technology in
Eveltoft
In the final days of the war, rebel factions launched daring missions to sabotage
the Ullac Regime’s technological infrastructure in Eveltoft, striking at the heart of its
control. These efforts came at great cost, with many operatives giving their lives to
ensure the regime’s fall.
--The Shadow Circuit – A group of rogue engineers and artificers from Ban
Mynydd, the Shadow Circuit infiltrated the regime’s nullification engines. They
overloaded key systems, disabling the anti-magic fields around Eveltoft, giving
magical forces a chance to push forward. Their final mission ended in tragedy, as they
detonated the engines with themselves still inside to prevent repairs.
--The Crimson Fangs – A mercenary band aligned with Wyrmbost, the Crimson
Fangs struck the surveillance towers controlling the regime’s scrying network. Under
Ophelia’s orders, they diverted attention from Holmea, drawing the regime’s forces
into costly street battles. Outnumbered and surrounded, the Fangs fought to the last

man, ensuring the rebellion’s secrecy until the final siege.
--The Keepers of the Rift – Though initially neutral, the Keepers turned against
the regime after witnessing the horrors of harvest technology. A covert strike team of
Keepers stormed the arcane research facilities, destroying experimental constructs
powered by Sev’rinn blood and preventing the deployment of new weapons. Their
leader, Elder Marlowe, sacrificed himself by triggering a magical collapse within the
facility to seal the laboratories forever.
--The Emberborn Saboteurs – A group of rebellious drake riders from Wyrmbost,
these saboteurs attacked the airship docks in Eveltoft. Using their swift mounts, they
set fire to the regime’s skyfleet before it could be deployed, though many were captured
and executed. Their sacrifice ensured that no regime airships would escape to rally
reinforcements.
--These heroic sacrifices paved the way for the final assault on Eveltoft, crippling
the regime’s ability to respond and giving the rebellion its decisive victory. Their names
became legend, honored by the Keepers and the new Ryndor, as a reminder that
freedom was won through courage, cunning, and sacrifice.

## Spells

New Spells of Ryndor
Magic in a World Twisted by the Weirding
The Weirding did not simply change the world—it rewrote its rules. The leylines
thrum with unstable resonance, old gods whisper through forgotten roots, and spells
once thought impossible now flicker into being across the scarred land of Ryndor. In
this chapter, you’ll discover new spells forged in the aftermath of unraveling reality—
gifts of the Rift, echoes of ancient magic, and tools born of desperation and adaptation.
Devour Life
Devour Life
3rd-level necromancy
Casting Time: 1 action
Range: 60 feet
Components: V, S
Duration: Instantaneous
You call upon the Many-Mouthed Mother's hunger to consume a fragment of a
creature’s essence. Choose one creature you can see within range. That creature must
make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the target takes 6d10 necrotic
damage, and you regain hit points equal to half the damage dealt. On a successful save,
the target takes half as much damage and you gain no healing.
If this damage reduces the target to 0 hit points, its body withers and caves
inward, its features partially devoured by an unseen force. You immediately gain

temporary hit points equal to your Warlock level + your Charisma modifier, and the
area where the creature died becomes tainted by the Weirding—strange whispers,
shifting shadows, or other minor sensory effects persist there for 1 minute.

At Higher Levels. When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher,
the damage increases by 1d10 for each slot level above 3rd.

## Special for the Many-Mouthed Mother Patron:

When you cast Devour Life, you may choose to whisper a truth to the dying target as part
of the spell. If the creature can understand language, it hears a psychic message only it
can perceive—either a memory, a secret, or a prophecy tied to the Weirding. This does
not prevent the damage but may have narrative effects at your DM’s discretion.
Wall of Mouths
Wall of Mouths
4th-level conjuration
Casting Time: 1 action
Range: 60 feet
Components: V, S, M (a scrap of raw meat and a pinch of salt)
Duration: Concentration, up to 1 minute
You conjure a writhing barrier of chattering, gnashing mouths in a 60-foot-long,
10-foot-high wall that is 1 foot thick. The wall appears at a point you choose within
range and lasts for the duration. The wall is difficult terrain and lightly obscures sight.
Each mouth on the wall whispers curses, hungers aloud, or laughs mockingly,
creating a maddening chorus that unsettles the mind and body alike.
When a creature starts its turn within 10 feet of the wall or moves into it for the
first time on a turn, it must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, the
creature takes 4d6 psychic damage and has disadvantage on the next attack roll or
ability check it makes before the end of its next turn. On a successful save, it takes half
damage and suffers no additional effects.
Creatures that move through the wall must also make a Dexterity saving throw
or take 3d8 slashing damage from the biting mouths. This happens in addition to the
psychic damage if both triggers apply.

At Higher Levels. When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher,
the psychic damage increases by 1d6 and the slashing damage by 1d8 for each slot level
above 4th.

## Flavor Notes for Ryndor:

In Weird Zones, the wall may mimic familiar voices or speak secrets the players
never revealed aloud.
Warlocks of the Many-Mouthed Mother may hear one mouth speak in her true
voice, giving cryptic guidance or demands mid-combat.
